# Implementation Plan

This is the ground-truth roadmap. Status is tracked per item.

Legend: `[x]` done, `[~]` in progress, `[ ]` pending.

Companion document: **`docs/ARCHITECTURE_PRINCIPLES.md`** — the durable
reference for the five universal multipliers and the per-pattern
enterprise upgrades that every item below is expected to satisfy. Read
that doc before implementing any item here.

> **For the _why_ behind every architectural decision below, see
> `docs/adr/` (Architecture Decision Records).** This plan is the
> build-order ledger; the ADR series is the rationale.

## Phase 0 — Foundations

- [x] Repo + tooling baseline (TS, ESLint, Prettier, Vitest, Husky, lint-staged)
- [x] ADR discipline established — `docs/adr/` series seeded with 15 backfilled decisions (0001–0015) covering modular-monolith, RLS tenancy, envelope encryption, audit hash-chain, 20-step command bus, `defineCommand` factory, SoD, outbox-as-DB-table, blind indexes, Stripe ports, carrier credentials, Clerk auth bridge. ADRs 0016–0022 reserved as stubs for parallel agents. See `docs/adr/README.md` for the process.
- [x] ESLint boundary rules from `ARCHITECTURE_PRINCIPLES.md` §D (cheapest enforcement layer): `@prisma/client` and the generated client path are private to `@pharmax/database` (every other workspace member imports the singleton + types from `@pharmax/database` — banned globally with override 1 dropping the ban inside `packages/database/**`); `withSystemContext` from `@pharmax/tenancy` is allowed only in `@pharmax/tenancy` (definition site), `@pharmax/command-bus` (`executeSystemCommand` orchestrator), `scripts/` (operator CLIs), and `*.test.ts` files (fixtures) — application code must go through a command handler. `no-restricted-imports` zoned overrides keep the existing legitimate call sites green and reject the next "I'll just import `@prisma/client` directly" PR at editor-squiggle time. Schema linter and command linter are still pending; tracked under Phase 5 enforcement work.
- [x] Local infra (`docker-compose`: Postgres, Redis, MinIO, Mailhog, PgAdmin)
- [x] `.env.example` expansion (S3/MinIO, app URL, encryption placeholders, session secret)
- [x] Dockerfile stubs for `apps/web` and `apps/worker`
- [x] `@pharmax/platform-core` package skeleton + first-party logger
- [x] **Billing module (Stripe webhooks)** — verifier, dispatcher, in-memory
      event store, transport-agnostic `handleStripeWebhook`, worker
      `processStripeWebhookEvent`, full test coverage. _(Landed
      out-of-order; nominally a phase-5 concern, but built early so the
      webhook contract was shaped before any HTTP transport was chosen.)_

## Phase 1 — Database baseline + apps + workflow spine

- [x] Prisma schema: tenancy core (organization, site, clinic, team, bucket, workstation)
- [x] Prisma schema: identity / RBAC (user, role, permission, junctions)
- [x] Prisma schema: workflow_policy
- [x] Prisma schema: audit primitives (command_log, order_event, audit_log, event_outbox, idempotency_key)
- [x] Prisma schema: billing FK promotion (Invoice / InvoiceLine / StripeCustomer)
- [x] First Prisma migration (`baseline`) — generated via `prisma migrate diff --from-empty`
- [x] `@pharmax/database` package wrapping the generated client (singleton, gitignored output)
- [x] Seed: 19 system permissions, 6 role templates, demo organization with site/clinic/team/buckets/workstation/user, v1 workflow policy stub
- [x] Prisma-backed `StripeWebhookEventStore` in `@pharmax/database` (idempotent inserts via `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` semantics)
- [x] `apps/web` Next.js 16 App Router skeleton (Tailwind v4, `/api/health`, `/api/webhooks/stripe` wired to the Prisma store, server-only env loader, console-backed `Logger`, Stripe client gracefully degrading when keys are absent)
- [x] `apps/worker` polling-based drainer (atomic `UPDATE … FROM (SELECT … FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED)` claim with lease, draining `stripe_webhook_event` and `event_outbox`; graceful SIGINT/SIGTERM shutdown with in-flight wait; `executeStripeWebhookEventDispatch` extracted from platform-core to support pre-claimed records). _BullMQ deferred to when a true queue-driven job appears (label render, email send, etc.); the outbox pattern is correctly implemented as DB polling because the source of truth is the table itself._
- [x] `@pharmax/platform-core` real impls: error hierarchy (`PharmaxError` + 7 subclasses with HTTP mapping, `toJSON` that excludes cause/stack); `Clock` interface + `systemClock` + `FrozenClock`/`AdvancingClock` test fixtures; monotonic `UlidFactory`; generic `defineEnv` (Zod) with secrets-safe error output; Pino logger with PHI-aware default redaction allowlist (apps/web and apps/worker refactored onto both `defineEnv` and `createPinoLogger`).
- [x] `@pharmax/tenancy` `TenancyContext` + `ScopedRepository` base — `AsyncLocalStorage`-backed `withTenancyContext` / `withSystemContext` / `requireCurrentContext`; positive registry of 24 tenant-scoped Prisma models (Organization filtered on `id`; PharmacySite, Clinic, Team, Bucket, Workstation, User, Role, UserRole, WorkflowPolicy, CommandLog, OrderEvent, AuditLog, AuditChainState, EventOutbox, IdempotencyKey, StripeCustomer, Invoice, InvoiceLine, Patient, Provider, Prescription, Order, OrderLine filtered on `organizationId`); 4 deliberately-excluded models (ClinicSite junction, Permission system table, RolePermission junction, StripeWebhookEvent pre-resolution) documented in `TENANT_EXCLUDED_MODELS` with the architectural justification. `tenant-scoped-models.test.ts` walks `Prisma.dmmf.datamodel.models` and asserts (a) every name in the scoped registry resolves to a real Prisma model, (b) every excluded name resolves to a real model, (c) scoped and excluded sets are disjoint, (d) every Prisma model is classified (scoped XOR excluded — no orphans), so a new model added in a schema migration cannot land without an explicit tenancy decision. `applyTenancyExtension(prisma)` Prisma `$extends` middleware throws `AuthorizationError(TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT)` on tenant-scoped queries with no active frame, passes through under `withSystemContext`, auto-injects `organizationId` into `where`/`data`/`upsert.create`, and throws `TENANCY_CROSS_ORG_WRITE` on mismatched writes; cross-org anti-leak property test driving 100 parallel queries across two orgs through a fake DB.
- [x] `@pharmax/rbac` permission registry + `requirePermission` guard — typed `PERMISSIONS` registry mirroring the 19 seeded codes (mirror parity asserted by a test that reads `prisma/seed.ts`); `EffectivePermissionLoader` interface with `InMemoryPermissionLoader` (tests) and `PrismaPermissionLoader` (one raw join, returns grouped `ResolvedGrant[]`); scope-aware resolver that filters grants by `TenancyContext.{siteId,clinicId,teamId}` against `UserRole.{siteId,clinicId,teamId}` (a SITE-pinned Pharmacist cannot PV1 at another site); per-context WeakMap cache so a command handler resolves once per request; `requirePermission(code)` guard throws `AuthorizationError(PERMISSION_DENIED)` with PHI-free metadata (`permission`, `organizationId`, `userId`, `correlationId`); `hasPermission` / `getEffectivePermissions` for UI affordance toggles; `configureRbac({ loader })` boot singleton, unconfigured = `InternalError(RBAC_NOT_CONFIGURED)`.
- [x] `@pharmax/rbac` enterprise upgrades (the increment that puts us beyond EONPRO; see `ARCHITECTURE_PRINCIPLES.md` §B.2):
  - **Separation of Duties** — `SOD_RULES` frozen registry typed against `PERMISSIONS` constants (no string drift); `checkSoD({attempted, resource, actor, priorActs})` pure predicate; `requireNoSoDViolation({...})` throwing wrapper for the command bus. Same user cannot perform both `PV1_APPROVE` and `FINAL_APPROVE` on the same order; same user cannot perform both `TYPING_COMPLETE` and `PV1_APPROVE` on the same order. SoD failures throw `AuthorizationError(SOD_VIOLATION)`; the command bus will reject with no audit-of-shame ambiguity when wired in Phase 2.
  - **Features (capabilities) registry** — `FEATURES` frozen registry parallel to `PERMISSIONS` for capability flags (`workflow.custom-buckets`, `intake.telehealth-callbacks`, `print.package-photos`, `shipping.easypost-outbound`, `integrations.dosespot-inbound`, etc.); `isFeatureCode` type guard; `FeatureFlagSource` interface with `InMemoryFeatureFlagSource` for tests; `resolveEffectiveFeatures()` with per-context `WeakMap` cache so the resolver runs once per request; `clearFeatureCacheForTests` escape hatch.
  - **Effective-with-source view** — `getEffectivePermissionsWithSource()` returns each permission with `source: 'role_default' | 'override_granted' | 'override_revoked' | 'not_available'` for the admin role editor; `getDeniedPermissionsWithReason()` returns the negative space ("why doesn't this user have X?") so the admin UI can explain misconfigurations rather than just hide affordances. Pure read; no auth side effects.
  - **Break-glass** — `buildBreakGlassGrant({user, permission, reason, durationMinutes})` validates the request: duration must be ≤ `BREAK_GLASS_MAX_MINUTES` (240), reason must be in the frozen `BREAK_GLASS_REASONS` registry (`PRODUCTION_INCIDENT`, `COVERING_FOR_ABSENT_PHARMACIST`, etc.), and the requesting user cannot grant themselves elevation. `BreakGlassWriter` interface separates the policy from persistence; the Phase 2 implementation will write a `BREAK_GLASS` audit chain entry, create a time-limited override row, and queue an auto-revoke job. Nightly worker job (Phase 5) emails `security@` with the day's break-glass log.
  - **101 contract tests across 9 files** cover the full RBAC surface (permissions registry, resolver, scope filtering, `requirePermission` guard, Prisma loader, features, feature-flag source, SoD rules, effective-with-source, break-glass policy).
- [x] `@pharmax/command-bus` 20-step contract — declarative `Command<TInput, TOutput>` interface (Zod input schema + RBAC permission + optional workstation requirement + per-command redact field list); `executeCommand` tenant orchestrator (validate → tenancy → RBAC → workstation → idempotency lookup → pre-tx `command_log` (RUNNING) → `$transaction` { `applyTenancySessionGuc` → handler → in-tx `audit_log` + `event_outbox` + `idempotency_key` } → mark `command_log` SUCCEEDED/FAILED); `executeSystemCommand` bootstrap orchestrator (no RBAC, in-tx `command_log` keyed on handler-resolved `targetOrganizationId`, `withSystemContext` requirement, `applySystemSessionGuc` invoked as first tx statement); `redactPayload` allowlist + always-redact set; deterministic `canonicalStringify`/`hashRequest` for idempotency matching; PHI-free errors (`COMMAND_INPUT_INVALID`, `COMMAND_IDEMPOTENCY_PAYLOAD_MISMATCH`, `COMMAND_WORKSTATION_REQUIRED`, `COMMAND_SYSTEM_CONTEXT_REQUIRED`); 29 contract tests asserting both positive writes AND negative "gate failure leaves zero DB footprint", including the RLS-GUC-before-audit ordering invariant.
- [x] `@pharmax/crypto` — envelope encryption with per-tenant KEK, **landed before any PHI table**. Implements the full primitive set the Phase 2 patient/prescription/order tables will depend on. **Canonical AAD encoding** (`crypto.v1` versioned, NUL-separated, sorted-key) over the record binding `{tenantId, table, column, recordId}` — every binding field demonstrably influences the AAD so a ciphertext moved between rows (different recordId, different column, different table, or different tenant) fails authentication on decrypt; empty fields and embedded NUL bytes are rejected at encode time. **Ciphertext envelope** is a JSON object (`{v: 1, alg: "AES-256-GCM", kek, wDek, iv, ct, tag}`) stored as a Prisma `Json` column; `parseEnvelope` is the choke point that rejects malformed shapes before the cipher sees them, and `ct === ""` is legitimate (zero-byte plaintext for empty PHI fields like `address_line_2`). **`KmsAdapter`** interface separates the seam between this package and the key store; production binds AWS KMS, dev/test binds `LocalKmsAdapter` which derives per-tenant KEKs via HKDF-SHA-256 (`info = "pharmax.kek.v1.<tenantId>.v<n>"`), rotates KEKs in-place via `rotateKek({tenantId})` (kid version bumped; historical wrapped DEKs continue to unwrap — the rotation guarantee), and derives per-tenant per-purpose 32-byte search keys (`info = "pharmax.search.v1.<tenantId>.<purpose>"`) that are decoupled from KEK lifecycle so blind-index columns survive KEK rotation. KEK-wrap is AES-256-GCM with random IV per wrap; the wrapped DEK is exactly 60 bytes (12 IV + 16 tag + 32 ciphertext). **`encryptField`/`decryptField`** generate a fresh DEK per call, mix the AAD into GCM, zero the plaintext DEK after use, and surface a GCM tag-verification failure as `AuthorizationError(AAD_MISMATCH)` (not a generic decrypt error — the security signal is "someone moved a ciphertext between rows"). Re-encrypting the same plaintext produces a different envelope (`iv`, `wDek`, `ct`, `tag` all change) so storage doesn't leak "these two rows hold the same value". **`blindIndex`** is HMAC-SHA-256 over `normalize(value)` keyed by the per-tenant per-purpose search key, base64url-encoded (43 chars) — deterministic for queryability, separated across tenants AND columns AND tables, returns `null` for empty-normalized values (caller leaves the column NULL rather than matching every NULL-equivalent row). Built-in normalizers: `normalizeForBlindIndex` (lowercase + trim + NFD-strip-combining-marks + whitespace collapse, so "Café" matches "Cafe" matches " JANE " matches "jane") and `normalizePhoneForBlindIndex` (digits-only, last-10). **`planCryptoShred`** is a pure, no-I/O intent boundary returning `{nextValue: null, reason, ...binding}` — callers apply the plan inside a command-handler transaction so the storage write, audit row, and outbox event commit atomically; reason vocabulary is frozen (`RIGHT_TO_BE_FORGOTTEN`, `TENANT_OFFBOARD`, `DATA_RETENTION_EXPIRY`, `PATIENT_DECEASED_RECORD_CLOSE`). **`configureCrypto`** is the boot singleton; reading without it throws `InternalError(CRYPTO_NOT_CONFIGURED)` (silence here would let a PHI write proceed unencrypted, the worst possible failure mode). **94 contract tests across 7 files** cover AAD determinism + per-field uniqueness + validation (13), envelope parse/serialize/guard (12), LocalKmsAdapter wrap/unwrap/rotation/tenant-isolation/search-key/empty-seed-rejection (22), end-to-end encrypt/decrypt with UTF-8/CJK/emoji/empty-plaintext roundtrip + AAD-mismatch on every binding field + cross-tenant ciphertext rejection + bit-flip tamper detection on `ct` and `tag` + IV-length guard + rotation continuity + JSON wire round-trip (15), blind-index determinism + normalization (case/accent/whitespace) + tenant/column/table separation + phone normalizer + null on empty + base64url shape (18), shred plan + reason validation + frozen-registry guard (10), configure singleton (4). **Wired at boot** in `apps/web` (`instrumentation.ts` → `src/server/bootstrap.ts`), `apps/worker` (`main.ts`), and `scripts/bootstrap-org.ts` — every entry point hard-fails in `NODE_ENV=production` because `LocalKmsAdapter` MUST be replaced by `AwsKmsAdapter` before prod promotion. Env contract: `PHARMAX_LOCAL_KMS_SEED` (≥32 chars, validated by Zod); apps/web and apps/worker MUST agree on this value or rows encrypted by one process are undecryptable by the other.
- [x] `@pharmax/command-bus` declarative `defineCommand({ name, inputSchema, permission, lockTarget, loadPolicy, sodRules, bumpVersion, redactFields, requireWorkstation, exec })` factory — compiles a declarative spec into a standard `Command<TInput, TOutput>` so the underlying `executeCommand` 20-step orchestrator is reused verbatim (the factory is sugar over the orchestrator, not a parallel path). Adds, in canonical order inside the bus tx after the tenancy GUC fires: **row lock** via `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` on a declared `lockTarget: { table: "order", by: (input) => ({ id }) }` returning `{ id, organizationId, clinicId, siteId, currentStatus, version, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion }` so the handler receives the freshly locked aggregate with the scope identifiers it needs to resolve per-site buckets or perform clinic-aware reads (no extra `findUnique` round-trip on the locked row — `clinicId` + `siteId` were added in lockstep with `StartTyping` so every in-flight workflow command gets them for free); missing row → `NotFoundError(ORDER_NOT_FOUND)`; **workflow policy load** by either `(code, version)` for create commands or by the locked target's `workflowPolicyId` for in-flight commands, asserts `status = "ACTIVE"` and throws `WORKFLOW_POLICY_NOT_FOUND` / `WORKFLOW_POLICY_INACTIVE` before the handler runs; **SoD rule resolution** translating declared rules (`eventTypeToPermission` translator from the command's domain package) into `requireNoSoDViolation` calls against `priorActs` derived from `order_event` history; **optimistic version CAS** via `updateMany({ where: { id, version: oldVersion } })` followed by an `UPDATE … RETURNING` and a row-count check that throws `ConflictError(ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH)` if a concurrent writer beat us; **`order_event` writeback** with monotonic per-order `sequenceNumber` (single `findFirst({ orderBy: { sequenceNumber: "desc" } })` + 1 inside the tx, advisory lock not needed because the row lock serializes), one row per declared `emits[]` entry, with `actorUserId`, `actorWorkstationId`, `correlationId`, `commandLogId` stamped from the tenancy frame and the bus's pre-tx `command_log` row; **saga compensation registry** with LIFO undo order on handler exception (compensators run inside the tx, then the original error re-throws to roll back). The factory's `exec` signature gives the handler `{ tx, ctx, input, policy, target, clock, registerSaga, emit }` — `target` is `null` when no `lockTarget` is declared (create commands), `policy` is `null` when no `loadPolicy` is declared. **21 contract tests across `define-command.test.ts`** assert: spec validation rejects `sodRules` or `loadPolicy` without `lockTarget`; the lock SQL fires inside the tx and uses `$queryRaw … FOR UPDATE` with the bound `id` parameter (no string interpolation); `ORDER_NOT_FOUND` short-circuits with zero downstream calls; policy load uses `findUnique({ organizationId_code_version })` for create commands and `findUnique({ id })` for in-flight commands; non-ACTIVE policy throws `WORKFLOW_POLICY_INACTIVE`; CAS bumps version exactly once and a zero-row updateMany throws `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` without writing `order_event` or audit; `sequenceNumber = head + 1` is monotonic and starts at 1 when head is null; declared `emits[]` flow into both `order_event` (per-row, in-tx) and `event_outbox` (via the bus's existing batch writer); saga compensators run in reverse declaration order on exec failure and the original error re-throws unchanged; canonical step ordering — session GUC → row lock → policy load → orderEvent.findFirst → exec → CAS → orderEvent.create → audit_log — is pinned by call-sequence assertions. See `ARCHITECTURE_PRINCIPLES.md` §B.6 + §C.3.
- [x] First end-to-end command: `CreateOrganization` shipped **through** `@pharmax/command-bus`, not as a plain function — the reference implementation for every subsequent command. New `@pharmax/orgs` package establishes the "domain packages own commands, bus package owns the bus" pattern that Phase 2 (`@pharmax/orders`, `@pharmax/verification`) will follow. The command runs via `executeSystemCommand` inside `withSystemContext("bootstrap:CreateOrganization")` — no RBAC, no idempotency cache, in-tx `command_log` keyed on the handler-resolved organization id. Inside one transaction: insert `Organization` (slug-unique; Prisma `P2002` → `ConflictError(ORG_SLUG_TAKEN)`) → clone the 6 system role templates from `@pharmax/rbac` into per-org `Role` rows + `RolePermission` grants (templates are the shared source of truth; `seed.ts` and this command both import them so the registries can't drift) → insert initial admin `User` (`INVITED`) → insert `OrgAdmin` `UserRole` grant (org-wide) → insert v1 `order.standard` `WorkflowPolicy` stub with the 11-state transition list. Bus then writes audit (`action: "organization.created"`, `resourceType: "Organization"`, system-context reason in metadata) + `event_outbox` row (`organization.created.v1`) in the same tx. Outbox handler registered in `apps/worker/src/drains/outbox-handlers.ts` logs a PHI-safe projection (no admin email surfaces even if upstream payload includes one). Operator CLI at `scripts/bootstrap-org.ts` (`pnpm bootstrap:org -- --slug=... --name=... --admin-email=... --admin-name=...`) drives the bus and prints the resulting ids. 7 contract tests pin the happy path, slug collision, missing-permission-registry diagnostics, and Zod input validation (bad slug, bad email, strict-mode extra fields).

## Phase 2 — Order workflow

- [x] **Postgres Row-Level Security baseline migration** (`20260522060000_rls_baseline`) — first Phase 2 migration, lands before any PHI table. Creates two Postgres roles (`pharmax_app` subject to RLS for normal runtime, `pharmax_system` with `BYPASSRLS` for the bootstrap path) — both `NOLOGIN` at creation; ops attaches credentials out of band. Enables AND **forces** RLS on all 18 tenant-scoped tables (FORCE means even the table owner is policy-checked, so a curious DBA in psql sees the same isolation runtime sees). Installs one `tenant_isolation` policy per table whose predicate is `current_setting('pharmax.system_context', true) = 'on' OR <tenant>` where `<tenant>` is `id = NULLIF(current_setting('pharmax.organization_id', true), '')::uuid` for `organization` and `"organizationId" = ...` for the rest; `NULLIF` collapses the empty-string GUC clear into a SQL NULL so an unset GUC fails the predicate (fail-closed). `audit_log` gets policy-level immutability: only `tenant_isolation_select` (FOR SELECT) and `tenant_isolation_insert` (FOR INSERT) policies — UPDATE/DELETE have no policy and are therefore denied by RLS, AND a redundant `REVOKE UPDATE, DELETE` from both app roles makes that immutability survive any future policy-table refactor. Session-GUC writers (`applyTenancySessionGuc` / `applySystemSessionGuc` / `clearSessionGuc`) live in `@pharmax/tenancy` and are invoked by the command bus as the FIRST statement inside every transaction (every value, including the empty-string clear and the literal `'on'`, is passed as a bound parameter — no string interpolation, no injection surface). Migration linter `scripts/check-migration-rls.ts` walks every migration in apply order and rejects any `CREATE TABLE` not paired with `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` + `CREATE POLICY` (either in the same migration or any later one) and not listed in `prisma/migrations/rls-exempt.txt`; any `DISABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` is a hard failure regardless of exemption. Four documented exemptions today (`permission`, `role_permission`, `clinic_site`, `stripe_webhook_event`) each with the architectural justification in a code-reviewed comment. See `ARCHITECTURE_PRINCIPLES.md` §B.1 + §C.1.
- [x] **Audit hash-chain writer + verifier** — `audit_log` gained three columns in migration `20260522190000_audit_chain` (`prev_hash` BYTEA nullable, `entry_hash` BYTEA NOT NULL, `seq` BIGINT NOT NULL) backed by a `(organizationId, seq)` unique index — the per-tenant integrity guarantee. The migration backfills `seq` (over `occurredAt`, `id`) and a sentinel `entry_hash = SHA-256("legacy:<id>")` for any pre-chain rows so the NOT NULL constraint is safe to enforce. `audit_chain_state` (one row per organization, RLS + FORCE-RLS protected, `SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE` only on the app/system roles) holds the latest `(latestHash, latestSeq, updatedAt)` so the writer never scans `audit_log` to find the head. SQL helper `audit_chain_lock_key(uuid)` derives a stable BIGINT advisory-lock key from the org UUID with a `0x6175646974636861` ('auditcha') salt to avoid collision with Prisma's migration lock; the function is `IMMUTABLE STRICT SECURITY INVOKER` and granted `EXECUTE` only to the two app roles. **`@pharmax/audit`** ships `writeAuditLogInTx(tx, input)` — the only supported audit insert path — which acquires `pg_advisory_xact_lock(audit_chain_lock_key(orgId))` as the FIRST statement, reads the chain head, computes `entryHash = SHA-256(canonical(prevHash, organizationId, seq, action, resourceType, resourceId, actorUserId, scope, metadata, occurredAt))`, inserts the audit row, and upserts the chain head — all inside the caller's tx so a rollback leaves the head untouched. Genesis insert path: head NULL → seq=1, prevHash=null; chained insert: seq=head.latestSeq+1, prevHash=head.latestHash. `@pharmax/command-bus` `createAuditLogInTx` delegates to the chain writer (handlers' audit shape is unchanged; the chain is invisible to command authors). **Canonical TLV encoder** is 1-byte field tag + 4-byte big-endian length + value bytes, with a NULL sentinel (`length=0xFFFFFFFF`) that distinguishes "field present but null" from "field present and empty"; field order is fixed and documented as version-controlled; JSON columns are canonicalized via sorted-key stringify matching `@pharmax/command-bus`'s hash encoder; bigint payloads inside scope/metadata are rejected at encode time (callers must string-encode); seq is fixed 8-byte big-endian uint64. `computeAuditEntryHash` is pure and exposed so the verifier and signing job re-derive hashes from persisted bytes — verifier byte-equivalence is the chain integrity guarantee. **`verifyChain(source, args)`** walks a tenant's chain in ascending seq order against an injected `ChainSource` (in-memory for tests, Prisma-backed in production) and fails fast on the first inconsistency with `InternalError(AUDIT_CHAIN_BROKEN)` carrying the offending seq and a reason tag (`entryHash mismatch`, `prevHash` mismatch, or `seq gap`); supports `startSeq`/`endSeq` bounds and a `startPrevHash` checkpoint for resumed walks. **47 contract tests across 3 files** — encoder determinism + per-field uniqueness (changing any of prevHash/orgId/seq/action/resourceType/resourceId/actorUserId/scope/metadata/occurredAt by even 1ms flips the hash) + TLV byte layout + seq encoding + JSON canonicalization + seq bounds (19), writer call ordering (lock → findUnique → audit.create → chainState.upsert) + advisory-lock parameter binding (orgId bound, not interpolated) + genesis vs chained paths + multi-insert chain continuity (13), verifier happy paths + tamper detection (mutating entryHash, action, scope, occurredAt by 1ms, or prevHash all trip AUDIT_CHAIN_BROKEN at the right seq) + seq gap detection + per-tenant isolation (verifying tenant A succeeds while tenant B's chain in the same source is broken) + resume-from-checkpoint with right/wrong startPrevHash (15). **Command-bus contract tests** additionally pin (a) the advisory lock fires AFTER the tenancy session GUC and BEFORE the audit_log create, (b) the lock-key derivation passes orgId as a bound parameter, (c) the genesis-insert audit row carries seq=1 + prevHash=null + a 32-byte entryHash, and (d) `audit_chain_state` is upserted in the same tx. **Daily Merkle-root signing job deferred** — when it lands it will read `audit_chain_state` rolling forward, build a per-day Merkle tree per tenant, sign with a KMS asymmetric key, and write the manifest to an S3 Object Lock bucket; see `ARCHITECTURE_PRINCIPLES.md` §B.3 + §C.4.
- [x] Patient, Provider, Prescription, Order, OrderLine schema with PHI envelope columns (`*Enc Json`) + blind-index columns (`*Bi String`, base64url HMAC-SHA-256, 43 chars) — single migration `20260523190000_phase2_patient_rx_order` that introduces seven new enums (`PatientStatus`, `ProviderStatus`, `PrescriptionStatus`, `OrderStatus` with the 11 workflow + 5 exception states, `OrderPriority`, `OrderLineStatus`, `IntakeSourceKind`), the five new tables, all indexes, FK relations, and in the same file promotes the three baseline placeholder columns to real FKs (`command_log.targetOrderId`, `order_event.orderId`, `invoice_line.orderId` — all `ON DELETE RESTRICT` so the audit trail can never lose its anchor). Every new tenant-scoped table comes under the RLS regime from `20260522060000_rls_baseline` (GRANT to `pharmax_app`/`pharmax_system`, `ENABLE` + `FORCE` row level security, single PERMISSIVE `tenant_isolation` policy on the `pharmax.system_context` / `pharmax.organization_id` GUC pair, applied via a DO block keyed on a `new_tables text[]` array) and is verified by `scripts/check-migration-rls.ts`. Patient identity is scoped to `(organizationId, clinicId)` by design — the same human at two clinics is two patient rows, because cross-clinic linkage is a deliberate audited admin action, not an implicit join. PHI columns required for identity (`firstNameEnc`, `lastNameEnc`, `dateOfBirthEnc`) are NOT NULL; demographic and contact PHI is nullable so intake can proceed against partial data. The DOB has two blind-index columns (`dobBi` for full-date exact match, `dobYearMonthBi` for fuzzy month-of-birth typo recovery) under distinct purposes so search keys can't cross-contaminate. Crypto-shred tombstone (`patient.cryptoShreddedAt`) is the column the right-to-be-forgotten flow writes when the DEKs are destroyed at the KMS; the row stays for FK integrity, the ciphertexts become unreadable. Provider rows are plaintext on purpose (NPI registry data is public; the PHI-sensitive piece is the patient↔provider association on the encrypted `prescription` row), and the model is organization-scoped (not clinic-scoped) so one prescriber covers multiple clinics in one org — clinically accurate. Prescription `sigEnc` is required encrypted PHI; drug identity (NDC, name, strength, form) is stored plain so inventory queries and clinical reports don't need decryption. Order keeps `currentStatus` + `currentBucketId` + `currentAssigneeUserId` denormalized for queue performance, an optimistic-lock `version` counter for CAS, `workflowPolicyId` + `workflowPolicyVersion` for replay-correctness, and `slaDeadlineAt` for the breach scanner. The queue-shaped order index is `(organizationId, currentBucketId, currentStatus, priority, slaDeadlineAt, receivedAt)` so the standard "next item in this bucket" scan is index-only; a second index `(organizationId, currentStatus, slaDeadlineAt)` powers the global breach scan. OrderLine carries `lotId` and `vialLabelId` as raw UUID placeholders ready for phase-4 promotion to real FKs. The `(table, column) → BI purpose` registry lives in `packages/database/src/phi/blind-index-purposes.ts` (`PATIENT_BLIND_INDEX_BINDINGS`, `PRESCRIPTION_BLIND_INDEX_BINDINGS`, `ALL_BLIND_INDEX_BINDINGS`), with seven contract tests asserting that every `*Bi` column has a registered purpose, no two purposes collide, every purpose matches `<table>.<column>` shape, the normalizer hint is one of `text`/`phone`/`raw`, and the DOB year-month purpose is distinct from the full-DOB purpose so search keys can't cross-contaminate. `@pharmax/database` exports the new row types (`Patient`, `Provider`, `Prescription`, `Order`, `OrderLine`) and the new enums alongside the existing surface, so downstream packages can `import { Patient } from "@pharmax/database"` without reaching into the generated path.
- [x] `@pharmax/workflow` policy v1 + state machine — pure, dependency-light engine that consumes an `OrderWorkflowPolicy` rather than reaching into `ORDER_STANDARD_V1` directly (the seam for future policy versions). `applyTransition(policy, currentState, command, params)` is a TOTAL function over `(state, command)` pairs returning `{ ok: true, ... } | { ok: false, code, reason }` — no exceptions, no I/O, no clock — so it's reusable from UI affordance checks, replayable from `command_log`, and unit-testable without a database. Transitions are one row per `(command, fromState)` pair (not `(fromState → set of allowed)`) so audit metadata can cite a stable `transitionId`; cross-cutting commands (`PLACE_HOLD`, `CANCEL`) are expanded into one transition row per source state with allow-list constants (`HOLD_FROM_STATES`, `CANCEL_FROM_STATES`) documenting the rule. Error codes (`WORKFLOW_INVALID_TRANSITION`, `WORKFLOW_PARAM_INVALID`, `WORKFLOW_PARAM_REQUIRED`, `WORKFLOW_STATE_TERMINAL`, `WORKFLOW_UNKNOWN_COMMAND`) are mapped to `PharmaxError` instances by the bus, not the engine — the engine doesn't import error classes. Determinism rule enforced: same input → same output bytes; no `Date`, no `Math.random`, no ULID. Tests cover the full transition table, terminal-state guards, and required-param paths (`RELEASE_HOLD` requires `releaseToState`, `REOPEN_FOR_CORRECTION` requires `reopenToState`).
- [x] **`@pharmax/patients` read-path primitives** — `redactPatient(row)` + `PATIENT_REDACTED_FIELD_NAMES` deny-list (pinned to the Prisma `Patient` dmmf via 4 contract tests so a schema change that adds a new `*Enc` / `*Bi` column fails the suite until the deny-list catches up); `PATIENT_BLIND_INDEX` namespace exposing one async helper per searchable field (`lastName` / `firstName` / `dateOfBirth` / `dateOfBirthYearMonth` / `phoneLast10` / `email` / `postalCode` / `mrn`) with domain-specific normalizers (`normalizeDobForBlindIndex` rejects non-`YYYY-MM-DD`, out-of-range years, impossible months/days; `normalizeDobYearMonthForBlindIndex` rejects non-`YYYY-MM`; phone re-uses `@pharmax/crypto`'s digit-only last-10 normalizer); `buildSearchWhere` translates a `PatientSearchQuery` into a Prisma `where` shape that exploits the existing `(organizationId, *Bi)` btree indexes (every condition is an equality on a blind-index column, AND-joined; returns `null` when every field normalizes to empty so the caller surfaces "at least one query field required" instead of running an unbounded scan); `searchPatients(prisma, options)` reads `requireCurrentContext()` for the tenant scope, clamps `limit` to `[1, 100]`, orders `createdAt DESC`, and returns full rows with envelopes intact (decryption is the caller's responsibility — the search layer never decrypts on behalf of a caller because two patients can share a name-BI hash and still differ on DOB; trusting the hash alone is a security bug, documented loudly at the call site); `PatientRepository` extends `ScopedRepository` with `findById` / `findByIdOrThrow` / `listByClinic` (status-filtered by default, `[1, 200]` page-size clamp) — the only ID-based read path. **39 contract tests across 3 files** — redact projection contains only allow-listed fields + no PHI-sentinel substrings + dmmf deny-list completeness (6); DOB shape normalization round-trips every valid form and rejects every malformed form (23); `buildSearchWhere` returns null on empty queries, builds AND-of-equalities on the right `*Bi` columns, skips fields that normalize to empty, applies `status = "ACTIVE"` by default with `includeNonActive` opt-out, applies the optional clinicId filter, and produces tenant-specific + cross-tenant-different + same-tenant-deterministic hashes (10).
- [~] Patient commands: **`RegisterPatient` shipped** (the first PHI-bearing command — reference for every future encryption + blind-index write). Lives in `@pharmax/patients` alongside the read-path primitives above. Runs through `executeCommand` (tenant-scoped, RBAC-gated on new `patients.create` permission) with a flat input schema where every PHI field is top-level so the bus's shallow redactor scrubs `firstName`, `lastName`, `dateOfBirth`, `middleName`, `sexAtBirth`, `ssnLast4`, `phone`, `email`, `addressLine1`/`addressLine2`/`city`/`state`/`postalCode`, and `mrn` from `command_log.requestPayload` (declarative `redactFields` list plus the bus's `ALWAYS_REDACT` defense-in-depth). DOB validation is two-stage: shape (`/^\d{4}-\d{2}-\d{2}$/`) then a calendar round-trip refinement that rejects normalization (e.g. `2026-02-30` → `2026-03-02`). Inside the bus tx (after the tenancy GUC fires): tenant-scoped clinic existence check → `randomUUID()` pre-issue → per-field `encryptField` with AAD `{tenantId, table: "patient", column, recordId}` so a ciphertext stolen from one row cannot be moved into another and decrypted → per-searchable-field `PATIENT_BLIND_INDEX` lookup (purposes from `@pharmax/database/phi`, normalizers selected by hint — text/phone/raw-with-caller-normalization, so a typo can't silently store a phone-shaped BI under the text normalizer) → `patient.create`. Audit emits `action: "patient.registered"` with **booleans-only** metadata (`hasMrn`, `hasPhone`, `hasEmail`, `hasAddress`, `hasSsnLast4`, `hasMiddleName`, `hasSexAtBirth`, plus `clinicId` + `commandLogId`); outbox emits `patient.registered.v1` carrying only ids + ISO timestamp. New RBAC permissions `patients.create` + `patients.read` added in lockstep across the typed registry, role templates (Pharmacy Technician = create+read, Pharmacist + Clinic Viewer = read), and `prisma/seed.ts` (21 codes seeded, mirror parity test updated). **19 contract tests** assert: required-only happy path leaves optional `*Enc`/`*Bi` columns null; all-fields happy path populates every column with envelope/BI shape; `command_log.requestPayload` censors every PHI field; audit metadata + outbox payload contain zero PHI substrings; decrypt round-trip recovers original plaintext through the configured `LocalKmsAdapter`; decrypting with the wrong `recordId` fails `AAD_MISMATCH`; identical plaintexts under the same tenant produce identical BIs; `firstNameBi` ≠ `lastNameBi` for the same word (cross-purpose isolation); full-DOB BI ≠ year-month BI (cross-key isolation); clinic-not-found path throws `ValidationError(PATIENT_CLINIC_NOT_FOUND)` with zero domain writes; Prisma `P2003` race maps to `ConflictError(PATIENT_CLINIC_RACE)`; missing `patients.create` permission throws `AuthorizationError(PERMISSION_DENIED)` with zero `command_log` row; Zod rejects bad clinic UUID, malformed DOB, calendar-impossible DOB, invalid email, extra fields (strict), and SSN with the wrong digit count.
- [~] Patient commands: **`CryptoShredPatient` shipped** (the right-to-be-forgotten command — reference for every future PHI shred). Lives in `@pharmax/patients` alongside `RegisterPatient`. Implemented as a manual `Command<I, O>` (not `defineCommand`) because the factory currently locks `order` rows only and this command targets `patient`. Input schema is `{ patientId: uuid, reason: CryptoShredReason }` validated against the `CRYPTO_SHRED_REASONS` literal union exported by `@pharmax/crypto` (`right-to-be-forgotten` / `data-retention-expiry` / `regulatory-order` / `tenant-offboarding` / `incident-response`); `redactFields: []` because the input itself is non-PHI (an id + an enum). Runs through `executeCommand` under new RBAC permission `patients.crypto_shred` (added in lockstep across `@pharmax/rbac` `PERMISSIONS` + `PERMISSION_METADATA` + the mirror-parity test, and `prisma/seed.ts` — 38 codes seeded). Inside the bus tx (after tenancy GUC fires): `patient.findUnique` (tenant + id; `NotFoundError(PATIENT_NOT_FOUND)` if missing) → double-shred guard (already-set `cryptoShreddedAt` → `ConflictError(PATIENT_ALREADY_SHREDDED)` with the original timestamp in metadata) → capture presence booleans for every PHI field (`hadMrn`, `hadSsnLast4`, `hadPhone`, `hadEmail`, `hadAddress`, `hadMiddleName`, `hadSexAtBirth`) for the audit metadata BEFORE we destroy the columns → call `planCryptoShred` once per `*Enc` column and once per `*Bi` column purely for `CRYPTO_SHRED_REASON` validation + audit list construction (the plan itself carries `nextValue: null` and performs no I/O) → single atomic `patient.updateMany({ where: { id, organizationId, cryptoShreddedAt: null } })` that nullifies all 14 `*Enc` columns (writing the `Prisma.DbNull` sentinel — plain TS `null` is a type error against Prisma's `NullableJsonNullValueInput | InputJsonValue` union because that union explicitly distinguishes SQL NULL from a JSON literal `null` payload, and we want SQL NULL so the envelope object is _gone_, not preserved as `null`) + all 8 `*Bi` columns (plain TS `null`, since these are `String?` columns), stamps `cryptoShreddedAt: now`, and flips `status: INACTIVE`. The CAS predicate on `cryptoShreddedAt: null` is the race guard: two concurrent shreds against the same row return `count: 0` for the loser, which maps to `ConflictError(PATIENT_SHRED_RACE_LOST)`. Audit emits `action: "patient.crypto_shredded"` with PHI-free metadata `{commandLogId, reason, had*: boolean × 7, shreddedEncColumns: string[], shreddedBiColumns: string[]}`; outbox emits `patient.crypto_shredded.v1` carrying only `{patientId, organizationId, reason, occurredAt}`. **16 contract tests** assert: happy path nullifies every `*Enc` column with `Prisma.DbNull` and every `*Bi` column with TS `null`, stamps `cryptoShreddedAt`, sets `status: INACTIVE`; audit metadata records reason + presence booleans + sorted shred column lists + no PHI / ciphertext / blind-index substrings anywhere in the chain-encoded audit row (BigInt-safe substring check); `command_log.requestPayload` preserves the verbatim non-PHI input (id + reason); outbox payload is exactly `{patientId, organizationId, reason, occurredAt}` with no clinic id or sibling fields; missing patient → `PATIENT_NOT_FOUND` with no domain writes; already-shredded patient → `PATIENT_ALREADY_SHREDDED` with the original `cryptoShreddedAt` in error metadata; concurrent shred (the `updateMany` CAS returning `count: 0`) → `PATIENT_SHRED_RACE_LOST`; missing `patients.crypto_shred` permission → `AuthorizationError(PERMISSION_DENIED)` with zero `command_log` row; Zod rejects malformed `patientId`, unknown shred `reason`, and extra fields (strict schema); every value in `CRYPTO_SHRED_REASONS` is accepted by the schema (iterative parametric test so a new reason added to `@pharmax/crypto` automatically gates here). Schema relaxation migration `20260603000000_phase2_patient_phi_columns_nullable_for_shred/migration.sql` drops `NOT NULL` from the seven `Patient` columns that `RegisterPatient` requires (`firstNameEnc`, `lastNameEnc`, `dateOfBirthEnc`, `firstNameBi`, `lastNameBi`, `dobBi`, `dobYearMonthBi`) — they remain required at the `RegisterPatient` Zod boundary but are nullable at the DB layer so the shred command can leave the row in an "ID + tombstone + status" terminal state. **120 test files / 1427 tests passing.**
- [~] Patient commands: **`UpdatePatient` shipped** — second PHI-bearing patient command. Tri-state input (`undefined` / `null` / value), selective re-encryption (only named columns re-encrypted), blind-index coupling (every `*Enc` move drags `*Bi` partner in the same UPDATE; DOB refreshes both `dobBi` and `dobYearMonthBi`), locked-out guards (`PATIENT_SHREDDED` for crypto-shredded rows, `PATIENT_MERGED_AWAY` for merged rows, `PATIENT_NOT_FOUND` for missing rows), CAS predicate re-checks `cryptoShreddedAt: null` AND `status: { not: MERGED }` so concurrent shred/merge between read and write surfaces as `PATIENT_UPDATE_RACE_LOST`. Identity fields (firstName, lastName, dateOfBirth) cannot be cleared (`null` rejected at Zod boundary + defense-in-depth handler check raising `PATIENT_UPDATE_IDENTITY_CANNOT_CLEAR`). Empty change set raises `PATIENT_UPDATE_NO_CHANGES` before any DB read. Audit metadata + outbox payload are PHI-free by construction: structural change-set lists (`updatedFields[]`, `clearedFields[]` sorted) + `clinicId` + `commandLogId`, never values. RBAC: new `patients.update` permission added to PharmacyTechnician role template (alongside `patients.create` + `patients.read`).
- [ ] Patient commands (remaining): `MergePatients`
- [~] Provider commands: **`RegisterProvider` shipped** in new `@pharmax/providers` package (the prescriber-roster counterpart to `@pharmax/patients`). Plaintext domain by design — NPI is a public CMS registry identifier, and practice contact info (office address, phone, email) is the prescriber's office, not patient data — so no encryption / no blind indexes. The one credential we treat as confidential is `deaNumber`: not technically PHI, but a controlled-substance prescribing credential whose leak into `command_log` would make a forensic dump of that log a tool for prescription fraud. The handler therefore (a) lists `deaNumber` in the bus's `redactFields` so it's censored from `command_log.requestPayload`, (b) expresses it as a `hasDea: boolean` in audit metadata, and (c) keeps it out of the outbox payload entirely. NPI is intentionally PRESERVED in audit metadata and the `provider.registered.v1` outbox payload — the whole point of the action is registering against the NPI registry; consumers (and SOC 2 reviewers) need the NPI for the event to be useful. Schema uniqueness is `@@unique([organizationId, npi])` (same prescriber can appear in two different tenants but only once per tenant); Prisma `P2002` on that constraint is mapped to a typed `ConflictError(PROVIDER_NPI_TAKEN)` the API layer will surface as 409. New RBAC permissions `providers.create` + `providers.read` added in lockstep across the typed `PERMISSIONS` registry, role templates (PharmacyTechnician = create+read, Pharmacist + ClinicViewer = read), and `prisma/seed.ts` (23 codes seeded). **15 contract tests** assert: required-only happy path leaves all optional columns omitted; all-fields happy path round-trips every column; `command_log.requestPayload` censors `deaNumber` while preserving NPI / names / credential / email; audit metadata carries `{npi, hasDea, hasCredential, hasContact, hasAddress, commandLogId}` with no DEA plaintext anywhere in the audit row JSON (BigInt-safe substring check covers the chain writer's `seq` column); outbox payload is `{providerId, organizationId, npi, occurredAt}` with no DEA / no names; Prisma `P2002` maps to `ConflictError(PROVIDER_NPI_TAKEN)` and writes no audit/outbox; RBAC denial leaves zero `command_log` row; Zod rejects 8 invalid input shapes (NPI not 10 digits, NPI non-digit, lowercase DEA, wrong-length DEA, malformed email, non-2-letter state, non-ZIP postal code, extra fields under strict schema). Deferred to future hardening: NPI registry snapshot lookup (auto-fill name/credential from CMS data, fail fast on typos) and DEA checksum validation (the last digit of a DEA number is a checksum; we accept shape only for now so a shape-valid-but-checksum-bad DEA doesn't block intake).
- [~] Provider commands (continued): **`UpdateProvider` shipped** in `@pharmax/providers` — the plaintext counterpart to `UpdatePatient`. Same tri-state input (`undefined` skips, `null` clears optional columns, value sets), same change-set audit shape (`updatedFields[]` + `clearedFields[]` sorted), same predicate-CAS pattern, simplified by the plaintext domain (no encryption, no blind-index coupling). **NPI is immutable**: the schema omits `npi` from the input and the strict Zod boundary surfaces submission as `COMMAND_INPUT_INVALID` — fixing a typo'd NPI is a `DeactivateProvider` + new `RegisterProvider` motion, not an edit (preserves the link between historical prescriptions and the row written under that NPI). **`status` is not editable here**: activation/deactivation is `DeactivateProvider`'s job (different operator intent, different audit shape, different downstream effects on existing prescriptions). **Locked-out guard**: `status === INACTIVE` rejects with typed `PROVIDER_INACTIVE` — the remediation is `ReactivateProvider` (future), not a back-door edit of the deactivated row. **Identity nulls refused**: Zod's schema doesn't allow `null` on `firstName`/`lastName`, and a defense-in-depth handler check throws `PROVIDER_UPDATE_IDENTITY_CANNOT_CLEAR` if a future schema change weakens that. **No-op rejection**: empty change set raises `PROVIDER_UPDATE_NO_CHANGES` BEFORE any DB read — a no-op edit shouldn't burn an audit row. **CAS predicate**: `updateMany` re-checks `status: ACTIVE`; a concurrent `DeactivateProvider` between read and write returns `count: 0` → typed `PROVIDER_UPDATE_RACE_LOST` (mirrors `PATIENT_UPDATE_RACE_LOST`). **PHI rule**: `deaNumber` plaintext is redacted from `command_log.requestPayload` (same as RegisterProvider) and NEVER appears in audit metadata or the outbox payload; presence is expressed as `hasDea: boolean` reflecting POST-UPDATE state (set→true, clear→false, untouched→preserves pre-read value — useful for compliance reports without exposing the credential string). NPI stays IN audit metadata + outbox payload as the action's anchor (public identifier; needed for the event to be meaningful). New RBAC permission `providers.update` added in lockstep across the typed `PERMISSIONS` registry, `PERMISSION_METADATA`, `prisma/seed.ts` (48 codes seeded; mirror-parity count bumped 47→48), and granted to `PharmacyTechnician` (mirrors `PATIENTS_UPDATE`); `OrgAdmin` carries it via `ALL_PERMS`. New `provider.updated.v1` event in the outbox; no `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION` wiring because provider events are not order events. **24 contract tests** across `update-provider.test.ts` assert: single-field happy path (only the named column lands in `data`; CAS predicate is `{id, organizationId, status: ACTIVE}`); mixed update+clear happy path (set values + SQL `null` for cleared optionals; untouched keys are absent from `data`); `hasDea` post-update semantics — clear flips to false, set flips to true, untouched preserves pre-read value (3 separate tests); `command_log.requestPayload` censors `deaNumber` only (other fields and `providerId` survive verbatim; DEA plaintext appears NOWHERE in the serialized command_log row); audit metadata carries `{npi, updatedFields (sorted), clearedFields (sorted), hasDea, commandLogId}` with no DEA plaintext anywhere in the audit row JSON (BigInt-aware substring check); outbox payload is exactly `{providerId, organizationId, npi, updatedFields, clearedFields, occurredAt}` with no DEA/PII substrings; PROVIDER_NOT_FOUND short-circuits with zero `updateMany`/audit/outbox writes; PROVIDER_INACTIVE refuses INACTIVE rows with zero downstream writes; PROVIDER_UPDATE_RACE_LOST (count=0 from `updateMany`) writes no audit/outbox; PROVIDER_UPDATE_NO_CHANGES short-circuits BEFORE the `findUnique` read (no DB roundtrip on a no-op); RBAC: missing `providers.update` → `PERMISSION_DENIED` with zero `command_log` row; Zod rejects 11 invalid input shapes (`npi` submitted (immutable), `status` submitted (separate command), extra fields under strict schema, DEA wrong shape, DEA wrong length, malformed email, non-2-letter state, non-ZIP postal code, `firstName: null`, `lastName: null`, non-UUID `providerId`).
- [~] Provider commands (continued): **`DeactivateProvider` shipped** in `@pharmax/providers` — the `ACTIVE → INACTIVE` transition. Deliberately a SEPARATE command from `UpdateProvider`, not a `status` key on it: a deactivation has a different operator intent, a different audit shape (it carries a REASON, not a column diff), a different permission grant (`providers.deactivate`), and a different downstream subscription surface — workers subscribed to `provider.deactivated.v1` can branch on `payload.reason` to decide whether to halt in-flight controlled-substance fills (yes for `DEA_SURRENDERED_OR_REVOKED` and `SANCTIONED`, no for `RETIRED`/`RELOCATED`/etc.). Splitting it out also makes the audit-log filter trivial ("show every deactivation last quarter, grouped by reason") and prevents a name/address edit from accidentally riding along with a status flip. **Pure status flip, no new table**: a structured `provider_deactivation` table would be carrying its weight only for analytics, and we get those reports cleanly from `audit_log.action = 'provider.deactivated'` filtered by `metadata.reason` — the Provider domain has nothing close to the per-order rework loop or re-deactivation frequency that justified `order_cancellation` / `order_hold`. If/when `ReactivateProvider` lands and re-deactivation history becomes a real reporting need, we migrate to a structured table then. **Reason is a closed TS literal union, NOT a Prisma enum**: 9 codes (`RETIRED`, `RELOCATED`, `RELATIONSHIP_ENDED`, `LICENSE_EXPIRED`, `DEA_SURRENDERED_OR_REVOKED`, `SANCTIONED`, `DECEASED`, `DUPLICATE_RECORD`, `OTHER`). We're not writing the code to a DB column, so a Postgres enum would be type-system overhead without payoff; the Zod-validated literal union at the input boundary + the audit/outbox carrying a verbatim string is sufficient for the structural signal. `OTHER` is the escape hatch and REQUIRES a non-empty `reasonText` (Zod refinement) so we never accidentally swallow an "other" with no explanation. **`reasonText` is redacted from `command_log.requestPayload`** via the bus's `redactFields` (same pattern as `cancellationReasonText`, `holdReasonText`, `pv1RejectionReasonText`); audit metadata and outbox payload carry a `hasReasonText: boolean` marker instead, so consumers know whether to surface "view rationale" in a UI without ever shipping the bytes. The reason CODE is safe and travels everywhere as a structured signal. **`hadDea: boolean` snapshot** is captured pre-deactivation (nullity of the row's `deaNumber` column at the moment of the flip) and lives in audit metadata + outbox payload for compliance reports ("how many providers we deactivated had a DEA on file?") — never the plaintext credential. **Locked-out guard**: `status === INACTIVE` rejects with typed `PROVIDER_ALREADY_INACTIVE` — silently succeeding on an already-deactivated provider would hide the fact that something else deactivated it first, which matters for the "did our deactivation actually fire?" question. **CAS predicate**: `updateMany` re-checks `status: ACTIVE`; a concurrent winning `DeactivateProvider` between our read and our write returns `count: 0` → typed `PROVIDER_DEACTIVATE_RACE_LOST` (the loser of the race gets a typed conflict, not a duplicate outbox event). **Only the `status` column is written** — no incidental edits ride along, asserted in tests. New RBAC permission `providers.deactivate` added in lockstep across the typed `PERMISSIONS` registry, `PERMISSION_METADATA`, `prisma/seed.ts` (50 codes seeded; mirror-parity count bumped 49→50; file header comment updated from "46 codes" to "50 codes"), and granted to `PharmacyTechnician` (same role that holds `PROVIDERS_CREATE`/`PROVIDERS_UPDATE` — provider-directory management is a tech-level operation; for severe cases — DEA suspension, sanctions — the operator chooses the severity-flagged reason code that downstream workers branch on). `OrgAdmin` carries it via `ALL_PERMS`. `PROVIDERS_UPDATE` alone is NOT sufficient (asserted in tests) — a separate grant prevents an "update operator" from inadvertently deactivating providers. New `provider.deactivated.v1` event in the outbox; no `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION` wiring because provider events are not order events. **~26 contract tests** across `deactivate-provider.test.ts` assert: happy-path flip with the exact CAS predicate (`{id, organizationId, status: ACTIVE}`) and exact data payload (`{status: INACTIVE}` only — no incidental column writes); reason-enum coverage (every non-OTHER code is accepted at Zod and surfaces in audit metadata + outbox payload verbatim, parameterized over the 8 non-OTHER codes); `OTHER` accepted with `reasonText`, rejected without (Zod `.refine`), rejected with empty-string `reasonText`; `command_log.requestPayload` censors `reasonText` to "[Redacted]" while `reason` code survives (BigInt-safe substring check confirms no sensitive narrative appears anywhere in the serialized command_log row); `reasonText` omitted entirely from command_log payload when not provided; audit metadata carries `{npi, reason, hasReasonText, hadDea, commandLogId}` with NO `reasonText` key present and no `reasonText` substring anywhere in the audit row JSON; outbox payload is exactly `{providerId, organizationId, npi, reason, hasReasonText, hadDea, occurredAt}` with no DEA / no reason text substrings; `hadDea` reflects pre-deactivation row nullity (true when DEA was on file, false when null); `hasReasonText` correctly false when omitted; `PROVIDER_NOT_FOUND` short-circuits with zero `updateMany`/audit/outbox writes; `PROVIDER_ALREADY_INACTIVE` refuses already-deactivated rows with zero downstream writes; `PROVIDER_DEACTIVATE_RACE_LOST` (count=0 from `updateMany`) writes no audit/outbox; RBAC: missing `providers.deactivate` → `PERMISSION_DENIED` with zero `command_log` row; `providers.update` alone is NOT sufficient (separate grant required); Zod rejects 5 invalid input shapes (non-UUID providerId, unknown reason code, extra fields under strict schema, `status` key submitted (caller cannot pick the target status), `reasonText` over 2000 chars).
- [~] Provider commands (continued): **`ReactivateProvider` shipped** in `@pharmax/providers` — the `INACTIVE → ACTIVE` mirror of `DeactivateProvider`. Same structural pattern (closed-enum reason; redacted `reasonText` on `command_log`; `hasReasonText` + `hadDea` boolean snapshots on audit metadata + outbox payload; locked-out guard; CAS predicate; pure status flip with no new table) inverted across two axes: status is flipped `INACTIVE → ACTIVE` rather than `ACTIVE → INACTIVE`, and the reason vocabulary is **deliberately distinct** rather than a syntactic inverse of `PROVIDER_DEACTIVATION_REASONS`. **Reason vocabulary** is 8 codes — `LICENSE_RESTORED`, `DEA_RESTORED`, `SANCTION_LIFTED`, `RELATIONSHIP_RESUMED`, `RETURNED_FROM_RETIREMENT`, `RELOCATED_BACK_INTO_AREA`, `ERRONEOUS_DEACTIVATION`, `OTHER` — and intentionally has neither parity nor symmetry with the deactivation set. Terminal deactivation codes (`DECEASED`, `DUPLICATE_RECORD`) have **no reactivation counterpart** by design — you cannot bring a deceased provider back, you cannot un-merge a duplicate. `ERRONEOUS_DEACTIVATION` exists **only on this side** as the audit-correction path for "we deactivated the wrong row" or "we filed the deactivation against the wrong reason code"; there is no deactivation analog (correcting a missed deactivation is a fresh `DeactivateProvider` call, not an audit fix). The `LICENSE_RESTORED` / `DEA_RESTORED` / `SANCTION_LIFTED` codes are STRUCTURAL counterparts of `LICENSE_EXPIRED` / `DEA_SURRENDERED_OR_REVOKED` / `SANCTIONED` — but they are independently named so a future "resume in-flight CS fills" worker can subscribe directly on `payload.reason === "DEA_RESTORED"` rather than negate "is this a deactivation reason inverse?". Each command therefore owns a CLOSED Zod enum that captures only the codes meaningful for that direction, and a contract test pins that distinction (rejects every deactivation-only code at the Zod boundary as `COMMAND_INPUT_INVALID`). **Two separable RBAC grants by design** — `providers.reactivate` is a distinct permission from `providers.deactivate`. An organization may want to allow a tech to take a provider OUT of service while requiring a higher-trust role to bring them BACK in (the high-trust direction is more dangerous: a wrongful reactivation can re-route prescriptions to a sanctioned prescriber). The mirror-parity test pins both `providers.deactivate` alone and `providers.update` alone are insufficient to call this command. New RBAC permission added in lockstep across the typed `PERMISSIONS` registry, `PERMISSION_METADATA`, `prisma/seed.ts` (52 codes seeded; mirror-parity count bumped 51→52), and granted by default to `PharmacyTechnician` alongside `providers.deactivate` (operational role; orgs that want stricter separation override the role at the per-org template-clone time); `OrgAdmin` carries it via `ALL_PERMS`. New `provider.reactivated.v1` event registered in `@pharmax/events` (own file + per-domain barrel + top-level type re-export + `ALL_DEFINITIONS` registry entry) with payload `{providerId, organizationId, npi, reason, hasReasonText, hadDea, occurredAt}`; the reason enum is duplicated as a Zod tuple in the event file rather than imported from `@pharmax/providers` to keep `@pharmax/events` dependency-free (the registry must NOT depend on producer packages or we get a cycle). The parity-guard repo scan automatically picks up the new `provider.reactivated.v1` literal everywhere it appears. **30 contract tests** across `reactivate-provider.test.ts` mirror the deactivation suite with reactivation-specific pins: happy-path flip with the exact CAS predicate (`{id, organizationId, status: INACTIVE}`) and exact data payload (`{status: ACTIVE}` only — no incidental column writes); reason-enum coverage parametric over the 7 non-OTHER reactivation codes; `OTHER` accepted with `reasonText`, rejected without (Zod `.refine`), rejected with empty-string `reasonText`; **typed-distinct vocabulary test** — the 8 deactivation-only codes (`RETIRED`, `RELOCATED`, `RELATIONSHIP_ENDED`, `LICENSE_EXPIRED`, `DEA_SURRENDERED_OR_REVOKED`, `SANCTIONED`, `DECEASED`, `DUPLICATE_RECORD`) are all rejected at the Zod boundary; `command_log.requestPayload` censors `reasonText` to "[Redacted]" while `reason` code survives (BigInt-safe substring check confirms no sensitive narrative appears anywhere in the serialized command_log row); `reasonText` omitted entirely from command_log payload when not provided; audit metadata carries `{npi, reason, hasReasonText, hadDea, commandLogId}` with NO `reasonText` key present and no `reasonText` substring anywhere in the audit row JSON; outbox payload is exactly `{providerId, organizationId, npi, reason, hasReasonText, hadDea, occurredAt}` with no DEA / no reason text substrings; `hadDea` reflects pre-reactivation row nullity (true when DEA was on file, false when null); `hasReasonText` correctly false when omitted; `PROVIDER_NOT_FOUND` short-circuits with zero `updateMany`/audit/outbox writes; `PROVIDER_ALREADY_ACTIVE` refuses already-active rows with zero downstream writes; `PROVIDER_REACTIVATE_RACE_LOST` (count=0 from `updateMany`) writes no audit/outbox; RBAC: missing `providers.reactivate` → `PERMISSION_DENIED` with zero `command_log` row; `providers.deactivate` alone is NOT sufficient (separate grant); `providers.update` alone is NOT sufficient (separate grant); Zod rejects 5 invalid input shapes (non-UUID providerId, unknown reason code, extra fields under strict schema, `status` key submitted (caller cannot pick the target status), `reasonText` over 2000 chars). Stale `(future)` / `(when shipped)` references in `UpdateProvider` and `DeactivateProvider` comments updated in lockstep; the `ReactivateProvider` exit message in `PROVIDER_ALREADY_INACTIVE` is now actionable rather than aspirational.
- [~] Provider commands (continued): **`SyncFromNpiRegistry` — slice 1 of N shipped** in new `packages/providers/src/npi-sync/` — the pure DIFF ENGINE for the NPI Registry reconciliation worker. The full feature (CMS NPPES HTTP client, sync-run/sync-check/reactivation-candidate schema, the worker itself, cron scheduling, operator review UI) is planned across ~6 slices; this slice lands the foundation that every subsequent slice consumes — the discriminated `SyncAction` vocabulary, the narrow `LocalProviderSnapshot` and `CmsNpiSnapshot` input shapes, and the pure `diffProviderAgainstCms(local, cms)` function that decides what the worker should do for one (local row, CMS snapshot) pair. **Why slice 1 is the pure function**: defines vocabulary the HTTP client (slice 2), schema (slice 3), and worker (slice 4) all consume; has zero IO so it's exhaustively unit-testable; reversible — if the vocabulary is wrong, edit one file rather than rip out infrastructure. **Six discriminated `SyncAction` kinds** with deliberate precedence ordering (`NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS` > `ENUMERATION_TYPE_MISMATCH` > `DEACTIVATE` > `REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE` > `UPDATE` > `NONE` — biggest data-integrity concern first; status transitions trump field drift because there's no point updating an inactive provider's address): (1) `NONE` with `reason: "no_diff" | "both_inactive"` (worker may still record a "checked" entry in `provider_sync_check` for auditability but dispatches no command); (2) `DEACTIVATE` (CMS marked NPI inactive; local row still active); (3) `UPDATE` (both active; field drift); (4) `REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE` (CMS active, local inactive — emits a human-review candidate, never auto-reactivates); (5) `NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS` (NPI in our roster but absent from CMS — almost always operator entry error, surface for review); (6) `ENUMERATION_TYPE_MISMATCH` (CMS returned NPI-2 organization for what we registered as an NPI-1 prescriber — operator entry error, surface for review). **Never auto-reactivates** — the rationale is doc'd verbatim in the file header and pinned by a test: a deactivation reason like `DECEASED` (CMS rarely deactivates immediately on death; "CMS active again" is almost certainly operator error), `DUPLICATE_RECORD` (auto-reactivation re-creates the duplicate), `SANCTIONED` (CMS NPI active doesn't mean the state-board disciplinary action was lifted — different registries), or `ERRONEOUS_DEACTIVATION` (the audit log already records the acknowledged error but the operator should still confirm via `ReactivateProvider` so the human decision is on the chain) all require human judgment + the original deactivation reason from audit_log to be safe. Worker always hands off to an operator. **Default deactivation reason is `LICENSE_EXPIRED`, NOT `DEA_SURRENDERED_OR_REVOKED`** — NPPES "D" doesn't say WHY an NPI is inactive; `LICENSE_EXPIRED` is the broadest match (covers revocation, expiration, voluntary surrender). DEA is a separate federal registry and we NEVER infer DEA status from NPI status; a contract test pins `reason !== "DEA_SURRENDERED_OR_REVOKED"` to prevent a future change from silently flipping the default. **Compile-time pin** via `satisfies (typeof PROVIDER_DEACTIVATION_REASONS)[number]`: if a future refactor removes `LICENSE_EXPIRED` from the deactivation vocabulary, this file breaks at compile time. **Does NOT auto-deactivate on `NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS`** — an NPI in our roster that CMS has no record of is almost always our operator entry error, not a CMS removal; auto-deactivating would burn the audit log on our own bad data. Surface for human review. **Does NOT clear a local address when CMS reports `practiceAddress: null`** — CMS occasionally scrubs address rows for reasons unrelated to whether the practice still exists; the "practice-still-exists" assumption is more useful than trusting CMS to be authoritative on an absence. Pinned by a test. **Normalization is intentionally simple for slice 1**: `trim()` for whitespace, uppercase-normalize for state codes, strict equality after that. No ZIP+4 stripping, no phone-format normalization, no Unicode folding. If false-positive UPDATEs show up in production, we tighten in a later slice; erring on "noise an operator filters" beats "silent drift the audit log can't explain". **Address tri-state semantics** for nullable fields (`addressLine2`, `phone`): CMS null + local value → `UPDATE` clearing; CMS value + local null → `UPDATE` setting; both null → no-op; both same → no-op (each tri-state pinned by a dedicated test). **`buildSyncDeactivationReasonText(cmsStatus, cmsLastUpdatedAt)` exported** so the worker (slice 4) reuses the exact same stable format (`"NPPES status: D (CMS updated 2026-05-15T12:34:56.000Z)"`) and contract tests can pin the format without re-deriving it. The string IS PHI-bearing-adjacent (CMS update timestamp, status code) and is REDACTED from `command_log.requestPayload` by `DeactivateProvider`'s `redactFields: ["reasonText"]`; it survives only in the redacted slot + the operator UI's "view rationale" affordance. **45 contract tests across `diff-engine.test.ts`** cover every branch and the precedence ordering: `NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS` (cms null) + precedence over local INACTIVE; `ENUMERATION_TYPE_MISMATCH` + precedence over CMS D status + precedence over local INACTIVE; `DEACTIVATE` happy path + stable `reasonText` format + ISO timestamp + precedence over field drift + the conservative-default `LICENSE_EXPIRED` (and explicit pin that it is NOT `DEA_SURRENDERED_OR_REVOKED`); `REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE` happy path + shape pin (zero auto-reactivation keys: `Object.keys(action)` is exactly `["kind"]`) + precedence over field drift; `NONE` for both-active-no-diff and both-inactive (+ pin that both-inactive does not diff fields even when they differ — the short-circuit semantics matter so a future maintainer doesn't "helpfully" add field comparison there); `UPDATE` for each individual field (firstName / lastName / credential / addressLine1 / city / postalCode / state) + composite (multiple fields merged into a single action) + the nullable-tri-state suite for `addressLine2` and `phone` (CMS null clears + CMS value sets + both null no-op) + the normalization suite (whitespace-trimmed names + whitespace-trimmed addresses + case-insensitive state code with the uppercase-output variant + whitespace-only CMS name treated as null + whitespace-only credential normalized to null + ignore CMS `practiceAddress: null` preserves local); precedence ordering pinned exhaustively (NOT_FOUND > REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE, ENUMERATION > DEACTIVATE, DEACTIVATE > UPDATE, REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE > UPDATE); discriminated-union narrowing test that pins each `kind`'s runtime key set to the expected shape (no spurious or missing keys); `buildSyncDeactivationReasonText` format pin + UTC ISO-stringify regardless of input timezone. Remaining slices: (3) new tables `provider_sync_run` (one row per worker run, per-org, with metrics) + `provider_sync_check` (one row per (run, provider), partitioned by month for retention) + `provider_reactivation_candidate` (operator review queue), all with RLS; (4) the worker itself — per-org runs, batched NPI fetches, dispatches `DeactivateProvider` / `UpdateProvider` via the command bus per diff action, persists candidates and not-found / mismatch rows for human review; (5) cron scheduling layer; (6) operator UI for the reactivation-candidate + not-found-at-CMS + enumeration-mismatch review queues.
- [~] Provider commands (continued): **`SyncFromNpiRegistry` — slice 2 of N shipped** in `packages/providers/src/npi-sync/cms-client.ts` — the **CMS NPPES HTTP client** that the worker (slice 4) will feed into the slice-1 diff engine. Wraps the public NPPES v2.1 registry API (`https://npiregistry.cms.hhs.gov/api/?number=<NPI>&version=2.1`) with rate limiting, retries, parsing, and per-NPI error capture. **Why slice 2 is the HTTP transport**: slice 1 defined the input shape (`CmsNpiSnapshot`); slice 2 produces it from real bytes. Slice 3 (sync_run/sync_check schema) and slice 4 (worker) both compose against the two-piece surface — no more pure-function slices left in the pipeline; from here the slices are persistence-bearing. **Two-method public surface** with deliberately different ergonomic profiles: (a) `fetchByNpi(npi): Promise<CmsNpiSnapshot | null>` — throws `PharmaxError` subclasses on transport / parse failure, returns the snapshot on hit, returns `null` when CMS confirms "not found" (200 response with `result_count: 0` — which slice 1's diff engine maps to `NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS`); idiomatic throw semantics for ops tools and "force resync this provider" admin paths. (b) `fetchManyByNpi(npis): Promise<Map<string, CmsFetchResult>>` where `CmsFetchResult = {ok: true; snapshot: CmsNpiSnapshot | null} | {ok: false; error: PharmaxError}` — never throws for per-NPI transport errors, surfaces them as tagged failures so the worker (slice 4) handles partial-batch failures cleanly (one NPI's CMS timeout doesn't poison the whole batch; failed NPIs get persisted to `provider_sync_check` with the error and retried next run). **Required `userAgent` at construction** — CMS recommends API consumers identify themselves (`"pharmax-pharmacy-os/1.0 (contact: ops@…)"`); empty string throws `CMS_NPI_REGISTRY_BAD_CONFIG` at construction so the misconfiguration is caught at boot, not at first request. **Polite rate limiter** via chained-promise gate (default `minRequestSpacingMs=125` → 8 req/s, well under CMS' anecdotal ~10/s ceiling): each call awaits the previous caller's "release" before claiming its own slot; release fires after `minRequestSpacingMs` via the injected `sleep`. Setting `minRequestSpacingMs=0` degrades to a no-op (used by tests to keep them fast). Concurrency / token-bucket are intentionally NOT implemented at this layer — slice 4's worker batches NPIs into chunks of N and serializes the chunks, which combined with this gate gives a predictable load profile; if a future slice needs higher throughput, the right shape is a token-bucket + bounded-concurrency pool, not retrofitted onto this gate. **Retry policy** with full-jitter exponential backoff (default `retryBaseMs=250`, `retryMaxMs=5000`, `maxRetries=3`): retryable failures are 429 / 5xx / network / timeout; non-retryable failures are 4xx (client error, not retry-fixable) and parse errors (`MALFORMED_RESPONSE` / `SCHEMA_MISMATCH` / `NPI_MISMATCH`). **`Retry-After` header honored** on 429 — parsed as delta-seconds (RFC 7231 common form); HTTP-date form unsupported (would need a `now()` source we don't carry). Invalid Retry-After values fall back to exponential backoff. **`AbortController` request timeout** (default 10s) translates to `CMS_NPI_REGISTRY_TIMEOUT` (retryable) — `AbortError` detection happens by `name === "AbortError"` so it survives the abort-signal-name normalization in the fetch shim. **Error vocabulary** with 9 discriminant codes exposed via `CMS_NPI_REGISTRY_ERRORS` (constant object so tests can switch on them without re-stringifying): `BAD_REQUEST` (4xx — likely malformed NPI from a programmer error); `RATE_LIMITED` (429 after retries exhausted); `SERVER_ERROR` (5xx after retries exhausted); `NETWORK_ERROR` (generic fetch failure after retries — DNS / ECONNRESET / etc); `TIMEOUT` (AbortController-fired after retries); `MALFORMED_RESPONSE` (200 with non-JSON body); `SCHEMA_MISMATCH` (200, JSON, but required fields absent or unrecognizable — surface CMS API version drift early); `NPI_MISMATCH` (200, JSON, result has `number !== queriedNpi` — defensive against a CMS API bug or response mix-up); `UNEXPECTED_STATUS` (3xx or other unhandled non-2xx). All map to `InternalError` (page-worthy from the client's perspective; slice 4's worker decides per-error whether to alert). **NPPES parser quirks handled explicitly**: (1) **empty strings → null** — NPPES sends `""` instead of `null` for missing first_name / last_name / credential / address line2 / phone (and the diff engine treats `""` and `null` as distinct values, so trim-empty normalization in the client is required to avoid spurious `UPDATE` actions when local has `null`); (2) **9-digit ZIP → hyphenated** — NPPES sends `"627010001"` unformatted, we store `"62701-0001"`; the parser formats 9-digit strings as `XXXXX-XXXX` and passes 5-digit ZIPs through unchanged; (3) **`basic.status` is sometimes absent** on legacy NPPES records — anything that isn't explicitly `"D"` is treated as `"A"` (active) to match the CMS docs' historical-record handling; (4) **`basic.last_updated` is `"YYYY-MM-DD"`** (date only, no time) — parsed as midnight UTC; falls back to `new Date()` for full ISO timestamps; throws `SCHEMA_MISMATCH` if neither form works; (5) **LOCATION address preferred over MAILING** — LOCATION is the practice address (what we care about for diff); MAILING is correspondence (P.O. boxes); the parser picks LOCATION when present, falls back to MAILING if no LOCATION exists, falls back to `null` if neither is present (rare — but slice 1's diff engine handles `practiceAddress: null` by preserving local rather than emitting a spurious clear); (6) **incomplete LOCATION addresses → null** — if the chosen address is missing line1 / city / state / postal_code, we return `null` rather than a partially-populated `CmsAddress` (a half-populated address comparing dirty against local would emit noise without giving the operator anything actionable). **Defensive NPI mismatch check** — if CMS returns a result whose `number` field doesn't match the queried NPI (which should NEVER happen for a single-NPI query — NPIs are globally unique), the parser throws `NPI_MISMATCH` rather than silently consuming wrong-NPI data. If multiple results come back (also should-never-happen), the parser picks the one with the matching `number`. **Phone format intentionally NOT normalized** — NPPES sends bare digits (`"2175550142"`); we may store hyphenated (`"217-555-0142"`); the client preserves what NPPES sent. If false-positive `UPDATE` actions from phone-format drift surface in production, slice 4's worker (or a slice-1 follow-up) adds phone normalization. The principle from slice 1 applies: noise an operator filters beats silent drift the audit log can't explain. **Injectable everything for tests**: `fetch` (function shape compatible with the global), `sleep` (`(ms) => Promise<void>`), `baseUrl`, all timing parameters. Tests never hit the real CMS API; they don't depend on fake timers either — the `sleep` injection records requested durations as numbers so retry-backoff assertions read naturally without timer machinery. **No caching at this layer** — cache invalidation is a worker concern; slice 4's "skip NPIs we synced in the last N hours" logic lives on the worker's `provider_sync_check` reads, not in the HTTP transport. **No logging at this layer** — slice 4's worker owns observability; the client emits typed errors with metadata (`npi`, `httpStatus`, `retryAfter`) so the worker decides what to ship to Datadog / Sentry. **No PHI considerations** — NPPES data is PUBLIC by design (the registry exists so payers and pharmacies can verify prescribers' enrollment); provider NPIs, names, practice addresses, credentials are not PHI. Defensive: response bodies are not echoed in error metadata; if a future slice adds logging, it should log at most `npi + result_count + http_status`. **54 contract tests across `cms-client.test.ts`** in five blocks: **parser happy paths** (full NPPES response → snapshot, result_count:0 → null, LOCATION preferred, MAILING fallback, no-addresses → null, incomplete-address → null); **parser normalization** (empty strings → null on identity fields, whitespace-only → null, 9-digit ZIP → hyphenated, 5-digit ZIP unchanged, empty address_2 / telephone_number → null, last_updated YYYY-MM-DD → midnight UTC, full ISO timestamp fallback); **parser status handling** (`A` / `D` / `""` / `X` / missing all behave correctly, parametric `it.each`); **parser errors** (MALFORMED_RESPONSE for invalid JSON, SCHEMA_MISMATCH for `null` body, NPI_MISMATCH for wrong-number result, pick-matching-result when multiple returned, SCHEMA_MISMATCH for unknown / missing enumeration_type, SCHEMA_MISMATCH for missing / unparseable last_updated); **client construction + input validation** (userAgent required + non-empty, NPI must be 10 digits, NPI must be numeric — both reject WITHOUT calling fetch); **transport errors** (4xx → `BAD_REQUEST` with NO retry; 429 retry with `Retry-After` honoring → success; 500 retry with exponential backoff → success; 429 / 5xx / network exhaust retries → typed errors; AbortError → TIMEOUT and retries; generic network error → NETWORK_ERROR and retries; persistent network failure → NETWORK_ERROR after retries; MALFORMED_RESPONSE on 200 with bad JSON; `Retry-After: 5` → sleep recorded as 5000ms; missing `Retry-After` falls back to backoff; invalid `Retry-After` falls back to backoff; backoff capped at `retryMaxMs`); **rate limiter** (`minRequestSpacingMs=0` records no sleeps; `minRequestSpacingMs=125` records a 125ms sleep between two requests); **`fetchManyByNpi`** (per-NPI results keyed by NPI; per-NPI error captured as `{ok: false, error: PharmaxError}` while sibling NPIs succeed; empty NPI list returns an empty map and makes zero fetch calls).
