Public surface from `@pharmax/providers/index.ts` expanded: `CmsNppesClient`, `CMS_NPI_REGISTRY_ERRORS`, `parseSingleNpiResponse`, and the option / result types (`CmsNppesClientOptions`, `CmsFetchResult`, `FetchFunction`, `Sleeper`).
- [~] Provider commands (continued): **`SyncFromNpiRegistry` — slice 4 of N shipped** in new `packages/providers/src/npi-sync/run-sync.ts` + `dispatch-adapters.ts` + 22 contract tests in `run-sync.test.ts` — the **per-org orchestrator** that ties slices 1 (diff engine), 2 (CMS HTTP client), and 3 (persistence schema) into a single executable unit of work. **Why slice 4 is the per-org orchestrator and NOT the cross-tenant drain**: the cross-tenant drain (slice 5) is a scheduling concern — "which orgs are due for a sync this tick, and how do we enter each org's tenancy frame?" The per-org sync is a domain concern — "given that we're inside an org's tenancy frame, reconcile its providers against CMS." Conflating them would force every slice-4 test to spin up `withTenancyContext` / `withSystemContext` / a configured command bus / a fake cross-tenant claim query. Splitting them lets the worker function be unit-testable with mocked Prisma + mocked CMS + mocked dispatchers — 22 tests for ~7ms total runtime — while the drain wrapper (slice 5) handles the tenancy-frame plumbing where it belongs. **Function signature is the DI surface**: `runNpiSyncForOrg(deps, input)` where `deps = {prisma, cmsClient, clock, logger, dispatchUpdateProvider, dispatchDeactivateProvider}` and `input = {organizationId, triggeredBy, triggeredByUserId, maxProviders?, cmsFetchBatchSize?}`. The two `dispatch*` adapters take `(typed command input, {idempotencyKey})` and return `DispatchResult = {ok: true, commandLogId} | {ok: false, raceCode}` — race classification is centralized in the adapter so the worker's per-action branches never see a typed `ConflictError` directly. **Six recognized race codes** (`PROVIDER_NOT_FOUND` / `PROVIDER_INACTIVE` / `PROVIDER_ALREADY_INACTIVE` / `PROVIDER_UPDATE_RACE_LOST` / `PROVIDER_UPDATE_NO_CHANGES` / `PROVIDER_DEACTIVATE_RACE_LOST`) cover every case where a concurrent operator action invalidated the worker's diff between read and dispatch; any other thrown error propagates to the run-level catch and flips the run to FAILED. **Per-action persistence semantics**: NONE → one `provider_sync_check` row (no dispatch, `dispatchedCommandLogId: null`), increments `noChangeCount`. UPDATE → dispatch `UpdateProvider({providerId, ...action.changes})` keyed `npi-sync:<runId>:<providerId>:UPDATE` → write check with `dispatchedCommandLogId` from the bus + `actionDetail` set to a sorted comma-joined list of changed keys (`firstName,lastName` etc.) → increment `providersUpdated`; on race-rejected dispatch, downgrade to a NONE check with `actionDetail: race:<raceCode>` and increment `noChangeCount` instead (the run still observed the diff; the FK link is null because no command committed). DEACTIVATE → dispatch `DeactivateProvider({providerId, reason: "LICENSE_EXPIRED", reasonText: buildSyncDeactivationReasonText(...)})` keyed `npi-sync:<runId>:<providerId>:DEACTIVATE` → same race-downgrade pattern → `actionDetail: <reason>` → increment `providersDeactivated`. REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE / NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS / ENUMERATION_TYPE_MISMATCH → write check FIRST (so its `id` exists for the review_item FK) → try `providerSyncReviewItem.create` with the full serialized snapshots → catch P2002 from the partial unique index `provider_sync_review_item_open_unique` and swallow (prior OPEN review row is still the operator's actionable handle; the just-written check row records the re-observation) → increment the corresponding counter. FETCH_FAILED (CMS-side, never emitted by the diff engine) → one check row with `action: FETCH_FAILED`, `errorCode` + `errorMetadata` populated from the `CmsFetchResult.error.code` + `.metadata` + `.message`, no dispatch, no review_item, increment `fetchFailedCount` (the operator UI in slice 6 may surface persistent fetch-failures as a separate emergency bucket; the worker just records the raw observation). **Idempotency key composition**: `npi-sync:<runId>:<providerId>:<UPDATE|DEACTIVATE>`. Crash-and-retry of the same run never double-dispatches (the bus dedups on the key); a fresh run with a different `runId` freely re-dispatches the same action if still applicable. The slice-5 reaper marks stuck IN_PROGRESS runs to FAILED, and a subsequent run picks the provider up via the standard `provider.findMany` enumeration with a new `runId`-keyed idempotency key — no stuck-run cleanup is needed in the worker itself. **Run finalization** is a single `providerSyncRun.update` with all 9 denormalized counters + completedAt + final status: `COMPLETED` if `fetchFailedCount === 0`, else `PARTIAL`. On any thrown error mid-run (DB connectivity, unrecognized command-bus exception, P2002 on review_item is NOT this case — that's the swallowed dedup path, but a non-P2002 review_item error IS this case), the catch block updates the run to `FAILED` with `errorCode` + `errorMessage` + `errorMetadata` synthesized from the cause (PharmaxError → copy `code` + `metadata`; plain Error → `errorCode: NPI_SYNC_RUN_UNEXPECTED`; unknown → stringify), then re-throws so the slice-5 drain sees the failure. If the finalize update ITSELF fails (e.g. DB connectivity lost), we log and leave the run IN_PROGRESS for the slice-5 reaper to sweep; we re-throw the original cause so observability gets the real signal, not the secondary failure. **CMS fan-out batching**: providers are listed once via `prisma.provider.findMany({orderBy: {id: "asc"}, take?: maxProviders})` (no cursor pagination at our scale; revisit when single-org provider counts pass ~10k). The list is sliced into chunks of `cmsFetchBatchSize` (default 50) and each chunk is fanned out via `cmsClient.fetchManyByNpi(npis)`. The CMS client's own rate limiter (slice 2, ~8 req/s) is the binding throughput constraint; the worker's batch size knob just shapes IO granularity. **Provider listing includes INACTIVE rows** by design — the diff engine emits `REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE` for "CMS active, local INACTIVE" pairs, so excluding INACTIVE here would silently disable that whole branch. **Sequential per-provider processing inside a batch**: CMS rate limiting already serializes; in-batch parallelism buys nothing while complicating counter increments and tx-boundary reasoning. If/when we move to a Postgres-bound (rather than CMS-bound) workload, we revisit with bounded `Promise.all` + atomic counter updates. **Client-contract violation as a structural error**: if `cmsClient.fetchManyByNpi(npis)` returns a Map missing an NPI we asked about, the worker throws `NPI_SYNC_CLIENT_CONTRACT_VIOLATION` — this is a slice-2 client bug, not a transient failure, and we want it to flip the run to FAILED with an actionable code rather than silently writing a per-provider FETCH_FAILED. **Snapshot serialization for review items**: `cmsSnapshot` JSONB carries the parsed `CmsNpiSnapshot` with `lastUpdatedAtCms` ISO-stringified (`null` for NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS since CMS returned nothing); `localSnapshot` JSONB carries the 13 columns the diff engine read from the Provider row (id, organizationId, npi, status, firstName/lastName/credential, addressLine1/Line2/city/state/postalCode, phone). DEA number is deliberately omitted from `localSnapshot` even though we have access to the row — operator review of "should we reactivate Provider X?" does not need DEA, and including it would broaden the surface where DEA touches an audit-bearing JSONB column (slice 6 review UI fetches the live Provider row when DEA is actually needed for the resolution decision). **Production dispatch adapter** (`buildProductionDispatchers(prisma)` in `dispatch-adapters.ts`) wires the worker's `DispatchUpdateProvider` / `DispatchDeactivateProvider` interfaces to real `executeCommand(UpdateProvider/DeactivateProvider, ...)` calls + a one-row `commandLog.findFirst({where: {commandName, idempotencyKey}})` lookup that resolves the `command_log.id` for the FK linkage. **CommandLogId lookup design**: the command bus does not return the row id it created (the `executeCommand` signature returns `TOutput` only); we use the bus's own idempotency key (which IS unique per `(organizationId, commandName, idempotencyKey)`) as the lookup handle. One extra read query per dispatched command at a worker that dispatches maybe a few dozen commands per org-run is trivial. The adapter asserts a tenancy frame is active before issuing the lookup (the lookup is tenant-scoped via the Prisma extension); a missing frame surfaces as a clear error instead of a silent null result. If the lookup returns null after a successful dispatch (a structural invariant violation: bus said success but `command_log` is missing), the adapter throws so the orchestrator marks the run FAILED with an actionable code. **Race classification** is exported as `classifyDispatchError(cause)` — checks `cause.code` against the six-code `RACE_CODES` set and returns the typed `ProviderRaceCode` if matching, else `null`. The adapter uses it; tests pin its behavior on every code + on non-Error inputs (null, undefined, strings, plain objects). **22 unit tests** in `run-sync.test.ts` cover every behavioral axis the worker controls: (1) **happy paths**: empty-org short-circuits to COMPLETED without calling CMS; NONE produces no dispatch + one check row; UPDATE dispatches with diffed fields + records `commandLogId` + `actionDetail`=sorted-changed-keys; DEACTIVATE dispatches with `LICENSE_EXPIRED` + reasonText containing CMS status timestamp + records `commandLogId`; REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE writes both check + review_item with non-null `cmsSnapshot`; NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS writes both with `cmsSnapshot: null`; ENUMERATION_TYPE_MISMATCH writes both with `actionDetail: local=NPI-1,cms=NPI-2`. (2) **fetch failures**: single FETCH_FAILED flips run to PARTIAL with `errorCode` + `errorMetadata.message` recorded; mixed batch of OK + FETCH_FAILED counts correctly across `noChangeCount` + `fetchFailedCount` while still finalizing PARTIAL. (3) **race handling**: UPDATE → PROVIDER_UPDATE_RACE_LOST downgrades to NONE check with `actionDetail: race:PROVIDER_UPDATE_RACE_LOST` and null `dispatchedCommandLogId`; UPDATE → PROVIDER_INACTIVE same downgrade pattern; DEACTIVATE → PROVIDER_ALREADY_INACTIVE same downgrade pattern. (4) **review-item dedup**: P2002 on `providerSyncReviewItem.create` is swallowed (still writes the check, still increments the counter, the review_item array stays empty); non-P2002 error on review_item propagates and flips run to FAILED with errorMessage carrying the cause. (5) **batching**: `cmsFetchBatchSize: 2` with 3 providers produces exactly 2 fetch calls with NPI lists `[a, b]` then `[c]`; `maxProviders: 3` with 10 providers in DB only scans 3. (6) **client-contract violation**: `fetchManyByNpi` returning an empty Map throws `NPI_SYNC_CLIENT_CONTRACT_VIOLATION` and flips run to FAILED with that code in `errorMetadata`. (7) **failure during run**: DB error mid-fanout (simulated via throw-on-Nth-check-create) catches at the run level, updates run to FAILED with `errorMessage` matching the cause, re-throws; PharmaxError carrying domain metadata propagates that metadata into `run.errorMetadata` for downstream observability. (8) **classifyDispatchError**: every recognized race code returns itself; every non-race input (plain Error, non-race code, null, undefined, string) returns null. (9) **counter sanity**: a mixed-action run's seven counters sum to `providersScanned` (invariant the dashboards assume). **No DB / HTTP / tenancy ALS in any test** — the entire test surface is pure mocks against the narrow DI interfaces; the slice-5 drain will exercise the real adapters end-to-end against the test database. **Public surface added to `packages/providers/src/index.ts`**: `runNpiSyncForOrg` + all 11 supporting types (`DispatchUpdateProvider`, `DispatchDeactivateProvider`, `DispatchResult`, `DispatchOptions`, `ProviderRaceCode`, `ProviderRowProjection`, `ProviderSyncPrismaSurface`, `RunNpiSyncForOrgDeps`, `RunNpiSyncForOrgInput`, `RunNpiSyncForOrgResult`, `RunNpiSyncForOrgSummary`) + `classifyDispatchError` + `buildProductionDispatchers` + `DispatchAdaptersPrismaSurface` + `ProductionDispatchers`. The two pure / library slices and the schema slice were exported the same way; this completes the importable contract for the slice-5 drain. **Why no integration tests** at this slice: the worker's contract is purely "given these mocked inputs, produce these writes + return this result" — the integration questions ("does the real Prisma extension scope correctly? does the real command bus thread the right correlation? does RLS reject cross-org writes?") are slice-5 / slice-6 concerns where the dispatchers, tenancy frames, and Postgres are all in the loop. Unit-only here keeps the per-slice cost low and the per-slice review surface focused. Remaining slices: (5) cron scheduling layer that enters per-org tenancy + invokes `runNpiSyncForOrg` + stuck-run reaper that sweeps still-IN_PROGRESS runs past the runtime ceiling to FAILED + per-org sync cadence config (default 24h between runs per org) + dead-letter for runs that consistently FAIL; (6) operator UI for the three review queues + per-run dashboards + provider-detail sync history + resolution commands (`ResolveReactivationCandidate`, `ResolveNotFoundAtCms`, `ResolveEnumerationTypeMismatch`) that close review_items and emit follow-up commands (`ReactivateProvider` / `DeactivateProvider` / `UpdateProvider`) per the operator's decision.
- [~] Provider commands (continued): **`SyncFromNpiRegistry` — slice 5 of N shipped** — the **cross-tenant scheduling layer + stuck-run reaper** that turns the slice-4 per-org orchestrator into an unattended background process. Three new worker drains in `apps/worker/src/drains/` (`claim-due-orgs-for-npi-sync.ts`, `npi-sync-scheduler.ts`, `reap-stuck-npi-sync-runs.ts`) + 14 tests + a new migration + a new RBAC role + a seeded per-org service identity + 8 new env knobs, all wired into `apps/worker/src/main.ts`. **Why slice 5 is the scheduling concern and NOT the domain concern**: slice 4 deliberately left "which orgs sync, when, and under what identity" to this slice. The pattern mirrors the existing `report-scheduler` exactly — a system-context claim that reads across tenants in one SQL pass, then a per-row loop that enters each org's tenancy to do the actual work — so a reviewer who understands the report scheduler understands this one. **The claim query** (`claimDueOrgsForNpiSync`) runs in system context and answers "which orgs are due this tick?" entirely from `provider_sync_run` history + provider existence, with no per-org cadence config table (cadence is a worker-level constant; a future per-org override would be a new `npi_sync_config` table queried here). Selection rules, all AND: (a) the org has ≥1 provider row (no point sweeping fresh empty tenants); (b) the org has NO `IN_PROGRESS` run (filtered in SQL even though the migration's partial unique index makes it a hard constraint — don't hand the dispatcher work it can't accept); (c) EITHER the org never completed a terminal run OR its most-recent COMPLETED/PARTIAL run finished more than `cadenceMs` ago. **FAILED runs deliberately do NOT count as "last successful"** — a stuck/abandoned FAILED run must not push the next sync further into the future, so the `last_terminal` CTE filters `status IN ('COMPLETED','PARTIAL')`. **Ordering is `lastSuccessfulRunAt ASC NULLS FIRST`** so never-synced orgs go first, then the most-overdue — fair queueing under cadence pressure. No `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` here (unlike the report scheduler): there's no row to lock — the "claim" IS the INSERT of the IN_PROGRESS run row inside `runNpiSyncForOrg`, and the new partial unique index is the lock. **The migration** `20260628000000_phase3_provider_sync_run_active_unique` adds `CREATE UNIQUE INDEX provider_sync_run_active_unique ON provider_sync_run(organizationId) WHERE status = 'IN_PROGRESS'` — making "at most one active sync per org" a database invariant rather than a best-effort filter. This matters for HA topologies: with >1 worker pod, two schedulers can both see an org as eligible (their claim queries run against the same pre-insert snapshot) and both attempt to create an IN_PROGRESS run; the partial unique index guarantees exactly one wins, and the loser's P2002 is caught + downgraded to SKIPPED. Mirrors the slice-3 `provider_sync_review_item_open_unique` pattern (partial unique on an "active" subset; historical COMPLETED/PARTIAL/FAILED rows accumulate freely). Index-only migration, so no RLS pairing needed (the table already has its policy from slice 3). **The dispatcher** (`createNpiSyncScheduler(...).tick()`) loops the claimed orgs sequentially — NOT in parallel, because each `runNpiSyncForOrg` already saturates the process-wide CMS rate gate (8 req/s), so org-level fan-out would just queue requests behind the same gate while complicating the resource shape. Per org: (a) resolve the per-org service user `npi-sync@<org-slug>.test` in system context (the email local-part is configurable via `NPI_SYNC_ACTOR_EMAIL_LOCAL_PART` for production deployments that pin a non-`.test` domain); a missing user → SKIPPED (config error; admin runs the seed) — same graceful-skip philosophy as the report scheduler's `ACTOR_NOT_FOUND`; (b) build a tenancy context for that org + actor with a fresh correlation id; (c) `withTenancyContext(...)` → `runNpiSyncForOrg(deps, {triggeredBy: "CRON", triggeredByUserId: null, maxProviders?, cmsFetchBatchSize?})` with production dispatchers from `buildProductionDispatchers(prisma)` (the slice-4 adapters that wire to the real command bus + command_log lookup). **Outcome tally**: SUCCEEDED (run COMPLETED or PARTIAL), FAILED (orchestrator threw OR returned status=FAILED), SKIPPED (no service user OR P2002 active-run race). **P2002 downgrade**: if `runNpiSyncForOrg` throws a Prisma unique violation (the active-run race), the dispatcher shape-checks `cause.code === "P2002"` and tallies SKIPPED rather than FAILED — losing the race to a sibling pod is benign, not an error. Non-P2002 throws tally FAILED (the orchestrator already finalized the run row to FAILED itself before re-throwing; the dispatcher just records the tally + logs). **Why no bus command wraps the per-org work**: `runNpiSyncForOrg` already owns its audit + outbox writes via the inner `UpdateProvider`/`DeactivateProvider` commands it dispatches; a bus command at the scheduler layer would add a noop outer tx — the scheduler is pure orchestration, identical to the report scheduler's rationale. **The reaper** (`createStuckNpiSyncRunReaper(...).tick()`) is a single cross-tenant `updateMany` that sweeps `provider_sync_run` rows stuck in `IN_PROGRESS` past `runtimeCeilingMs` (default 60 min) to `FAILED` with `errorMessage: "sync run exceeded runtime ceiling"` + structured `errorMetadata: {reaper: true, runtimeCeilingMs, reapedAt}` so an operator can distinguish a reaped run from an orchestrator-finalized FAILED. **Why the reaper matters**: a worker that crashes mid-run (OOM, scaling event, an exception that escapes the orchestrator's outer catch) leaves an IN_PROGRESS row that the partial unique index would otherwise block the next sync on forever. The reaper unblocks the org. **Reaper concurrency**: `updateMany` with no nested mutation is safe to run from multiple pods — they converge to the same FAILED target; the `status = 'IN_PROGRESS'` WHERE predicate IS the idempotency guard (a reaped row is excluded from future sweeps). Runs in system context (cross-tenant); no per-org tenancy entry because a stuck run that never finished has no real completion event to broadcast — there's nothing to audit beyond the row flip itself. **The RBAC role** `NpiSyncWorker` (machine-only, ORGANIZATION scope) grants exactly `providers.update` + `providers.deactivate` — the two commands the diff engine produces for non-review-item actions. Least-privilege mirror of `WebhookService` / `ReportsScheduler`: a compromised npi-sync identity can update provider demographics + deactivate prescribers (no PHI exposure, no terminal-state order writes); recovery is purely operational. Review-item creation is a direct tenant-scoped insert by the worker, NOT a bus command, so it needs no permission. The role is added to `ROLE_TEMPLATES` and is not on the `MFA_REQUIRED_ROLE_CODES` set (machine identity, never logs into the UI). **The seed** provisions `npi-sync@<org-slug>.test` per org with the `NpiSyncWorker` role granted org-wide — same upsert + idempotent-grant pattern as the shipping-webhook + reports-scheduler service users. **8 env knobs** in `apps/worker/src/env.ts`: `NPI_SYNC_SCHEDULER_BATCH_SIZE` (10), `NPI_SYNC_SCHEDULER_INTERVAL_MS` (5 min — coarse because cadence is the binding constraint), `NPI_SYNC_CADENCE_MS` (24h), `NPI_SYNC_MAX_PROVIDERS_PER_ORG` (optional cap; 0/unset = unlimited; ramps CMS pressure during initial deploy), `NPI_SYNC_CMS_FETCH_BATCH_SIZE` (50), `NPI_SYNC_REAPER_INTERVAL_MS` (10 min), `NPI_SYNC_RUNTIME_CEILING_MS` (60 min), `NPI_SYNC_ACTOR_EMAIL_LOCAL_PART` (optional override). **Wiring into `main.ts`**: one shared `CmsNppesClient` instance (so the 8 req/s rate gate is process-wide, not per-org) feeds the scheduler; two new poll loops (`npi-sync-scheduler`, `npi-sync-reaper`) join the existing six in the boot log, the `start()` fan-out, and the graceful-shutdown `Promise.all(stop())`. **14 tests**: the claim function (3 — empty result, projection + cadence/batch threading, DB-error propagation); the scheduler (8 — empty batch, happy-path-2-orgs with triggeredBy=CRON + per-org slug actor lookup + DI surface assertions, custom `actorEmailLocalPart`, omit-optional-knobs, skip-when-no-actor + continue, FAILED-on-throw + continue, FAILED-on-status-FAILED-without-throw, P2002→SKIPPED downgrade); the reaper (3 — happy-path FAILED + errorMetadata blob + cutoff math, no-op zero-row without warn noise, cutoff threading). All against mocked Prisma + mocked `runNpiSyncForOrg` (the orchestrator's own behavior is exhaustively covered by slice 4's 22 tests; the scheduler tests only assert the wiring). **One type-adaptor cast in main.ts**: the worker's narrow `ProviderSyncPrismaSurface` types JSON columns as `Record<string, unknown>` but Prisma's generated input types are stricter under `exactOptionalPropertyTypes`; the `prisma as unknown as ...client` cast at the single production wiring site is the standard adaptor between a typed narrow interface (worker-internal, fully test-anchored) and Prisma's generated wide types — the same pattern used elsewhere for `Prisma.InputJsonValue` boundaries. Remaining slices: (6) operator UI for the three review queues + per-run dashboards + provider-detail sync history + resolution commands (`ResolveReactivationCandidate`, `ResolveNotFoundAtCms`, `ResolveEnumerationTypeMismatch`) that close review_items and emit follow-up commands per the operator's decision; a `MANUAL`-triggered sync entry point (operator clicks "sync this org now" → `triggeredBy: "MANUAL"`, `triggeredByUserId` set) that reuses `runNpiSyncForOrg` directly; optional per-org cadence override config + dead-letter for runs that consistently FAIL.
- [~] Provider commands (continued): **`SyncFromNpiRegistry` — slice 3 of N shipped** in migration `20260616000000_phase3_provider_npi_sync` + 3 new Prisma models in `prisma/schema.prisma` — the **persistence schema** for the NPI Registry reconciliation worker. The two pure / library slices are done; slice 3 lands the audit-trail tables that the worker (slice 4) will write to. **Three new tables**, each with a deliberate access pattern: (1) **`provider_sync_run`** — one row per worker invocation per org, carrying summary metrics (`providersScanned` / `providersFetchedFromCms` / `providersUpdated` / `providersDeactivated` / `reactivationCandidatesCreated` / `notFoundAtCmsCount` / `enumerationTypeMismatchCount` / `fetchFailedCount` / `noChangeCount`) denormalized on the row so dashboards can answer "show me last week's run rates" without scanning the per-check table; status enum `IN_PROGRESS | COMPLETED | PARTIAL | FAILED` (PARTIAL is the run-succeeded-structurally-but-some-NPI-fetches-failed case; FAILED is the abort-before-completion case the slice-5+ reaper sets when a run exceeds its runtime ceiling); trigger enum `CRON | MANUAL | BACKFILL` with `triggeredByUserId` set non-null only for MANUAL runs; `errorMessage` + `errorMetadata` JSONB carry PharmaxError contents for FAILED runs (PHI-free by the platform-core contract). (2) **`provider_sync_check`** — one row per (run, provider). High-volume audit row (~1k providers × daily runs × N orgs = ~365k rows/year/org). Action enum mirrors slice 1's `SyncAction.kind` (`NONE | UPDATE | DEACTIVATE | REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE | NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS | ENUMERATION_TYPE_MISMATCH`) plus a 7th `FETCH_FAILED` value for `CmsFetchResult.ok=false` (the diff engine never emits FETCH_FAILED — it's a worker-layer concept). Carries denormalized `cmsStatus` (CHAR(1)) + `cmsLastUpdatedAt` so the operator UI can show "CMS said this on this date" without re-fetching; denormalized `npi` so historical checks survive a future NPI rekey on the local Provider row; `dispatchedCommandLogId` FK to `command_log` is non-null when the worker dispatched UpdateProvider / DeactivateProvider for this check (null for NONE, review-item-emitting actions, FETCH_FAILED) — closes the audit traceback "what sync caused this DeactivateProvider call?"; `errorCode` + `errorMetadata` set when action=FETCH_FAILED. (3) **`provider_sync_review_item`** — the operator review queue. The worker writes a row whenever the diff engine emits an action requiring HUMAN judgment per slice 1's "never auto-reactivate" contract: REACTIVATION_CANDIDATE, NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS, ENUMERATION_TYPE_MISMATCH. Status enum `OPEN | RESOLVED | DISMISSED`; resolution enum `REACTIVATED | DEACTIVATED | NPI_CORRECTED | DISMISSED_AS_FALSE_POSITIVE | DISMISSED_NO_ACTION` set together with `resolvedAt` + `resolvedByUserId` on transition (the NPI_CORRECTED resolution is the audit path for a typo'd NPI fixed via the immutable-NPI Deactivate + Register motion). **Snapshots as JSONB**: `cmsSnapshot` (nullable; null for NOT_FOUND_AT_CMS since CMS returned nothing) and `localSnapshot` (always populated) capture discovery-time evidence so operators see what was observed WHEN it was observed, not the current state. NPPES data is PUBLIC (no encryption needed); the local snapshot is provider-directory data (NPI / name / address / credential) — none of which is PHI under HIPAA Safe Harbor. **`resolutionNotes`** is PHI-adjacent operator free-text and will be redacted from `command_log.requestPayload` by the slice-6 resolution command's `redactFields` (same pattern as `OrderCancellation.dispositionReasonText`). **Why three tables and not one**: the run row's metrics are aggregates; the per-check rows are the disaggregated source. Making the run row a materialized view of the checks would force a single-source refresh and complicate the stuck-run reaper (which needs to mutate `status` on still-IN_PROGRESS rows). The review_item queue has a fundamentally different access pattern (operators querying by status + age, with mutation on resolve / dismiss) than the append-only audit rows; mixing them would force every operator-UI query to filter by action kind. **Partial unique index** `provider_sync_review_item_open_unique ON provider_sync_review_item(organizationId, providerId, kind) WHERE status = 'OPEN'` is the structural anti-duplicate-review guarantee — at most one open review per (provider, kind). If the worker re-emits the same finding in a later run before the operator resolves the prior one, the second insert lands on the unique violation and the worker treats P2002 as "already open, skip" (defense-in-depth on top of the worker's own "is there already an open review?" lookup; the index is also the lookup index for that check). Prisma's schema language cannot express partial unique indexes; the index lives in raw SQL with the same `Prisma cannot express` comment pattern `order_hold_active_hold_unique` uses. **Indexes** designed for the access patterns that matter: `provider_sync_run` gets `(organizationId, startedAt DESC)` for "last N runs", `(organizationId, status)` for the reaper sweep, `(organizationId, triggeredByUserId)` sparse for the "what did <user> trigger?" report; `provider_sync_check` gets `(organizationId, providerSyncRunId)` for run-detail view, `(organizationId, providerId, checkedAt DESC)` for per-provider history, `(organizationId, action, checkedAt DESC)` for the "all DEACTIVATE actions last quarter" report, `(organizationId, npi, checkedAt DESC)` for alternate provider lookup, `(organizationId, dispatchedCommandLogId)` for the audit traceback (sparse); `provider_sync_review_item` gets `(organizationId, kind, status, discoveredAt DESC)` for the per-kind queue view, `(organizationId, status, discoveredAt DESC)` for the all-kinds queue view, `(organizationId, resolvedByUserId, resolvedAt DESC)` for the "what reviews has <user> resolved?" report (sparse), and the partial unique. **No partitioning yet** on `provider_sync_check`: at our projected workload (~2M rows/year aggregate) the indexes are sufficient; retrofitting to a monthly-partitioned table is a structural migration the application code is partition-agnostic about (Prisma reads/writes go through the table name). When row counts justify it (10M+ band) we partition then; the comment header pins this decision and the schema linter doesn't object. **RLS shape** mirrors the baseline: each of the three tables gets `ENABLE` + `FORCE` row-level security + one PERMISSIVE `tenant_isolation` policy via the standard DO block on the `pharmax.system_context` / `pharmax.organization_id` GUC pair. `scripts/check-migration-rls.ts` confirms the ENABLE + CREATE POLICY pairing on every CREATE TABLE in the migration. **FK actions are all RESTRICT** — same audit-trail invariant as everywhere else (no silent destruction of audit data via cascade). A provider, run, user, command_log, or check row referenced by downstream sync data cannot be hard-deleted. **Tenant-scope registry** updated in lockstep: `TENANT_SCOPED_MODELS` in `packages/tenancy/src/tenant-scoped-models.ts` registers `ProviderSyncRun`, `ProviderSyncCheck`, and `ProviderSyncReviewItem` with standard `{organizationId}` filter kind; the registry-parity contract test passes (every Prisma model is classified as scoped OR excluded; new models without classification are a build failure). **Six new Prisma enums** at the top of the schema (`ProviderSyncRunStatus`, `ProviderSyncRunTrigger`, `ProviderSyncCheckAction`, `ProviderSyncReviewItemKind`, `ProviderSyncReviewItemStatus`, `ProviderSyncReviewItemResolution`) — `ProviderSyncReviewItemKind` is deliberately a SUBSET of `ProviderSyncCheckAction` (only the actions requiring human review can appear on a review item; NONE / UPDATE / DEACTIVATE / FETCH_FAILED have no review-item analog by construction). **Back-relations added in lockstep**: `Organization` gets `providerSyncRuns` / `providerSyncChecks` / `providerSyncReviewItems`; `User` gets `providerSyncRunsTriggered` (the MANUAL-run actor) + `providerSyncReviewsResolved` (the resolver); `CommandLog` gets `providerSyncChecksDispatched` (the dispatched-command backpointer) + `providerSyncReviewsResolved` (the resolver-command backpointer); `Provider` gets `syncChecks` + `syncReviewItems`. **Gate hygiene** done in lockstep (NOT new functional work): fixed a pre-existing SQL-style `--` comment in `prisma/schema.prisma` near the `ReportScheduleRunStatus` enum that was breaking `prisma generate` (background scaffolding had typo'd one `//` as `--`; Prisma's `getDmmf` rejected the file with a context error). With the fix, `prisma generate` succeeds; the schema linter reports 56 models, 50 tenant-scoped, 6 excluded. **No tests added in this slice** — the schema is the contract; behavior tests land with slice 4's worker (which reads/writes through this schema and exercises every column with real data). The registry-parity test in `packages/tenancy/src/tenant-scoped-models.test.ts` automatically picks up the three new models and asserts their classification. Remaining slices: (4) the worker itself — per-org runs, batched NPI fetches via `CmsNppesClient`, diff engine call per row, dispatches `DeactivateProvider` / `UpdateProvider` via the command bus for actionable rows, writes `provider_sync_check` for every check, writes `provider_sync_review_item` for human-review actions with the worker-side "skip if open exists" guard riding on the partial unique; (5) cron scheduling layer + stuck-run reaper that sweeps still-IN_PROGRESS runs past the runtime ceiling to FAILED; (6) operator UI for the three review queues + per-run dashboards + provider-detail sync history.
- [~] Order commands: **`CreateOrder` shipped** in new `@pharmax/orders` package — the reference implementation for every subsequent order-aggregate command. Runs through the new `defineCommand` factory, exercising the create-command path (no `lockTarget` because the order doesn't exist yet, `loadPolicy: { code: "order.standard", version: 1 }` so the new row is born at the right policy id+version, `bumpVersion` omitted because the row is born at `version=0`, `redactFields: []` because `CreateOrder` inputs carry no decrypted PHI — the patient identity lives on the encrypted `patient` row created earlier by `RegisterPatient`). Inside the handler (after the factory has loaded the active policy): tenant-scoped clinic lookup (stale id → `NotFoundError(ORDER_CLINIC_NOT_FOUND)`), tenant-scoped site lookup (`ORDER_SITE_NOT_FOUND`), `clinic_site` link check (`ConflictError(ORDER_SITE_NOT_LINKED_TO_CLINIC)` because "wrong site for this clinic" is a fixable caller error, not an auth violation), patient existence + clinic-pin check (the patient model is scoped to `(organizationId, clinicId)` per the Phase 2 schema decision, so a clinic mismatch surfaces as `ORDER_PATIENT_CLINIC_MISMATCH` rather than the generic NOT FOUND), bulk prescription lookup scoped to `(organizationId, clinicId, patientId)` so a stale or cross-clinic rxId returns `ORDER_PRESCRIPTION_MISMATCH` with the offending id list (not a privacy leak: telling the caller "rx 5 isn't on this patient" is fine; what we don't do is silently insert the order line and discover the mismatch in the fill room), intake bucket resolution by `(organizationId, siteId, code: BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS.RECEIVED)` — the bucket code comes from the canonical `OrderPrimaryState → bucket code` map exported by `@pharmax/workflow`, so this command and every future in-flight workflow command (`StartTyping` onward) resolve buckets through the same source of truth (a hardcoded "INBOX" string here would let the seed and the commands drift apart silently); today the map resolves `RECEIVED → "INBOX"`, matching the default `WORKFLOW` bucket that `prisma/seed.ts` creates per site (`InternalError(ORDER_INTAKE_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED)` if missing — surface the misconfiguration loudly rather than orphan the order in a nonexistent queue). Then one `order.create` (writing `currentStatus = RECEIVED`, `currentBucketId`, `workflowPolicyId`, `workflowPolicyVersion`, `version: 0`, `receivedAt = clock.now()`, `intakeSourceKind`, `priority`, optional `externalOrderNumber` / `intakeSourceRefId`) followed by one `orderLine.create` per input line (each with `quantityToFill: Prisma.Decimal`, `daysSupplyToFill: int`, scoped `organizationId` + `clinicId` for RLS). The factory then writes `order_event { eventType: "order.received.v1", sequenceNumber: 1, payload: {...} }` and the bus writes `audit_log { action: "order.created" }` + `event_outbox` + `idempotency_key` in the same tx. **Audit metadata is PHI-free by construction**: `{clinicId, siteId, intakeSourceKind, priority, lineCount, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion}` — no patientId, no patient name, no DOB. **Outbox payload** carries `{orderId, organizationId, clinicId, siteId, patientId, priority, intakeSourceKind, lineCount, occurredAt}` — `patientId` is a system UUID, not PHI, and downstream consumers (queue counter, SLA scanner, billing event projection) need it to scope their work. RBAC permission `orders.create` (already registered in the typed `PERMISSIONS` registry and seeded in `prisma/seed.ts` from Phase 1) is now also granted by default to the `PharmacyTechnician` role template — the operational role that performs intake; `Pharmacist` keeps `orders.read` only because manual intake by a pharmacist is the exception, not the convention (admins can grant `orders.create` per-role-edit when needed). **`ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION`** translator exported from `@pharmax/orders` so the bus's SoD helper can map `order.received.v1` → `ORDERS_CREATE` when later commands cite this order's history. **18 contract tests** across `create-order.test.ts` assert: happy path returns `{ orderId, orderLineIds[2], currentStatus: "RECEIVED", version: 0 }` and writes order + 2 order_lines + 1 order_event (seq=1) + audit + outbox + idempotency in canonical order; outbox payload carries the resolved orderId + scope + lineCount + ISO timestamp; audit metadata holds scope + policy + lineCount with zero patientId / firstName / DOB substrings; Zod rejects bad clinicId UUID, empty lines array, extra fields under strict mode, and negative `quantityToFill`; every scope failure (`ORDER_CLINIC_NOT_FOUND`, `ORDER_SITE_NOT_FOUND`, `ORDER_SITE_NOT_LINKED_TO_CLINIC`, `ORDER_PATIENT_NOT_FOUND`, `ORDER_PATIENT_CLINIC_MISMATCH`, `ORDER_PRESCRIPTION_MISMATCH` with the offending id, `ORDER_INTAKE_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED`, factory-thrown `WORKFLOW_POLICY_NOT_FOUND`, factory-thrown `WORKFLOW_POLICY_INACTIVE`) short-circuits with zero `order.create` / `auditLog.create` / `eventOutbox.createMany` calls; no tenancy frame throws `TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT` with zero DB writes; missing `orders.create` permission throws `PERMISSION_DENIED` with zero `order.create` calls. **End-to-end bootstrap is now closed-loop**: `CreateOrganization`'s optional `initialSite` block creates the `PharmacySite` row AND provisions the 7 canonical workflow buckets in the same transaction (via `provisionDefaultBucketsForSite`, the shared helper that the standalone `ProvisionDefaultBuckets` SystemCommand also dispatches to) — so a freshly bootstrapped org with an initial site can accept its first `CreateOrder` immediately without an admin "provision buckets" step. The `INBOX` bucket resolution this command performs against `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS.RECEIVED → "INBOX"` is therefore guaranteed to resolve on a fresh-org-with-site path; multi-site orgs that omit `initialSite` still call `ProvisionDefaultBuckets` per site after creating each site (the standalone command remains the backfill entry point for existing orgs and the per-site bootstrap entry point for additional sites).
- [~] Order commands (continued): **`AddPrescription` shipped** in `@pharmax/orders` — first end-to-end exercise of the `defineCommand` factory's `lockTarget` + `bumpVersion` CAS path on an existing order (CreateOrder was `version=0` insert with no lock). New RBAC permission `orders.add_prescription` added to the typed `PERMISSIONS` registry, `PERMISSION_METADATA`, `prisma/seed.ts` (24 codes seeded; mirror-parity regex broadened from `[a-z][a-z0-9.]+` to `[a-z][a-z0-9._]+` so compound action names with `_` pass the mirror test), and granted by default to `PharmacyTechnician`. New `order.prescription.added.v1` event wired into `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION`. Declarative spec: `lockTarget: { table: "order", by: (i) => ({ id: i.orderId }) }`; deliberately no `loadPolicy` — AddPrescription is not a state transition, so the order's stamped `workflowPolicyId`/`Version` stay put and the workflow engine isn't consulted (the engine is for state-machine transitions; "is this state mutable for adding lines" is a separate domain rule that lives in this command as the frozen `ADDABLE_STATES = {RECEIVED, TYPING_IN_PROGRESS, TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO}` set; any other state → `ConflictError(ORDER_NOT_IN_ADDABLE_STATE)` with `{orderId, currentStatus, addableStates}` so the UI can prompt for `ReopenForCorrection`). Inside the handler (after the factory's `SELECT … FOR UPDATE`): **rich-metadata optimistic-concurrency check** — caller passes `expectedOrderVersion` and the handler compares against `target.version`, on mismatch throws `ConflictError(ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH)` with both `expectedVersion` + `actualVersion` in metadata (the factory's CAS becomes defense-in-depth that only fires if a future bug bypasses the in-handler check). **Narrow scope reads**: lock SELECT list intentionally excludes `clinicId`/`patientId` to keep PHI-adjacent ids out of the lock-and-log path; a separate `tx.order.findFirst` recovers `{clinicId, patientId, siteId}` for the prescription validation. **Prescription cross-check**: single `tx.prescription.findFirst` scoped to `(orgId, order.clinicId, order.patientId)` returns null for ANY of stale id / wrong clinic / wrong patient — all surface as `ConflictError(ORDER_PRESCRIPTION_MISMATCH)`, the same code `CreateOrder` throws (imported from `./create-order.js` so callers see one stable error rather than two near-duplicates). `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` is imported from `@pharmax/command-bus` for the same reason — single source of truth across the factory CAS path and this handler. **Duplicate-line guard**: `orderLine.findFirst({orderId, prescriptionId})` rejects accidental re-add with `ConflictError(ORDER_PRESCRIPTION_ALREADY_ON_ORDER)` carrying `existingOrderLineId` in metadata; deliberate split-fill (two lines for the same Rx with different quantities) is a future `SplitFillLine` concern, kept as an explicit separate command so the accidental case isn't silently masked. Then one `orderLine.create` with scoped `organizationId`/`clinicId`/`orderId`/`prescriptionId` + `quantityToFill` (`Prisma.Decimal(18,4)`) + `daysSupplyToFill`; the factory then issues `order.updateMany({where: {id, organizationId, version: from}, data: {version: to}})` (defense-in-depth CAS), writes `order_event { eventType: "order.prescription.added.v1", sequenceNumber: head+1, payload: {...} }` with monotonic seq off `orderEvent.findFirst orderBy desc`, and the bus writes `audit_log { action: "order.prescription.added" }` + `event_outbox` + `idempotency_key` in the same tx. **Audit metadata + outbox payload are PHI-free by construction**: audit `{orderId, prescriptionId, orderLineId, clinicId, fromVersion, toVersion, quantityToFill, daysSupplyToFill}`, outbox same plus `{organizationId, siteId, occurredAt}`. Drug name is plaintext on the Prescription row but patient-identifying in context, so AddPrescription never reads or emits it; consumers JOIN to Prescription when they need it. **30 contract tests** across `add-prescription.test.ts` assert: `ADDABLE_STATES` set is exactly the three expected states; happy-path returns `{orderId, orderLineId, fromVersion, toVersion}` and writes lock → scope-read → rx scope → dup-check → orderLine → CAS (verified `from`/`to` in updateMany args) → order_event (`seq=head+1`, `actorUserId` from ctx) → audit → outbox → idempotency in canonical order; lock SELECT uses bound parameters for both `orderId` and `organizationId` (no string interpolation); also succeeds in `TYPING_IN_PROGRESS` and `TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO`; `order_event` seq=1 when head is null (theoretical zero-event order); audit metadata + outbox payload contain zero `firstName`/`lastName`/`dateOfBirth`/`drugName`/`ndc`/`sig` substrings (JSON.stringify with BigInt-aware replacer covers the chain writer's `seq` column); audit metadata records the `fromVersion → toVersion` transition (parametric on initial version); Zod rejects 8 invalid input shapes (bad orderId UUID, bad prescriptionId UUID, zero/negative `quantityToFill`, zero/negative `daysSupplyToFill`, negative `expectedOrderVersion`, non-integer `daysSupplyToFill`) + strict-mode extra fields with zero lock attempts; order-missing (lock returns no row) → factory-thrown `ORDER_NOT_FOUND` with zero downstream writes; 8 non-addable states (`TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1` through `CANCELLED`) all throw `ORDER_NOT_IN_ADDABLE_STATE` with zero orderLine/CAS/audit/outbox writes; stale `expectedOrderVersion` throws `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` with both versions in metadata and zero writes; prescription-mismatch and already-on-order both short-circuit before the orderLine insert; no tenancy frame → `TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT` with zero lock; missing `orders.add_prescription` → `PERMISSION_DENIED` with zero lock.
- [~] Order commands (continued): **`CancelOrder` shipped** in `@pharmax/orders` — the workflow's emergency exit and the first MULTI-FROM-STATE command (reachable from every non-terminal state per `@pharmax/workflow`'s `CANCEL_FROM_STATES`). Lands the **structured-domain-record + reason-code pattern** that `PlaceHold`, `RejectPV1`, `RejectFinalVerification`, and `ReopenForCorrection` will all reuse: one new tenant-scoped table (`order_cancellation`) with a closed enum for the reason, an optional PHI-bearing free-text column redacted from `command_log` and excluded from audit metadata + outbox payload, a unique-on-`orderId` constraint as the structural anti-double-write guarantee, RESTRICT FKs to the order, workflow policy, command log, and actor user so the audit trail can never lose its anchors, and per-tenant indexes shaped for the reporting questions operators actually ask ("how many cancellations this week?", "top reasons by clinic?", "what did this user cancel?"). New `CancellationDisposition` Postgres enum (`PATIENT_REQUEST`, `PROVIDER_REQUEST`, `CLINIC_REQUEST`, `INSURANCE_DENIAL`, `INVENTORY_UNAVAILABLE`, `DUPLICATE_ORDER`, `DATA_ENTRY_ERROR`, `PATIENT_INELIGIBLE`, `OTHER`) — `OTHER` is the escape hatch and the Zod refine on the command input requires a non-empty `dispositionReasonText` when the structured reason is `OTHER` (the cost of missing context on `OTHER` is large; closing the loop in Zod means a SOC 2 reviewer reading the table can always answer "why?" without guessing). Migration `20260523220000_phase2_order_cancellation` adds the table, enum, indexes, FKs, GRANTs to the two app roles, `ENABLE` + `FORCE` row-level security, and the standard `tenant_isolation` policy on the `pharmax.system_context` / `pharmax.organization_id` GUC pair — all in one file, the linter `scripts/check-migration-rls.ts` confirms the RLS pairing. Declarative spec: `lockTarget: { table: "order", by: (i) => ({ id: i.orderId }) }` + `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` + `redactFields: ["dispositionReasonText"]` (the free-text reason MAY carry PHI like "patient passed away on …"; the bus's shallow redactor scrubs it from `command_log.requestPayload`, the audit row carries a `hasReasonText: boolean` instead, and the outbox payload carries the boolean + structured enum but NEVER the text). Inside the handler (after the factory's `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` + policy load): policy-version gate identical to the typing commands (rejects non-`order.standard@v1` as `ORDER_CANCEL_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED`); pure-engine `applyTransition(policy, currentState, "CANCEL")` against the in-memory `ORDER_STANDARD_V1` policy returns the per-source-state `wf.v1.cancel_from_*` transitionId; engine error codes map to typed errors (`WORKFLOW_STATE_TERMINAL` → `ConflictError(ORDER_ALREADY_TERMINAL)` for SHIPPED / CANCELLED, `WORKFLOW_INVALID_TRANSITION` → `ConflictError(ORDER_CANCEL_INVALID_FROM)` as the typed escape hatch if a future v2 policy narrows `CANCEL_FROM_STATES`); `orderCancellation.create` writes the structured row with `cancelledByUserId = ctx.actor.userId`, `cancelledFromStatus` captured BEFORE the status flip (the whole point of the row is letting reports answer "which stage do we lose orders at?"), `workflowPolicyId/Version` for replay correctness, and `commandLogId` as the forensic backpointer; Prisma `P2002` on the `orderId` unique → typed `ConflictError(ORDER_ALREADY_CANCELLED)` (under the row lock this branch should be unreachable, but the constraint protects against future code that forgets to lock). Then one `order.update` flipping `currentStatus → CANCELLED` and nulling `currentAssigneeUserId` (no one is working a cancelled order; the queue UI filters by status so the order disappears from every active queue without a bucket move — `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS` documents this: "CANCELLED is terminal; the order leaves all active queues, so no bucket mapping is needed"); the factory then issues its `bumpVersion` CAS, writes `order_event { eventType: "order.cancelled.v1", sequenceNumber: head+1, … }`, and the bus writes `audit_log { action: "order.cancelled" }` + `event_outbox` + `idempotency_key` in the same tx. **Audit metadata is PHI-free by construction**: `{orderId, cancellationId, fromState, toState, transitionId, dispositionReason, hasReasonText, cancelledByUserId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, commandLogId}`. **Outbox payload** carries `{orderId, organizationId, cancellationId, dispositionReason, hasReasonText, cancelledByUserId, cancelledFromStatus, transitionId, occurredAt}` — downstream consumers (billing event projection, dashboard counts, clinic notification) route on the structured enum + the `cancelledFromStatus` snapshot. New RBAC permission `orders.cancel` added in lockstep across the typed `PERMISSIONS` registry, `PERMISSION_METADATA`, `prisma/seed.ts` (25 codes seeded; the mirror-parity regex from the `add_prescription` work already accepts underscored codes), and granted by default to both `Pharmacist` (final cancellation authority) and `PharmacyTechnician` (operational intake-time cancellation); `OrgAdmin` carries it via the `ALL_PERMS` template. `order.cancelled.v1` → `ORDERS_CANCEL` wired into `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION` so the bus's SoD helper translates the new event correctly when future commands cite this order's history. **SoD invariant**: no `sodRules` declared today — `ORDERS_CANCEL` is not in the SoD registry; cancellation is a corrective/operational action, not a verification step. If a future regulatory regime requires "the actor who cancelled cannot be the one who created" that rule lands in `@pharmax/rbac/separation-of-duties.ts` and surfaces here via `sodRules`. `OrderCancellation` row type + `CancellationDisposition` enum exported from `@pharmax/database` alongside the existing surface. **36 contract tests across `cancel-order.test.ts`** assert: happy path returns `{orderId, cancellationId, currentStatus: "CANCELLED", cancelledFromStatus: "RECEIVED", version: 4, transitionId: "wf.v1.cancel_from_received"}` and writes lock → policy.findUnique(by id) → orderCancellation.create → order.update(status + null assignee, NO bucket, NO version) → order.updateMany(CAS keyed on the locked version) → orderEvent.create(seq = head+1) → auditLog.create → eventOutbox.createMany → idempotencyKey.create in canonical order; the bus-generated `commandLogId` is a ULID and flows into both the cancellation row and audit metadata; **parametric happy path over every from-state in `CANCEL_FROM_STATES`** (14 states: 10 non-terminal forward states + `TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO` + `PV1_REJECTED` + `FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED` + `ON_HOLD`) — each writes the expected `wf.v1.cancel_from_<state>` transitionId and `cancelledFromStatus` matches the source state; explicit `dispositionReasonText` round-trips to the row, is censored from audit JSON (BigInt-aware replacer covers the chain writer's `seq` column), and a `hasReasonText: true` boolean appears in both audit metadata and outbox payload while the literal text appears in NEITHER; whitespace-only `dispositionReasonText` is treated as absent (`hasReasonText: false`, row stores `null`); outbox payload carries scope + reason + fromState + ISO timestamp; audit metadata carries transition + policy + actor + reason without PHI markers; Zod rejects non-UUID `orderId`, unknown `dispositionReason` value (e.g. `"PIZZA"`), `OTHER` without `dispositionReasonText`, `OTHER` with whitespace-only `dispositionReasonText`, and strict-mode extra fields; `OTHER` with non-empty text succeeds and persists the text; lock miss → `ORDER_NOT_FOUND`; `WORKFLOW_POLICY_NOT_FOUND` + `WORKFLOW_POLICY_INACTIVE` (factory-thrown) short-circuit; unsupported policy version → `ORDER_CANCEL_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED`; terminal states (`SHIPPED`, already-`CANCELLED`) → `ORDER_ALREADY_TERMINAL` with zero domain writes (no orderCancellation, no order.update, no order_event, no audit, no outbox); P2002 unique-violation on the cancellation insert → `ORDER_ALREADY_CANCELLED` with zero downstream writes (constructed via real `Prisma.PrismaClientKnownRequestError` for fidelity); factory CAS miss → `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` with the cancellation row and order.update having run (in the fake; the real tx rolls back) but `order_event` / `audit_log` / `event_outbox` NOT written; no tenancy frame → `TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT`; missing `orders.cancel` → `PERMISSION_DENIED` with zero lock attempts. Bus-level idempotency-replay is verified by `packages/command-bus/src/execute-command.test.ts` — this suite asserts the COMMAND-LEVEL guarantee (one cancellation row, one audit, one outbox per successful call; the unique constraint blocks a second attempt structurally).
- [~] Order commands (continued): **`PlaceHold` + `ReleaseHold` shipped** in `@pharmax/orders` — the first **reversible** structured-domain-record pair, complementing the terminal `OrderCancellation` pattern introduced by `CancelOrder`. Lands the **single-row reversible record** convention that the rejection-loop pair (`RejectPV1` → fix → `ResumeAfter…`) and the rework loop (`ReopenForCorrection`) will reuse: one `order_hold` table where the SAME row captures both the placement (held-at / held-by / held-from-status / reason) and the release (released-at / released-by / released-to-status / release-reason), so reports can answer "how long was order X held? by whom? for what reason? released to where?" in one row read instead of joining placement and release tables. **Partial unique index** `order_hold_active_hold_unique ON order_hold(orderId) WHERE releasedAt IS NULL` is the structural anti-double-hold guarantee — Prisma's schema language cannot express this constraint, so it's added directly in the SQL migration (`20260524000000_phase2_order_hold`) and surfaces a P2002 collision as `ORDER_ALREADY_ON_HOLD` (defense-in-depth on top of the workflow engine's `ON_HOLD`-state check, which the row lock already serializes; this catches a hypothetical future bug where the engine guard is bypassed). Multiple historical holds per order are allowed (a long-running order may go on hold three times for three different reasons); only one ACTIVE hold at a time, by structural constraint. New `HoldReason` Postgres enum (`WAITING_FOR_PROVIDER`, `WAITING_FOR_PATIENT`, `WAITING_FOR_INSURANCE`, `INVENTORY_BACKORDER`, `PRESCRIPTION_AMBIGUITY`, `COMPLIANCE_REVIEW`, `DUPLICATE_INVESTIGATION`, `OTHER`) and `HoldReleaseReason` enum (`RESOLVED`, `INFO_RECEIVED`, `ADMIN_OVERRIDE`, `OTHER`) — `OTHER` is the escape hatch and the Zod refine requires non-empty `reasonText` / `releaseReasonText` when the structured reason is `OTHER`, same closed-loop convention as `CancelOrder`. RLS + FORCE-RLS on the new table with the standard `tenant_isolation` policy on the GUC pair — `scripts/check-migration-rls.ts` passes. **Workflow engine wiring**: `PLACE_HOLD` was already expressed as one transition row per source state in `HOLD_FROM_STATES` (14 non-terminal states; `applyTransition` returns `wf.v1.place_hold_from_<state>`); `RELEASE_HOLD` is a parameterized transition from `ON_HOLD` taking `releaseToState` as input and emitting the canonical `wf.v1.release_hold` transitionId. **`PlaceHold` declarative spec**: `lockTarget: { table: "order", by: (i) => ({ id: i.orderId }) }` + `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` + `bumpVersion` + `redactFields: ["reasonText"]` (the free-text reason MAY carry PHI like "patient unreachable since hospitalization on…"; the bus's shallow redactor scrubs `reasonText` from `command_log.requestPayload`, the audit row carries a `hasReasonText: boolean` instead, and the outbox payload carries the boolean + structured enum but NEVER the text). Inside the handler: policy-version gate (`ORDER_PLACE_HOLD_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED` for non-`order.standard@v1`); `applyTransition(policy, currentState, "PLACE_HOLD")` returns the per-source-state `wf.v1.place_hold_from_*` transitionId; engine errors map to typed errors (`WORKFLOW_STATE_TERMINAL` → `ConflictError(ORDER_HOLD_TERMINAL_STATE)` for SHIPPED / CANCELLED, `WORKFLOW_INVALID_TRANSITION` → `ConflictError(ORDER_HOLD_INVALID_FROM)` which is the typed code for already-`ON_HOLD` or any future v2 narrowing of `HOLD_FROM_STATES`); `orderHold.create` writes the row with `heldByUserId = ctx.actor.userId`, `heldFromStatus = target.currentStatus` captured BEFORE the status flip (the whole point of the row is being able to restore exactly this state on release), `workflowPolicyId/Version` for replay correctness, and `placeCommandLogId` as the forensic backpointer; Prisma `P2002` on the partial unique index → typed `ConflictError(ORDER_ALREADY_ON_HOLD)`. Then one `order.update` flipping `currentStatus → ON_HOLD` and nulling `currentAssigneeUserId` (no one is working a held order; **`currentBucketId` is intentionally NOT changed** because the UI filters by `currentStatus` so the order disappears from active queues automatically — preserving the prior bucket lets ReleaseHold restore queue placement on release without a second bucket lookup). The factory's CAS, `order.cancelled.v1`-style `order_event` writeback, audit, outbox, and idempotency row all commit in the same tx. **`ReleaseHold` declarative spec**: same lock/policy/CAS triad + `redactFields: ["releaseReasonText"]` (symmetric PHI redaction). Inside the handler: explicit `target.currentStatus !== ON_HOLD` guard throwing `ORDER_NOT_ON_HOLD` (the engine guard catches the same case but the explicit check produces a more precise error code than the generic invalid-transition); `orderHold.findFirst({orderId, releasedAt: null})` resolves the active hold (the row whose `heldFromStatus` is the restore target); if missing while the order is `ON_HOLD`, throws `ORDER_HOLD_RECORD_CORRUPT` as an `InternalError` (this represents a data-integrity failure — the order's status and the hold table disagree — and should page on-call); `releaseToState = activeHold.heldFromStatus`; `applyTransition(policy, ON_HOLD, "RELEASE_HOLD", { releaseToState })` returns `wf.v1.release_hold` and maps `WORKFLOW_PARAM_INVALID` → `ConflictError(ORDER_RELEASE_INVALID_TARGET)` (defensive: a v2 policy might forbid restoring to a state that's been removed). `orderHold.updateMany({where: {id, releasedAt: null}, data: {releasedAt: clock.now(), releasedByUserId, releasedToStatus, releaseReason, releaseReasonText, releaseCommandLogId}})` is the close-the-hold write — `updateMany + count===1` check detects a concurrent releaser (returns 0 rows because the partial-unique-index NULL constraint was satisfied at lookup time but a sibling tx closed it before our update); on count !== 1, throws `ORDER_NOT_ON_HOLD` because the concurrent writer raced us to release. Then `order.update` restoring `currentStatus → releaseToState` (assignee stays null — whoever picks the order up next claims it via the next-stage Start\* command); the factory's CAS, `order.hold_released.v1` `order_event`, audit, outbox, and idempotency commit together. **Audit metadata is PHI-free by construction** on both sides: PlaceHold `{orderId, holdId, fromState, toState, transitionId, reason, hasReasonText, heldByUserId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, commandLogId}`; ReleaseHold `{orderId, holdId, fromState, toState, transitionId, releaseReason, hasReleaseReasonText, heldByUserId, releasedByUserId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, commandLogId}` — both placer and releaser ids appear so downstream consumers can audit hold-by/release-by handoffs without joining back to the row. **Outbox payloads** mirror audit metadata with scope + ISO timestamp added; `order.held.v1` and `order.hold_released.v1` are the consumer event types and route to dashboard counters + clinic notification + a future "stale hold" alert worker (Phase 3 SLA work). New RBAC permissions `orders.place_hold` + `orders.release_hold` added in lockstep across the typed `PERMISSIONS` registry, `PERMISSION_METADATA`, `prisma/seed.ts` (27 codes seeded; mirror-parity test bumped to 27), and granted by default to both `Pharmacist` and `PharmacyTechnician` role templates (holds are an operational action, not a verification step — both roles can place and release; admins can narrow with override grants if a regulatory regime requires it). `order.held.v1` → `ORDERS_PLACE_HOLD` and `order.hold_released.v1` → `ORDERS_RELEASE_HOLD` wired into `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION` so the bus's SoD helper translates the new events correctly when future commands cite this order's history. **SoD invariant**: no `sodRules` declared on either command — holds are corrective/operational actions, not verification sign-offs; a single tech may both place and release the same hold (the typical happy path: place a hold for "waiting for clinic callback", release it when the clinic calls back). A future SoD rule could be added on ReleaseHold (`forbiddenPriorActs: [PLACE_HOLD]` on the same order) if regulatory review demands it; the path is already in place. `OrderHold` row type + `HoldReason` + `HoldReleaseReason` enums exported from `@pharmax/database`. **73 contract tests total** — `place-hold.test.ts` (37) covers: happy path from all 14 states in `HOLD_FROM_STATES` (parametric `it.each` asserting correct `wf.v1.place_hold_from_<state>` transitionId and `heldFromStatus`); reasonText PHI redaction (literal text appears on the row but NOT in `command_log.requestPayload`, audit, or outbox — `hasReasonText: true/false` boolean substitution); whitespace-only `reasonText` normalizes to null + `hasReasonText: false`; Zod validation (non-UUID `orderId`, unknown `reason`, `OTHER` requires `reasonText`, `OTHER` rejects whitespace-only `reasonText`, strict-mode extra fields); workflow + state failures (`ORDER_NOT_FOUND`, `WORKFLOW_POLICY_NOT_FOUND`, `WORKFLOW_POLICY_INACTIVE`, `ORDER_PLACE_HOLD_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED`, `ORDER_HOLD_INVALID_FROM` when already `ON_HOLD`, `ORDER_HOLD_TERMINAL_STATE` for SHIPPED and CANCELLED, `ORDER_ALREADY_ON_HOLD` via P2002 from the partial unique index — constructed via real `Prisma.PrismaClientKnownRequestError` for fidelity, `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` on CAS miss); tenancy + RBAC (`TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT`, `PERMISSION_DENIED` for missing `ORDERS_PLACE_HOLD`, `ORDERS_RELEASE_HOLD` is NOT a substitute); idempotency (first call writes exactly one hold row, one audit, one outbox, one idempotency key). `release-hold.test.ts` (36) covers: happy path restoring from all 13 valid `heldFromStatus` values (parametric `it.each` asserting `releaseToState = heldFromStatus` and `wf.v1.release_hold` transitionId); both `heldByUserId` and `releasedByUserId` appear in audit + outbox (handoff visibility); optional release without explicit `releaseReason` is accepted (both columns stay null); `releaseReasonText` PHI redaction symmetric to PlaceHold; Zod validation symmetric; workflow + state failures (`ORDER_NOT_FOUND`, `WORKFLOW_POLICY_NOT_FOUND`, `WORKFLOW_POLICY_INACTIVE`, `ORDER_RELEASE_HOLD_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED`, `ORDER_NOT_ON_HOLD` when order isn't currently held OR when a concurrent releaser raced us, `ORDER_HOLD_RECORD_CORRUPT` when order is `ON_HOLD` but no active hold exists, `ORDER_RELEASE_INVALID_TARGET` for engine-rejected restore states, `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` on CAS miss); tenancy + RBAC symmetric; idempotency. The reversible-record pattern is now proven and ready for `ReopenForCorrection` (the next reversible-corrective command) to reuse.
- [x] Order commands (remaining): **`ReopenForCorrection` shipped** in `@pharmax/orders` — migration `20260529000000_phase3_order_correction_reopen` adds append-only `order_correction_reopen` + `ReopenReason` enum. Parameterized `REOPEN_FOR_CORRECTION` from `PV1_REJECTED` or `FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED` back to allowed rework targets; writes structured reopen record, updates bucket + assignee, emits `order.reopened.v1`. RBAC: +1 permission (`orders.reopen_for_correction`, 34 total). **8 contract tests**.
- [~] Verification commands: **`StartTyping` shipped** in new `@pharmax/verification` package — the reference implementation for every subsequent in-flight workflow command (`StartPV1`, `ApprovePV1`, `StartFinalVerification`, `ApproveFinalVerification`, then `Reject*` and `MarkTypingMissingInfo` exception paths). Exercises the `defineCommand` factory's full in-flight path that `CreateOrder` did not: `lockTarget: { table: "order", by: (i) => ({ id: i.orderId }) }` for `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` on the order row before any other write inside the tx, `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` so the factory reads `workflowPolicyId` + `workflowPolicyVersion` off the locked row (replay correctness — an order created under v1 stays under v1 even if v2 is later activated mid-flight), and `bumpVersion: { from: target.version, to: target.version + 1 }` so the factory's `updateMany where: { id, organizationId, version: from }` CAS surfaces concurrent writers as `ConflictError(ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH)` instead of a silent overwrite. **First production use of `@pharmax/workflow::applyTransition`**: handler resolves the in-memory `ORDER_STANDARD_V1` engine policy from the loaded `(code, version)` (rejects unsupported versions as `TYPING_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED` — explicit policy-replay coupling), calls the pure-engine guard against `(currentState, "START_TYPING")`, and maps engine error codes to typed `PharmaxError` instances (`WORKFLOW_STATE_TERMINAL` → `ConflictError(TYPING_ORDER_TERMINAL)`, `WORKFLOW_INVALID_TRANSITION` → `ConflictError(TYPING_INVALID_TRANSITION)`, `WORKFLOW_UNKNOWN_COMMAND` → `InternalError`). Inside the handler (after factory has locked the row + loaded the policy): resolves the per-site `TYPING` bucket directly from `target.siteId` because `LockedOrderTarget` was widened to include `clinicId` + `siteId` alongside the workflow columns (`@pharmax/command-bus` `lockOrderRow` projection extended in lockstep so every in-flight order command gets scope identifiers for free — no extra findUnique round-trip on the locked row); the bucket code is the canonical one for `TYPING_IN_PROGRESS` resolved through `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS` in `@pharmax/workflow` (single source of truth shared with `CreateOrder`'s `RECEIVED → INBOX` lookup — a hardcoded string in either command would let the two drift apart silently); `InternalError(TYPING_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED)` if missing — loud failure beats silently orphaning an order in a nonexistent queue. Then one `order.update` setting `currentStatus = TYPING_IN_PROGRESS`, `currentBucketId = typingBucketId`, `currentAssigneeUserId = ctx.actor.userId` (the version column is intentionally untouched here — the factory's CAS step writes it next in its own `updateMany` so a missed increment surfaces as a stable error code). Audit emits `action: "order.typing.started"` with PHI-free metadata `{orderId, fromState, toState, transitionId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, siteId, bucketIdAfter, typistUserId, commandLogId}`; outbox emits `order.typing.started.v1` carrying `{orderId, organizationId, siteId, typistUserId, bucketId, transitionId, fromState, toState, occurredAt}`. **`ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION`** in `@pharmax/orders` updated to map `order.typing.started.v1` → `TYPING_START` so the bus's SoD helper translates the new event correctly when later commands cite this order's history (this is the first such mapping post-`CreateOrder`'s seed entries). **SoD invariant**: no `sodRules` declared because the registry has no rule with `attempted: TYPING_START` — the typist may be the order's intaker; the SoD constraint that matters is at `PV1_APPROVE` (typist cannot approve their own PV1) and lands when `ApprovePV1` ships. **SLA interval invariant**: this command does NOT yet write `WAIT_BEFORE_TYPING` / `TYPING_ACTIVE` interval rows — the `order_stage_interval` table is explicitly deferred to Phase 3 per the schema comment on `order.slaDeadlineAt`; the per-stage timestamps recorded today (audit `occurredAt`, `order_event.occurredAt`) are sufficient input to backfill that table when it lands. RBAC permission `TYPING_START` was already in the typed registry and seeded; the `PharmacyTechnician` role template already carries the grant — no RBAC migration needed. **16 contract tests across `start-typing.test.ts`** assert: happy path returns `{ orderId, currentStatus: "TYPING_IN_PROGRESS", version: 1, transitionId: "wf.v1.start_typing" }` and writes lock → policy.findUnique(by id) → bucket.findFirst (sited from `target.siteId`, no extra `order.findUnique`) → order.update(state only) → order.updateMany(CAS) → orderEvent.create(seq = head+1) → auditLog.create → eventOutbox.createMany → idempotencyKey.create in the canonical order; CAS keyed on `(id, organizationId, version: 0)` writes `{ version: 1 }` only; `order.update.data` carries no `version` field (proves the handler doesn't shortcut the factory); `orderEvent.sequenceNumber = head + 1` (with head=1 from CreateOrder → seq=2; defensive head=null → seq=1); outbox payload + audit metadata carry the resolved scope + transition identity with zero `firstName`/`lastName`/`dateOfBirth`/`patientId` substrings; Zod rejects non-UUID `orderId` + extra fields under `.strict()` with zero DB writes; lock miss → `ORDER_NOT_FOUND` with zero downstream writes; `WORKFLOW_POLICY_NOT_FOUND` + `WORKFLOW_POLICY_INACTIVE` (factory-thrown) short-circuit with zero `order.update`; unsupported policy version → `TYPING_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED` with zero `order.update`; wrong source state (e.g. `TYPING_IN_PROGRESS`) → `TYPING_INVALID_TRANSITION`; terminal state (`SHIPPED`) → `TYPING_ORDER_TERMINAL`; missing typing bucket → `TYPING_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED`; factory CAS miss (`order.updateMany` returns count=0) → `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` with `order.update` having run but `order_event` / `audit_log` / `event_outbox` NOT written (proves the CAS sits between the handler's state write and the factory's downstream writes); no tenancy frame → `TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT` with zero DB writes; missing `TYPING_START` permission → `PERMISSION_DENIED` with zero lock attempts. - [~] Verification commands (continued): **`CompleteTypingReview` shipped** in `@pharmax/verification` — second instance of the in-flight workflow pattern established by `StartTyping`, proving the `defineCommand` shape generalizes across edges of the same v1 engine (every downstream verification command — `StartPV1`, `ApprovePV1`, `StartFinalVerification`, `ApproveFinalVerification` — is now a mechanical application of this template). RBAC permission `typing.complete` and `order.typing.completed.v1` event-→-permission mapping were already in place from the post-StartTyping seed pass; no permission registry change needed. Declarative spec: same `lockTarget: { table: "order", by: (i) => ({ id: i.orderId }) }` + `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` + `bumpVersion` triad as StartTyping. Inside the handler (after the factory's `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` + policy load): policy-version gate identical to StartTyping (rejects non-`order.standard@v1` as `TYPING_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED` — **shared error code imported from `./start-typing.js`** so operators see ONE stable code per failure class regardless of which typing command surfaced it; same reuse for `TYPING_ORDER_STATE_UNKNOWN`, `TYPING_INVALID_TRANSITION`, `TYPING_ORDER_TERMINAL`). Pure-engine guard against `(currentState, COMPLETE_TYPING_REVIEW)` returns `wf.v1.complete_typing_review` with `fromState: TYPING_IN_PROGRESS`, `toState: TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1`; engine error codes map to typed `PharmaxError` instances exactly as in StartTyping. Destination bucket resolved via `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS.TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1` → `"PV1"` (shared map keeps lookup consistent with `CreateOrder`'s `INBOX` and `StartTyping`'s `TYPING`); missing bucket → command-unique code `PV1_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` because "PV1 bucket missing" vs. "TYPING bucket missing" are different operator remediations and dashboards need to distinguish them. **Assignee-clear semantics** (the unique-to-this-command invariant): `order.update` sets `currentStatus = TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1`, `currentBucketId = pv1BucketId`, **and `currentAssigneeUserId: null`**. The typist is done; the order belongs in the PV1 queue as unassigned so any pharmacist can claim it via `StartPV1` (which will set the assignee to the pharmacist). The historical "typist identity" is preserved on the `order_event` row's `actorUserId` column — clearing the live pointer doesn't destroy the audit record. The current `LockedOrderTarget` projection does NOT include `currentAssigneeUserId`, so the previous-assignee value is NOT recorded on this command's audit/outbox payloads; widening the projection is a cross-cutting change deferred until a future command genuinely needs it (documented in the handler header). Audit emits `action: "order.typing.completed"` with PHI-free metadata `{orderId, fromState, toState, transitionId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, siteId, bucketIdAfter, completedByUserId, commandLogId}`; outbox emits `order.typing.completed.v1` carrying `{orderId, organizationId, siteId, completedByUserId, bucketId, transitionId, fromState, toState, occurredAt}`. **SoD invariant**: no `sodRules` declared — the typist completes their own typing review (that's the point — they assert they typed it correctly). The constraint that matters downstream is `PV1_APPROVE` vs. `TYPING_COMPLETE` by the same actor and lands when `ApprovePV1` ships, against the order's `order_event` history via the bus's SoD helper. **SLA interval invariant**: same as StartTyping — no `order_stage_interval` row yet; Phase 3 will retrofit every command in lockstep to close `TYPING_ACTIVE` and open `WAIT_BEFORE_PV1`. **19 contract tests across `complete-typing-review.test.ts`** assert: happy path returns `{ orderId, currentStatus: "TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1", version: 2, transitionId: "wf.v1.complete_typing_review" }` and writes lock → policy.findUnique(by id) → bucket.findFirst (sited PV1) → order.update(state + bucket + `currentAssigneeUserId: null`) → order.updateMany(CAS keyed on `version=1`, writes `{ version: 2 }`) → orderEvent.create(seq = head+1 = 3 with `head = 2` from StartTyping) → auditLog.create → eventOutbox.createMany → idempotencyKey.create in canonical order; a dedicated assignee-clear test pins `currentAssigneeUserId: null` in the update args so a careless future refactor that leaves the typist assigned fails loudly; outbox payload + audit metadata carry zero `firstName`/`lastName`/`dateOfBirth`/`patientId`/`drugName`/`ndc`/`sig` substrings (BigInt-aware replacer covers the chain writer's `seq` column); defensive head=null → seq=1; Zod rejects non-UUID `orderId` + extra fields under `.strict()` with zero DB writes; lock miss → `ORDER_NOT_FOUND`; `WORKFLOW_POLICY_NOT_FOUND` + `WORKFLOW_POLICY_INACTIVE` (factory-thrown) short-circuit; unsupported policy version → `TYPING_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED`; wrong source state — `RECEIVED` (not yet typing) and `TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1` (already complete; the engine guard catches double-completes that bypass the bus's idempotency key) — both throw `TYPING_INVALID_TRANSITION`; terminal states `SHIPPED` and `CANCELLED` both throw `TYPING_ORDER_TERMINAL`; missing PV1 bucket → `PV1_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` with zero `order.update`; factory CAS miss (`order.updateMany` returns count=0) → `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` with `order.update` having run but `order_event` / `audit_log` / `event_outbox` NOT written; no tenancy frame → `TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT` with zero DB writes; granting `TYPING_START` alone without `TYPING_COMPLETE` → `PERMISSION_DENIED` with zero lock attempts (pins the permission boundary — both grants come together via the `PharmacyTechnician` role template in production, but the bus enforces them independently). - [~] Verification commands (continued): **`StartPV1` shipped** in `@pharmax/verification` — third in-flight verification command and the first that crosses a stage boundary (typist → pharmacist). Structurally identical triad with the typing-stage commands (`lockTarget: { table: "order", by: (i) => ({ id: i.orderId }) }` + `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` + `bumpVersion`), exercising the same pure-engine guard via `@pharmax/workflow::applyTransition` against `(TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1, START_PV1)` to land at `PV1_IN_PROGRESS` via `wf.v1.start_pv1`. **New PV1-stage error vocabulary** (`PV1_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED`, `PV1_INVALID_TRANSITION`, `PV1_ORDER_TERMINAL`, `PV1_ORDER_STATE_UNKNOWN`) introduced here and intended for SHARED reuse by `ApprovePV1` / `RejectPV1` — same "one stable code per failure class per stage" convention the typing stage uses; `PV1_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` is REUSED from `CompleteTypingReview` because both commands resolve the same PV1 bucket and a missing bucket has the same operator remediation. Destination-bucket resolution unconditionally writes `currentBucketId` to the canonical PV1 bucket (resolved via shared `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS.PV1_IN_PROGRESS`) so the column converges to a deterministic end-state even if an admin shuffled buckets between transitions. **Assignee semantics** (symmetric to `StartTyping`): the pharmacist claims the order — `currentAssigneeUserId = ctx.actor.userId`, reversing `CompleteTypingReview`'s assignee-clear. **SoD invariant**: deliberately no `sodRules` declared even though this is the first PV1-stage command. The SoD constraint is on the SIGN-OFF (`PV1_APPROVE`), not on opening the review — a pharmacist may START a PV1 on an order they typed (e.g., to read it and immediately reject for being wrong) but must not APPROVE it; declaring rules here would trigger a useless `order_event` history read for zero enforcement value (the registry has no rule with `attempted: PV1_START`). `ApprovePV1` will be the first `sodRules`-bearing command in the codebase.
