RBAC permission `pv1.start` granted to `Pharmacist` role. **21 contract tests across `start-pv1.test.ts`** cover the same surface as the typing-stage commands (happy path returns + ordered writes, assignee-set, outbox payload, audit-PHI-free, Zod validation, lock miss, policy missing/inactive/unsupported, wrong source states including `TYPING_IN_PROGRESS` and `PV1_IN_PROGRESS`, terminal states `SHIPPED` + `CANCELLED`, missing PV1 bucket, CAS miss, no tenancy frame, missing `PV1_START` permission), plus a dedicated **"no SoD history read"** test that pins exactly one `orderEvent.findFirst` call (the factory's seq+1 lookup, ORDER BY desc LIMIT 1) — proves the absence of `sodRules` actually results in zero history-load overhead, and is the regression guard that catches a future change which silently adds the unnecessary clause. `order.pv1.started.v1` → `PV1_START` wired into `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION` in `@pharmax/orders/events.ts` so `ApprovePV1`'s SoD helper can translate this event when inspecting history. **Sibling housekeeping** done as gate hygiene during this slice (NOT new functional work): (a) added `OrderCancellation` to `TENANT_SCOPED_MODELS` in `@pharmax/tenancy/tenant-scoped-models.ts` to keep the parity test green after the externally-scaffolded `OrderCancellation` Prisma model landed — it carries `organizationId` and is per-order 1:1 with `Order`, so the standard `{organizationId}` filter shape applies; (b) ran `prettier --write` on the externally-scaffolded `packages/orders/src/commands/cancel-order.ts` to unblock the format-check gate (purely cosmetic). Verification chain remaining: `RejectPV1`, `StartFinalVerification`, `ApproveFinalVerification`, `RejectFinalVerification` (plus `MarkTypingMissingInfo` / `ResumeTypingAfterInfoReceived` exception loop).
- [~] **`verification_record` schema** shipped via migration `20260525000000_phase2_verification_record` — the FIRST table written by a workflow command alongside a state transition. Two new Postgres enums (`VerificationStage = {PV1, FINAL}`, `VerificationDecision = {APPROVED, REJECTED}`) plus the `verification_record` table holding one immutable row per pharmacist signoff (Approve OR Reject, PV1 OR Final). One table for BOTH stages: same shape (pharmacist + decision + policy stamp + command log + occurredAt), differs only in WHO can do them (enforced by SoD + RBAC, not by row); splitting would force reporting unions (rejection rate across stages) for no isolation benefit. Multiple rows per `(orderId, stage)` are EXPECTED across rework loops (REJECTED PV1 → typist re-types → APPROVED PV1) so no `(orderId, stage)` unique constraint — the workflow engine prevents double-approve at the state level, not the schema. Per workflow-safety.mdc: every row carries `workflowPolicyId` + `workflowPolicyVersion` (replay-correctness anchor), and every REJECTED row carries a non-null `rejectionReasonCode` enforced by DB CHECK constraint `verification_record_rejection_reason_required` (`decision = 'REJECTED' AND reason IS NOT NULL` OR `decision = 'APPROVED' AND reason IS NULL` — the reason vocabulary is a code string not a Postgres enum so new reasons don't need schema migrations). **IMMUTABLE by THREE-LAYER defense in depth**, mirroring `audit_log`: (1) GRANT only `SELECT, INSERT` to `pharmax_app` + `pharmax_system` (no UPDATE/DELETE), (2) RLS policies cover ONLY `FOR SELECT` and `FOR INSERT` so RLS denies UPDATE/DELETE by absence-of-policy, (3) explicit `REVOKE UPDATE, DELETE` on both app roles so a future "GRANT ALL" regression must explicitly re-grant. Three reporting indexes — `(organizationId, orderId, stage, occurredAt)` for the order timeline, `(organizationId, pharmacistUserId, occurredAt)` for "what did this pharmacist verify today?", and `(organizationId, stage, decision, occurredAt)` for rejection-rate-by-stage. All FKs RESTRICT — an order, user, workflow policy, or command log referenced by a record cannot be deleted. PHI-free by design (free-text pharmacist notes deferred to a future encrypted-column migration; PV1 rejection captures a coded reason, not free text). Registered in `TENANT_SCOPED_MODELS` (now 26 entries with `VerificationRecord` + `OrderHold`).
- [~] Verification commands (continued): **`ApprovePV1` shipped** in `@pharmax/verification` — **the first `sodRules`-bearing command in the codebase AND the first command that writes a structured domain record alongside its state transition**. Wired `order.pv1.approved.v1` → `PV1_APPROVE` into `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION` in `@pharmax/orders/events.ts` so `FINAL_APPROVE`'s future SoD check (the `sod.pv1-final-same-actor` rule's `forbiddenPriorActs: [PV1_APPROVE]`) can translate this event when it lands. Declarative spec: same `lockTarget` + `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` + `bumpVersion` triad as the typing-stage commands, PLUS the new clause `sodRules: [{ attempted: PV1_APPROVE, against: "target", translate: orderEventTypeToPermission }]`. The factory's step 3 (between policy-load and exec) invokes `requireNoSoDViolationForOrder({ tx, orderId, attempted, translate })` which calls `tx.orderEvent.findMany({ where: { orderId }, orderBy: { sequenceNumber: "asc" }, select: { eventType: true, actorUserId: true, sequenceNumber: true }})` and projects each row through `orderEventTypeToPermission`; system-emitted rows (`actorUserId: null`) and rows whose `eventType` is not in the translator are silently skipped (they're not "acts" under SoD); the RBAC `requireNoSoDViolation` then walks the `sod.typing-pv1-same-actor` rule and throws `AuthorizationError(SOD_VIOLATION)` with `{ruleId, attemptedPermission, collidingPriorAct, priorActSequence, resourceRef, actorUserId, organizationId, correlationId}` if the actor about to call ApprovePV1 was the same actor who emitted `order.typing.completed.v1` (translated to `TYPING_COMPLETE`) on this order. The tx rolls back BEFORE the handler's `exec` runs — zero domain mutations, zero new events, zero new audit/outbox rows, zero verification_record writes, zero bucket lookup. **PV1-stage error codes REUSED** from `start-pv1.js` (`PV1_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED`, `PV1_INVALID_TRANSITION`, `PV1_ORDER_TERMINAL`, `PV1_ORDER_STATE_UNKNOWN`). Pure-engine guard against `(currentState, APPROVE_PV1)` returns `wf.v1.approve_pv1` with `fromState: PV1_IN_PROGRESS`, `toState: PV1_APPROVED_READY_FOR_FILL`. Destination bucket: first command in the codebase to resolve the FILL bucket via `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS.PV1_APPROVED_READY_FOR_FILL` → `"FILL"`; missing bucket → **new `FILL_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` code** (will be SHARED with `StartFill` when it ships). **Verification record write**: `tx.verificationRecord.create` runs BEFORE `tx.order.update` (constraint-failure ordering — same tx, both commit-or-rollback atomically, but writing the record first surfaces a CHECK-constraint failure with an obviously-related error rather than "order updated but no record"). The row carries `{stage: PV1, decision: APPROVED, pharmacistUserId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, rejectionReasonCode: null, commandLogId}` — the `null` reason is REQUIRED by the DB CHECK constraint for APPROVED rows; sending a non-null reason fails at INSERT time. The new `verificationRecordId` flows into audit metadata + outbox payload as a forensic backpointer. **Assignee-clear semantics**: symmetric to `CompleteTypingReview` — the pharmacist is done, the order belongs in the FILL queue as unassigned so any tech can claim it via `StartFill`; historical "approving pharmacist" identity preserved on `verification_record.pharmacistUserId` + `order_event.actorUserId` + `audit_log.metadata.approvingPharmacistUserId`. Audit emits `action: "order.pv1.approved"` with PHI-free metadata `{orderId, fromState, toState, transitionId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, siteId, bucketIdAfter, approvingPharmacistUserId, verificationRecordId, commandLogId}`; outbox emits `order.pv1.approved.v1` carrying `{orderId, organizationId, siteId, approvingPharmacistUserId, bucketId, transitionId, fromState, toState, verificationRecordId, occurredAt}`. **24 contract tests across `approve-pv1.test.ts`**: happy path returns `{orderId, currentStatus: "PV1_APPROVED_READY_FOR_FILL", version: 4, transitionId: "wf.v1.approve_pv1", verificationRecordId}` and writes lock → SoD findMany → policy.findUnique → bucket.findFirst(sited FILL) → verificationRecord.create(APPROVED, null reason) → order.update(state+bucket+`currentAssigneeUserId: null`) → order.updateMany(CAS keyed on `version=3`, writes `{version: 4}`) → orderEvent.create(seq = head+1 = 5 with `head = 4` from StartPV1) → auditLog.create → eventOutbox.createMany → idempotencyKey.create in canonical order; dedicated assignee-clear test; dedicated **vr-before-order ordering** test; outbox payload pin; audit-PHI-free pin; **6 dedicated SoD tests**: (1) **history-load shape**: `orderEvent.findMany` fires exactly once with `where: {orderId}`, `orderBy: {sequenceNumber: "asc"}`, and the minimal `select: {eventType, actorUserId, sequenceNumber}` (no payload column, no PHI), (2) **SOD_VIOLATION on same-actor TYPING_COMPLETE**: pharmacist who also completed typing on this order → `AuthorizationError(SOD_VIOLATION)` with metadata pinning `ruleId: "sod.typing-pv1-same-actor"`, `collidingPriorAct: "typing.complete"`, `priorActSequence: "3"`, `resourceRef: "order:<orderId>"`, AND zero downstream writes (no verificationRecord.create, no order.update, no orderEvent.create, no auditLog.create, no eventOutbox.createMany, no bucket.findFirst — proves SoD rolls back BEFORE the handler runs, AND that the pharmacist's "approval intent" must not be persisted when the attempt was forbidden), (3) **different-actor immunity**: typist completed typing under TYPIST_ID, pharmacist now approving under PHARMACIST_ID → happy path, all writes fire, (4) **no-rule-trigger immunity**: history with NO `order.typing.completed.v1` event (legacy/migrated order) → SoD has nothing to forbid, happy path proceeds, (5) **system-event immunity**: history row with `actorUserId: null` and `eventType: order.typing.completed.v1` is correctly skipped by the loader (defensive: a system-emitted event must not falsely trigger SoD), (6) **unmapped-event immunity**: history row with `eventType: order.note.added.v1` (not in the translator) is silently skipped even when performed by the would-be-violating actor — defensive against future informational events. Workflow + scope failure suite: lock miss → `ORDER_NOT_FOUND` with zero `orderEvent.findMany` (SoD never runs because there's no target); `WORKFLOW_POLICY_NOT_FOUND` + `WORKFLOW_POLICY_INACTIVE` (factory step 2 raises BEFORE step 3 SoD) → zero `orderEvent.findMany`; **unsupported policy version → `PV1_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED` raised IN-HANDLER post-SoD**, so `findMany` HAS run for this case — pinned distinctly to prove the factory step ordering (policy-load → SoD → exec) is what the handler observes; wrong source state `TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1` (PV1 not started) and `PV1_APPROVED_READY_FOR_FILL` (already approved; double-approve guard) → `PV1_INVALID_TRANSITION`; terminal `SHIPPED` → `PV1_ORDER_TERMINAL`; missing FILL bucket → `FILL_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` with zero verificationRecord/order writes; CAS miss → `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` with verificationRecord.create AND order.update having run in the fake (real tx rolls back atomically) but `order_event`/`audit_log`/`event_outbox` NOT written downstream; no tenancy → `TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT`; granting `PV1_START` alone without `PV1_APPROVE` → `PERMISSION_DENIED` (per-permission boundary within a single stage — both grants come together via the `Pharmacist` role in production, but the bus enforces them independently).
- [~] Verification commands (continued): **`RejectPV1` shipped** in `@pharmax/verification` — the COUNTERPART to `ApprovePV1` and the rework-loop entry point. Two intentional asymmetries with `ApprovePV1`: (1) **No `sodRules`** — the SoD registry rule `sod.typing-pv1-same-actor` is scoped to `attempted: PV1_APPROVE` only; self-rejection by the typist is HEALTHY self-correction ("I see the typing error I made — bouncing it back to myself") and must be allowed. Adding `sodRules` here would cost an `orderEvent.findMany` per rejection while enforcing nothing (`RULES_BY_ATTEMPTED.get(PV1_REJECT)` returns undefined); a dedicated test pins this absence to prevent the regression. (2) **Destination bucket via exception-state map** — `PV1_REJECTED` is an exception state (not a primary forward state) so it's resolved via the new `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE` companion to `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS`; today it maps `PV1_REJECTED → "TYPING"` (bounce back to typing queue for rework). Missing bucket reuses the `TYPING_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` code (already re-exported from `start-typing.js`) — same operator remediation as a missing typing bucket at any other point. **Reason code registry** in new `rejection-reasons.ts`: frozen `PV1_REJECTION_REASONS` tuple (`DOSE_INCORRECT`, `SIG_AMBIGUOUS`, `MISSING_INFO`, `DATA_ENTRY_ERROR`, `DRUG_INTERACTION`, `ALLERGY_CONFLICT`, `DUPLICATE_THERAPY`, `PRESCRIBER_VERIFICATION_NEEDED`, `INSURANCE_PRIOR_AUTH_REQUIRED`, `DRUG_UNAVAILABLE`, `OTHER`) — STRING list not Postgres enum because reason vocabularies grow per-clinic over time, a code change is cheaper than a schema migration, AND a future per-tenant policy slice can branch on `policy.id` to vary the list (a global Postgres enum couldn't). `as const` + readonly tuple gives compile-time exhaustiveness; `Zod.enum(PV1_REJECTION_REASONS)` at the input boundary surfaces unknown codes as `COMMAND_INPUT_INVALID`; the DB CHECK constraint enforces non-null on REJECTED rows as defense in depth; an `isPV1RejectionReason` type guard + `PV1_REJECTION_REASONS_SET` (O(1) membership) cover code paths that load a reason from a DB row and need to narrow the type. Separate PV1 vs Final registries planned (Final reasons describe FILL errors, different operator audience) — a unified list would be over-broad or generic enough to be useless for reports. Same `lockTarget` + `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` + `bumpVersion` triad. **Verification record write** uses the SAME `verification_record` table as ApprovePV1 with `{stage: PV1, decision: REJECTED, rejectionReasonCode}` (non-null reason REQUIRED by the DB CHECK constraint for REJECTED rows). **Assignee-clear semantics** identical to ApprovePV1 — the pharmacist is done, the order belongs in the TYPING queue as unassigned so any typist can claim it for rework via `StartTyping` (the engine's exception-loop transitions permit this). Audit emits `action: "order.pv1.rejected"` with PHI-free metadata including `rejectionReasonCode` (a stable code, not free text); outbox emits `order.pv1.rejected.v1`. **23 contract tests across `reject-pv1.test.ts`** cover: happy path returns + ordered writes (verificationRecord BEFORE order.update); assignee-clear; reason-code validation (rejects unknown codes via Zod, accepts every frozen code); outbox payload pin; audit-PHI-free pin; **dedicated no-SoD-history-load test** pinning that `orderEvent.findMany` is NEVER called (the factory's seq-next path uses `findFirst`, so the absence of `findMany` proves no SoD wiring was accidentally added); the full set of workflow + scope failures (lock miss, policy missing/inactive/unsupported, wrong source states, terminal states, missing typing bucket, CAS miss, no tenancy, missing `PV1_REJECT` permission). RBAC permission `pv1.reject` already in the typed registry + `Pharmacist` role template from the rbac slice. **Sibling housekeeping** done as gate hygiene during the ApprovePV1/RejectPV1 slice (NOT new functional work): `OrderHold` and `VerificationRecord` registered in `TENANT_SCOPED_MODELS` (now 26 entries); `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE` map added to `@pharmax/workflow/status-bucket-map.ts` alongside the existing primary-state map (introduced by `RejectPV1`, will be SHARED with `RejectFinalVerification`, `MarkTypingMissingInfo`, `PlaceHold`, etc. as each exception-bucketing command lands). Verification chain remaining: `StartFinalVerification`, `ApproveFinalVerification`, `RejectFinalVerification` (plus `MarkTypingMissingInfo` / `ResumeTypingAfterInfoReceived` exception loop).
- [~] Verification commands (continued): **`StartFinalVerification` shipped** in `@pharmax/verification` — **the FIRST FINAL-stage command**, opening the verification loop that closes when `ApproveFinalVerification` releases the order to ship (or `RejectFinalVerification` bounces it back to FILL for rework). Wired `order.final.started.v1 → FINAL_START` into `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION` in `@pharmax/orders/events.ts` so the FINAL stage joins the order-event vocabulary (the `forbiddenPriorActs` lookups on the `sod.pv1-final-same-actor` and `sod.fill-final-same-actor` rules don't reference `FINAL_START`, but the translator entry is in place for future commands that may emit related events). Structurally identical to `StartPV1` (its PV1-stage analog): same `lockTarget: { table: "order", by: (i) => ({ id: i.orderId }) }` + `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` + `bumpVersion` triad, different edge of the same v1 engine — pure-engine guard against `(currentState, START_FINAL_VERIFICATION)` returns `wf.v1.start_final_verification` with `fromState: FILL_COMPLETED_READY_FOR_FINAL`, `toState: FINAL_VERIFICATION_IN_PROGRESS`. **FINAL-stage error vocabulary introduced** (`FINAL_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED`, `FINAL_ORDER_STATE_UNKNOWN`, `FINAL_INVALID_TRANSITION`, `FINAL_ORDER_TERMINAL`) — to be REUSED by `ApproveFinalVerification` and `RejectFinalVerification` (same "one stable code per failure class per stage" convention as the typing and PV1 stages let callers stably distinguish "the FINAL-stage handlers don't recognize this policy" from "the PV1-stage handlers don't"). **`FINAL_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` introduced** for the destination-bucket misconfiguration, paralleling `PV1_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` / `FILL_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED`; will be REUSED by the FINAL-stage siblings ONLY for the failure mode where the FINAL bucket itself is missing (Approve resolves the SHIPPING bucket, Reject resolves the FILL bucket — those will introduce their own per-destination codes, since operators reading dashboards need to know WHICH bucket the site is missing). Destination bucket: `FINAL_VERIFICATION_IN_PROGRESS → "FINAL"` from the shared `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS` map; same bucket on both sides of this transition (the order is already sitting in FINAL on entry from `FILL_COMPLETED_READY_FOR_FINAL`), but the lookup still runs because the shared map is the source of truth and writing `currentBucketId` unconditionally keeps the column in a deterministic end-state if an admin re-pointed a bucket mid-flight. **Assignee-SET semantics** (symmetric to `StartPV1`): `CompleteFill` (when it lands) will clear the assignee to NULL when the order enters the FINAL queue; this command sets it to `ctx.actor.userId` so the pharmacist owns the order until `ApproveFinalVerification` / `RejectFinalVerification` / `PlaceHold`. **SoD asymmetry — the load-bearing design point** (same antipattern guard as `StartPV1` and `RejectPV1`): the SoD registry has TWO rules whose `attempted` is `FINAL_APPROVE` (`sod.pv1-final-same-actor` forbids prior `PV1_APPROVE` by the same actor; `sod.fill-final-same-actor` forbids prior `FILL_COMPLETE` by the same actor) but ZERO rules for `attempted: FINAL_START`. The two-pharmacist invariant is enforced at SIGN-OFF, NOT at OPEN-REVIEW — a pharmacist who PV1-approved an order CAN open it for final review (to coach a junior, or to notice an upstream error worth rejecting), but CANNOT sign off. This command therefore has NO `sodRules` clause; declaring one would cost an `orderEvent.findMany` per start with zero enforcement value (`RULES_BY_ATTEMPTED.get(FINAL_START)` returns undefined). A dedicated test asserts that `orderEvent.findMany` is never called (only `findFirst` for the factory's seq-next path runs), preventing a future maintainer from "symmetrically" adding `sodRules` here. Audit emits `action: "order.final.started"` with PHI-free metadata `{orderId, fromState, toState, transitionId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, siteId, bucketIdAfter, pharmacistUserId, commandLogId}`; outbox emits `order.final.started.v1` carrying `{orderId, organizationId, siteId, pharmacistUserId, bucketId, transitionId, fromState, toState, occurredAt}`. **27 contract tests across `start-final-verification.test.ts`**: happy path returns `{orderId, currentStatus: "FINAL_VERIFICATION_IN_PROGRESS", version: 7, transitionId: "wf.v1.start_final_verification"}` and writes lock → policy.findUnique → bucket.findFirst(sited FINAL) → order.update(state+bucket+`currentAssigneeUserId: PHARMACIST_ID`) → order.updateMany(CAS keyed on `version=6`, writes `{version: 7}`) → orderEvent.create(seq = head+1 = 8 from `head = 7` post-CompleteFill) → auditLog.create → eventOutbox.createMany → idempotencyKey.create in canonical order; dedicated assignee-SET test; defensive seq=1 test for null event-head; outbox payload pin; audit-PHI-free pin; **dedicated no-SoD-history-load test** pinning that `orderEvent.findMany` is NEVER called and that `findFirst` is the ONLY `orderEvent` read (the factory's seq-next path); workflow + scope failure suite covering FOUR pre-FILL source states (`RECEIVED`, `PV1_IN_PROGRESS`, `PV1_APPROVED_READY_FOR_FILL`, `FILL_IN_PROGRESS`) — explicitly pinning "No final verification before fill completion" per workflow-safety.mdc as the v1 policy gating that the command surfaces as `FINAL_INVALID_TRANSITION`, plus one PV1-rework exception state (`PV1_REJECTED`) for the rework-loop guard; double-start guard (already `FINAL_VERIFICATION_IN_PROGRESS`) and double-approve guard (`FINAL_VERIFICATION_APPROVED_READY_FOR_SHIP`) also surface `FINAL_INVALID_TRANSITION` (the latter pins that a retry post-approval cannot re-open the review and override the prior sign-off — `ReleaseToShip` is the only legal next step); both terminal states (`SHIPPED`, `CANCELLED`) surface `FINAL_ORDER_TERMINAL`, missing FINAL bucket surfaces `FINAL_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` with zero downstream writes, CAS miss surfaces `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` with `order.update` having run in the fake (real tx rolls back atomically) but `order_event`/`audit_log`/`event_outbox` NOT written downstream; **per-permission boundary tests** — granting `FINAL_APPROVE` alone (intra-stage), `FINAL_REJECT` alone (intra-stage), AND `PV1_APPROVE` alone (cross-stage) ALL surface `PERMISSION_DENIED` with zero lock attempt, pinning that the bus enforces `FINAL_START` independently so a "reviewer" role (start-only, no sign-off) is expressible without `Pharmacist` template inheritance AND that a PV1-only pharmacist cannot open a FINAL review (cross-stage isolation important for ramp-up or compliance-driven SoD policies); no-tenancy surfaces `TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT`. RBAC permission `final.start` already in the typed registry + `Pharmacist` role template + seed from the rbac slice. **Sibling housekeeping** done as gate hygiene during this slice (NOT new functional work): (a) prettier formatting fixed on `scripts/check-prisma-schema.ts` + `scripts/check-prisma-schema.test.ts` (externally scaffolded files that landed without running through the formatter), (b) one-line typecheck fix in `scripts/check-prisma-schema.ts` to make Prisma's DMMF `relationOnDelete: string | undefined` projection compatible with `ModelLike.relationOnDelete?: string` under `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` (conditional spread — semantically equivalent, just respects the "absent when not relevant" contract on the optional property). FINAL chain remaining: `ApproveFinalVerification` (TWO `sodRules` clauses — first command with multi-rule SoD; FIRST writer of `verification_record` for the FINAL stage AND first writer of a SHIPPING-bucket transition; releases order to ship via `(FINAL_VERIFICATION_IN_PROGRESS, APPROVE_FINAL_VERIFICATION) → FINAL_VERIFICATION_APPROVED_READY_FOR_SHIP`) and `RejectFinalVerification` (no `sodRules` — self-rejection is healthy self-correction, same asymmetry as `RejectPV1`; writes `verification_record` with `stage: FINAL, decision: REJECTED`; introduces `FINAL_REJECTION_REASONS` registry sibling to `PV1_REJECTION_REASONS`; destination bucket via `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE` extension mapping `FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED → "FILL"` for the rework loop back to fill).
- [~] Verification commands (continued): **`ApproveFinalVerification` shipped** in `@pharmax/verification` — **THE LAST SAFETY GATE BEFORE A DRUG LEAVES THE BUILDING** and the codebase's first **multi-rule SoD** command, first **FINAL-stage `verification_record` writer**, and first writer of a **SHIPPING-bucket transition**. Wired `order.final.approved.v1 → FINAL_APPROVE` AND `order.fill.completed.v1 → FILL_COMPLETE` into `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION` in `@pharmax/orders/events.ts` — `FILL_COMPLETE` is wired AHEAD of the FILL-stage command (`CompleteFill` ships later) because `ApproveFinalVerification` needs to detect a prior `order.fill.completed.v1` by the same actor to fire `sod.fill-final-same-actor`; the entry costs nothing until a real CompleteFill event lands in some order's history, and pre-wiring keeps the translator complete the moment that command ships. **Multi-rule SoD design — the load-bearing new pattern**: the rbac registry has TWO rules whose `attempted` is `FINAL_APPROVE` (`sod.pv1-final-same-actor` forbids prior `PV1_APPROVE` by same actor; `sod.fill-final-same-actor` forbids prior `FILL_COMPLETE` by same actor), but the handler declares a SINGLE `sodRules: [{ attempted: FINAL_APPROVE, against: "target", translate: orderEventTypeToPermission }]` entry — `requireNoSoDViolation` (in `@pharmax/rbac/separation-of-duties.ts`) walks ALL registry rules matching `attempted` in one pass against the loaded history (`RULES_BY_ATTEMPTED.get(FINAL_APPROVE)` returns both rules in declaration order). Declaring TWO `sodRules` entries here would have doubled the `orderEvent.findMany` cost with zero enforcement gain — the bus's `for (const rule of spec.sodRules)` loop calls `requireNoSoDViolationForOrder` once per entry, and that helper loads history independently per call; the multi-rule fan-out lives in the registry, by design. A dedicated test asserts `findMany` fires exactly ONCE, pinning this efficiency invariant against a future "let's add another sodRules clause for clarity" regression. **Deterministic rule-firing order**: when BOTH `PV1_APPROVE` and `FILL_COMPLETE` by the same actor exist in history, the registry's declaration order (`sod.pv1-final-same-actor` first, `sod.fill-final-same-actor` second) determines which violation surfaces — `sod.pv1-final-same-actor` wins. A dedicated test pins this so any future re-ordering of `RULES` is a tracked surface-area change (clients display `ruleId` to operators and audit log it; the surfaced code must be stable). Same `lockTarget` + `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` + `bumpVersion` triad as the rest of the verification stack. **FINAL-stage error vocabulary REUSED** from `start-final-verification.js` (`FINAL_POLICY_UNSUPPORTED`, `FINAL_INVALID_TRANSITION`, `FINAL_ORDER_TERMINAL`, `FINAL_ORDER_STATE_UNKNOWN`) — same "one stable code per failure class per stage" convention the typing and PV1 stages established. **`SHIPPING_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` introduced** — the FIRST SHIPPING-bucket resolution in the codebase; will be SHARED with `ReleaseToShip` and `ConfirmShipment` when those land (all three resolve the same site-scoped `"SHIPPING"` bucket from `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS.FINAL_VERIFICATION_APPROVED_READY_FOR_SHIP`, so operator remediation is identical regardless of which command surfaces it). Destination bucket: `FINAL_VERIFICATION_APPROVED_READY_FOR_SHIP → "SHIPPING"`. **`verification_record` write** uses the same table as ApprovePV1/RejectPV1 with `{stage: FINAL, decision: APPROVED, rejectionReasonCode: null}` (null reason REQUIRED by DB CHECK constraint for APPROVED rows) — single GROUP BY on the already-indexed table now yields FINAL-stage rejection-rate-by-pharmacist reports out of the box. **Constraint-failure ordering** symmetric to ApprovePV1: `verificationRecord.create` BEFORE `order.update` so a CHECK failure surfaces a record-shaped error rather than an "order updated but no record" inconsistency (atomicity is the same — single tx — but ordering matters for diagnosis). **Assignee-clear semantics** symmetric to ApprovePV1: the approving pharmacist is done, the order belongs in the SHIPPING queue as unassigned so any shipping clerk can claim it via `ReleaseToShip`; the pharmacist's identity is preserved on `verification_record.pharmacistUserId`, `order_event.actorUserId`, and `audit_log.metadata.approvingPharmacistUserId`. Audit emits `action: "order.final.approved"` with PHI-free metadata `{orderId, fromState, toState, transitionId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, siteId, bucketIdAfter, approvingPharmacistUserId, verificationRecordId, commandLogId}`; outbox emits `order.final.approved.v1` carrying `{orderId, organizationId, siteId, approvingPharmacistUserId, bucketId, transitionId, fromState, toState, verificationRecordId, occurredAt}`. **Operational consequence pinned in handler comment**: the outbox event is the trigger for downstream label-generation workers — the handler does NOT generate shipping labels directly (workflow state lives in the bus; side effects live in workers); the worker subscribes to `order.final.approved.v1`, validates Rx-label existence, and queues shipping-label generation. Separation of concerns + correlationId-linked audit chain across the boundary. **28 contract tests across `approve-final-verification.test.ts`**: happy path returns `{orderId, currentStatus: "FINAL_VERIFICATION_APPROVED_READY_FOR_SHIP", version: 8, transitionId: "wf.v1.approve_final_verification", verificationRecordId}` and writes lock → policy.findUnique → orderEvent.findMany(SoD load) → bucket.findFirst(sited SHIPPING) → verificationRecord.create(stage: FINAL + null reasonCode) → order.update(state + bucket + assignee-CLEAR) → order.updateMany(CAS keyed on version=7, writes {version: 8}) → orderEvent.create(seq = head+1 = 8) → auditLog.create → eventOutbox.createMany → idempotencyKey.create in canonical order; verification_record-before-order.update ordering pin; assignee-clear pin; outbox payload pin; audit-PHI-free pin; **dedicated single-findMany-call pin** (the multi-rule efficiency invariant); **SoD violation pinned for sod.pv1-final-same-actor** (PHARMACIST_B previously approved PV1, now tries final) with full `metadata: {ruleId, attemptedPermission: "final.approve", collidingPriorAct: "pv1.approve", priorActSequence, resourceRef, actorUserId, organizationId, correlationId}` shape + zero downstream writes (no record, no order update, no events, no audit, no outbox, no bucket lookup); **SoD violation pinned for sod.fill-final-same-actor** (PHARMACIST_B previously completed fill, now tries final) — independent rule, same shape; **dual-violation deterministic-ordering pin** (when BOTH forbidden prior acts by the same actor exist, `sod.pv1-final-same-actor` wins because it's first in `RULES`); different-actor immunity (the healthy three-actor default chain — PHARMACIST_A approved PV1, FILL_TECH completed fill, PHARMACIST_B approves final — proceeds normally); sparse-history (degenerate replay shape) doesn't raise; system-emitted prior acts (`actorUserId: null`) skipped; unmapped events (e.g. `order.note.added.v1`) skipped; full workflow + scope failure suite covering wrong source states (`FILL_COMPLETED_READY_FOR_FINAL` pinning "no FINAL approve before FINAL start", already-approved double-approve guard, `PV1_REJECTED` exception-state guard), terminal `SHIPPED` state, missing SHIPPING bucket, CAS miss with verification_record + order.update having run in the fake (real tx rolls back atomically) but order_event/audit/outbox NOT written downstream; **cross-stage permission isolation** test (`PV1_APPROVE` alone surfaces `PERMISSION_DENIED` — PV1 perms don't carry into FINAL stage); intra-stage permission isolation (`FINAL_START` alone surfaces `PERMISSION_DENIED` — a reviewer role expressible without sign-off); no-tenancy surfaces `TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT`. RBAC permission `final.approve` already in the typed registry + `Pharmacist` role template + seed from the rbac slice. **Sibling housekeeping** done as gate hygiene during this slice (NOT new functional work): prettier formatting fixed on `packages/integration-tests/src/lib/db.ts`, `packages/integration-tests/src/lib/seed.ts`, `packages/integration-tests/src/verification-record.test.ts`, and `scripts/check-command-files.ts` (externally scaffolded files that landed without running through the formatter); lockfile sync for the new `@pharmax/integration-tests` workspace package. FINAL chain remaining: `RejectFinalVerification` (no `sodRules` — self-rejection is healthy self-correction, same asymmetry as `RejectPV1`; writes `verification_record` with `{stage: FINAL, decision: REJECTED}`; introduces `FINAL_REJECTION_REASONS` registry sibling to `PV1_REJECTION_REASONS`; destination bucket via `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE` extension mapping `FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED → "FILL"` for the rework loop back to fill).
- [~] Verification commands (continued): **`RejectFinalVerification` shipped** in `@pharmax/verification` — **THE VERIFICATION SUITE IS COMPLETE.** The pharmacist refuses to release the FILLED vial and bounces the order back to FILL for rework (wrong drug pulled, wrong strength, expired/held lot, damaged label, etc.). Wired `order.final.rejected.v1 → FINAL_REJECT` into `ORDER_EVENT_TYPE_TO_PERMISSION` in `@pharmax/orders/events.ts` so the FINAL stage's event vocabulary is now fully wired (4 of 4: started/approved/rejected, plus the cross-stage `fill.completed` translator entry from the ApproveFinalVerification slice). **THREE intentional asymmetries** worth pinning here (and pinned in the handler header + dedicated tests): (1) **No `sodRules` — same self-correction pattern as `RejectPV1`**: the SoD registry rules `sod.pv1-final-same-actor` and `sod.fill-final-same-actor` are scoped to `attempted: FINAL_APPROVE`, NOT `FINAL_REJECT`. A pharmacist who PV1-approved or completed-the-fill on the order MAY (and operationally SHOULD) be allowed to spot their own error mid-final-review and reject the order — forbidding self-rejection would push the actor toward "approve anyway and ask someone to fix it later", the worst possible outcome (wrong drug ships). The handler therefore has no `sodRules` clause; `RULES_BY_ATTEMPTED.get(FINAL_REJECT)` returns undefined and the factory's step-3 SoD load is correctly skipped. A dedicated test pins the absence of `orderEvent.findMany` (only `findFirst` for the factory's seq-next path runs) to prevent a future maintainer from "symmetrically" adding SoD here. (2) **Destination bucket is "FILL", NOT "TYPING" like `RejectPV1`**: by the time the order reaches `FINAL_VERIFICATION_IN_PROGRESS`, typing AND PV1 have both already passed — the prescription itself is correct. What failed at final review is the PHYSICAL FILL (wrong NDC pulled from inventory, wrong strength, expired lot assigned, label damaged, etc.). Routing back to typing would force a typist to re-validate an already-validated prescription; routing back to PV1 would force the PV1 pharmacist to re-approve work they already approved. The work to redo is the fill, so the order lands in the FILL bucket as unassigned via the new `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE` entry `FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED → "FILL"` (this slice closes the last remaining "[~] not yet mapped" entry in the exception-state map — only `TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO` and `ON_HOLD` remain). Missing bucket REUSES the `FILL_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` code from `approve-pv1.ts` — same operator remediation as any other command that needs the FILL bucket, so the operator dashboard surfaces a single actionable "this site needs a FILL bucket seeded" error regardless of which command tripped it. (3) **Different reason-code registry — `FINAL_REJECTION_REASONS` sibling to `PV1_REJECTION_REASONS`**: FILL-error vocabulary, different operator audience (fill tech, not typist), different compliance ties. Codes are `WRONG_DRUG_PULLED`, `WRONG_STRENGTH`, `WRONG_QUANTITY`, `LABEL_INCORRECT`, `LABEL_DAMAGED`, `EXPIRED_LOT_ASSIGNED`, `HELD_LOT_ASSIGNED`, `MISSING_AUXILIARY_LABEL`, `VIAL_INTEGRITY`, `WRONG_PATIENT_ASSIGNED`, `OTHER`. **Three codes pin specific workflow-safety rules from `.cursor/rules/01-workflow-safety.mdc`**: `EXPIRED_LOT_ASSIGNED` is the "No expired lot assignment" rule (the upstream `AssignLot` should reject expired lots at input, but this code exists for the case where a lot expired between assignment and final review), `HELD_LOT_ASSIGNED` is the "No held lot assignment" rule, and `LABEL_DAMAGED` covers "No silent printer failures" reaching the vial — so an audit query "how many `LABEL_DAMAGED` rejections this month?" doubles as a printer-reliability KPI. Same frozen-tuple-as-Zod-enum pattern as `PV1_REJECTION_REASONS` (same `as const` + `ReadonlySet` + `isFinalRejectionReason` type-guard triplet), same per-tenant-policy override potential. **Cross-registry input guard pinned by dedicated test**: sending a PV1-stage code like `DOSE_INCORRECT` to `RejectFinalVerification` surfaces `COMMAND_INPUT_INVALID` at the Zod boundary (the two registries look alike, and a `DOSE_INCORRECT` at FINAL stage is semantically wrong since typing already passed PV1; most importantly, an API-layer transposition that sends a PV1 code to a FINAL rejection would otherwise commit a meaningless rejection with no operator signal). Same `lockTarget` + `loadPolicy: { from: "target" }` + `bumpVersion` triad as the rest of the verification stack. **`verification_record` write** completes the `(stage, decision)` matrix in the table — now all four combinations `(PV1, APPROVED)`, `(PV1, REJECTED)`, `(FINAL, APPROVED)`, `(FINAL, REJECTED)` are written by production commands, so reporting can answer "rejection rate by stage by pharmacist by month" with a single GROUP BY off the already-indexed table. **Constraint-failure ordering** symmetric to every other verification command: `verificationRecord.create` BEFORE `order.update`. **Assignee-clear semantics** symmetric to `ApproveFinalVerification`: order belongs back in FILL queue as unassigned so any tech can pick it up. Audit emits `action: "order.final.rejected"` with PHI-free metadata `{orderId, fromState, toState, transitionId, workflowPolicyId, workflowPolicyVersion, siteId, bucketIdAfter, rejectingPharmacistUserId, reasonCode, verificationRecordId, commandLogId}`; outbox emits `order.final.rejected.v1` carrying `{orderId, organizationId, siteId, rejectingPharmacistUserId, bucketId, transitionId, fromState, toState, reasonCode, verificationRecordId, occurredAt}`. **26 contract tests across `reject-final-verification.test.ts`**: happy path returns `{orderId, currentStatus: "FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED", version: 8, transitionId: "wf.v1.reject_final_verification", verificationRecordId, reasonCode: "WRONG_DRUG_PULLED"}` and writes lock → policy.findUnique → bucket.findFirst(sited FILL) → verificationRecord.create(REJECTED, non-null reasonCode) → order.update(state+bucket+assignee-CLEAR) → order.updateMany(CAS keyed on `version=7`, writes `{version: 8}`) → orderEvent.create(seq = head+1 = 8) → auditLog.create → eventOutbox.createMany → idempotencyKey.create in canonical order; verification_record-before-order ordering pin; assignee-clear pin; outbox payload pin; audit-PHI-free pin; **dedicated FINAL_REJECTION_REASONS smoke test** that loops over every code in the frozen list and asserts each round-trips through Zod and lands on the verification_record (catches future "added a code to the registry but forgot to update Zod" regressions); **dedicated no-SoD-history-load test** pinning that `orderEvent.findMany` is NEVER called and that `findFirst` is the ONLY `orderEvent` read; **dedicated self-rejection-allowed test** asserting the happy path completes regardless of actor identity; full input-validation suite covering non-UUID orderId, unknown reasonCode, missing reasonCode, extra fields under strict schema, AND the **cross-registry guard** (sending `DOSE_INCORRECT` — a valid PV1 code — to FINAL surfaces `COMMAND_INPUT_INVALID`); full workflow + scope failure suite covering wrong source states (`FILL_COMPLETED_READY_FOR_FINAL` pinning "no FINAL reject before FINAL start"; `FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED` double-reject guard; `FINAL_VERIFICATION_APPROVED_READY_FOR_SHIP` retract-after-approval guard — pins that a pharmacist CANNOT undo an approval by rejecting after-the-fact, because the two-pharmacist sign-off is immutable and the remediation for a post-approval issue is `CancelOrder` + recall, NOT a surreptitious rejection that bypasses the audit trail), terminal `SHIPPED` state surfaces `FINAL_ORDER_TERMINAL`, missing FILL bucket surfaces `FILL_BUCKET_NOT_CONFIGURED` with zero record/order writes, CAS miss surfaces `ORDER_VERSION_MISMATCH` with verification_record + order.update having run in the fake (real tx rolls back atomically) but order_event/audit/outbox NOT written downstream; **cross-stage permission isolation test** (`PV1_REJECT` alone surfaces `PERMISSION_DENIED` — PV1 perms don't carry into FINAL stage, mirroring the `ApproveFinalVerification` cross-stage isolation); intra-stage permission isolation (`FINAL_APPROVE` alone surfaces `PERMISSION_DENIED` — pins that a hypothetical "approver-only" or "rejector-only" sub-role is expressible at the FINAL stage too); no-tenancy surfaces `TENANCY_NO_CONTEXT`. RBAC permission `final.reject` already in the typed registry + `Pharmacist` role template + seed from the rbac slice. **Sibling housekeeping** done as gate hygiene during this slice (NOT new functional work): prettier formatting fixed on `packages/orgs/src/commands/provision-default-buckets.test.ts`, `packages/orgs/src/commands/create-organization.test.ts`, and `scripts/bootstrap-org.ts` (externally scaffolded files that landed without running through the formatter). **Verification suite now complete** — every state-machine edge in the `order.standard@v1` policy that touches verification (TYPING through FINAL, both approve and reject branches, both start and complete sides) is shipped under `defineCommand` with audit-chain + outbox + RBAC + SoD where applicable + PHI-safe metadata + comprehensive contract tests. Next major milestone: FILL stage (`StartFill`, `AssignLot`, `CompleteFill`) — at which point the `order.fill.started.v1` / `order.fill.completed.v1` translator entries become live, the `sod.fill-final-same-actor` rule starts firing on real history, and the `EXPIRED_LOT_ASSIGNED` / `HELD_LOT_ASSIGNED` rejection codes here gain real upstream prevention via `AssignLot`'s lot-status guard.
- [x] **Tier 1 hardening — schema linter, command linter, DB integration test harness, ProvisionDefaultBuckets, end-to-end bootstrap closed-loop.** Lands the foundational guardrails that every subsequent command and migration is checked against, plus the missing piece that lets a freshly bootstrapped org accept its first order. **Schema linter (`scripts/check-prisma-schema.ts`)** walks both `Prisma.dmmf.datamodel.models` AND the raw `schema.prisma` text (dmmf intentionally omits non-unique `@@index` declarations, so structural rules over indexes need the raw source) and enforces seven rules: R1 `@@map` is snake_case; R2 tenant-scoped models declare `organizationId`; R3 every tenant-scoped index leads with `organizationId`; R4 only relations targeting `Organization` are restricted from `onDelete: Cascade` (junction tables like `InvoiceLine → Invoice` keep cascades legitimately); R5 `status` fields are typed by their dedicated enum, not `String`; R6 `*Bi` blind-index columns pair with either an `*Enc` envelope sibling (PHI hash) or a plaintext `String` sibling (search-normalization hash like `rxNumberBi` paired with `rxNumber`); R7 the `Patient`, `Prescription`, `Order` triangle uses the `(table, column) → BI purpose` registry from `@pharmax/database/phi`. Caught and fixed the `IdempotencyKey.organization` relation that was using `Cascade` — promoted to `Restrict` in migration `20260526000000_idempotency_key_restrict_fk` so an org deletion must force an explicit shred path with audit trail rather than silently destroying idempotency state. Wired into `pnpm verify`. **Command linter (`scripts/check-command-files.ts`)** walks every file under `packages/*/src/commands/*.ts` (excluding tests) via the TypeScript AST and asserts each exports one of three valid shapes: a `defineCommand(...)` call, an `export const Foo: Command<...> = { … }` typed object, or an `export const Foo: SystemCommand<...> = { … }` typed object — catches the next "I'll just write a plain function in commands/" PR at editor-squiggle time. Currently 17 command files. Wired into `pnpm verify`. **DB integration test harness (`packages/integration-tests`)** is a dedicated workspace member using `vitest` + the `pg` node driver directly (NOT Prisma) so tests can issue `SET ROLE pharmax_app`, `SET LOCAL pharmax.organization_id`, and inspect failures at the raw SQL layer. Vitest config pins `singleFork: true` (session GUCs and advisory locks don't tolerate parallel forks against the same DB); the harness exposes `connect()`, `withClient()`, `setTenantContext()`, `setSystemContext()`, `clearContext()`, and `assertSchemaReady()` (the last surfacing actionable errors on `ECONNREFUSED` so the operator knows to start Docker before re-running). Tests run via dedicated `pnpm test:integration` script and are EXCLUDED from the default `pnpm test` so unit tests stay fast and DB-free. **First integration test suite (`verification-record.test.ts`)** locks in the verification-record DB invariants: (a) RLS blocks cross-tenant SELECT as `pharmax_app` even when the row exists, (b) RLS allows same-tenant SELECT when the GUC is set correctly (regression sentinel against accidental policy-drop), (c) `REVOKE UPDATE, DELETE` denies both operations to `pharmax_app` AND `pharmax_system` (defense in depth: `pharmax_system` is `BYPASSRLS` but explicit revokes are not bypassed), (d) the `verification_record_rejection_reason_required` CHECK constraint rejects every illegal `(decision, reason)` combination (APPROVED-with-reason, REJECTED-without-reason, REJECTED-with-empty-string-reason) and accepts every legal one — the same constraint that the Approve/Reject command pair relies on for "non-null reason on REJECTED rows" to be a structural guarantee rather than a wishful application-level assertion. **`ProvisionDefaultBuckets` SystemCommand** in `@pharmax/orgs` is the idempotent bucket-provisioning entry point — accepts `{organizationId, siteId}`, verifies the site belongs to the org (cross-org wiring → `ValidationError(PROVISION_BUCKETS_SITE_ORG_MISMATCH)`, missing site → `NotFoundError(PROVISION_BUCKETS_SITE_NOT_FOUND)`), then upserts seven canonical buckets (`INBOX`, `TYPING`, `PV1`, `FILL`, `FINAL`, `SHIPPING`, `EMERGENCY` — the last with `kind: EMERGENCY`, the rest `WORKFLOW`) keyed on the live `(organizationId, code)` unique constraint. Idempotent by construction: an existing row is left untouched (operator-readable counts are returned as `{created, alreadyPresent}` so a backfill run reports "0 created, 7 already present"); the returned `bucketIdsByCode` map is always complete, with a defensive `InternalError(PROVISION_BUCKETS_INCOMPLETE)` if any canonical code somehow lacks an id (this should be unreachable but failing loud here beats orphaning an order in a nonexistent queue under load). Canonical order in `CANONICAL_BUCKETS` determines `sortOrder` in steps of 10, leaving room for admins to insert custom buckets between defaults (`sortOrder: 15` slots between INBOX and TYPING) without renumbering. **Workflow-map coverage regression test** asserts every code referenced by `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS` AND `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE` is in `DEFAULT_BUCKET_CODES` — so a future state→bucket entry that adds a new code forces an update to the canonical provisioning set, eliminating the failure mode where a new state lands orders in a non-existent bucket. Reusable transaction-scoped helper `provisionDefaultBucketsForSite(tx, {organizationId, siteId})` is the single SQL writer that BOTH the SystemCommand AND `CreateOrganization`'s `initialSite` path dispatch to — same site validation, same upserts, same `sortOrder` stepping — so on-disk shape is identical regardless of which entry point provisioned the buckets. Audit emits `action: "org.buckets.provisioned"` with metadata `{siteId, organizationId, created, alreadyPresent, commandLogId, occurredAt}`; outbox emits `org.buckets.provisioned.v1`. 12 contract tests cover happy path (7 buckets created on first run), idempotency (second run is `{created: 0, alreadyPresent: 7}` with no `bucket.create` calls), mixed state (some pre-existing → only missing are created, returned map is still complete), site validation (missing → `NotFoundError`, cross-org → `ValidationError`), audit/outbox shape, and the workflow-map coverage regression. **`CreateOrganization` end-to-end bootstrap closure** — added optional `initialSite: {code, name, timezone?}` to the command input; when provided, the handler creates a `PharmacySite` row (status ACTIVE, timezone defaults to UTC) AND calls `provisionDefaultBucketsForSite` IN THE SAME TX as the org/role/admin-user/workflow-policy inserts. If bucket provisioning fails, the entire org-create rolls back — atomic by construction, never leaves a half-bootstrapped tenant where `CreateOrder` would explode on "bucket not found". When `initialSite` is provided the audit row's `metadata.initialSite` carries `{siteId, siteCode, bucketsCreated, bucketsAlreadyPresent}` (no per-bucket id map — that's high-cardinality and uninteresting to ops; the outbox carries counts, the command output carries the full map for the caller); when omitted, `metadata.initialSite` is null (so downstream consumers can route on the presence of the field). The handler emits an ADDITIONAL `org.buckets.provisioned.v1` outbox event alongside `organization.created.v1` whenever buckets are provisioned, keeping the consumer event stream identical regardless of provisioning entry point. **`scripts/bootstrap-org.ts` operator CLI** gained `--site-code`, `--site-name`, and `--site-timezone` flags with strict both-or-neither validation: passing `--site-code` without `--site-name` (or vice versa) exits non-zero with a usage message rather than silently falling back to "no site created" (the operator typo case); `--site-timezone` without the other two also exits non-zero. The CLI summary now prints `initialSiteId` and a per-code bucket-id listing on success. 13 contract tests across `create-organization.test.ts` cover the initialSite happy path (site + 7 buckets in one command), `timezone` default of `UTC`, dual outbox events with correct aggregateType (`Organization` for org.created.v1, `PharmacySite` for org.buckets.provisioned.v1), audit metadata initialSite snapshot, the omitted-initialSite no-op path (no site/bucket calls, single outbox event, `metadata.initialSite: null`), and Zod rejection of lowercase site codes. **`pnpm verify` is fully green**: 73 test files / 1068 unit tests pass, ESLint clean, Prettier clean, all typechecks pass, schema linter passes (31 models, 27 tenant-scoped, 4 excluded), command linter passes (17 command files), migration RLS linter passes (8 migrations, 4 exempt tables), `prisma validate` passes.
- [x] Fill commands: **`@pharmax/fill` + `@pharmax/labels` shipped** — full FILL slice with Zebra/ZPL thermal vial labels. Migration `20260527000000_phase4_fill_inventory_print` adds `Product`, `Lot`, `LotAssignment`, `InventoryTransaction`, `LabelPrinter`, `PrintTemplate`, `PrintJob`, `VialLabel` (RLS + tenant indexes). **Commands**: `StartFill` (transition → `FILL_IN_PROGRESS`, 18 tests), `AssignLot` (lot site/NDC/expiry/hold guards + inventory delta, 10 tests), `PrintVialLabel` + `ReprintVialLabel` (server-side ZPL render, `print_job` PENDING + outbox, workstation required, reprint reason registry, 8+3 tests), `CompleteFill` (requires lot + vial label + COMPLETED print per line → `FILL_COMPLETED_READY_FOR_FINAL`, 7 tests), `ConfirmVialLabelPrint` in `@pharmax/labels` (agent callback PENDING/SENT → COMPLETED/FAILED, 7 tests). **RBAC**: 31 permissions (+4: `fill.assign_lot`, `fill.print_vial_label`, `fill.reprint_vial_label`, `labels.confirm_print`); `PharmacyTechnician` role template updated. **Events**: `order.fill.started.v1 → FILL_START`, `order.fill.completed.v1 → FILL_COMPLETE` (pre-wired). **Remaining FILL-adjacent**: worker handler for `labels.vial_print.requested.v1`, `apps/print-agent`, seed demo printers/templates/lots, `ReopenForCorrection` for FINAL→FILL rework when order is not in `PV1_APPROVED_READY_FOR_FILL`.

## Phase 3 — SLA, productivity, custom buckets

- [ ] `@pharmax/sla` interval recorder + breach evaluator + scheduler tick
- [x] **`@pharmax/sla` foundation shipped** — migration `20260528100000_phase3_order_stage_interval` adds `OrderStageInterval` + `OrderStageIntervalKind` enum (10 wait/active kinds, RLS, partial unique one-open-per-order); migration `20260609000000_phase3_stage_interval_exception_kinds` extends the enum with `HOLD_ACTIVE`, `WAIT_AFTER_PV1_REJECT`, and `WAIT_AFTER_FINAL_REJECT` for the non-primary commands. Package `@pharmax/sla` exposes `openInitialWaitBeforeTyping`, `transitionStageIntervals`, `applyCommandStageIntervalTransition`, `closeOpenStageInterval`, `openStageInterval`, the `COMMAND_STAGE_INTERVAL_TRANSITION` / `COMMAND_STAGE_INTERVAL_CLOSE_ONLY` registries, and the state-to-kind helpers `intervalKindForOrderState` / `STAGE_INTERVAL_KIND_FOR_PRIMARY_STATE` / `STAGE_INTERVAL_KIND_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE` (`packages/sla/src/stage-interval-state-map.ts`). **Wired end-to-end across every v1 workflow-mutating command**: primary path (`CreateOrder` → `ConfirmShipment`) closes/opens via the static `applyCommandStageIntervalTransition` lookup; exception path (`PlaceHold`, `ReleaseHold`, `RejectPV1`, `RejectFinalVerification`, `CancelOrder`, `ReopenForCorrection`) covered by the next item. Shared test stub `@pharmax/sla/test-utils`. **24 unit tests** in `interval-recorder.test.ts` including the empty-set invariant `expect(KNOWN_NON_SLA_COMMANDS.size).toBe(0)` that catches the next forgotten command. Remaining for Phase 3: breach evaluator + `slaDeadlineAt` computation, scheduler tick, emergency bucket escalation.
- [x] **SLA semantics resolved for every v1 workflow-mutating command** (`packages/sla/src/interval-recorder.ts`) — `KNOWN_NON_SLA_COMMANDS` is now `new Set<string>([])` and a unit test asserts the empty-set invariant (the regression that catches "added a new workflow command but forgot to decide its SLA stance"). The previously-deferred 6 commands resolve into four distinct shapes that now define how every future command answers the question. **(1) `RejectPV1` / `RejectFinalVerification`** — recommendation accepted: pharmacist rejection **closes** `PV1_ACTIVE` / `FINAL_VERIFICATION_ACTIVE` and **opens** a new `WAIT_AFTER_PV1_REJECT` / `WAIT_AFTER_FINAL_REJECT` interval (added in migration `20260609000000_phase3_stage_interval_exception_kinds`). The reasoning: bury-rework-in-active-time is unrecoverable in reports (you cannot un-mix a rework loop after the fact), whereas closing gives clean per-decision-attempt time that aggregators can re-sum into a "total PV1 time including rework" KPI when ops asks for it. The `now` capture moved to before `order.update` in both reject handlers so the SLA close/open and the rejection record use the same timestamp; `actorUserId` is the rejecting pharmacist on the close call (audit trail attributes the time-spent block to the right human) and `null` on the wait-kind open via the existing `isActiveIntervalKind` predicate. **(2) `PlaceHold` / `ReleaseHold`** — recommendation accepted: `PlaceHold` is a transition that closes whatever is open and opens `HOLD_ACTIVE`; `ReleaseHold` is a transition that closes `HOLD_ACTIVE` and opens the stage interval that corresponds to the order's restored status. Two architectural sub-decisions fell out of this: **(2a) close from an unknown kind.** `PlaceHold` is the first **multi-from-state** command — an order can be held from any in-flight workflow state, so the close half cannot statically assert an `expectedKind`. The fix: `COMMAND_STAGE_INTERVAL_TRANSITION`'s `close` field became optional (`readonly close?: OrderStageIntervalKind`) and `applyCommandStageIntervalTransition` now calls `closeOpenStageInterval` + `openStageInterval` directly (instead of delegating to `transitionStageIntervals`) so it can conditionally omit `expectedKind` when the entry has none. Every existing command keeps its assertive close — only `PlaceHold` opts out. **(2b) open the right interval on release.** `ReleaseHold` resolves the next interval kind by looking up the restored state in the new **state-to-interval map** module (`packages/sla/src/stage-interval-state-map.ts`, exported from the package root): `STAGE_INTERVAL_KIND_FOR_PRIMARY_STATE` covers the 11 happy-path `OrderStatus` values exhaustively (compile-time check via `Record<OrderPrimaryState, …>`), `STAGE_INTERVAL_KIND_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE` covers the 5 exception states partially (`CANCELLED` intentionally omitted — it's terminal), and `intervalKindForOrderState(state)` is the public lookup that returns `OrderStageIntervalKind | null`. The handler-direct pattern (call `closeOpenStageInterval` + `openStageInterval` from the command rather than routing through the recorder's static table) lets `ReleaseHold` and `ReopenForCorrection` resolve `openKind` at runtime from input parameters; `actorUserId` is set on active-kind opens and null on wait-kind opens. **(3) `CancelOrder`** — terminal close-only: already wired through `COMMAND_STAGE_INTERVAL_CLOSE_ONLY` in the previous slice so any currently-open interval closes and no successor opens. No duplicate `CANCELLED_TERMINAL` row — `OrderCancellation.cancelledFromStatus` already answers "which stage was the order in when cancelled?". **(4) `ReopenForCorrection`** — handler-direct call (same pattern as `ReleaseHold`): close the rejection wait interval (`WAIT_AFTER_PV1_REJECT` or `WAIT_AFTER_FINAL_REJECT`, looked up from `fromState` via the state-map) and open the interval that corresponds to `input.reopenToState`. Keeps the static `COMMAND_STAGE_INTERVAL_TRANSITION` table free of data-driven entries — the recorder's contract stays "command name → static pair" and runtime branching stays in the handler. **Coverage:** new unit tests in `interval-recorder.test.ts` lock the four new transition shapes (`PlaceHold` multi-from-state close + `HOLD_ACTIVE` open with actor; `RejectPV1` close `PV1_ACTIVE` + `WAIT_AFTER_PV1_REJECT` open without actor; `RejectFinalVerification` symmetric; expected-kind mismatch surfaces as `InvariantViolationError`); contract tests in `place-hold.test.ts`, `release-hold.test.ts`, `reject-pv1.test.ts`, `reject-final-verification.test.ts`, and `reopen-for-correction.test.ts` use the shared `createOrderStageIntervalTxStub` + `initialOpenIntervalKind` `buildPrismaFake` overrides to assert each command emits the right `orderStageInterval.updateMany` (close) and `orderStageInterval.create` (open) calls with the correct `kind`, `actorUserId`, and timestamps. **Report-layer contract** (for the breach evaluator and dashboards): `HOLD_ACTIVE`, `WAIT_AFTER_PV1_REJECT`, and `WAIT_AFTER_FINAL_REJECT` are **excluded** from per-stage breach windows by default — a held order is not eating its PV1/fill/final budget while paused, and a rejected order's rework time is not the original pharmacist's first-pass time. Dashboards that need the inclusive number aggregate over the kind union explicitly. All gates green: `pnpm typecheck`, `pnpm lint`, `pnpm format:check`, `pnpm prisma:validate`, `pnpm check:migrations`, `pnpm check:schema`, `pnpm check:commands`, `pnpm test` (181 files, 1974 tests). With this in, the breach evaluator (next bullet) has a clean kind-to-policy mapping to consume.
- [ ] Custom bucket admin CRUD (already shape-defined in `Bucket` table)
- [ ] `@pharmax/productivity` activity events (login, logout, heartbeat, opened, claimed, scan, print, idle)
- [ ] Productivity report views + materialized refresh job

## Phase 4 — Hardware, inventory, shipping

- [~] `apps/print-agent` — **shipped v1** (poll SENT jobs for paired workstation, file/tcp ZPL transport, `ConfirmVialLabelPrint` with idempotency); workstation pairing + signed device tokens still pending

- [x] `@pharmax/scan` GS1 / NDC parsers + scan validation in `CompleteFill` — **shipped** in `@pharmax/scan` (`normalizeNdc`, `parseGs1`, `parseScannedValue`, `validateFillCompletionScans`); `CompleteFill` requires per-line `lotScan` + `vialLabelScan` with HARD_STOP on lot/NDC/vial mismatch; **18 unit tests** across scan + updated CompleteFill contract tests

- [x] `@pharmax/shipping` multi-carrier (EasyPost / FedEx / UPS) + per-tenant credentials + signed inbound tracking webhooks — **shipped end-to-end with plug-and-play credential admin; FedEx adapter production-hardened against EONPRO reference**.

  _FedEx production hardening (EONPRO-derived):_ `FedExShippingAdapter` now ships directly (no rate-quote pre-roundtrip — EONPRO pattern; `rateQuote` stays available on the client for explicit rate-shopping). Ship payload uses `labelResponseOptions: "LABEL"` (returns base64 PDF inline as `PurchasedLabel.labelPdfBase64` — no second HTTP fetch for the print path), full label spec (`PAPER_4X6` / `COMMON2D` / `TOP_EDGE_OF_TEXT_FIRST` / `NONE` rotation), `DROPOFF_AT_FEDEX_LOCATION` default pickup, phone-number digits-only normalization, ET-resolved `shipDatestamp`. `ShippingAdapter` contract gains `labelPdfBase64: string | null` on `PurchasedLabel` and optional `cancelLabel(input) → CancelLabelResult`; UPS surfaces its base64 PNG label there too. New FedEx surfaces: `FedExClient.cancelShipment` + `trackShipment` + `trackShipmentBatch` (30-per-call chunking with merge), `FedExShippingAdapter.cancelLabel` (idempotent — 4xx "already cancelled" → success, 5xx → `FEDEX_CANCEL_FAILED`). UI-ready exports: `FEDEX_SERVICE_TYPES` (10 services with category + ETA + One Rate eligibility) and `FEDEX_PACKAGING_TYPES` (9 packagings with One Rate weight caps). `normalizeFedExStatus` maps **47 FedEx derived status codes** → `ShipmentTrackingEventKind` for future FedEx tracking poller / webhook ingestion alongside the existing EasyPost path; `isFedExTrackingNumber` shape predicate for candidate filtering. **42 new tests** (4 FedEx adapter ship + cancel paths, 7 FedEx client OAuth + error + track, 4 FedEx services registry, 12 FedEx status map + tracking-number shape, 15 fanout from existing tests). **110 test files / 1343 tests passing.**

  _Inbound:_ migrations `20260530000000_phase4_shipment_tracking_event` (`shipment_tracking_event` table + `ShipmentStatus` lifecycle values + cached `lastTrackingEventAt/Kind`) and `20260531000000_phase4_easypost_webhook_event` (`easypost_webhook_event` RLS-exempt inbox); `@pharmax/shipping` ships `verifyEasyPostSignature` (HMAC-SHA256, timing-safe), `parseEasyPostTrackerWebhook` (Zod), `normalizeEasyPostStatus`, `RecordShipmentTrackingEvent` command (idempotent at row + bus layer, newer-only cache advancement, audit/outbox), `handleEasyPostWebhook` (transport-agnostic entry), `processEasyPostWebhookEvent` + `executeEasyPostWebhookEventDispatch` (worker dispatch, pluggable `WebhookTargetResolver`), in-memory + Prisma event stores. `apps/web` exposes `POST /api/webhooks/easypost`; `apps/worker` claims rows via `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED`, resolves shipment + per-org service user in system context (eslint Override 3b allowlists `apps/worker/src/drains/**`), enters tenancy, executes the command through the standard bus. Per-org `shipping-webhook@<org-slug>.test` service user seeded.

  _Outbound (multi-carrier, per-tenant):_ migration `20260601000000_phase4_carrier_credential` adds `carrier_credential` table (per-(org, provider) with envelope-encrypted `apiKeyEnc` + `webhookSecretEnc` via `@pharmax/crypto` AAD-bound to `{tenantId, "carrier_credential", "apiKey"|"webhookSecret", id}`, partial-unique-active index, RLS + tenant-scoped). New enums `ShippingProvider` (`EASYPOST/FEDEX/UPS`) + `CarrierCredentialStatus` (`ACTIVE/DISABLED`). `ShippingAdapter` interface; **EasyPost** + **FedEx** (OAuth2 client_credentials with cached token + Ship + Cancel + Track + Track-batch) + **UPS** (OAuth2 with shipper-number `x-merchant-id`, `/api/shipments/v2403/ship`, service-code translation) clients + adapters; `configureShipping({ factories: { EASYPOST?, FEDEX?, UPS? } })` factory registry (each factory receives a per-org `CarrierCredentialContext` with decrypted API key + webhook secret + carrierAccountId + baseUrl override); `resolveShippingAdapter` decrypts credential and invokes factory; **`RegisterCarrierCredential`** admin command (plug-and-play: operator pastes API key, command encrypts via `@pharmax/crypto`, replaces any prior ACTIVE row → DISABLED for audit; `apiKey`+`webhookSecret` redacted from `command_log.requestPayload`); `PurchaseShipmentLabel` takes `provider`, resolves per-org credential at call time, builds the right adapter, and stamps `provider`+`credentialId` on audit/outbox. Permissions: `ship.purchase_label` + `ship.manage_carrier_credentials` (37 total).

  _FedEx tracking poller (shipped):_ migration `20260602000000_phase4_shipment_tracking_source_carriers` extends `ShipmentTrackingSource` with `FEDEX` + `UPS`. `apps/worker/src/drains/claim-active-fedex-shipments.ts` runs a cross-tenant SQL filter (`carrier = FEDEX AND status NOT IN (terminal) AND externalTrackerId IS NULL AND (lastTrackingEventAt IS NULL OR < NOW - staleThresholdMs)`) in system context; `apps/worker/src/drains/fedex-tracking-poller.ts` is the per-tick drainer that groups by org, decrypts the per-org FedEx credential via `@pharmax/crypto` (colon-split packed API key + carrierAccountId), instantiates a `FedExClient` per org, calls `trackShipmentBatch` (30-per-call chunks with merge), and dispatches `RecordShipmentTrackingEvent` with `source = "FEDEX"` and synthetic `externalEventId = "fedex:{trackingNumber}:{statusCode}:{occurredAt.toISOString()}"` (DB unique constraint + bus idempotency cache make repeated polls of the same status no-ops). Wired as a 4th poll loop in `apps/worker/src/main.ts` (intervals: 5min default, batch size 100, stale threshold 2h — EONPRO-matched). Per-shipment / per-org failures isolated; tick tally counts `claimed / polled / recorded / skippedNoCredential / skippedNoStatus / failed`. **7 new tests** (3 claim shape + parameter binding, 4 poller end-to-end: happy path with DL → DELIVERED + correct externalEventId shape, no-credential skip, idle, no-status skip). **112 test files / 1350 tests passing.**

  _UPS tracking poller (shipped):_ `@pharmax/shipping` adds `normalizeUpsStatus` (UPS `currentStatus.type` enum: `M/MV → CREATED`, `I/P → IN_TRANSIT`, `O → OUT_FOR_DELIVERY`, `D → DELIVERED`, `RS → RETURN_TO_SENDER`, `X/NA → EXCEPTION`) + `isUpsTrackingNumber` (canonical `^1Z[A-Z0-9]{16}$`). `UpsClient.trackShipment` calls `GET /api/track/v1/details/{trackingNumber}` (UPS Track v1 has no batch endpoint), wrapped by `trackShipmentBatch` which iterates sequentially with per-tracking-number error isolation (a 4xx on one tracking number does not abort the rest of the batch). `apps/worker/src/drains/claim-active-ups-shipments.ts` and `apps/worker/src/drains/ups-tracking-poller.ts` mirror the FedEx orchestration exactly: cross-tenant claim in system context, group-by-org credential decryption (`carrier_credential` packed apiKey + shipper-number), one `UpsClient` per org, `RecordShipmentTrackingEvent` dispatch with `source = "UPS"` + synthetic `externalEventId = "ups:{trackingNumber}:{statusType}:{occurredAt.toISOString()}"`, same `claimed/polled/recorded/skippedNoCredential/skippedNoStatus/failed` tally. Wired as a 5th poll loop in `apps/worker/src/main.ts` (intervals: 5min default, batch size **50** — smaller than FedEx because UPS is per-call, stale threshold 2h). UPS activity timestamps reconstructed from `YYYYMMDD` + `HHMMSS` → UTC ISO (no TZ surfaced by UPS; the stable externalEventId is what dedupes, not the exact timestamp). **9 new tests** (3 claim shape + parameter binding, 1 status map across all UPS types + 2 tracking-number shape branches, 2 client GET + per-tracking-number error isolation, 5 poller end-to-end: happy path with D → DELIVERED, no-credential skip, idle, no-status skip, per-tracking 4xx → failed). **119 test files / 1411 tests passing.**

  _Boot-time factory registry wiring (shipped):_ `apps/web/src/server/bootstrap.ts` and `apps/worker/src/main.ts` both call `configureShipping({ factories: { EASYPOST: createEasyPostFactory(), FEDEX: createFedExFactory(), UPS: createUpsFactory() } })` after `configureCrypto` (crypto must be wired first so `resolveShippingAdapter` can decrypt credentials on first call). Closes the loop on the multi-carrier slice — `PurchaseShipmentLabel`, `RecordShipmentTrackingEvent`, and both tracking pollers can now resolve credentials end-to-end without throwing `SHIPPING_NOT_CONFIGURED`.

  _Shipment exception buckets (shipped):_ closes the operational loop on EasyPost / FedEx / UPS exception events. `RecordShipmentTrackingEvent`'s `shipment.tracking.recorded.v1` outbox payload now also surfaces `trackingEventId` (DB row id of the just-recorded ledger entry). New `apps/worker/src/drains/escalate-on-shipment-exception.ts` outbox handler filters on `kind ∈ {EXCEPTION, FAILED_DELIVERY, RETURN_TO_SENDER}`, resolves the per-org service user in system context (same `shipping-webhook@<org-slug>.test` actor used by the inbound webhook drain), enters tenancy, and dispatches the new `EscalateOrderToEmergencyBucket` command (`@pharmax/shipping/src/commands/escalate-order-to-emergency-bucket.ts`). The command takes the standard `defineCommand` skeleton (order row lock, version CAS, audit + outbox), resolves the seeded `EMERGENCY` bucket by `(organizationId, code)`, and CAS-moves `order.currentBucketId → EMERGENCY.id` only when the order is not already there — the "already in EMERGENCY" branch writes a `order.shipment_escalation_reaffirmed.v1` audit + outbox row so the timeline records every reaffirming carrier event without re-bumping the version under concurrent retries. `LockedOrderTarget` widened to include `currentBucketId` (additive, non-PHI, same rationale as `siteId` already being there) so the command reads it off the lock without a second roundtrip. New permission `ship.escalate_to_emergency` (39 total); seed + `RBAC` updated. `currentStatus` is intentionally NOT mutated — the order keeps the workflow state it died in (typically `SHIPPED`); the bucket move is an OPERATIONAL signal, not a workflow transition. Idempotency: bus key `escalate:{shipmentId}:{externalEventId}` short-circuits re-deliveries before hitting the DB; the row-level "already in EMERGENCY" branch is the second line of defense. **14 new tests** (4 command: first-time escalate, already-escalated reaffirm, no-EMERGENCY bucket guard, order-not-found guard; 10 handler: 3 escalation kinds × happy path, 5 non-escalation kinds skip, no-service-user error, malformed-payload error). **122 test files / 1441 tests passing.**

  _WebhookService role + ResolveOrderEscalation (shipped):_ closes both remaining Phase 4 shipping items. **(1) Least-privilege webhook identity** — new `WebhookService` role template in `@pharmax/rbac` (ORGANIZATION-scoped, only `ship.record_tracking_event` + `ship.escalate_to_emergency`); `prisma/seed.ts` updated to grant the per-org `shipping-webhook@<org-slug>.test` service user this role instead of `OrgAdmin`. Compromised webhook secret can now only record telemetry + route to EMERGENCY — no PHI exposure, no terminal-state writes. **(2) Operator disposition flow** — new `ResolveOrderEscalation` command in `@pharmax/shipping` with three dispositions: `RETURN_TO_SHIPPING` (back to SHIPPING bucket for re-ship), `RETURN_TO_FILL` (back to FILL bucket for physical re-fill), `KEEP_IN_EMERGENCY` (audit-only acknowledgement that triage is in progress). Guards the order is actually in EMERGENCY before mutating; validates target bucket exists and is `WORKFLOW`-kind; CAS-bumps version on bucket-move modes; redacts `reasonText` per the PHI invariant. Emits `order.escalation_resolved.v1` (bucket-move) or `order.escalation_acknowledged.v1` (keep). New permission `ship.resolve_escalation` (40 total), granted to `ShippingClerk` template. **(3) Operator CLI** — `scripts/resolve-emergency-bucket.ts` (registered as `pnpm resolve:emergency`), follows the `bootstrap-org` pattern: resolves operator by `--as-user=<email>` in system context, enters tenancy, dispatches the command through the standard bus. Minute-bucketed idempotency key. The CLI is the canonical operational interface until a web operator console lands — that console will dispatch the same command through an authenticated HTTP route. **+14 new tests** (7 `ResolveOrderEscalation` contract: 3 dispositions × happy + 3 guards + 1 PHI invariant; +6 from updated `ROLE_TEMPLATES` length / role.create count assertions; +1 from `ALL_PERMISSION_CODES` length bump). **123 test files / 1448 tests passing.**

  _Remaining:_ web operator console (Phase 5 frontend slice) — the EMERGENCY queue view + a disposition form/modal that POSTs to an authenticated `/api/ops/orders/:id/resolve-escalation` route that internally calls `ResolveOrderEscalation`. The backend capability is fully shipped; what's missing is the auth + layout primitives the route would sit behind.

- [x] Shipment exception buckets — **shipped** (see "Shipment exception buckets" sub-bullet above)

- [~] Pre-shipment package-photo capture — **schema + command + storage port + RBAC + HTTP routes + boot wiring + S3 production adapter + dock-side capture UI + unmatched-bucket triage UI + S3 production boot-wire + order-timeline render shipped**; janitor + image-stream route remain.

  _Capture command + storage port (shipped):_ closes the EONPRO parity gap on dock-side package-photo capture. **(1) Schema** — migration `20260606000000_phase5_package_photo` adds the `package_photo` table (org-scoped append-only domain row carrying capture context — `siteId` / `clinicId?` / `capturedByUserId` / `capturedAtWorkstationId?` — plus `pharmacyExternalOrderNumber`, match metadata — `matched` / `matchStrategy` / `matchedOrderId?` / `matchedPatientId?` / `matchedAt?` — tracking metadata — `trackingNumber?` / `trackingSource?` / `sourceShipmentId?` — storage-pointer fields — `storageBucket` / `storageKey` / `contentType` / `fileSize` / `sha256` — and an envelope-encrypted `notesEnc` JSONB column for incidental PHI in operator notes); two new enums `PackagePhotoTrackingSource` (`ORDER` / `TRACKING_EVENT` / `MANUAL`) and `PackagePhotoMatchStrategy` (`EXTERNAL_ORDER_NUMBER` / `MANUAL_PATIENT_ID` / `UNMATCHED`); a unique `(organizationId, sha256)` index for byte-level dedup of operator retakes; reporting-friendly indexes on `(org, capturedAt)`, `(org, externalOrderNumber)`, `(org, matchedOrderId)`, `(org, matchedPatientId)`, `(org, capturedByUserId, capturedAt)`, `(org, matched)`, `(org, trackingNumber)`, `(org, clinicId, capturedAt)`, `(org, siteId, capturedAt)`. All FKs `ON DELETE RESTRICT` (the photo row is an audit anchor — order/user/clinic/site/workstation/command_log/shipment cannot be deleted without first archiving the photo). RLS `ENABLE` + `FORCE` + `tenant_isolation` policy keyed on the standard `pharmax.system_context` / `pharmax.organization_id` GUC pair (matches the migration-RLS linter contract). **(2) Tenancy registry** — `PackagePhoto` registered in `TENANT_SCOPED_MODELS` as `{ kind: "organizationId" }` so the Prisma extension's anti-leak guard fires on cross-org reads. **(3) RBAC** — new `ship.capture_package_photo` permission (46 total), granted to `ShippingClerk` + `PharmacyTechnician` role templates; seeded; `permissions.test.ts` length assertion bumped. **(4) `@pharmax/package-capture` package** — new sibling to `@pharmax/shipping`; ships `PackagePhotoStorage` port (interface: `beginUpload({ organizationId, contentType, bytes }) → { uploadToken, bucket, key, sha256, fileSize, contentType }` + `resolveUploadToken(token) → ResolvedPackagePhotoUpload | null`), `InMemoryPackagePhotoStorage` test/dev adapter (sha256 over raw bytes via `node:crypto`, org-prefixed key shape `org/{orgId}/photo/{sha256}`, opaque `randomUUID()` token), and a boot-time `configurePackagePhotoStorage` singleton that throws `InternalError(PACKAGE_PHOTO_STORAGE_NOT_CONFIGURED)` when read before configuration so a missed wire fails loud at first dispatch. **(5) `CapturePackagePhoto` command** — direct `Command<I, O>` (not `defineCommand`) because it's an append-only observation — capturing a photo is NOT a workflow state transition (no order lock, no `version` bump, no `order_event`). Flow: resolves the `uploadToken` to `{bucket, key, sha256, fileSize, contentType}` (defends against leaked tokens by verifying `upload.organizationId === ctx.organizationId` → typed `PACKAGE_PHOTO_UPLOAD_TOKEN_TENANT_MISMATCH`); auto-matches `(organizationId, externalOrderNumber)` against `Order` and inherits `siteId` / `clinicId` / `patientId` from the matched row; resolves tracking number with **manual override > matched-order's-latest-shipment > none** precedence (`MANUAL` / `ORDER` / `null` source enum); envelope-encrypts optional `notes` via `@pharmax/crypto` AAD-bound to `{tenantId, "package_photo", "notes", recordId}`; on `(organizationId, sha256)` collision (P2002) translates to a typed `PACKAGE_PHOTO_DUPLICATE_BYTES` `ConflictError` carrying the existing photo id (UI treats it as success — "you've already captured this photo"). `redactFields: ["notes"]` scrubs the plaintext from `command_log.requestPayload`; audit + outbox payloads echo only structural fields (`photoId`, `matched`, `matchStrategy`, `trackingSource`, `hasNotes`, `sha256`, `fileSize`, `contentType`) — no notes plaintext, no PHI. The `uploadToken` pattern keeps binary bytes off the bus's `canonicalStringify`-driven idempotency cache (large + non-deterministic-serializing `Buffer`s never cross the bus surface). `requireCallerSiteId(ctx)` throws `InternalError(PACKAGE_PHOTO_CAPTURE_SITE_REQUIRED)` for unmatched captures from a service identity without `siteId` in scope — site-pinned `ShippingClerk` grants always carry it; the loud failure prevents silent fallback to an arbitrary site. **+15 new tests** (3 in-memory storage adapter — sha256/fileSize/key shape + bucket override + cross-org isolation + maintenance helpers; 4 configure singleton — unconfigured/configured/replace/reset; 8 command — happy matched + auto-tracking, manual-override > matched, unmatched + caller-site fallback, notes encryption + audit/outbox redaction invariant, workstation context threading, upload-token unknown, upload-token tenant-mismatch, P2002 → `PACKAGE_PHOTO_DUPLICATE_BYTES` with existing photo id).

  _HTTP routes + boot wiring (shipped):_ closes the web-tier loop so a real client can round-trip a photo end-to-end against the in-memory adapter. **(1) Boot wiring** — `apps/web/src/server/bootstrap.ts` calls `configurePackagePhotoStorage({ storage: new InMemoryPackagePhotoStorage() })` after the crypto step (the storage adapter doesn't touch crypto today, but the production S3 adapter will reach for the same KMS key the rest of `@pharmax/crypto` uses, so the ordering convention is locked in now).
