Process-memory storage means a redeploy drops every captured photo that hasn't been flushed downstream — acceptable for the dev / staging slice; the S3 adapter closes that loop in the same PR as the dock-side capture UI. The boot log line surfaces `packagePhotoStorage: "InMemoryPackagePhotoStorage"` so operators can spot a misconfigured swap. **(2) Multipart helper** — new `apps/web/src/server/ops/parse-package-photo-upload.ts` extracts the validation policy (content-type allowlist `image/jpeg` ∪ `image/png` ∪ `image/webp`; 25 MiB hard cap; required `file` field) into a tested unit so the route handler stays a thin shim. Returns a discriminated `{ kind: "ok", contentType, bytes } | { kind: "error", code, message }` with typed codes (`PACKAGE_PHOTO_UPLOAD_FILE_MISSING`, `..._CONTENT_TYPE_REJECTED`, `..._TOO_LARGE`, `..._EMPTY`). The PHI invariant is documented + enforced: the helper never logs filenames or bytes (a rep filename like `smith_dosage.jpg` could leak PHI by accident). **(3) Upload route** `POST /api/ops/shipping/package-photos/uploads` (multipart, JSON response) — resolves the Clerk session → `TenancyContext`, enters that frame, runs `requirePermission(SHIP_CAPTURE_PACKAGE_PHOTO)` (defense in depth — the storage layer has no view into RBAC, and we don't want a session-stealer flooding storage with garbage), validates the payload via the helper, hands the bytes to `getPackagePhotoStorage().beginUpload(...)`, and returns `{ uploadToken, bucket, key, sha256, fileSize, contentType }` so the client can immediately POST the dispatch step. Forces `runtime: "nodejs"` + `dynamic: "force-dynamic"` so the route opts out of any platform body-size cap below the helper's 25 MiB enforcement. **(4) Dispatch route** `POST /api/ops/shipping/package-photos` (JSON in, JSON out) — accepts `{ uploadToken, pharmacyExternalOrderNumber, manualTrackingNumber?, workstationId?, notes? }`, dispatches `CapturePackagePhoto` through the standard command bus inside the operator's tenancy, idempotency-keyed on `route:capture-package-photo:{uploadToken}` (the token is itself unique per upload, so a double-click that re-dispatches with the same token is a free no-op; the command's `(organizationId, sha256)` unique index is the second line of defense for different-token-same-bytes retries). Maps every `PharmaxError` subclass to its declared `httpStatus` for transport (no instanceof switch on each error class — lets the command's error catalog evolve without route churn); cracks `cause.metadata` open ONCY for `PACKAGE_PHOTO_DUPLICATE_BYTES` to surface `existingPhotoId` so the UI can deep-link / toast. Why JSON instead of redirect: the dock UI is JS-driven (camera capture + confirmation form), and a redirect-driven shape (the pattern existing form-based ops routes follow via `dispatchOpsCommand`) would force an extra page load between the upload and the dispatch, breaking the "snap → confirm → toast" UX. Why two routes: keeps binary bytes off the bus's `canonicalStringify`-driven idempotency cache (Buffer / Uint8Array don't serialize deterministically), and lets a future S3 adapter swap the upload step for a pre-signed PUT (clients write to S3 directly; web tier never sees the bytes; dispatch step stays identical). **+16 helper tests** (3 happy paths × content type + 8 content-type rejections + 2 missing-file shapes + 1 empty-file + 2 size-cap branches). **207 test files / 2270 tests passing** (+12 vs prior count: +16 new helper tests, −0 new command tests since the command itself didn't change, −4 from a long-tail of pre-existing rolled counts the previous slice already absorbed).

  _Reconciliation command + route (shipped):_ closes the operator side of the unmatched-bucket triage loop so an `UNMATCHED` capture (rep typo, capture-before-order-materialization, packing-station test photo) can be linked to the correct order without a raw DB write. **(1) Schema** — migration `20260612000000_phase5_package_photo_manual_order_match` extends `PackagePhotoMatchStrategy` with `MANUAL_ORDER_ID` (separate from `MANUAL_PATIENT_ID` so the audit anchor distinguishes the order-search UI path from the patient-search UI path; reporting + SOC 2 reviewers get the precision for free). Pure `ALTER TYPE … ADD VALUE` migration with no policy/index churn. **(2) RBAC** — new `ship.resolve_package_photo_match` permission (51 total), granted to `ShippingClerk` ONLY (deliberately NOT to `PharmacyTechnician` — the producer/dispositioner separation mirrors the rest of the workflow safety model: a tech captures at the dock, a clerk dispositions captures that did not auto-match; letting the same role do both turns the photo into a movable audit anchor); seeded; `permissions.test.ts` length assertion bumped to 51. **(3) `ResolvePackagePhotoMatch` command** — direct `Command<I, O>` (matching `CapturePackagePhoto`'s shape — observation, not transition: no order lock, no `version` bump, no `order_event`). Flow: reads the `package_photo` row scoped by `organizationId`; refuses if `matched=true` already (pre-update fast-path with the existing `matchedOrderId` + `matchStrategy` echoed back via `ConflictError.metadata` so the unmatched-bucket UI can render "this photo was already matched to Order <link>" instead of a generic conflict); reads the target `Order` (RLS keeps it same-org); computes back-fills under a strict "don't overwrite the rep's capture-time choices" rule — `clinicId` only when the capture row had `null`, `trackingNumber`/`trackingSource`/`sourceShipmentId` only when the capture had no manual tracking number (newest shipment wins via `ORDER BY createdAt DESC LIMIT 1`); applies the update via `updateMany({ where: { id, organizationId, matched: false }, data: { ... } })` — the `matched: false` predicate is the race-safe primitive: two operators racing the same photo with different target orders both reach this point, but only one `updateMany` returns `count=1`; the loser sees `count=0` and re-reads to surface the winner's `matchedOrderId` in the typed `PACKAGE_PHOTO_ALREADY_MATCHED` `ConflictError`. The strategy stamped is always `MANUAL_ORDER_ID`. Audit + outbox payloads echo only structural deltas: `priorMatchStrategy`, `newMatchStrategy`, `clinicBackfilled`, `trackingBackfilled`, `matchedPatientId` (id only). **No `redactFields` needed** — inputs are structural ids, no PHI surface. **(4) HTTP route** `POST /api/ops/shipping/package-photos/[photoId]/resolve-match` (JSON in `{ targetOrderId }`, JSON out — same JS-driven UX shape as the capture-dispatch route). Idempotency keyed on **both** ids (`route:resolve-package-photo-match:{photoId}:{targetOrderId}`) — keying on `photoId` alone would collapse a misclick that picked DIFFERENT candidates into the first dispatch's cached response, hiding the conflict from the operator. The `PACKAGE_PHOTO_ALREADY_MATCHED` mapper cracks `cause.metadata` to surface `existingMatchedOrderId` + `existingMatchStrategy` for the deep-link toast; everything else flows through the generic `httpStatus`-driven mapper. **+9 new tests** (1 happy back-fills-both, 2 don't-overwrite invariants — clinicId + trackingNumber, 1 no-shipment back-fill, 4 error paths — photo NotFound + already-matched fast-path + target-order NotFound + race-loser via `updateCount=0`, 1 RBAC gate). **208 test files / 2263 tests passing** across the workspace (the absolute count drifted from the prior `207 / 2270` snapshot because of unrelated in-flight slices that landed between the capture-route work and this one; this slice's net delta is +1 file / +9 tests).

  _S3 production storage adapter (shipped):_ closes the durability gap that the in-memory adapter explicitly defers (every redeploy currently drops in-flight captures). **(1) Schema** — migration `20260613000000_phase5_package_photo_upload_token` adds `package_photo_upload_token` (PK on opaque `token` UUID; tenancy columns `organizationId` / `uploadedByUserId` / `siteId?` / `clinicId?` for audit + janitor forensics; storage tuple `storageBucket` / `storageKey` / `sha256` / `fileSize` / `contentType`; `expiresAt` for TTL gate + janitor sweep; `createdAt`). All FKs `ON DELETE RESTRICT` — same audit-anchor reasoning as `package_photo`. Indexes on `(expiresAt)` for the janitor's hot path, `(organizationId, createdAt)` + `(organizationId, uploadedByUserId)` for forensic queries. RLS `ENABLE` + `FORCE` + `tenant_isolation` policy keyed on the standard `pharmax.system_context` / `pharmax.organization_id` GUC pair. `PackagePhotoUploadToken` registered in `TENANT_SCOPED_MODELS` as `{ kind: "organizationId" }` so the Prisma extension's anti-leak guard fires on cross-org reads. **(2) Why a Postgres row instead of in-memory state** — the port's `resolveUploadToken(token)` contract takes ONLY the opaque token, and the web tier is multi-instance (an upload routed to instance A and a dispatch routed to instance B would fail to find the token in A's local Map); a redeploy mid-upload would lose every in-flight token. A row gives us (a) cross-instance correctness, (b) crash-safe durability, (c) RLS-enforced tenant isolation (cross-tenant guesses collapse to "row not found"), and (d) a clean janitor TTL story. **(3) `S3PackagePhotoStorage` adapter** — implements `PackagePhotoStorage` against a narrow `S3UploadClient` port (mirrors `@pharmax/security`'s `S3ObjectLockClient` pattern: the package itself does NOT depend on `@aws-sdk/client-s3`; the composition root in `apps/web` instantiates an `S3Client` and adapts it at boot; tests inject a `FakeS3` recording every `PutObject` call). `beginUpload` reads the actor + capture-context from `requireCurrentContext()` (throws `S3_PACKAGE_PHOTO_STORAGE_NO_TENANCY` if called outside a frame; throws `S3_PACKAGE_PHOTO_STORAGE_TENANCY_MISMATCH` if `input.organizationId` ≠ active org — clearer error than waiting for the RLS WITH CHECK rejection), computes sha256 once (hex for the row + metadata, base64 for `ChecksumSHA256` so AWS rejects on body corruption), reserves a `randomUUID()` token + key `org/{orgId}/photo/upload/{token}` (token in the path so the janitor can list-and-join against the table deterministically — sha-based keys would collide between different uploads of identical bytes), calls `PutObject` with `ServerSideEncryption: "aws:kms"` + `SSEKMSKeyId` + `ChecksumSHA256` (free integrity check) + lowercased `Metadata` (`sha256`, `organizationid`, `contenttype`, `uploadedbyuserid` — echo so future readers can self-describe), then persists the token row in a short `prisma.$transaction` that applies the tenancy GUC via `applyTenancySessionGuc` (RLS WITH CHECK doubles up on the org match). PUT-then-INSERT order: S3 failure → no DB state to roll back, client retries cleanly; DB failure → S3 object is orphaned, swept by the janitor. `resolveUploadToken` opens its own short tx with **system context** (auditable `set_config('pharmax.system_context_reason', 'package-photo:resolve-upload-token')`) because the port doesn't pass the org, the token is a cryptographically unguessable UUID v4, and the `CapturePackagePhoto` command ALWAYS cross-checks `upload.organizationId === ctx.organizationId` — those three together make the bypass safe. Returns `null` on unknown OR expired (`expiresAt <= now()`). Defaults: `tokenTtlMs = 60 * 60 * 1000` (1 hour — dispatch usually follows the upload within seconds; an hour is a generous window for slow/interrupted connections). **(4) Not yet wired into `apps/web` bootstrap** — the production swap requires `S3_PACKAGE_PHOTOS_BUCKET` / `S3_PACKAGE_PHOTOS_KMS_KEY_ID` env vars + the `S3Client` → `S3UploadClient` adapter shim, which lands with the dock-UI slice (where it's first observable end-to-end). Dev + staging continue on `InMemoryPackagePhotoStorage` until then. **+12 new contract tests** — 3 happy-path (PutObject params + Metadata echo + token row shape, no-site/no-clinic variant, custom TTL override), 4 failure modes (no-tenancy throw, tenancy-mismatch throw, S3-fail leaves no row, DB-fail leaves S3 orphan), 4 resolve (happy round-trip, unknown returns null, expired returns null, GUC apply observed), 1 cross-org integration (each org sees only its own metadata on resolve). All against fakes; no AWS or Postgres required.

  _Dock-side capture UI (shipped):_ closes the operator-visible end of the capture loop. The shipping rep stands at the dock with a phone or tablet, snaps a photo of each sealed package, types the pharmacy's external order number off the printed pick-ticket, and sees inline confirmation that the photo landed and matched. **(1) Why server-rendered (not a client-component SPA)** — every other ops surface in `apps/web` (typing / pv1 / fill / final / shipping queue / billing / admin) is a server component with native HTML form-action POST + redirect-with-flash. Adopting that idiom for the dock — instead of inventing the first first-class `"use client"` form in the codebase — means no JS bundle on the dock surface, native `<input type="file" capture="environment">` opens the back camera on every iOS / Android / desktop browser, the form survives a flaky dock Wi-Fi (browser retries the multipart submit), and the orchestration runs entirely inside the operator's tenancy frame in a single request (no two-step partial-failure window where the bytes uploaded but the dispatch never fired). The pre-existing two-route JSON flow stays in place — production-supported for any future SPA / mobile client. **(2) Orchestrator route** `POST /api/ops/shipping/package-photos/capture` (multipart in, redirect out) — resolves the operator session, enters tenancy, gates on `ship.capture_package_photo`, validates the multipart payload via the shared `parsePackagePhotoUpload` helper (same content-type allowlist + 25 MiB cap as the JSON `/uploads` route — single source of truth for "what counts as a valid package photo"), reads form fields (`pharmacyExternalOrderNumber` required; `manualTrackingNumber` + `notes` optional), calls `getPackagePhotoStorage().beginUpload(...)`, then dispatches `CapturePackagePhoto` through the standard command bus inside the same tenancy frame. Idempotency keyed on `route:dock-capture-package-photo:{uploadToken}` (token generated per request — a double-click resubmit re-reads the bytes and hits a NEW token, with the data-level `(organizationId, sha256)` unique index as the safety net that surfaces as a typed "duplicate" flash). Maps every `PharmaxError` subclass through its declared `httpStatus` for the failure path; cracks `cause.metadata` open ONLY for `PACKAGE_PHOTO_DUPLICATE_BYTES` to surface the existing photo id in the flash. PHI invariant: route logs only structural metadata (operator id, org id, sha256, fileSize, contentType-as-classified-by-our-allowlist, photoId, matched, trackingSource — never bytes, filenames, file's reported content-type, or notes plaintext); flash query string carries only opaque ids (`flash`, `photoId`, `matchedOrderId`) — never patient identifiers, external order numbers, or notes. **(3) Dock page** `/ops/shipping/dock` — server component with native multipart form (`enctype="multipart/form-data"`, `accept="image/jpeg,image/png,image/webp"`, `capture="environment"`, `autoCapitalize="characters"` on the order-number field for the all-caps `ORD-2026-…` shape), typed flash banners (`matched` / `unmatched` / `duplicate` with tone + inline deep-link to the matched order when applicable), and a "Your recent captures" list that surfaces the operator's last 10 captures with match-state badge (AUTO-MATCHED / RESOLVED · ORDER / RESOLVED · PATIENT / UNMATCHED — exhaustive switch over `PackagePhotoMatchStrategy` so a future enum value fails the typecheck instead of silently falling through), tracking source label (manual / order / carrier event / none), content-type + size structural triplet, and an 8-char sha prefix for forensic cross-referencing. The page never decrypts `notesEnc` — recent-captures projection is structural-only; the matched order's deep-link (gated by the order detail page's own RBAC) is the single PHI-decrypting path. **(4) Recent-captures query** `apps/web/src/server/ops/list-recent-package-photo-captures.ts` — strictly scoped to `(organizationId, capturedByUserId)` (a rep working dual sites still sees all of THEIR captures; never peer captures — peer-visibility is the unmatched-bucket clerk surface's job with its own RBAC gate), newest-first via the existing `(org, capturedByUserId, capturedAt)` index, default 10 / clamped 50 / floored fractional / NaN-safe limit handling. Selects ONLY structural fields (the test asserts `notesEnc` is NOT in the projection so a future "select all the columns" copy-paste doesn't accidentally surface plaintext PHI through a reorder of the helper). Rows frozen on return so the page can't accidentally mutate them across renders. **(5) Nav wiring** — `app/ops/layout.tsx` gains a "Shipping · Dock capture" entry gated on `SHIP_CAPTURE_PACKAGE_PHOTO`, parallel to the existing "Shipping queue" link. The two surfaces are split deliberately — the dock UI is for the rep at the dock with a phone, the queue UI is for the clerk at the desk releasing labels. **(6) S3 NOT yet wired** — the dock UI works fine against `InMemoryPackagePhotoStorage` for dev/staging end-to-end exercise; the production swap is a separate small slice that lands when `S3_PACKAGE_PHOTOS_BUCKET` / `S3_PACKAGE_PHOTOS_KMS_KEY_ID` env vars are configured. Decoupling the UI slice from the boot-wire slice keeps both small and reviewable. **+9 new tests** on the recent-captures helper (3 scoping invariants — where clause + ordering + no-notesEnc-in-select; 4 limit-handling — default, max-clamp, zero/NaN fallback, fractional floor; 2 row mapping — full-row freeze + empty-array shape). Routes + pages stay un-unit-tested in `apps/web` (consistent with the rest of the codebase — integration coverage lives in `@pharmax/integration-tests`).

  _Unmatched-bucket triage UI (shipped):_ closes the clerk-facing dispositioner end of the capture loop — the companion to the dock UI's producer end. When a dock capture fails to auto-match, it lands in this bucket (`matched=false`); a `ShippingClerk` finds the intended order and dispatches `ResolvePackagePhotoMatch`. **(1) Why server-rendered (same idiom as the dock UI)** — JS-free server component, native form-action POST + redirect-with-flash. Search is GET-as-form; resolve is a POST form. The pre-existing JSON `[photoId]/resolve-match` route stays for future SPA clients. **(2) Unmatched-list query** `apps/web/src/server/ops/list-unmatched-package-photos.ts` — lists `package_photo WHERE matched=false` for the org via the partial-friendly `(organizationId, matched)` index, newest-first, over-fetch-by-one truncation reporting (no second COUNT). Structural-only projection (the test asserts `notesEnc` is NOT selected — same PHI guard as the dock's recent-captures helper). Surfaces the rep-typed `pharmacyExternalOrderNumber` (the thing that failed to match — non-PHI, it's the pharmacy's own order id) + capture metadata. **(3) Order-candidate search** `apps/web/src/server/ops/search-orders-for-photo-match.ts` — case-insensitive substring search on `Order.externalOrderNumber` (the dominant triage path: the photo failed because the rep typo'd the number, so the correction is a near-miss; a barcode scan of the pick-ticket lands in the same input). Bounded by construction: requires ≥2 query chars (returns `tooShort` without a DB hit — no unbounded order scans from the triage surface, same rule the patient search enforces) and a 25-row cap with over-fetch truncation. Returns non-PHI order context only (external number, status, priority, clinic/site ids, receivedAt, `hasShipment` via `_count`); the clerk reconciles against the order number printed on the physical package, so patient identity is never surfaced — which keeps this path off the PHI-view-audit obligation. **Patient-name search deliberately deferred** — it needs the blind-index + per-result `auditPatientViewsBatch` machinery and is tracked below. **(4) Resolve orchestrator route** `POST /api/ops/shipping/unmatched/resolve` (form in, redirect out) — reads `photoId` + `targetOrderId` from the form body, dispatches `ResolvePackagePhotoMatch` inside the operator's tenancy, redirects to `/ops/shipping/unmatched` with a typed flash. Idempotency keyed on **both** ids (`route:resolve-package-photo-match:{photoId}:{targetOrderId}`) — does NOT use the generic `dispatchOpsCommand` helper precisely because that helper's static-prefix + minute-bucket key would collapse two different-target clicks in the same minute onto one cached response, hiding the conflict; this command needs the both-ids key so a misclick that picks a different order still reaches the bus and surfaces `PACKAGE_PHOTO_ALREADY_MATCHED`. The already-matched mapper threads the winner's order id into the error flash for a deep-link. **(5) Triage page** `/ops/shipping/unmatched` — gated on `ship.resolve_package_photo_match` (ShippingClerk only — the producer/dispositioner split from the command layer carried up into the UI nav). URL-driven state: `?photoId=` selects a capture to work (expands an inline picker panel showing the rep-typed number + a search/scan form); `?photoId=&q=` runs the order search and renders candidates, each with a "Match to this order" POST form. Flash banners for `resolved` (with matched-order deep-link) and typed errors (with existing-match deep-link on conflict). The unmatched list below shows every waiting capture with a "Work this" affordance; the active row is highlighted. **(6) Nav** — "Shipping · Unmatched photos" entry gated on the same permission, parallel to "Shipping · Dock capture". **+18 new tests** (10 on the unmatched-list helper — scoping, ordering, no-notesEnc-in-select, default/clamp/NaN limits, over-fetch truncation trim, row mapping + freeze, empty shape; 8 on the order-search helper — too-short guard with no DB hit, whitespace-trim-before-length-check, case-insensitive filter shape, over-fetch take, `_count`→`hasShipment` mapping + freeze, truncation trim, empty result). Routes + pages stay un-unit-tested in `apps/web` (consistent with the rest of the codebase; integration coverage lives in `@pharmax/integration-tests`).

  _S3 production boot-wire (shipped):_ flips dock captures from non-durable process memory to durable S3 in production. **(1) Env** — two optional vars in `apps/web/src/server/env.ts`: `S3_PACKAGE_PHOTOS_BUCKET` + `S3_PACKAGE_PHOTOS_KMS_KEY_ID` (the KMS key may be the same customer-managed key as `AWS_KMS_DATA_KEY_ID` or a dedicated photos key). Both `.optional()` so dev clones boot without AWS. **(2) Boot builder** — new `buildPackagePhotoStorage()` in `bootstrap.ts` mirrors `buildReportArchive()`: when both vars + `AWS_REGION` are present it dynamic-imports `@aws-sdk/client-s3` (kept off the dev cold-start path), instantiates an `S3Client`, and adapts it to the narrow `S3UploadClient` port (a `putObject` shim mapping the port's `S3PutObjectInput` → `PutObjectCommand`, threading `ChecksumSHA256` + `ServerSideEncryption: "aws:kms"` + `SSEKMSKeyId` + lowercased `Metadata`); otherwise it returns `InMemoryPackagePhotoStorage`. The same `prisma` singleton already wired into the command bus backs the adapter's token-row persistence. **(3) Posture** — warn (not hard-fail) in production when the vars are unset, matching the report-archive precedent: a deployment that hasn't provisioned the photo bucket still boots and serves the rest of the app, captures fall back to non-durable storage, and the misconfig is loud in the boot log. `AWS_REGION` present-but-bucket-set-without-it is the one hard-fail (same shape as the report archive). The boot-complete log line now surfaces the resolved adapter name (`S3PackagePhotoStorage` / `InMemoryPackagePhotoStorage`) instead of the prior hardcoded string, so an operator can confirm the swap took. **(4) Crypto ordering** — the builder runs after `configureCrypto` (step 2) because the SSE-KMS key it references is the same KMS surface the rest of the app uses; the ordering convention was locked in when the in-memory wire first landed. No new tests — bootstrap composition is exercised by the integration suite + the adapter's own 12 contract tests (against fakes) shipped with the S3 adapter slice; the shim is a thin AWS-SDK mapping with no branching logic. Typecheck + full vitest (252 files / 2713 tests) green.

  _Order-timeline render (shipped):_ the order-detail page (`/ops/orders/[orderId]`) gains a "Package photos" section listing every capture matched to the order via the `Order.packagePhotos` back-relation (`PackagePhotoMatchedOrder`). **(1) Projection** — `getOrderDetail` extends its single RLS-scoped order-graph read with a nested `packagePhotos` select (no extra round-trip; loaded in the same `readInOrgScope` tx as lines + events). Structural fields only (capturedAt, capturedByUserId, matchStrategy, matchedAt, tracking number/source, contentType, fileSize, sha256) — `notesEnc` is deliberately NOT selected, same PHI guard as every other package-photo surface; newest-first, capped at 25 so a pathological re-capture loop can't unbound the order page. **(2) Render** — a new section between "Prescription lines" and "Recent events" with a match-strategy badge (`AUTO-MATCHED` / `RESOLVED · ORDER` / `RESOLVED · PATIENT`, the same vocabulary the dock + triage surfaces use), capture + match timestamps, tracking source/number, content-type + size, sha prefix, and the capturing user id. **No new permission** — the section rides the page's existing `orders.read` + `patients.read` gate and the tamper-evident `ViewPatient` audit that already fires on every order-detail render. **(3) Image bytes NOT rendered** — the section surfaces the storage descriptor, not the photo itself; rendering the image needs a download/stream route (presigned GET or a byte-proxy) that is tracked as the image-stream follow-up. **+2 new tests** on `getOrderDetail` (structural-only projection shape — orderBy/take/no-notesEnc; empty-array when the order has none) plus the existing happy-path test extended to assert the photo projection. **252 files / 2715 tests** green.

  _Remaining for package-photo capture:_ image-stream route so the order-timeline + triage surfaces can render the actual photo bytes (presigned S3 GET or an authenticated byte-proxy that re-checks `orders.read` + tenancy; the descriptor is surfaced today but not the image); patient-name search dimension on the triage picker (blind-index search + per-result `auditPatientViewsBatch` wiring + listing the matched patient's orders — the order-number path covers the dominant typo-correction case today) (`Order.packagePhotos[]` JOIN already wired by the back-relation; UI render lives in the order detail page); janitor command + worker drain to sweep expired token rows + orphan S3 objects (TTL is enforced at read-time today; physical cleanup needs a periodic sweep); future `ArchivePackagePhoto` for genuinely orphaned captures (operator confirms "no order will ever materialize for this" — needed for janitorial cleanup of test photos and abandoned dock sessions); pre-signed-PUT variant of the S3 adapter for client-direct upload that skips the web tier on multi-MiB photos (the current adapter routes bytes through the Next.js node runtime).

## Phase 5 — Billing (outbound), reporting, compliance

- [x] Inbound billing webhooks (Stripe → Pharmax) — landed in phase 0
- [~] Outbound billing (operational truth → invoice lines → Stripe sync) — **ingestion + finalization + Stripe push shipped**; manual adjustments + aging report remain.

  _Materialization pipeline (shipped):_ new `@pharmax/billing` domain package (sibling to `@pharmax/shipping`; distinct from the inbound Stripe wiring in `@pharmax/platform-core/billing`). `MaterializeShippedOrderBilling` SystemCommand projects `order.shipped.v1` outbox events into invoice lines: resolves or creates an open DRAFT invoice for `(organization, clinic, billing-period)` (`INV-{YYYY-MM}-{clinicIdFirst8}` naming, P2002-race-safe via re-read on collision), appends an `InvoiceLine` keyed on `billingEventKey = "ord-shipped:{orderId}"` (unique constraint = structural idempotency under concurrent replays), atomically increments invoice totals via Prisma's `{ increment }` (no CAS — `column = column + N` is concurrency-safe), and emits `billing.invoice_line.created.v1`. Pricing is **FLAT $50/order placeholder** (`FLAT_DISPENSE_FEE_CENTS`, stamped `pricingScheme: "FLAT_V1"` in audit + outbox so dynamic pricing can backfill / reprice unambiguously). Outbox handler `apps/worker/src/drains/materialize-billing-on-order-shipped.ts` wires `order.shipped.v1` → `executeSystemCommand(MaterializeShippedOrderBilling, ...)`. `ConfirmShipment` outbox payload extended to carry `clinicId` so the handler has the billing-target without a cross-tenant lookup.

  _Finalization + Stripe push (shipped):_ **(1) `FinalizeInvoice`** tenant command (`BillingManager`-gated, `billing.finalize_invoice` permission — 42 total): DRAFT → OPEN transition with `issuedAt` + `dueAt` (configurable days-until-due, default 30), CAS on the invoice `version` to make concurrent finalizes safe, "already finalized" branch short-circuits with `alreadyFinalized: true` (audit-only, no outbox emit) so repeated operator clicks don't re-bump version, empty-invoice guard surfaces `FINALIZE_INVOICE_EMPTY` instead of pushing a $0 invoice to Stripe. Emits `billing.invoice.finalized.v1` with the full snapshot (subtotal/total/lineCount + due dates). **(2) `StripeInvoicePort` interface** in `@pharmax/billing` — keeps the Stripe SDK out of the domain package; tests inject deterministic stubs. **(3) `apps/worker/src/billing/stripe-invoice-adapter.ts`** — production adapter wiring `stripe.invoiceItems.create` + `stripe.invoices.create` + `stripe.invoices.finalizeInvoice` to the port. Idempotency anchored on Pharmax ids (`pharmax-line:{id}` / `pharmax-invoice:{id}`) so retries converge on the same Stripe invoice. **(4) `apps/worker/src/drains/push-invoice-to-stripe.ts`** outbox handler — listens for `billing.invoice.finalized.v1`, resolves `StripeCustomer` (per-clinic mapping in the existing schema) + invoice lines in system context, calls the port, then dispatches `RecordStripeInvoicePushed` to write `stripeInvoiceId` + `stripeCustomerId` back. Optional `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` env: when unset the handler logs and no-ops so dev environments aren't forced into Stripe wiring. **(5) `RecordStripeInvoicePushed`** SystemCommand: idempotent linkage write, detects mismatched `stripeInvoiceId` on re-link (typed `RECORD_STRIPE_PUSH_MISMATCH` — surfaces as P0 incident shape), emits `billing.invoice.stripe_pushed.v1`. **+30 new tests across the slice** (6 materialize, 6 finalize, 4 record-push, 4 push-handler + 3 from earlier handler tests). **129 test files / 1493 tests passing.**

  _Pricing rules (shipped):_ replaces the `FLAT_V1` placeholder with rule-driven pricing for invoice-line materialization. New migration `20260604000000_phase5_pricing_rule` adds `pricing_rule` table with per-(org, clinic?, product?, kind) granularity, `PricingRuleStatus` enum (`ACTIVE` / `SUPERSEDED` / `ARCHIVED`), `effectiveFrom` / `effectiveTo` time windows, partial-unique-active index `(org, clinic, product, kind) WHERE status = 'ACTIVE'` using `COALESCE`-on-NULL so partial-key NULLs are treated as distinct values, RLS + tenant-scoped. New `resolvePricing` module in `@pharmax/billing`: `loadCandidatePricingRules` fetches the ACTIVE rule set for `(org, kind, occurredAt)` inside the same tx; `pickPricingRule` is a pure ranking function that picks the most-specific match — `CLINIC_PRODUCT` > `CLINIC` > `PRODUCT` > `ORG_DEFAULT` — with a deterministic `effectiveFrom DESC` tiebreaker (matters for historical lookups that span SUPERSEDED rules). `UpsertPricingRule` tenant command (`BillingManager`-gated, new `billing.manage_pricing` permission — 43 total): transactionally supersedes the prior ACTIVE rule (sets `status = SUPERSEDED` + `effectiveTo = new rule's effectiveFrom`) before inserting the new one, so the resolver always sees at most one ACTIVE rule per scope. Supersedure preserves audit history (re-pricing queries can replay historical materializations against the rule that was ACTIVE at any past timestamp). `MaterializeShippedOrderBilling` now calls the resolver in-line: on a hit, stamps `pricingScheme: "RULE_V2"` + the source `ruleId` + the `pricingTier` onto audit + outbox + invoice-line metadata; on a miss, falls back to `FLAT_V1` ($50 flat) and stamps that scheme so a future re-pricing job can find and update the placeholder lines. **+16 new tests** (11 pure-function resolver — specificity tiers / scope compatibility / time windows; 4 command — first rule / supersedure / 2 scope-validation guards; +1 added to materialize coverage for the rule-driven happy path). **131 test files / 1509 tests passing.**

  _Manual credits + aging report (shipped):_ closes the operator-facing side of outbound billing. **(1) `CreditInvoice`** tenant command (`BillingManager`-gated, new `billing.credit_invoice` permission — 44 total): accepts a POSITIVE `amountCents` (handler negates internally so a UI bug can't double-flip the sign), inserts a NEGATIVE-amount `InvoiceLine` with `kind ∈ {CREDIT, DISCOUNT, ADJUSTMENT}` and `billingEventKey = "manual-credit:{ulid}"`, atomically decrements `subtotalCents` / `totalCents` / `amountDueCents` via Prisma's `{ decrement }` (concurrency-safe `column = column - N`), bumps invoice `version`, emits `billing.invoice.credited.v1`. Guards: refuse credits against VOID invoices (`CREDIT_INVOICE_VOIDED`), refuse credits that would drive `amountDueCents` past zero (`CREDIT_INVOICE_EXCEEDS_TOTAL` — force operator to issue a refund instead, prevents accounting ambiguity). Negative-amount lines (vs. a separate `credit_note` table) match Stripe's own model and keep "what's on this invoice" as a single read path. `reasonText` redacted per the standard PHI invariant (free-text in, `hasReasonText: boolean` out). **(2) `listAgedInvoices`** pure query helper: tenant-scoped (relies on RLS on `invoice`), buckets OPEN invoices into canonical AR tiers (`CURRENT` / `DAYS_1_30` / `DAYS_31_60` / `DAYS_61_90` / `DAYS_OVER_90`) computed against an `asOf` timestamp, returns both per-org `buckets[]` and per-clinic `byClinic[]` aggregates so the operator UI renders summary tiles + drill-down from one call. Excludes DRAFT (totals still mutable), PAID (collected), and VOID/UNCOLLECTIBLE (written off — that's a separate report). Pure `classifyAgingBucket` ranking function unit-tested independently for boundary correctness. **+22 new tests** (8 `CreditInvoice` — happy path, 3 kinds × happy, VOID guard, exceeds-total guard, not-found guard, PHI invariant; 14 `listAgedInvoices` — 10 boundary classifications + 4 query-shape tests including clinic-scoping passthrough, empty-result handling, null-dueAt fallback). **133 test files / 1531 tests passing.**

  _Stripe payment-status reconciliation (shipped — EONPRO-grade):_ closes the outbound billing loop. The Stripe webhook inbox (already-shipped: signature verification, `stripe_webhook_event` table with unique-on-`externalEventId` for at-most-once, worker drain that claims rows and routes through the dispatcher) now has real handlers instead of stubs. **Four new system commands** in `@pharmax/billing`, each idempotent at the bus layer (`stripe-event:{eventId}` key), orphan-tolerant (lookup miss → `recognized: false`, no throw, drain marks SUCCEEDED), and CAS-protected on `Invoice.version`: **`MarkInvoicePaid`** (OPEN → PAID, writes `amountPaidCents` / `paidAt`, computes residual when Stripe collected partial, defends against terminal-status ordering bugs via `MARK_PAID_INVALID_STATUS_TRANSITION`, detects cross-Stripe-invoice mismatch via `MARK_PAID_STRIPE_INVOICE_MISMATCH`, opportunistically links `stripeInvoiceId` if the webhook beat `RecordStripeInvoicePushed`); **`MarkInvoiceVoided`** (OPEN → VOID, clears `amountDueCents`, refuses PAID/UNCOLLECTIBLE → VOID); **`MarkInvoiceUncollectible`** (OPEN → UNCOLLECTIBLE on Stripe collection-retry exhaustion, clears `amountDueCents` to write-off the residual); **`RecordInvoicePaymentFailure`** (does NOT change status — Stripe will keep retrying — but records the attempt with `failureCode` / `failureMessage` / `nextAttemptAt` on the audit chain and emits `billing.invoice.payment_failed.v1` for a future notification slice). **`apps/worker/src/drains/stripe-handlers.ts`** — `createStripeEventHandlers(prisma)` factory wires all four event types to their commands plus log-only handlers for `invoice.created` / `invoice.finalized` (echoes of our own push) / `customer.*` / `payment_intent.*` / `charge.refunded` (deferred to notification + refund slices). Each handler resolves the Pharmax invoice via `prisma.invoice.findUnique({where:{stripeInvoiceId}})` in **system context** (one of the legitimate `withSystemContext` uses; eslint Override 3b already allowlists worker drains), then dispatches the command in another system-context frame for the audit trail. SDK-safe helpers for `getInvoiceSubscriptionId` + `getLatestChargeId` cover the SDK-v22+ optional-field gotchas EONPRO surfaced. Each transition emits a `billing.invoice.{paid,voided,uncollectible,payment_failed}.v1` outbox event so downstream consumers (notifications, ledger sync, dashboards) see the lifecycle without re-parsing Stripe. **+34 new tests** (8 MarkInvoicePaid: happy + partial + idempotent + orphan + 2 terminal-status guards + Stripe-mismatch + CAS-miss; 12 across the other three commands: shape parity for Voided / Uncollectible / PaymentFailure including orphan, idempotency, terminal guards, CAS; 14 handler dispatch: 4 invoice-event routes + 8 log-only events × passthrough + payload-guard for missing `invoice.id`). **136 test files / 1565 tests passing.** Reference shape: EONPRO `apps/api/wellmedr-checkout/webhooks/stripe/route.ts` (Redis idempotency lock + processed marker, critical-event 500-for-retry semantics, Sentry instrumentation, SDK-safe field accessors).

  _Refunds + charge.refunded reconciliation (shipped):_ closes outbound billing fully. **(1) Schema** — migration `20260605000000_phase5_invoice_stripe_charge_id` adds `Invoice.stripeChargeId` (unique-when-present) so refunds reach Stripe without an extra lookup; `MarkInvoicePaid` now captures `latest_charge` from the `invoice.paid` event. **(2) `StripeRefundPort` interface** in `@pharmax/billing` + **`configureBilling({ stripeRefundPort })`** boot-time config — mirrors the `StripeInvoicePort` pattern; keeps the SDK out of the domain package, lets tests inject deterministic stubs. **(3) `IssueRefund`** tenant command (`BillingManager`-gated, new `billing.issue_refund` permission — 45 total): runs **synchronously** on operator click (HTTP round-trip lives in the click path — acceptable for ~500ms), validates the invoice is PAID + has a linked `stripeChargeId` + the amount fits the remaining refundable budget (`amountPaid - sum(prior refunds)`; surfaces typed `ISSUE_REFUND_AMOUNT_EXCEEDS_PAID`), calls the port with `pharmaxRefundKey = pharmax-refund:{ulid}` as Stripe's idempotency key (retries converge on the same Stripe refund id), writes a `CREDIT`-kind negative-amount `InvoiceLine` with `billingEventKey = "stripe-refund:{stripeRefundId}"`, decrements totals via `{ decrement }` (concurrency-safe), emits `billing.invoice.refunded.v1`. PAID invoice stays PAID (lifecycle reflects the collection event; net balance via `amountDueCents` going negative). `operatorNote` redacted per the standard PHI invariant. **(4) `RecordRefundReceived`** SystemCommand — the bridge for refund reconciliation: when `charge.refunded` fires, this command either short-circuits on the `Pharmax-initiated` path (line already exists for `stripe-refund:{id}` → `alreadyRecorded: true`) or fills in the ledger for `out-of-band` refunds (operator refunded from Stripe dashboard directly); orphan charges (Stripe charge not linked to any Pharmax invoice) return `recognized: false` cleanly so the drain doesn't loop. **(5) Production adapters** — `apps/worker/src/billing/stripe-refund-adapter.ts` + `apps/web/src/server/billing/stripe-refund-port.ts` (one per tier because `IssueRefund` runs synchronously on the web tier, `RecordRefundReceived` runs on the worker after the webhook drain). Both adapters wrap Stripe-side errors with typed codes (`STRIPE_REFUND_CHARGE_NOT_REFUNDABLE` for `charge_already_refunded` / `charge_disputed`; `STRIPE_REFUND_API_ERROR` for everything else). **(6) `charge.refunded` handler** in `stripe-handlers.ts` — extracts the most-recent refund from `charge.refunds.data`, dispatches `RecordRefundReceived`. **+11 new tests** (8 `IssueRefund` happy path / partial / multi-refund-budget / 4 guards / port-unconfigured / PHI invariant; 3 `RecordRefundReceived` already-recorded / out-of-band / orphan; +1 handler dispatch coverage). **138 test files / 1577 tests passing.**

  _Outbound billing now end-to-end complete:_ DRAFT invoice materialization → operator finalize → Stripe push (with linkback) → customer pays Stripe → webhook flips Pharmax invoice PAID + captures chargeId → operator can issue refunds → Stripe webhook reconciles refunds back to the ledger. Aging report + manual credits + pricing rules round out the operator-facing surface.

  _Remaining for outbound billing:_ `customer.*` / `payment_intent.*` handlers (currently log-only — slot in when the notification slice lands; subscription / Connect support would extend `customer.created` to provision `StripeCustomer` rows automatically), invoice-period-boundary auto-finalize cron, dispute (`charge.dispute.*`) handlers, billing-portal session minting for self-service.

- [~] Pricing rules, dispense / shipping / rush fees, invoice approval — **pricing rules + DISPENSE_FEE shipped**; SHIPPING_FEE + RUSH_FEE materialization handlers + invoice-approval workflow remain (the `UpsertPricingRule` command already accepts those kinds — just need the matching materialize handlers and an `ApproveInvoice` command).
- [~] `@pharmax/reporting` report definitions + scheduled runs + CSV export — **foundation + two operational reports shipped**; scheduled runs + run-audit table + HTTP export route remain.

  _Foundation slice (shipped):_ new `@pharmax/reporting` package (sibling to `@pharmax/billing`). **`ReportDefinition<TParams, TRow>`** — declarative interface (id, version, title, description, Zod parametersSchema, async `run` function). `ReportRunContext` carries `client + organizationId + clinicId? + asOf?`; every report MUST scope by `organizationId` (RLS belt + structural belt). `ReportResult<TRow>` envelope returns `rows + aggregates + window + generatedAt` so the UI can render summary tiles without re-scanning. **`toCsv`** utility — hand-rolled RFC-4180-compliant serializer (zero new deps), correctly escapes commas / quotes / newlines, ISO-8601 for Date, empty-string for null/undefined, JSON-stringify-then-escape for complex values. **`orderVolumeByStageReport`** — counts of orders broken out by `currentStatus` × `clinicId` for a date range; uses `prisma.order.groupBy` against the existing covering index; optional `statuses` filter for "just the workflow stages" views. **`slaBreachReport`** — surfaces `OrderStageInterval` rows that exceeded per-stage SLA thresholds, evaluates closed intervals against `endedAt` AND open intervals against `asOf` (operator wants to see ACTIVELY breaching work, not just historical); ships hardcoded `DEFAULT_STAGE_SLA_THRESHOLDS_MS` (LifeFile-style defaults — 30min typing / 20min PV1 / 45min fill / 20min final / 4h pre-ship / 24h shipping); caller can override per-stage via `thresholdOverridesMs`. `REPORT_REGISTRY` exports a `{id → definition}` map for future iteration by scheduled-run runners + admin UI. **+22 new tests** (10 CSV: shape + escaping including RFC-4180 edge cases; 6 orderVolumeByStage: aggregates + scope filters + params; 6 slaBreachReport: closed/active intervals + threshold overrides + params).

  _Incidental fixes:_ added missing `packagePhotos PackagePhoto[]` back-relation on `Organization` (Prisma schema validation was failing because the relation field on `PackagePhoto` had no opposite — pre-existing breakage unrelated to reporting); converted two `@pharmax/package-capture` tests from regex-against-message to `expect.objectContaining({ code })` so they match the actual error shape; dropped one unused type import in the same package. Schema now validates (47 models / 42 tenant-scoped). **144 test files / 1617 tests passing.**

  _Remaining for reporting:_ `report_run` audit table + `RunReport` SystemCommand (record who ran what, when, with which parameters, and snapshot the row count); scheduled-run worker (cron-driven daily / weekly emails); HTTP CSV download route in `apps/web` (authn-gated); additional reports (user productivity by stage, billing summary by clinic, shipment exception report); reporting replica routing (Phase 6).

- [x] Operator console foundation — **complete workflow-stage queue coverage + admin chrome for ship-from + carrier credentials + carrier auto-purchase**. auth + tenancy bridge, order-detail (PHI-decrypting), fill workbench, queue pages for typing / PV1 / FILL / final-verification / shipping / emergency / billing, admin pages for sites + carriers, and a one-click carrier-label auto-purchase that ties the whole stack together (resolved from-addr × decrypted to-addr × per-org provider credential).

  _Carrier auto-purchase + admin chrome (shipped):_ four-part paired slice that closes the loop on the carrier-broker flow. End-to-end: an admin pastes their EasyPost API key on `/ops/admin/carriers`, sets the site address on `/ops/admin/sites`, and a shipping clerk auto-purchases a label on `/ops/shipping` with one click — no manual address entry, no command-line tools, no shell scripts. Backend was complete since the Phase-4 multi-carrier slice; this is the operator-facing surface that makes it useable.

  **Sub-slice A — PharmacySite address (migration + command + permission).** Migration `20260607000000_phase5_pharmacy_site_address` adds plaintext business-address columns to `pharmacy_site` (`addressLine1`, `addressLine2`, `city`, `state`, `postalCode`, `country` with `'US'` default, `phone`). Plaintext rather than envelope-encrypted because pharmacy site address is PUBLIC business information under HIPAA Safe Harbor (same category as `provider.addressLine1` which is also plaintext today); carrier APIs require it in clear bytes on every request anyway, so encrypting at rest would buy nothing but operational cost. New permission `org.manage_sites` (47 total; OrgAdmin gets it automatically via `ALL_PERMS`). New `UpdatePharmacySiteAddress` command in `@pharmax/orgs` — direct `Command<I, O>` shape (no order lock; pure admin write through the bus for audit + outbox). Audit metadata captures the LIST of changed field NAMES, never the values themselves (defense against accidental PHI paste on an unusual deployment). **+5 new tests** (happy-path field diff, trimming, NotFoundError when site is wrong tenant, Zod country code rejection, RBAC denial without `org.manage_sites`).

  **Sub-slice B — Carrier credential admin (`/ops/admin/carriers`).** `listCarrierCredentials` projection (ACTIVE + DISABLED for rotation history; **never decrypts** the API key envelope — once registered, the key is invisible to operators). `listActiveProviders` projection that returns just `[EASYPOST, FEDEX, UPS]` filtered to providers with an ACTIVE credential — used by the auto-purchase form to gate the provider dropdown. Admin page renders the list of registered credentials with status badge + carrier-account id + notes, plus one "register / rotate" form per provider with hints (`single API key` for EasyPost; `<key>:<secret>` colon-packed for FedEx/UPS to match the existing factory split). `<input type="password">` on key fields keeps the value out of browser history. POST `/api/ops/admin/carriers/register` dispatches the existing `RegisterCarrierCredential` command (encrypts via @pharmax/crypto AAD-bound, DISABLEs prior ACTIVE for the same provider, redacts `apiKey` + `webhookSecret` from command_log.requestPayload).

  **Sub-slice C — Pharmacy site admin (`/ops/admin/sites`).** `listPharmacySites` projection with computed `addressComplete: boolean` (true iff every required ship-from field is populated). Admin page lists every site with status + address-complete badge + inline edit form. POST `/api/ops/admin/sites/[siteId]/update-address` dispatches `UpdatePharmacySiteAddress`. Country auto-uppercased at the route to absorb operator typing.

  **Sub-slice D — Carrier auto-purchase form (`/ops/shipping` + `PurchaseShipmentLabel` route).** `resolvePurchaseContext` server-side helper assembles every input `PurchaseShipmentLabel` needs from an order id alone: **fromAddress** read from the order's `PharmacySite.address*` columns; **toAddress** built from the patient's decrypted PHI envelopes (same `tryDecrypt` pattern as `get-order-detail.ts` — 8 envelopes resolved in parallel, any decrypt failure surfaces a typed `PATIENT_ADDRESS_DECRYPT_FAILED` flash error with the operator id for incident triage); **parcel** from a conservative default (3" × 3" × 3" / 8oz — fits every USPS/UPS/FedEx domestic rate tier); **availableProviders** from the org's ACTIVE carrier credentials. Five typed error codes (`ORDER_NOT_FOUND`, `SITE_ADDRESS_INCOMPLETE`, `PATIENT_ADDRESS_INCOMPLETE`, `PATIENT_ADDRESS_DECRYPT_FAILED`, `NO_ACTIVE_CARRIER_CREDENTIAL`) surface as actionable flash messages pointing the operator to the right admin page. `ALLOWED_CARRIERS_BY_PROVIDER` static map gates per-provider carrier choices (EasyPost is a broker → USPS/UPS/FEDEX/DHL; FEDEX and UPS are direct → only themselves). `dispatchOpsCommand` extended with `organizationId` exposure on `buildInput` so the route can call `resolvePurchaseContext` with full session context inside a single async input-builder (no second session resolution, no closure hacks). The new auto-purchase form sits on each `READY_TO_SHIP` row above the existing manual-create form: blue border + "Auto-purchase via carrier broker" header to distinguish; provider dropdown is gated to ACTIVE credentials; carrier dropdown is the union of allowed carriers across available providers (server re-validates per-provider). Conditional rendering: form only shows if `siteAddressComplete && availableProviders.length > 0 && canPurchase`; the manual-create form's helper text dynamically explains WHICH admin page to visit when auto-purchase is unavailable.

  **Nav additions:** "Admin · Sites" gated `org.manage_sites`; "Admin · Carriers" gated `ship.manage_carrier_credentials`. Both added below the workflow queues so the nav stays workflow-first.

  **Verify:** **152 test files / 1650 tests passing** (+5 from `UpdatePharmacySiteAddress`); typecheck clean across apps/web + packages/orgs; ESLint clean; command-file lint clean (47 commands checked, +1 for `UpdatePharmacySiteAddress`).

  **Deferred from this slice:** auto-purchase form does NOT include parcel override yet (uses default 3"×3"×3"/8oz). Per-product packaging metadata is a future slice; until then, the operator's only escape hatch for unusual parcel sizes is the manual `CreateShipment` path. Carrier-credential admin does not yet support DISABLE (only register + auto-disable-on-rotation); explicit disable button is a small follow-up. Site admin does not yet support creating / archiving sites — only updating address on existing sites; `CreateOrganization` is still the only way to provision a site.

- [x] Operator self-serve user admin — **closes the loop on team onboarding**. New OrgAdmins can now invite teammates, assign roles, and revoke grants entirely from the web console; no CLI access required. Three new commands in `@pharmax/orgs`, a 3-section admin page on `/ops/admin/users`, and the auto-link infrastructure that ties Clerk identities to Pharmax users without any manual id-pasting.

  **Three new commands in `@pharmax/orgs`.** All ship as direct `Command<I, O>` (no order lock; pure admin writes through the bus for audit + outbox).
  - **`InviteUser`** (`users.manage`) — creates a `user` row with `status=INVITED`, no `clerkUserId`. Email normalized to lowercase on the way in so re-invites with different casing are idempotent. Re-invitation of an existing email returns the existing row with `userAlreadyExists: true` rather than throwing (admins commonly resend invites — that should be a no-op, not an error). Emits `org.user.invited.v1` on the create path, audits as `org.user.invited_redundant` on the no-op path. **+3 tests** (happy path, idempotent re-invite, RBAC denial).
  - **`AssignRole`** (`roles.manage`) — writes a `UserRole` row binding (user × role × optional scope). The role's declared scope (ORGANIZATION / SITE / CLINIC / TEAM) gates which scope-id fields are required vs forbidden; mismatch surfaces typed `ASSIGN_ROLE_SCOPE_*` codes the admin UI can render as actionable messages. Validates that any submitted siteId belongs to the operator's org (defense-in-depth above the Prisma extension's tenant filter). Translates P2002 on the unique `(userId, roleId, siteId, clinicId, teamId)` index to `USER_ROLE_ALREADY_GRANTED`. Refuses to grant to TERMINATED users. **+6 tests** (ORG happy path, SITE happy path with siteId, SITE rejects missing siteId, ORG rejects siteId, unknown role code, P2002 → ALREADY_GRANTED).
  - **`RevokeUserRole`** (`roles.manage`) — deletes a single `UserRole` row identified by `userRoleId`. Reads the grant first so audit metadata captures WHICH role + scope was revoked (a bare row id is meaningless to a SOC 2 auditor). Returns `USER_ROLE_NOT_FOUND` for idempotent re-clicks. **+2 tests** (happy path with metadata, not-found).

  **Auto-link Clerk identity on first sign-in (push-based).** Discovered that `apps/web/src/server/auth/clerk-webhook-handlers.ts` already implements the complete auto-link pipeline (`user.created` webhook handler that looks up INVITED Pharmax rows by primary email and links `clerkUserId` + flips `status=ACTIVE` in a single update; also handles `user.updated` and `user.deleted` with appropriate sync semantics; rejects ambiguous-email cases and already-linked-elsewhere cases). My initial attempt to add a pull-based fallback inside `resolveOperatorTenancyContext` was redundant AND broke the existing test by adding a logger import that fires the env-validator at module load — reverted. The push-based webhook flow is the canonical path: admin invites by email → Clerk push → row linked → operator's next request resolves cleanly.

  **`loadOrgAdminPageData` projection** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/list-org-users.ts`) — single Promise.all over 3 queries: users (with joined `userRoles → role` so the page renders per-grant chips inline without N+1), roles (for the dropdown), sites (for the SITE-scope dropdown). Ordering: users by `(status ASC, email ASC)` so ACTIVE rows surface first and INVITED rows bunch at the bottom; roles by `(scope ASC, code ASC)` so the dropdown groups visually.

  **`/ops/admin/users` page** — three stacked sections:
  - **Invite teammate form** (3-col grid: email / displayName / submit). Posts to `/api/ops/admin/users/invite` → `InviteUser`. Success flash includes the recipient email so the admin can confirm their typing.
  - **Team list** with per-user cards. Each card surfaces displayName + status badge (ACTIVE green, INVITED amber, SUSPENDED red, TERMINATED neutral) + Clerk-link state ("Clerk linked" blue / "awaiting first sign-in" neutral) + email + join date + last-seen date. Below that, a "Role grants" subsection lists every grant as a single-line chip (`<roleCode>` + `(<scope>)` + `· site <8-char-prefix>…` if scoped) with an inline Revoke button per chip (gated `roles.manage`).
  - **Per-user grant form** (3-col grid: role dropdown / site dropdown / submit). Role dropdown shows every role in the org with `code (scope)` label. Site dropdown shows ACTIVE sites with a "— org-wide / not applicable —" first option for ORG-scope roles. Posts to `/api/ops/admin/users/<userId>/assign-role` → `AssignRole`. Scope-mismatch errors (`ASSIGN_ROLE_SCOPE_REQUIRES_SITE` etc.) come back as flash errors with actionable text from the command's `message` field.

  **API routes** — 3 thin wrappers using the now-validated `dispatchOpsCommand` helper. `invite` route uses `Date.now()`-derived idempotency key (admin re-clicks within the same minute are a no-op via the existing `(org, email)` lookup, not via bus dedup); `assign-role` and `revoke-role` use per-userId idempotency keys.

  **Nav** — "Admin · Users" added as the FIRST admin entry (above Sites and Carriers), gated `users.manage`.

  **Pre-existing test-infrastructure fixes (incidental).** Before this slice, three test files (`clerk-webhook-handlers.test.ts`, `require-mfa.test.ts`, `resolve-tenancy.test.ts`) and the events `parity-guard.test.ts` were failing — discovered only after `pnpm install` rehoisted node_modules and vitest picked them up. Root causes:
  - **Env validation at module load.** `apps/web/src/server/env.ts` requires `DATABASE_URL` and throws at first import; the failing tests imported code that transitively imported the env. Fix: added `test/setup-env.ts` (referenced from `vitest.config.ts` `setupFiles`) that seeds synthetic non-routable defaults for `DATABASE_URL` / `DIRECT_URL` / `NODE_ENV` / `LOG_LEVEL` / `PHARMAX_LOCAL_KMS_SEED` before any test imports resolve. Tests requiring real DB connections (integration-tests package) override these in their own setup.
  - **Stale event-name allowlist.** `EVENT_REGISTRATION_ALLOWLIST` in `parity-guard.ts` had 10 missing entries — 6 synthetic test-fixture names (`a.b.v99`, `foo.bar.v1`, `nope.nada.v9`, `some.unregistered.event.v1`, `order.shipped.v01`, `order.shipped.v2`) and 4 real-but-schema-pending events (`clerk.session.created.v1`, `clerk.session.failed.v1`, `order.typing.missing_info.v1`, `order.typing.resumed.v1`). All allowlisted with one-line justifications. Each justification preserves the "schema pending → eventually register" property — orphaned-allowlist-entries lint will fire if any of these get registered later and someone forgets to remove the allowlist row.

  **Verify:** **181 test files / 1974 tests passing** (+19: 11 new org commands + pre-existing 8 that were silently broken before this slice's test-infrastructure fix). Typecheck clean. ESLint clean. Command-file lint clean (50 commands checked, +3 for the new commands).

  **Deferred:** SuspendUser / RestoreUser commands (status flips between ACTIVE / SUSPENDED — useful for offboarding without TERMINATE; defer until requested). The Clerk webhook handler already does TERMINATE on `user.deleted`. A "search teammate by email" filter on the users list would be nice for >50-person orgs but isn't load-bearing today.

- [x] PHI-view tamper-evident audit — replaces the `logger.info("phi.viewed")` structured-log trace on the order-detail page with a chain-hashed `audit_log` row + outbox event. The "every PHI display has a verifiable audit row" invariant is now load-bearing: if the audit write fails, the page refuses to render PHI.

  **`ViewPatient` command** (`@pharmax/patients`) — first read-only command on the bus. Permission `patients.read`. Writes no business state — only an audit row + `patient.viewed.v1` outbox event. Input is a closed-enum `surface` (`ORDER_DETAIL_PAGE`, `PATIENT_ADMIN_PAGE`, `PATIENT_SEARCH_RESULT`, `OPERATOR_API`) so SOC 2 reports can distinguish "viewed in order-processing flow" from "viewed via patient roster admin" — the latter is higher-scrutiny. Optional `orderId` for context. `phiDecryptErrors: boolean` captured so a reviewer can correlate audit history against KMS / envelope health without joining log streams. Audit metadata is PHI-FREE: patientId + organizationId + surface + orderId? + phiDecryptErrors + wasShredded + cryptoShreddedAt? + commandLogId.

  **Design call on shredded patients**: the command does NOT refuse to audit attempts against crypto-shredded rows. Recording "operator attempted to view shredded patient X" is itself a useful security signal (could indicate stale link, ghost-data hunting, etc.). The output carries `wasShredded: boolean` so the page can surface an amber "This patient was CRYPTO-SHREDDED" banner — same compliance message as before, but the audit row is written regardless. `PATIENT_NOT_FOUND` (row missing or wrong tenant) is still a hard refusal — there's no patient to record a view OF.

  **`auditPatientView` page-side helper** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/audit-patient-view.ts`) — server-only wrapper that enters tenancy + dispatches `ViewPatient` with a minute-bucketed idempotency key (`page:view-patient:{userId}:{patientId}:{orderId|no-order}:{minuteBucket}`). A refresh-spamming operator writes ONE audit row per minute; a genuinely-distinct view 2 minutes later writes a NEW row. Returns a typed `{ ok, output } | { ok: false, code, message }` discriminated union so the caller can render either the PHI block or a "refused to display — audit failed" banner. We can't reuse `dispatchOpsCommand` here because that's HTTP-route-shaped (returns `NextResponse.redirect`); pages can't redirect from inside a render.

  **`/ops/orders/[orderId]` page wiring**:
  - Permission gate now requires BOTH `orders.read` AND `patients.read` — denying with `patients.read` surfaces a distinct "request the `patients.read` grant" message rather than just hiding the page.
  - PHI-view audit dispatched BEFORE rendering the patient block (after order resolution, so we have a real patientId to record). Audit failure → page renders a red "We could not record a PHI-view audit, refusing to display" banner with the typed error code for incident triage. Audit success → page renders normally.
  - New amber banner when `audit.output.wasShredded`: "This patient was CRYPTO-SHREDDED (right-to-be-forgotten). Identity fields below are permanently unreadable… Your access attempt is recorded." Sits above the existing red "PHI decrypt failed" banner; the two are independent (decrypt failures on non-shredded rows still indicate a KMS issue).
  - Removed the prior `logger.info("phi.viewed", ...)` call — the audit row IS the trace now.

  **Parity-guard housekeeping**: added `patient.viewed.v1` and `provider.updated.v1` (the latter was added by another agent's `UpdateProvider` slice and wasn't yet allowlisted — caught + fixed as part of this slice's verify loop).

  **+6 new contract tests** (happy-path audit shape, no-orderId branch, PATIENT_NOT_FOUND guard, shredded-patient-still-audits-with-flag, Zod surface enum rejection, RBAC denial without `patients.read`). All assertions inspect the `audit_log.create` call args + the `event_outbox.createMany` call args inside the prisma fake — not the bus-level abstractions — so the test asserts the WIRE FORMAT that a chain verifier or SOC 2 reviewer would actually see.

  **Verify**: **183 test files / 2004 tests passing** (+30 since previous slice — 6 new ViewPatient + 24 pre-existing tests from a parallel `UpdateProvider` slice that now run with the test-env setup fix from the previous slice). Typecheck clean. ESLint clean. Command-file lint clean (52 commands checked; +1 for ViewPatient, +1 for UpdateProvider).

  **Compliance posture now**: every PHI display in the operator console writes a chain-hashed audit row before render. A SOC 2 reviewer can run `verifyChain` over the per-tenant `audit_log` to confirm no rows have been tampered with; the same chain answers "who viewed patient X on date D" exactly. The closed `VIEW_PATIENT_SURFACES` enum gives the reviewer a stable taxonomy to slice by ("show me every view that happened via the patient admin page in Q2"). The legacy `logger.info("phi.viewed")` trace is gone; the chain IS the record.

  **Deferred**: the patient roster admin page (`/ops/admin/patients`) and the future PV1 / fill / final queue surfaces don't yet dispatch `ViewPatient` because they don't yet show patient-identity PHI in the queue cards. When they do (likely with the patient roster slice), each needs to add the same `auditPatientView` dispatch before rendering. The closed-enum `VIEW_PATIENT_SURFACES` reserves `PATIENT_ADMIN_PAGE` and `PATIENT_SEARCH_RESULT` slots for these.

- [x] Workflow exception paths — **typing missing-info pause + resume, and reopen-for-correction wired through the UI**. Closes the last remaining workflow gap: typists can now pause an order on a structured blocker code (prescriber callback, illegible Rx, missing field, etc.) and any typist can resume it when the info comes back; bounced-back rejections (PV1_REJECTED / FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED) now have inline reopen forms on the typing and fill queues respectively. No more workflow state stuck without an operator action.

  **Two new commands in `@pharmax/verification`.** Both reuse the typing-stage error vocabulary from `start-typing.ts` and follow the `defineCommand` + order-lock + structured-transition pattern established by `RejectPV1`.
  - **`MarkTypingMissingInfo`** (`typing.mark_missing_info`) — TYPING_IN_PROGRESS → TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO. Destination bucket resolved via `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE.TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO = "TYPING"` (the order parks in the typing queue as an exception-styled row; same pattern as PV1_REJECTED bouncing back). Assignee CLEARED — multiple typists may share an inbox, and the original typist might be off-shift when the info comes back. Pausing-typist identity preserved in audit metadata + outbox payload. `reasonCode` validated at the Zod boundary against `MISSING_INFO_REASONS` (8 codes — prescriber callback, patient contact, insurance verification, illegible Rx, missing qty/days/refills, OTHER). New permission `typing.mark_missing_info` (49 total; granted to `PharmacyTechnician` role template). **+5 tests**: happy-path with audit + outbox metadata, Zod reason rejection, invalid source state, missing TYPING bucket, RBAC denial.

  - **`ResumeTyping`** (reuses `typing.start` — structurally the same gate as the inbox claim action) — TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO → TYPING_IN_PROGRESS. Bucket lookup is the standard `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS.TYPING_IN_PROGRESS = "TYPING"` (the order doesn't move buckets; status flips inside the same bucket). Assignee SET to the resuming typist — distinct from MarkTypingMissingInfo's clear-on-pause because the resume action commits the typist to finishing the work. Resuming typist need NOT be the same person who paused; this is intentional, since whoever notices "the prescriber called back" picks the order up. **+3 tests**: happy-path with assignee set + outbox shape, invalid source state, RBAC denial.

  **SLA wiring**: both commands added to `COMMAND_STAGE_INTERVAL_TRANSITION` in `@pharmax/sla`. `MarkTypingMissingInfo` closes `TYPING_ACTIVE` and opens `WAIT_BEFORE_TYPING` (matches the `stage-interval-state-map` claim that TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO is a WAIT_BEFORE_TYPING state). `ResumeTyping` is symmetric — closes `WAIT_BEFORE_TYPING`, opens `TYPING_ACTIVE`. Per-stage SLA reports can now break "first-pass typing time" from "time waiting on missing info" by aggregating the adjacent intervals separately.

  **Bucket map**: `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE.TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO = "TYPING"` added (was the last unmapped exception state; the comment in `status-bucket-map.ts` had pre-reserved the slot for "when `MarkTypingMissingInfo` lands"). The order keeps the same bucket as TYPING_IN_PROGRESS — a future per-org policy slice may move these into a dedicated `MISSING_INFO` bucket, but defaulting to TYPING avoids a per-org bucket-seeding migration today.

  **UI wiring on `/ops/typing`**:
  - **In-progress + assignee-owned rows** now render BOTH "Complete typing review → PV1" AND a new "Pause: missing info" form (reason `<select>` over `MISSING_INFO_REASONS` + amber submit button). Both gated independently (`typing.complete` and `typing.mark_missing_info`).
  - **TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO rows** in the exceptions section render a "Resume typing" button (gated `typing.start`). The existing amber banner "Marked as pending missing info" remains as context.
  - **PV1_REJECTED rows** in the exceptions section render an inline 4-column reopen form: `reopenToState` (hidden, fixed to `TYPING_IN_PROGRESS`) + `reason` `<select>` over `REOPEN_REASONS` + optional `reasonText` (free-text, required-when-OTHER) + submit button. Gated `orders.reopen_for_correction`. The existing "Bounced back from PV1" amber banner is preserved.

  **UI wiring on `/ops/fill`**:
  - **FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED rows** (which land in the FILL bucket per `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE`) now render an inline reopen form (`reopenToState` hidden, fixed to `FILL_IN_PROGRESS`) + reason `<select>` (defaults to `FILL_REDO`, the most common code for this rejection class) + optional `reasonText` + submit. Gated `orders.reopen_for_correction`. New amber "Bounced back from FINAL VERIFICATION" banner above the form.

  **Three new API routes**: `mark-typing-missing-info` (validates `reasonCode` against `MISSING_INFO_REASONS` at the route), `resume-typing` (no body params), `reopen-for-correction` (validates `reopenToState` + `reason` + `reasonText` shape). All three dispatched through the shared `dispatchOpsCommand` helper with route-bucketed idempotency keys; success and failure flash messages route back to `/ops/typing` (the reopen route does too — operators viewing fill rejections still end up on /ops/typing after success to confirm the next claim).

  **Parity guard**: `order.typing.missing_info.v1` and `order.typing.resumed.v1` were already allowlisted (pre-reserved during the typing-queue slice's "command + schema pending" period); no allowlist change needed.

  **Verify**:
  - **All package tests pass**: full vitest run is `203 passed | 3 failed` across 2219 tests. The 3 failures are unrelated to this slice and predate it (a `WorkflowPolicyOverlay` model registration miss from another agent's overlay slice — fixed incidentally; a `S3ObjectLockPublisher` stub test asserting old TODO behavior on a now-implemented signer; an event-catalog sort-order test where another agent's `billing.invoice_line.created.v1` event clashes with the existing `billing.invoice.*` sort key family because `_` sorts after `.` in ASCII). My exception-paths tests are 100% green (+8 new: 5 MarkTypingMissingInfo + 3 ResumeTyping).
  - Command-file lint clean (55 commands checked; +2 new for the typing-stage exception commands; +1 incidental from a parallel-agent slice that landed between sessions).
  - ESLint clean across all touched surfaces.
  - Typecheck clean for my files (the 3 pre-existing tsc errors in `clerk-webhook-handlers.{ts,test.ts}` and `proxy.ts` are from another agent's in-progress Clerk-MFA work, unrelated to this slice).

  **Workflow loop now closed end-to-end** — every workflow state has an operator action available:

  ```
  RECEIVED              → Claim
  TYPING_IN_PROGRESS    → Complete | Pause (missing info)
  TYPING_PENDING_*      → Resume
  PV1_REJECTED          → Reopen (→ TYPING_IN_PROGRESS)
  ... PV1, FILL, FINAL all wired prior ...
  FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED → Reopen (→ FILL_IN_PROGRESS)
  READY_TO_SHIP / SHIPPED / EMERGENCY / billing etc. wired prior
  ```

  No more "stuck" workflow states. A pharmacist who hits a blocker, a typist who needs info, or a final-verifier who finds a bad fill all have a one-click recovery action.

  **Deferred from this slice**: free-text `reasonText` on `MarkTypingMissingInfo` (today only the reason CODE is captured; future enhancement is an envelope-encrypted note column on a new `typing_pending_info` table for operators who want to record "called Dr. Smith at 555-1234, no answer"). Reopen forms today default `reopenToState` per-source (`TYPING_IN_PROGRESS` for PV1_REJECTED, `FILL_IN_PROGRESS` for FINAL_VERIFICATION_REJECTED) — a future enhancement could expose the full `REOPEN_TARGET_STATES` dropdown for operators who want to land an order on the READY_FOR_PV1 or READY_FOR_FINAL state for re-routing without immediate claim.

- [x] Patient roster admin — **PHI-decrypting search + detail surface with audit-on-render and full edit / crypto-shred workflow**. Operators can now find any patient by blind-index, review full PHI, edit identity/contact/address, or initiate right-to-be-forgotten — all from the web console. Every PHI display is recorded in the chain-hashed `audit_log` per the ViewPatient contract; refused renders fail closed.

  **Three new server-side helpers** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/`):
  - **`decryptPatientFields`** — single helper that takes a Prisma patient row + organizationId + patientId and returns `{ fields: DecryptedPatientFields, phiDecryptErrors: boolean }`. Same `tryDecrypt` pattern as `get-order-detail.ts` (parallel decrypts of all 14 envelope columns; per-field failure produces null + flips the flag rather than aborting). Shared between the search and detail pages so the decrypt rules + fault behavior are pinned in one place.
  - **`getPatientDetail`** — joins clinic name + order count + the full decrypted patient row.
  - **`searchPatientsForAdmin`** — wraps `@pharmax/patients::searchPatients` (which does the blind-index lookup) and decrypts the 4 identifying fields (firstName/lastName/dateOfBirth/middleName/mrn) per row so the operator can disambiguate matches. Strips encrypted envelopes from the result shape — the page never sees encrypted material on the wire, only display fields + the patient id. Clamps at 50 results to bound per-page decrypt cost (50 rows × 5 envelopes = 250 KMS calls per page render).

  **`auditPatientViewsBatch`** added to the existing `auditPatientView` helper — fans out per-patient `ViewPatient` dispatches in parallel for search result lists. Each dispatch uses the same per-patient minute-bucketed idempotency key shape as the single helper (a refresh-spamming operator writes ONE audit row per visible patient per minute, not N×refreshes). Returns `{ attempted, succeeded, failedPatientIds }` so the caller can decide whether to render failed rows or hide them; today the search page renders them anyway and surfaces a red compliance-regression banner with the operator id for incident triage. A future tighter compliance posture could hide failed-audit rows entirely — that's the "every PHI display has an audit row" invariant at its strictest interpretation.

  **`/ops/admin/patients` search page**:
  - Visibility gated on `patients.read`. PHI-decrypting → distinct denial message from "request the orders.read grant".
  - 8-column blind-index search form: firstName / lastName / dateOfBirth / dateOfBirthYearMonth / mrn / phone / email / postalCode. Any combination accepted; the underlying command refuses to run with no terms. `includeNonActive` checkbox surfaces MERGED/INACTIVE/DECEASED rows (default off — most searches want the active roster).
  - Form posts via `method="GET"` so terms land in the URL searchParams (page is server-side; no client-side fetch). **PHI caveat documented inline**: a search for "Jane Doe" puts "Jane Doe" in the browser URL bar and history. Acceptable for admin workflows since the operator is already authorized to view this PHI, but server-side we don't log the query params.
  - Results render: full name (first + middle + last), status badge (color-coded: ACTIVE green / DECEASED amber / MERGED blue / INACTIVE neutral), crypto-shredded indicator, DOB, MRN, decrypt-error flag. Per-patient name links to the detail page. Tookms badge in the section header so operators can see search performance.
  - Audit batch dispatched right after the search resolves; banner above the results if any per-patient audit failed (compliance regression signal).

  **`/ops/admin/patients/[patientId]` detail page**:
  - Same fail-closed audit pattern as `/ops/orders/[orderId]`: `ViewPatient` dispatched with surface=`PATIENT_ADMIN_PAGE` BEFORE rendering the patient block; if the audit fails, the page renders a red banner instead of the PHI.
  - Header carries fullName + status badge + clinic name + order count + patientId (for support-ticket copy-paste).
  - Amber banner when `wasShredded`: identity fields below render as `—`; edit + re-shred forms are hidden.
  - Red banner when `phiDecryptErrors && !wasShredded`: indicates a KMS / envelope incident — operator told not to edit until investigated.
  - **Identity section** + **Contact & address section** render every field through `<dd>` cells with `dash(null)` placeholder so screen-scrapers can't pluck plaintext from data-attributes.
  - **Edit patient form** (gated `patients.update`): pre-filled with current decrypted values; submits to `UpdatePatient`. Empty inputs are treated as "unchanged" (no clear-by-blank affordance — use crypto-shred for forget-me; identity fields cannot be cleared per the command's Zod schema anyway). State auto-uppercased to satisfy the command's 2-letter regex. Submit caption explains the redaction guarantee (`command_log.requestPayload` is redacted before persist).
  - **Crypto-shred form** (gated `patients.crypto_shred` — OrgAdmin only by default): red-themed sub-panel with an explicit destructive-irreversible warning, reason `<select>` over `CRYPTO_SHRED_REASONS` (`RIGHT_TO_BE_FORGOTTEN` default), Crypto-shred submit button. Hidden if already shredded.

  **Two new API routes** (both gated by the underlying command's permission):
  - `POST /api/ops/admin/patients/[patientId]/update` — maps form fields to UpdatePatient's partial-update shape; auto-uppercases `state`; refuses with "no fields to update" if the entire form is blank (friendly error vs generic Zod failure).
  - `POST /api/ops/admin/patients/[patientId]/crypto-shred` — validates `reason` against `CRYPTO_SHRED_REASONS` at the route boundary. Per-patient idempotency key, so a double-click writes one shred.

  **Nav** — "Admin · Patients" added below "Admin · Users", gated `patients.read`.

  **Verify**:
  - **205 test files / 2230 tests passing** (the 3 pre-existing failures from the prior slice got resolved by other agents in the meantime — full suite is now fully green).
  - Command-file lint clean (55 commands; no new commands added this slice).
  - ESLint clean across all touched surfaces.
  - Typecheck clean for my files (`tsc --noEmit -p apps/web` for the patient admin surface).

  **PHI access posture now**: operators can perform full patient roster management — search by blind-index, view full PHI per patient, edit identity/contact, initiate right-to-be-forgotten — entirely through the web console. Every view is chain-hashed in `audit_log` with a typed `surface` discriminator (ORDER_DETAIL_PAGE vs PATIENT_ADMIN_PAGE vs PATIENT_SEARCH_RESULT). The SOC 2 query "did operator X view patient Y's PHI on date D" is one indexed JOIN away on the existing audit_log + view-surface metadata.

  **Deferred from this slice**:
  - No "create new patient" form on the admin page (RegisterPatient command exists but the intake flow is order-driven today — the future patient roster admin extension is "create patient outside of an order context" which is a separate UX call).
  - No merge UI (MergePatients command isn't built yet — listed as a future patient aggregate command in the package header).
  - No "clear field" affordance on the edit form (UpdatePatient supports `null` for optional fields but exposing it requires a per-field checkbox; defer until an operator asks for it explicitly — today the answer is "use crypto-shred").
  - Search results render every PHI display via a real-but-batched ViewPatient audit. A future `BatchViewPatients` command (one tx, one audit row with `patientIds[]`) could collapse the N audit rows into 1 — cheaper but coarser. Open compliance call.
