- [x] Operator-console Sentry / observability wiring — **every dispatch failure, audit failure, and PHI-decrypt failure now ships to Sentry with full operator + tenant + command tags, full stack trace, and PHI-scrubbed event payloads**. Closes the visibility gap that was leaving production issues to "the operator told us their click didn't work".

  **What was already there** (built in prior slices, just not fully wired through the operator path):
  - `@sentry/nextjs` SDK installed; `sentry.{client,server,edge}.config.ts` + `instrumentation.ts` wired
  - `initSentry()` called from `bootstrap.ts`; gated by `SENTRY_DSN` (no-op when unset, no-op in `NODE_ENV=test`)
  - `sentry-scrubber.ts` allowlist + tested PHI redaction `beforeSend` + `beforeBreadcrumb`
  - `createSentryErrorReporter()` reporter bridged into `logger.ts` so `logger.error(..., { error: cause })` auto-fires `Sentry.captureException` with the stack; `logger.error(...)` without an Error fires `captureMessage` instead

  **What this slice added**:

  **`withSentryOpsScope`** helper (`apps/web/src/server/observability/ops-scope.ts`) — wraps an async callback in a `Sentry.withScope` frame that pins:
  - `user.id` = Pharmax operator user id (same id the audit chain uses, so dashboards join cleanly)
  - `user.username` = operator displayName (PHI-safe admin identity)
  - Tags: `organizationId`, `commandName`, `route`, `surface`
  - Context block `operator` = { userId, organizationId, displayName?, clerkUserId? } — survives the scope and ends up on every captured event inside it
  - Optional bindings (commandName, route, surface, clerkUserId, displayName) only set the corresponding fields when provided — absent values don't pollute the scope. PHI-safe by construction: patient ids, order ids, prescription ids are NOT placed on the scope (those land on event `extra` payloads case-by-case and go through `sentry-scrubber.beforeSend` first).

  **`dispatchOpsCommand` wiring** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/dispatch-from-route.ts`):
  - Whole try/catch body now runs inside `withSentryOpsScope` with operator + organization + commandName + route bindings.
  - The catch branch forwards `cause` as `error: cause` in the log context (was silently dropped before) — converts the Sentry event from `captureMessage` (string only) to `captureException` (full stack). Also adds `commandName` to the log context for log-line filtering.
  - Result: every operator dispatch failure now ships to Sentry with operator id, organization id, command name, route, AND the full underlying error stack. Triageable in the Sentry dashboard without touching production logs.

  **`auditPatientView` wiring** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/audit-patient-view.ts`):
  - Same treatment: wrapped in `withSentryOpsScope` with `commandName: "ViewPatient"` + `surface` binding.
  - Catch branch forwards `cause` as `error` in the log context. Audit-failure events now carry a stack and are filterable by patient surface.

  **`decryptPatientFields` warn-on-failure** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/decrypt-patient.ts`):
  - The per-field `tryDecrypt` catch was silently swallowing the cause; replaced with a structured `logger.warn("ops.patient.decrypt.field_failed", { tenantId, table, column, recordId, error: cause })`. KMS down / envelope corruption / AAD mismatch (cross-tenant leak attempt) now surfaces in Sentry with full context. Page still renders with null for the failed field + the existing red banner; failing closed at the page level keeps the operator informed without aborting the render.

  **Next.js error boundaries** (`apps/web/app/error.tsx` + `apps/web/app/global-error.tsx`):
  - `app/error.tsx` catches segment-render errors (`useEffect` → `Sentry.captureException` with `boundary: "app-segment"` tag + the framework-supplied `error.digest` for the reference id). Renders a friendly fallback with a "Try again" button (`reset()` invoked) and the digest as a copyable incident reference.
  - `app/global-error.tsx` is the root-level boundary — catches errors that escape the root layout itself (rare but fatal). Same Sentry capture pattern with `boundary: "app-root"` tag. Renders its own `<html>` + `<body>` since the root layout is already crashed at this point.

  **Test coverage**: `ops-scope.test.ts` mocks `@sentry/nextjs::withScope` and exercises (a) callback return value propagation, (b) user identity setting with + without displayName, (c) optional tag setting only when provided, (d) context block shape with + without clerkUserId, (e) error propagation through the scope. **+6 new tests**.

  **PHI invariant** through the whole pipeline:
  1. `logger.error(..., { ...ctx, error: cause })` — Pino redactor scrubs `ctx` against the platform-core redaction allowlist BEFORE forwarding to the reporter
  2. Reporter calls `Sentry.captureException(error, { extra: scrubbed_ctx })`
  3. `sentry-scrubber.beforeSend` runs against the event — drops anything not on the per-field allowlist (operator id + organizationId + commandName + route are explicitly permitted; patient ids and any free-text strings outside the allowlist are dropped)
  4. Event leaves the process
     Three independent scrub layers — operator id can reach Sentry, patient PHI cannot.

  **Verify**: **213 test files / 2331 tests passing** (+6 new ops-scope tests). Command-file lint clean (58 commands). ESLint clean across all of `apps/web/{app,src}`. Pre-existing failing tests from prior slices are now resolved.

  **What's NOT wired in this slice** (deferred):
  - **Page-level Sentry scope on PHI-decrypting server components** — `getOrderDetail` + `getPatientDetail` + `searchPatientsForAdmin` execute outside `dispatchOpsCommand`'s scope frame because they're called from page render, not from a POST route. Errors that escape them today land on the segment error boundary (which DOES capture to Sentry, but without the operator+command tags). A follow-up could add a `renderPageWithOpsScope` wrapper that the page entry points call, but the current state is "errors are captured, just without the rich tagging the POST routes get".
  - **Sentry breadcrumbs on operator actions** — `Sentry.addBreadcrumb` could record "operator opened /ops/pv1 → claimed order X → approved" so a downstream error has the action history. Useful for triage but not blocking; defer.
  - **Performance / tracing samples** — `tracesSampleRate` and `profilesSampleRate` default to 0 (off). Enabling at >0 adds runtime overhead + cost; a separate enable-with-baseline-tuning slice.
  - **Worker-tier observability extension** — `apps/worker` already has its own Sentry init + bridge (`apps/worker/src/observability/sentry-init.ts`); this slice only touched apps/web. The worker drains have their own log calls that already forward `cause` as `error`. The remaining gap there is `withSentryOpsScope`-equivalent for outbox handler dispatch, but that's a separate slice.

- [x] On-demand report runner + CSV download — **closes the reporting loop end-to-end**. Operators can now select a report from the registry, supply parameters, and download a CSV. Every run writes a chain-hashed audit row + a `report_run` ledger entry; the SOC-2 query "what reports did operator X run this quarter with which filters" is one indexed JOIN.

  **`report_run` table** (migration `20260614000000_phase5_report_run`):
  - Records every report execution: `id`, `organizationId`, `reportId`, `reportVersion`, `parameters` (JSONB, post-Zod-parse), `aggregates` (JSONB), `rowCount` (denormalized for filtering), `windowFrom`/`windowTo`/`generatedAt`, `runByUserId` (nullable — reserved for the future scheduled-run worker which will set `runViaScheduleId` instead), `commandLogId`.
  - Three indexes: `(org, generatedAt DESC)` for "recent runs", `(org, reportId, generatedAt DESC)` for "runs of report X", and a partial `(org, runByUserId, generatedAt DESC) WHERE runByUserId IS NOT NULL` for operator history dashboards.
  - Standard RLS policy keyed on `pharmax.system_context` / `pharmax.organization_id` GUCs — registered in `TENANT_SCOPED_MODELS` as `{ kind: "organizationId" }` so the Prisma extension's anti-leak guard fires on cross-org reads.
  - The full row set is NOT persisted; downloads re-run against the same parameters + window (stable output for historical date-range reports). A future cached-result slice may add row-set persistence for non-deterministic reports.

  **`RunReport` command** (`@pharmax/reporting/commands/run-report.ts`):
  - Single entry point for both operator-initiated runs (POST routes) AND future scheduled runs (worker dispatches the same command under a per-org service user).
  - Input is `{ reportId: string, parameters: unknown }` — the bus-level Zod parse is shallow; the handler resolves the report definition from `REPORT_REGISTRY` and re-validates `parameters` against the report's own Zod schema. A bad reportId surfaces as `REPORT_NOT_FOUND` (NotFoundError); bad parameters surface as `REPORT_PARAMETERS_INVALID` (ValidationError with `issues` from Zod's flatten for per-field UI rendering).
  - Output carries `reportRunId` + `reportId` + `reportVersion` + window + rowCount + aggregates + the row set itself. The row set is in-memory only so the download route can stream CSV without a separate fetch; the persisted ledger entry is the long-lived record.
  - Audit metadata + `report.run.v1` outbox event carry the report id + version + row count + aggregates + ISO window — no PHI. The route runs inside the bus's tx, so the report read + audit row + report_run row commit atomically.
  - New permission `reports.run` (54 total; granted to OrgAdmin via `ALL_PERMS`). Existing role templates (Pharmacist / BillingManager) can be extended to include `reports.run` in a follow-up; for now the default is OrgAdmin-only access.
  - `redactFields` is empty for now — today's reports take non-PHI params (date ranges, status enums, clinic ids). The header note pins the responsibility: when a PHI-bearing parameter lands, this list MUST be updated.
  - **+4 contract tests**: happy-path (order-volume-by-stage with synthetic groupBy result; asserts the report_run row data + audit metadata + `report.run.v1` outbox shape), REPORT_NOT_FOUND, REPORT_PARAMETERS_INVALID (from-after-to), RBAC denial without `reports.run`.

  **`REPORT_REGISTRY` extraction** (`@pharmax/reporting/report-registry.ts`):
  - Pulled out of `index.ts` to break a circular import — `RunReport` needs the registry, and the registry needs the report definitions; both go through `report-registry.ts` now and `index.ts` re-exports.
  - `ReportDefinitionAny` is the type-erased shape the registry stores. Dynamic Zod re-parse inside `RunReport.handle` re-narrows to the actual schema for type-safe consumption inside the report's own `run` function.

  **`/ops/reports` page** — registered reports catalog:
  - Visibility gated on `reports.run`. Lists every `REPORT_REGISTRY` entry with title + description + id + version. Each entry links to `/ops/reports/[reportId]`.

  **`/ops/reports/[reportId]` page** — per-report parameter form:
  - Date inputs default to `today-30d → today`; refreshing preserves the last range via URL searchParams.
  - Form POSTs to the download route. No client-side fetch — the operator clicks Submit and the browser downloads the CSV directly.

  **`/api/ops/reports/[reportId]/run` route**:
  - Custom POST handler (NOT `dispatchOpsCommand` because the success response is a CSV body, not a redirect). Replicates the dispatch helper's contract manually: session resolve → tenancy build → minute-bucketed idempotency key → `RunReport` dispatch inside `withSentryOpsScope` → serialize via `toCsv` → stream as `text/csv; charset=utf-8` with `content-disposition: attachment; filename="<reportId>__<from>_to_<to>.csv"`.
  - `x-pharmax-report-run-id` response header exposes the ledger id for support tickets + log correlation. `cache-control: private, no-store` so a shared workstation doesn't surface the download to a different operator.
  - On failure, redirects back to the report page with `?error=<code>: <message>` flash — same operator-friendly pattern as the rest of `/ops/*`.

  **Nav** — "Reports" added between Billing and Admin entries, gated `reports.run`.

  **Parity guard**: `report.run.v1` was pre-allowlisted by another agent under "BLOCKER: RunReport command (`@pharmax/reporting`) emits this; schema pending registration in its own slice." A follow-up slice (below) registered the proper `EventDefinition` and renamed the wire-name from `report.run.v1` → `reporting.run.completed.v1` to match the established `<domain>.<aggregate>.<past-tense-action>.<version>` convention used by every other event; the allowlist entry is gone.

  **Follow-up: `reporting.run.completed.v1` registration (shipped):** closes the only remaining "schema pending" BLOCKER on the parity-guard allowlist. New file `packages/events/src/events/reporting/run-completed-v1.ts` defines the event (org + reportRunId + reportId + version + rowCount + scalar `aggregates` record + ISO window + generatedAt + nullable `runByUserId`) with `owner: "reporting"` (added to the `EventOwner` union — `"reporting"` slot now exists alongside `"sla"`, `"billing"`, etc.), `retention: "7y"` (matches the `report_run` ledger retention so the outbox event and the persisted row die together), `phiSafe: true` (today's aggregates are scalar counters; PHI-bearing aggregates would need a per-event schema redesign, not a flag flip), `routingKey: "tenant.reporting"`. The row set is deliberately NOT in the payload — consumers re-run the report (deterministic for the date-range reports we ship) or query `report_run` by id through tenant-scoped RLS. Domain barrel + 4 contract tests (`reporting/index.test.ts`) pin owner / phiSafe / retention / event-count invariants alongside the `compliance` barrel. `RunReport` producer + `run-report.test.ts` assertion updated to the new event type in lockstep. `EVENT_REGISTRY` now holds 60 definitions; allowlist down to 16 entries (all permanent test fixtures or aspirational-producer BLOCKERs). **Verify**: events + reporting packages 22 test files / 135 tests passing; `events:validate` ok; `events:migrate-check` shows no `unaccounted` failures.

  **Follow-up: SOC 2 code-evidence map (shipped).** The existing SOC 2 framework (`docs/soc2/{controls-inventory,trust-service-criteria-mapping,evidence-inventory}.md` + `docs/security/control-matrix.md` + `docs/compliance/evidence-collection-guide.md`) maps every Common Criterion + HIPAA safeguard to **policy + ADR + narrative + cadence** — i.e. "what the control is and how Pharmax implements it conceptually." A technical auditor reading those docs can confirm the control is _designed_ but cannot find, without code archaeology, the specific `.test.ts` files that prove the control _fires_. This slice closes that gap by adding `docs/soc2/code-evidence-map.md` — a strict engineering-grade companion that for every code-grounded control gives: (1) **Feature code** — exact file paths inside `packages/*/src/` and `apps/*/src/` that implement the control; (2) **Schema / Audit tables** — the Prisma models or migration files that store the control's runtime evidence; (3) **Automated tests** — the specific `.test.ts` files (and within them, the test names) that fail if the control is silently removed; (4) **CI gate** — the `pnpm` script (run on every PR via `.github/workflows/ci.yml`) that pins the structural invariant. Coverage: ~35 controls across CC2 (audit + outbox), CC4 (monitoring + access-review), CC5 (architectural invariants + CI gates), CC6 (the densest section: 13 rows for identity / RBAC / RLS / MFA / grants / SoD / encryption / blind indexes / webhooks / deprovisioning), CC7 (chain verification + Merkle signing + break-glass + incident response), CC8 (change management + workflow versioning), plus AC sections (A1 / PI1 / C1) and the HIPAA §164.312 technical-safeguard crosswalk that maps each HIPAA Technical Safeguard 1:1 to its underlying CC control. CC1 / CC3 / CC9 are noted as governance-only with no code evidence; the Privacy P-series is noted as clinic-mediated. **Eight gaps are explicitly enumerated** at the bottom of the map (G1–G8) with the follow-up slice ID each is tracked under (`tf1` for Terraform, `kms1` for production KMS adapter swap, `ar1` for scheduled access-review worker, `it1` for cross-package integration tests, plus operational gaps for restore drills and BCP tabletop). Cross-references wired bidirectionally: `controls-inventory.md` header, `control-matrix.md` intro + cross-references section, `trust-service-criteria-mapping.md` header, `evidence-collection-guide.md` header, and `docs/soc2/README.md` (directory listing + auditor walkthrough step + engineering procedure) all point into the new code-evidence map. The directory listing in the README explicitly names the new file. A `scripts/soc2/check-evidence-map.ts` path-existence sanity script is described at the bottom of the map as a future slice — until it lands, drift is caught by the `pnpm verify` pipeline plus the quarterly evidence refresh sign-off. **Why this matters for SOC 2 posture**: when an auditor asks "show me the test that proves CC6.3 (SoD) is enforced", the answer is now a one-line lookup: `packages/verification/src/commands/approve-pv1.test.ts` (the typist-cannot-self-approve-PV1 test) — not a 20-minute code archaeology. This is the single highest-leverage document an auditor with engineering background reads. **Verify**: prettier clean across the touched files; cross-reference graph manually re-traced from each entry point (README → map; matrix → map; inventory → map; evidence-guide → map; TSC mapping → map). No code changes; no test changes; doc-only slice.

  **Follow-up: event-registry parity catch-up + reason-code mirror parity test (shipped).** Five BLOCKER entries left on the parity-guard allowlist were stale relics of "command shipped, schema pending" loops where the schema landed but the allowlist row was not cleaned up. This slice closed all five plus a silent drift risk on the reason-code mirrors. **(1) Typing exception-loop events registered.** `order.typing.missing_info.v1` and `order.typing.resumed.v1` were both EMITTED by `MarkTypingMissingInfo` / `ResumeTyping` (commands shipped two slices back, see lines 247–265 above) but their schemas were never formally registered — the producer Zod boundary validated the closed `reasonCode` enum but no central registry pinned the wire format. New files `packages/events/src/events/order/typing-missing-info-v1.ts` + `typing-resumed-v1.ts` define the payload schemas (orderId / organizationId / siteId / pausing-or-resuming typist user id / bucketId / transitionId / fromState / toState / occurredAt; plus `reasonCode` on the missing-info event mirroring `MISSING_INFO_REASONS`), both owned by `"verification"`, `retention: "7y"`, `phiSafe: true`, `routingKey: "order.lifecycle"`. Allowlist BLOCKERs removed; registry now holds 65 definitions. **(2) Reporting domain naming consistency** — the schedule-event trio (`report.schedule.created.v1`, `report.schedule.disabled.v1`, `report.schedule.updated.v1`) had landed under the OLD `report.*` prefix while the sibling `reporting.run.completed.v1` had been deliberately moved to `reporting.*` to match the `<domain>.<aggregate>.<past-tense-action>.<version>` convention and the `@pharmax/reporting` package name. Renamed all three events to `reporting.schedule.created/updated/disabled.v1` — touched: the 3 event-definition `name` fields, the 3 producer commands (`create-/update-/disable-report-schedule.ts` `outboxEvents[].eventType`), the 1 producer test assertion that pinned the wire-name (`create-report-schedule.test.ts:154`), and 3 allowlist BLOCKER deletions. Audit-log `action` strings were INTENTIONALLY left as `report.schedule.*` because audit actions follow a different convention (aggregate-type prefix — `order.typing.started`, `provider.updated`, `patient.viewed` — where the leading segment is the aggregate root, not the owning domain). The audit-action convention is internally consistent across all 25+ commands; event-name convention is `<domain>.<aggregate>.<action>.<version>`. Reporting barrel test (`reporting/index.test.ts`) rebuilt: now asserts `EXPECTED_COUNT = 4` (was the stale `1`), pins the `reporting.` name-prefix invariant, plus owner / phiSafe / retention / routingKey. **(3) Cross-package reason-code mirror parity test.** Multiple event payload schemas in `@pharmax/events` mirror reason-code enums (`PV1_REJECTION_REASONS`, `FINAL_REJECTION_REASONS`, `MISSING_INFO_REASONS`) that are CANONICALLY owned by `@pharmax/verification`. The mirrors are inlined (not imported) because reversing the dependency edge — domain packages depend on `@pharmax/events` to emit; events cannot depend on a consumer — would create a runtime cycle. Without a parity test, a maintainer adding a new reason code (e.g. `"EXPIRED_PRESCRIPTION"` to `PV1_REJECTION_REASONS`) would pass producer-side validation and silently fail consumer-side validation when the drainer parsed the outbox row. New cross-package test `scripts/check-event-reason-mirrors.test.ts` lives at repo root (where every workspace is already a devDependency of `pharmax` — no new package-dependency edges added) and asserts that for each (canonical list, event payload field) pair we ship today, the mirrored enum is set-equal to the source-of-truth list. Uses Zod 4 public introspection surface (`ZodObject.shape` getter + `ZodEnum.options` getter — pinned in a comment so a future Zod minor bump that reshuffles `_def` doesn't silently break the parity gate). **(4) Pre-existing test bump.** `packages/rbac/src/permissions.test.ts:52` permission-count assertion was stale at `56` since `COMPLIANCE_ACCESS_REVIEW_RECORD` landed in the prior slice (bringing the registry to 57). Bumped to 57 to clear the unrelated failure. **Verify**: full repo sweep is **227 test files / 2495 tests passing** (+5 new — 3 reason-code mirror + 2 reporting barrel invariants); `events:validate` shows 65 registered / 14 on allowlist (down from 19 — only permanent test fixtures + one real-but-aspirational BLOCKER (`order.note.added.v1`, the planned `NoteAdded` command) remain); `events:migrate-check` clean; `pnpm -r typecheck` clean across all packages + apps; ESLint clean; Prettier clean. Net effect on the registry: **5 BLOCKERs closed in one pass**, every shipped event now has a properly registered schema, the reporting domain is single-prefix-consistent (`reporting.*` across all 4 events), and the reason-code drift risk is permanently pinned.

  **Verify**: **219 test files / 2451 tests passing** (+4 new). Command-file lint clean (59 commands; +1 for RunReport). ESLint clean. Typecheck clean across all of `apps/web` (pre-existing clerk-webhook-handlers errors got fixed by another agent's slice in the meantime).

  **End-to-end reporting flow now web-actionable**:
  1. OrgAdmin opens `/ops/reports` → picks "Order volume by stage"
  2. Form pre-fills today-30d → today; admin adjusts → clicks "Run + download CSV"
  3. POST hits `/api/ops/reports/order-volume-by-stage/run` → tenancy resolved → `RunReport` dispatched
  4. Bus runs the report against the org's tx (groupBy on `order` table); persists `report_run` row + audit + outbox; returns rows
  5. Route serializes via `toCsv`, streams as attachment; browser downloads `order-volume-by-stage__2026-04-28_to_2026-05-28.csv`
  6. The `report_run` row + chain-hashed audit row are visible to a SOC-2 reviewer indefinitely; rerun produces stable output

  **Deferred from this slice**:
  - **"View past runs" UI** — `/ops/reports/runs` listing historical executions with download-again links. The `report_run` ledger has the data; this is a UI-only follow-up.
  - **Additional reports** — each is a `ReportDefinition` file + a `REPORT_REGISTRY` entry; the framework absorbs them with zero new infrastructure (rich run form, CSV download + archive, scheduling, email notification, delivery tracking all inherited). **Five reports now shipped**: `order-volume-by-stage`, `sla-breach-report`, `shipment-exception-breakdown` (counts by carrier+status, exception-rate bps, carrier multi-enum), **`lot-expiry-warnings`** (active/on-hold lots expired or expiring within a `withinDays` horizon — number param field with default 90, product-name enrichment, UTC-midnight day math, expired/expiring-soon aggregates; +4 tests), **`billing-summary-by-clinic`** (invoice totals/paid/due grouped by clinic+status over an `issuedAt` window via Prisma `groupBy` `_sum`, statuses multi-enum, null-sum coercion; +5 tests), and **`user-productivity-by-stage`** (the explicit SLA-rule requirement — per-user avg + total active work seconds per workflow stage, for `*_ACTIVE` `OrderStageInterval` rows that ended in-window, attributed by `actorUserId`; findMany + TS duration-average aggregation like the SLA report since `groupBy` can't average a computed `endedAt − startedAt`; negative-duration guard; +6 tests). and **`verification-rejection-rate`** (the "rejection rates / rework rates" requirement — per-stage PV1/FINAL approved-vs-rejected pivot from `verification_record` `groupBy(stage, decision)`, rejection rate in bps, stages multi-enum; +5 tests). Remaining ideas: throughput by clinic/team. **254 test files / 2731 tests passing.** _Seven reports now span workflow / SLA / shipping / inventory / billing / productivity / quality._

  - **Reporting read-replica routing (still deferred, Phase 6)** — the history-scanning reports (productivity, SLA, rejection-rate) reinforce the need to keep heavy analytical scans off the OLTP primary. Deferred deliberately: the seam touches the well-tested `RunReport` core AND its production value (offloading to a replica) can't be validated in this environment without a provisioned replica, so building it now would be partially unverifiable. Lands when a replica URL is available — `ReportRunContext.client` becomes a replica-backed tenant-scoped read handle while `report_run` + audit + outbox stay on the primary command tx.

  - **Dedicated `notifications.read` permission (shipped)** — the notifications health view + nav link now gate on `notifications.read` (category "Notifications") instead of `reports.manage_schedule`, decoupling delivery-health visibility from schedule management ahead of notifications expanding beyond reports. Added to `PERMISSIONS`, the seed permission list, and the permission-count test (58); granted org-wide via OrgAdmin's `ALL_PERMS`. The per-schedule run-history rollup stays under `reports.manage_schedule` (it lives inside the schedule page).
  - **Reporting replica routing** — today reports run against the live transactional Prisma client. Heavy analytics will move to a reporting replica (Phase 6); `ReportRunContext.client` becomes the replica handle when that lands.
  - **Per-report parameter forms** — today the form is hardcoded `from + to` date pair (works for both shipped reports since they both take a DateRangeParams). When a report with a richer parameter schema lands, we'll need a schema-introspection helper that renders the matching form controls.

- [x] Scheduled report runner — **closes the reporting loop with unattended execution**. Operators create cron-driven schedules through an admin UI; the worker's `report-scheduler` poll loop dispatches due schedules under a per-org `reports-scheduler@<org-slug>.test` service identity, advances `nextRunAt` from the cron expression, and writes outcome (SUCCEEDED / FAILED / SKIPPED) back to the schedule row. Every dispatch flows through `RunReport`, so the SOC-2 trail (chain-hashed audit + `report_run` ledger) is identical whether the operator clicked "Run + download" or the cron tick fired.

  **What we shipped (single slice)**:
  - **Schema + migration**: `report_schedule` table (`20260615000000_phase5_report_schedule`) with `cronExpression` (TEXT, validated by cron-parser at command time + worker time), `timezone` (IANA), `parametersTemplate` (JSONB with placeholder support), `status` (`ReportScheduleStatus` — ACTIVE / PAUSED / DISABLED — partial index `report_schedule_due_idx` filters on ACTIVE only so the worker's claim is fast even with thousands of disabled rows), and `lastRunAt` / `lastRunStatus` / `lastRunReportRunId` / `lastRunErrorCode` / `runCount` denormalized columns for the admin UI's health badge. Unique on `(org, reportId, name)`. Full RLS via the standard `tenant_isolation` pattern.
  - **Placeholder resolver** (`@pharmax/reporting/schedule/resolve-template.ts`) — closed enum of nine relative-date placeholders (`now`, `now-1h`, `now-6h`, `now-12h`, `now-24h`, `now-7d`, `now-14d`, `now-30d`, `now-90d`). The bounded vocabulary keeps the parse trivial and the audit trail readable ("ran with from=now-30d" tells SOC-2 the exact intent). Pure function; substitutes only top-level string-valued matches, passes other values through.
  - **Cron wrapper** (`@pharmax/reporting/schedule/cron.ts`) — thin facade over cron-parser v4. `validateCron({ expression, timezone, from })` returns `{ ok, nextRunAt }` in one call so commands can both check validity AND compute the initial fire-time. `computeNextRun` for the worker's per-tick advance.
  - **Three commands**, all gated on `reports.manage_schedule`:
    - `CreateReportSchedule` — validates report id against `REPORT_REGISTRY`, validates cron + timezone, **dry-runs** the resolved template against the report's own Zod schema (surfaces misconfigs at create time, not at first tick), inserts with `nextRunAt = computeNextRun(now)`. P2002 translates to `SCHEDULE_NAME_TAKEN`.
    - `UpdateReportSchedule` — partial edits (`name` / `cronExpression` / `timezone` / `parametersTemplate` / `status`). Refuses to change `reportId` (admin creates a new schedule + disables the old). Recomputes `nextRunAt` when cron or timezone changes (anchored at update-time, NOT the old `nextRunAt` — the operator's intent is "fire on the new schedule starting now"). Allows STATUS-only edits even when the report id is no longer in the registry (so DISABLED-as-cleanup still works after a report is removed).
    - `DisableReportSchedule` — soft-delete to status `DISABLED`. Idempotent: a re-disable audits as `report.schedule.disable_redundant` so a reviewer can distinguish reaffirming intent from fresh disables (no outbox emit on the no-op path).
  - **Worker tick** (`apps/worker/src/drains/report-scheduler.ts`) — `claimDueReportSchedules` uses `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED WHERE status = 'ACTIVE' AND nextRunAt <= NOW()` so concurrent worker replicas claim disjoint subsets. For each row: resolve the per-org service user via the `reports-scheduler@<org-slug>.test` convention (missing user → SKIPPED + advance nextRunAt + log, NOT a hot-loop on config error); resolve placeholders at tick time; build tenancy; dispatch `RunReport` with minute-bucketed idempotency key per `(scheduleId, minute)`; advance `nextRunAt` via cron-parser; update `lastRun*` columns + increment `runCount`. Per-schedule failures are isolated; the tick reports `{ claimed, succeeded, failed, skipped }` to structured logs.
  - **Per-org service identity** (seed): `reports-scheduler@<org-slug>.test` user + new `ReportsScheduler` role template (machine-only, scope ORGANIZATION, permissions = `[reports.run]` ONLY). The scheduler dispatches `RunReport` but cannot create / edit / disable schedules — `reports.manage_schedule` stays with `OrgAdmin`.
  - **Admin UI** at `/ops/admin/report-schedules`: list page sorts by `lastRunAt DESC` (matches index) with status + last-run health badges (SUCCEEDED green / FAILED red / SKIPPED amber); `/new` form with the four inputs (name, report dropdown driven by REPORT_REGISTRY, cron expression with common-pattern hints, timezone, parameters template JSON textarea defaulting to `{from: "now-30d", to: "now"}`); `/[id]/edit` page with full edit form + a separate red "Disable" sub-form so the operator can't accidentally disable while editing other fields. Three API routes (`create`, `update`, `disable`) thread through the shared `dispatchOpsCommand` helper with route-bucketed idempotency keys.
  - **Wiring**: `report-scheduler` poll loop registered in `apps/worker/src/main.ts` (default 30s interval, 25-row batch); two new envs `REPORT_SCHEDULER_BATCH_SIZE` / `REPORT_SCHEDULER_INTERVAL_MS`. Nav link "Admin · Report schedules" added to `apps/web/app/ops/layout.tsx` gated on `reports.manage_schedule`. Three new outbox events (`report.schedule.created.v1` / `.updated.v1` / `.disabled.v1`) allowlisted in `parity-guard.ts` pending full event schema landing alongside Phase 6 reporting expansion.
  - **+13 new tests, 0 regressions** (`resolve-template.test.ts` 14 / `cron.test.ts` 6 / `create-report-schedule.test.ts` 6 / `disable-report-schedule.test.ts` 3 / `claim-due-report-schedules.test.ts` 2 / `report-scheduler.test.ts` 4) covering placeholder resolution, cron parse/timezone behavior, command happy paths + guards + P2002 translation + RBAC denial, the claim query's row projection, and the tick's happy/skip/fail outcomes. **227 test files / 2495 tests passing.**

  **End-to-end flow**:
  1. Admin opens `/ops/admin/report-schedules/new`, picks "Order volume by stage", enters cron `0 9 * * 1`, timezone `America/New_York`, template `{from: "now-7d", to: "now"}`, submits
  2. `CreateReportSchedule` validates cron + dry-runs the template; inserts with `nextRunAt = 2026-06-01T13:00:00Z` (9am Mon NYC = 13:00 UTC); flash "Schedule created — next fire computed."
  3. Worker tick at 13:00 UTC Monday claims the row via `SELECT FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED`; resolves `reports-scheduler@acme.test`; resolves placeholders against now; dispatches `RunReport` with the resolved `{from, to}` Date pair; writes report_run + audit + outbox; advances `nextRunAt` to `2026-06-08T13:00:00Z`; bumps runCount
  4. Admin opens `/ops/admin/report-schedules` and sees the row with `lastRunStatus = SUCCEEDED`, `runCount = 1`, next run timestamp updated

  **Deferred from this slice**:
  - **Notification adapter** — today scheduled runs land in `report_run` + audit; nobody is automatically told "your weekly report is ready." A future slice wires per-org email (Resend / SES) or a webhook adapter that fires on `report.run.v1` for runs with `runViaScheduleId IS NOT NULL`.
  - **CSV persistence (S3)** — on-demand runs stream CSV to the browser; scheduled runs currently do NOT persist the CSV anywhere. A "View past runs" UI requires storing the CSV (org-scoped key, SSE-KMS encrypted) so a follow-up can offer download-again.
  - **Schedule history page** — `/ops/admin/report-schedules/[id]/runs` listing the per-schedule run history. The `report_run` ledger carries the data; the page is UI-only.
  - **Rich parameter forms in admin** — today the admin form is a JSON textarea (the most flexible for arbitrary report shapes, but unfriendly for non-engineers). A future slice can introspect each report's Zod schema and render typed form controls. Same blocker as the on-demand runner.

- [x] Scheduled-report notification adapter — **closes the "scheduled but silent" half-loop**. Schedules now carry an operator-managed `recipients` list + `notifyOn` preference; the worker tick threads a `scheduleId` through `RunReport` onto `report_run.runViaScheduleId` and the `reporting.run.completed.v1` outbox payload; a new outbox handler fans the run completion out via `@pharmax/notifications` to each recipient through a production `ResendNotificationChannel` (or `InMemoryNotificationChannel` in dev). Operator-initiated runs are intentionally NOT mailed — the browser already streamed the CSV.

  **What we shipped (single slice)**:
  - **Schema + migration** (`20260616000000_phase5_report_schedule_notifications`): `report_schedule` gains `recipients TEXT[]` + `notifyOn ReportScheduleNotifyOn` (ALWAYS / FAILURE_ONLY / NEVER). Plaintext recipient list because these are operator addresses (`billing@acme.test`-style), NOT patient PHI — the notification PHI gate (`PHI_SENTINEL_PREFIX_KEYS` in `@pharmax/notifications`) catches context-level PHI; the recipient address itself is operator metadata. Defaults `recipients = '{}'` and `notifyOn = ALWAYS` so the previous slice's behavior (scheduled but silent) is preserved for any pre-existing rows.
  - **Plumbing**: `RunReport` accepts an optional `scheduleId` input (UUID); when present, it lands on `report_run.runViaScheduleId` AND on the `reporting.run.completed.v1` outbox payload's new `runViaScheduleId` field. The worker tick passes `scheduleId: row.id` so every scheduled run is distinguishable from operator-initiated downstream. The `reporting.run.completed.v1` event schema is extended (still v1 since we have no external consumers); the `reporting.schedule.created.v1` schema gains `recipientCount` + `notifyOn`; the `reporting.schedule.updated.v1` `newStatus` enum gains `PAUSED` to match the producer.
  - **Command surface**: `CreateReportSchedule` + `UpdateReportSchedule` accept `recipients: string[]` (Zod-validated as RFC-5321 emails, capped at 50) and `notifyOn` (ALWAYS / FAILURE_ONLY / NEVER). The boundary de-dupes + lowercases the recipient list so a typo (`["a@x", "A@X"]`) doesn't fan out twice. Audit row carries recipient COUNT (not the addresses themselves — operator metadata doesn't need to repeat on every audit row).
  - **Template registry**: `REPORT_RUN_COMPLETED_V1` registered in `@pharmax/notifications`. Required context: `scheduleName`, `reportTitle`, `runStatus`, `windowFromIso`, `windowToIso`, `rowCount`, `generatedAtIso`, `dashboardLink`. `phiAllowed: false`; `channelKinds: ["email"]`.
  - **Renderer** (`apps/worker/src/notifications/render-report-completed-email.ts`): pure function turning the context into `{ subject, text, html }`. Subject reflects status (✓/✗/⚠ prefix + status word). HTML body has status-color-coded badge, aggregates list, prominent "Open in Pharmax" deep-link button. All user-supplied strings HTML-escaped. **+7 tests** (status formatting, aggregate sorting, link presence, locale number formatting, FAILED error line, escape).
  - **Resend adapter** (`apps/worker/src/notifications/resend-notification-channel.ts`): production `NotificationChannel` over the Resend SDK. Routes only `email` recipients. Idempotency: passes the caller's `idempotencyKey` straight through as Resend's `Idempotency-Key` header so retries dedupe vendor-side. PHI-capability: `false` (no BAA today). Transport failures (5xx, network error) translate to `NOTIFICATION_TRANSPORT_ERROR`. **+6 tests** (happy-path send + header propagation, `NOTIFICATION_RECIPIENT_KIND_UNSUPPORTED` + `NOTIFICATION_PHI_REJECTED` + `NOTIFICATION_CONTEXT_MISSING_KEY` guards, transport-error translation paths).
  - **Outbox handler** (`apps/worker/src/drains/notify-on-report-run-completed.ts`): consumes `reporting.run.completed.v1`. Five explicit skip gates with structured logs at each one (operator-initiated → skip, channel unconfigured → skip, schedule deleted between dispatch and notify → skip, notifyOn=FAILURE_ONLY on SUCCEEDED → skip, recipients empty → skip). Per-recipient failure isolation: a single 5xx for one address doesn't abort the rest; total failure (every recipient bounced) throws `NOTIFICATION_FANOUT_TOTAL_FAILURE` so the drainer re-tries the row with backoff (a Resend outage isn't a "permanently dispatched" outcome). **+11 tests** covering all five skip gates, happy-path fan-out across 2 recipients, partial failure isolation, total failure rethrow, and org-mismatch defense-in-depth.
  - **Boot wiring** (`apps/worker/src/main.ts`): when both `RESEND_API_KEY` + `NOTIFICATION_FROM_EMAIL` are set, constructs `ResendNotificationChannel` and `configureNotifications`; otherwise falls back to `InMemoryNotificationChannel` (dev/test) and logs a warning in production. The outbox handler resolves the channel at dispatch time via `getNotificationChannel()` — a missing channel is a benign skip + structured log, NOT a hot-loop on retries. New envs: `RESEND_API_KEY`, `NOTIFICATION_FROM_EMAIL`, `OPS_CONSOLE_BASE_URL` (used to build deep-links in the email body).
  - **Admin UI**: `/ops/admin/report-schedules` list page adds a "Notify" column (notifyOn + recipient count); `/new` form adds a recipients textarea (comma/space/newline-separated parser at the route boundary) + notifyOn `<select>`; `/[id]/edit` form mirrors with the values pre-filled. The update route uses the textarea's presence (vs missing key) to disambiguate "operator submitted an empty list" from "field not in this submission" — the former is an explicit edit, the latter leaves the column untouched.
  - **Registry parity test fix** (`apps/worker/src/drains/registry-contract.test.ts`): added synthetic `reporting.run.completed.v1` payload so the cross-check between handler keys + registered events stays exhaustive.
  - **+24 new tests, 0 regressions**. **231 test files / 2541 tests passing.**

  **End-to-end flow**:
  1. Admin opens `/ops/admin/report-schedules/new`, fills the form with `recipients = ["ops-lead@acme.test"]` + `notifyOn = ALWAYS`, submits
  2. Worker tick at `nextRunAt` dispatches `RunReport({ reportId, parameters, scheduleId: row.id })` → `report_run` row written with `runViaScheduleId = row.id`, `reporting.run.completed.v1` event written to outbox with `runViaScheduleId` populated
  3. Outbox drain claims the event; `notify-on-report-run-completed.ts` handler loads the schedule's recipients + notifyOn, composes the notification context, calls `channel.send` with idempotency key `report-run-notify:{reportRunId}:{recipient}`
  4. `ResendNotificationChannel` POSTs to Resend with the `Idempotency-Key` header; on success, marks the outbox row DISPATCHED
  5. Recipient gets the email with subject `[Pharmax] ✓ Weekly volume Mondays — SUCCEEDED`, status-color badge, aggregates list, and a deep-link button back to the report

  **Deferred from this slice**:
  - **Resend delivery webhook** — Resend pushes bounce / delivered / opened / clicked events; a future drain consumes them and updates a `notification_delivery` table for per-recipient health. For now, our local view ends at "Resend accepted the send" (the `delivery.status = "delivered"` from the SDK).
  - **In-app delivery** — `@pharmax/notifications` has an `in-app` channel kind; today's template only lists `email`. Adding in-app is one entry on the template's `channelKinds` array + a Prisma-backed adapter in a future slice.
  - **Per-template content overrides** — operators may eventually want to customize the subject/body for their org. The template registry is the right place to expose overrides via DB rows joined at send time. Out of scope today.

- [x] Scheduled-run CSV archive + run history UI + email download link — **closes the SOC-2 evidence loop end-to-end**. Every scheduled `RunReport` now serializes its row set to CSV, hashes it (sha256), uploads to S3 under SSE-KMS, persists the pointer (`csvObjectBucket`, `csvObjectKey`, `csvSizeBytes`, `csvSha256Hex`, `csvPersistedAt`) on the `report_run` row, and the run-completion email includes a "Download CSV" button that streams the bytes back through a tenancy-scoped route. Operators get two new history pages (org-wide + per-schedule) listing the last 100 runs with one-click downloads. The archive is also wired into the on-demand `RunReport` path via an optional `persistCsv` input — today defaulted off; future "operator wants to keep this run's CSV" UI toggle is a one-line route change.

  **What we shipped (single slice)**:
  - **Schema + migration** (`20260617000000_phase5_report_run_csv_archive`): `report_run` gains `csvObjectBucket`, `csvObjectKey`, `csvSizeBytes`, `csvSha256Hex`, `csvPersistedAt` — all nullable so historical rows + on-demand runs that don't opt in continue to work. New partial index `report_run_with_csv_idx ON (organizationId, generatedAt DESC) WHERE csvObjectKey IS NOT NULL` keeps the "show me downloadable runs" history page query cheap.
  - **`ReportRunArchivePort`** (`packages/reporting/src/archive/`) — three files: the port + types (with four typed error codes: `REPORT_RUN_ARCHIVE_NOT_FOUND`, `INTEGRITY_VIOLATION`, `TRANSPORT_ERROR`, `ORG_MISMATCH`), an `InMemoryReportRunArchive` for tests + dev, and a `configureReportRunArchive` boot-time singleton. The package stays SDK-free; both apps wire their own real adapter at boot.
  - **`S3ReportRunArchive`** (also in `@pharmax/reporting`; SDK-free because it takes a narrow `S3ReportRunArchiveSurface` port both apps implement against `@aws-sdk/client-s3`). PutObject uses `ChecksumSHA256` + `ServerSideEncryption: aws:kms` + the configured `SSEKMSKeyId` + user metadata `(pharmax-org-id, pharmax-run-id, pharmax-sha256-hex)`. GetObject re-hashes the body and compares against the stored metadata — guards against silent corruption from a bucket policy / KMS rotation. Cross-checks the stored org metadata against the caller before returning bytes (defense in depth). **+6 tests** (key composition + headers + metadata, PutObject error translation, NOT_FOUND on null Body, ORG_MISMATCH, INTEGRITY_VIOLATION on tampered body, contentType passthrough).
  - **`RunReport`** extended with optional `persistCsv: boolean` input. When true: pre-allocate the report-run id (so the archive key embeds it), serialize the row set via existing `toCsv`, compute sha256, call `archive.put` (failure throws `REPORT_RUN_ARCHIVE_PUT_FAILED` and rolls back the bus tx — orphan S3 object > orphan DB row), then insert the `report_run` with the archive columns populated. Soft-skips with a structured log when `persistCsv: true` but no archive is configured (dev env). The output gains an `archive: { bucket, key, sha256Hex, sizeBytes } | null` descriptor. The persist logic is factored into a `maybePersistCsv` helper so the main handler reads linearly. **+3 new tests** (happy path with InMemory archive + column persistence + size match, soft-skip when unconfigured, default-off when omitted).
  - **Worker tick** now passes `persistCsv: true` on every scheduled dispatch — the contract that scheduled-run CSVs are always durable + downloadable.
  - **Boot wiring**: `apps/worker/main.ts` constructs `S3ReportRunArchive` when both `REPORT_ARCHIVE_S3_BUCKET` + `REPORT_ARCHIVE_S3_KMS_KEY_ID` are set, else `InMemoryReportRunArchive` (with prod warning). The web tier (`apps/web/src/server/bootstrap.ts`) mirrors the same fallback so a single-host dev setup stays consistent; the web's adapter is built behind a dynamic SDK import to keep cold-start fast for clones that don't use S3. Three new envs (`REPORT_ARCHIVE_S3_BUCKET`, `REPORT_ARCHIVE_S3_KMS_KEY_ID`, `AWS_REGION` reuse) declared in both apps. `@aws-sdk/client-s3` added as a dep to both apps.
  - **Download route** `GET /api/ops/reports/runs/[reportRunId]/download` — Clerk session resolution → `reports.run` permission check → tenancy-scoped `report_run` lookup (`getReportRunForDownload` returns null when the row lacks any of the four archive columns, so missing archives produce a friendly redirect, not a 500) → `archive.get` (which re-validates sha256) → streams as `text/csv` with `Content-Disposition: attachment` named `{reportId}__{from}_to_{to}.csv`. Errors map to `/ops/reports/runs?error=...` redirects with operator-actionable messages (not archived, archive unavailable, integrity violation).
  - **History pages**: `/ops/reports/runs` (org-wide, last 100; reports catalog link in header) and `/ops/admin/report-schedules/[id]/runs` (per-schedule; "View run history" CTA added to the schedule edit page). Both list the report title + window + generated-at + rows + size + source badge ("operator" vs "schedule") and either a "Download CSV" green button or a "Not archived" gray badge per row. New "Reports · History" nav item gated on `reports.run`.
  - **Notification email enhancement**: `REPORT_RUN_COMPLETED_V1` template gains an optional `downloadLink` context key. Renderer adds a primary "Download CSV" button (when present) + secondary "Re-run in Pharmax" button, mirrored in the plaintext fallback. The outbox handler issues a narrow `reportRun.findUnique({ select: { organizationId, csvObjectKey } })` and composes the deep-link URL when both checks pass (CSV is archived AND row's org matches the payload's). **+5 new tests** (renderer downloadLink button + omit when undefined; handler includes/omits downloadLink based on CSV presence; org-mismatch defense-in-depth omit).
  - **+19 new tests, 0 regressions** (4 InMemory archive + 6 S3 adapter + 3 RunReport persist + 3 handler downloadLink + 2 renderer downloadLink + 1 registry-event payload). Also fixed two pre-existing drift items not from this slice: `ROLE_TEMPLATES.length` test count bumped to 9 (NpiSyncWorker was added by another agent), and two `consistent-type-imports` lint errors in NPI sync drain files. **236 test files / 2573 tests passing.**

  **End-to-end flow**:
  1. Admin creates a schedule with recipients
  2. Worker tick fires `RunReport({ ..., scheduleId, persistCsv: true })`
  3. Handler serializes the rows to CSV → sha256 → `S3ReportRunArchive.put` (PutObject with `ChecksumSHA256`, SSE-KMS, metadata stamps) → inserts `report_run` with pointer columns + `reporting.run.completed.v1` outbox event
  4. Outbox drain consumes the event; `notify-on-report-run-completed.ts` loads the schedule's recipients, calls `reportRun.findUnique` to check the CSV pointer, builds context with `downloadLink: https://ops/api/ops/reports/runs/{id}/download`
  5. `ResendNotificationChannel.send` posts to Resend with both buttons; recipients click Download CSV, route resolves session → `reports.run` check → tenancy-scoped row lookup → `S3ReportRunArchive.get` (which re-hashes body) → streams CSV as attachment

  **Deferred from this slice**:
  - **Resend delivery webhook** — same as the prior slice; still pending.
  - **CSV signed-URL fast path** — today the route streams CSV through the web tier (fine for our row counts; SOC-2-grade RBAC re-check at every download). A future S3 pre-signed-URL path would shave the web hop for very large reports. Worth doing when the largest scheduled report exceeds 5 MB.
  - **CSV retention lifecycle** — S3 objects today are immortal. A bucket lifecycle rule (e.g. transition to Glacier after 90 days, expire after 7 years) is a Terraform-only follow-up.
  - **On-demand persist toggle in UI** — the `persistCsv` input is wired into `RunReport` but the on-demand reports form doesn't expose it yet. A checkbox + route handling lands when operators ask for "keep this run for later" semantics on manual runs.

- [x] Resend delivery webhook (per-recipient notification health) — **closes the notification observability loop**. Every tenant-scoped send now writes a `notification_delivery` row (QUEUED → SENT/FAILED) via a transport-agnostic decorator; a signature-verified Resend webhook advances the row to DELIVERED / BOUNCED / COMPLAINED / DELIVERY_DELAYED and stamps engagement events. The earlier slice ended at "Resend accepted the send"; this slice tracks what actually happened to each email.

  **What we shipped (single slice)**:
  - **Schema + migration** (`20260618000000_phase5_notification_delivery`) — matched the pre-existing `NotificationDelivery` + `ResendWebhookEvent` models (another agent had landed the models + enums + tenancy-registry entries + db exports but no migration/runtime). `notification_delivery` is tenant-scoped (RLS `tenant_isolation`), upsert anchor `(organizationId, idempotencyKey)`, with a partial-unique index on `providerMessageId` so the webhook can `findUnique` by the Resend `email_id` cross-tenant. `resend_webhook_event` is the RLS-exempt idempotency ledger (unique `svixMessageId`), same shape as `clerk_webhook_event`. Added a partial-unique on `providerMessageId` to the model.
  - **`PersistentNotificationChannel`** (`@pharmax/notifications`) — a `NotificationChannel` decorator + a `NotificationDeliveryStore` port (Prisma-free, tenancy-free, so the package stays a leaf). On send: `recordQueued` → `inner.send` → `markSent(providerMessageId)` / `markFailed`. Store-write failures are NON-fatal (surfaced via an `onStoreError` hook) so a ledger hiccup never turns a sent email into a failed outbox row → duplicate resend. Skips persistence when `organizationId` is absent. **+5 tests**.
  - **`PrismaNotificationDeliveryStore`** (`apps/worker`) — the Prisma binding lives in the app, NOT in `@pharmax/database`, because the store needs `withSystemContext` from `@pharmax/tenancy` and `tenancy → database` already; a store in the database package would invert that edge into a cycle. Upserts under system context with explicit org. Wired into the boot decorator wrapping the Resend/in-memory channel.
  - **Pure event mapper** (`apps/web/src/server/notifications/resend-webhook.ts`) — `mapResendEvent(event)` → `{ providerMessageId, lastEventType, lastEventAt, status?, failureReason? }`. Lifecycle events set `status`; engagement events (sent/opened/clicked) carry `lastEventType` only. Rejects no-email-id / unknown-type / bad-timestamp. **+11 tests**.
  - **Webhook route** `POST /api/webhooks/resend` — Svix signature verify (reuses `svix`, like the Clerk receiver) → idempotent insert into `resend_webhook_event` (P2002 → fast replay 200) → map → apply to `notification_delivery` by `providerMessageId` in system context, with a **monotonic guard** (drops events whose `created_at` ≤ the row's `lastEventAt` so out-of-order Svix deliveries can't regress the projection) → record ledger outcome (APPLIED/NOOP/FAILED). 503 when unconfigured; 400 on bad signature; 5xx on apply failure (Svix retries; dedupe makes it safe). The `/api/webhooks/(.*)` proxy matcher already exempts it from auth. **+7 route tests**.
  - **Wiring**: notify handler passes `organizationId` + `correlationId` (reportRunId) on each send so the decorator persists + rolls up per run. New env `RESEND_WEBHOOK_SECRET` (web). Also fixed a pre-existing missing export (`PackagePhotoMatchStrategy` / `PackagePhotoTrackingSource`) in `@pharmax/database` that was blocking the web typecheck (another agent's package-photo file).
  - **+23 new tests, 0 regressions.**

  **Follow-up shipped — notifications health view**: `/ops/admin/notifications` lists the 100 most-recent `notification_delivery` rows (recipient, template, status badge, last event, failure reason) with an All / Problems-only filter (`?problems=1` → BOUNCED / COMPLAINED / DELIVERY_DELAYED / FAILED). The per-schedule run-history page (`/ops/admin/report-schedules/[id]/runs`) gained a **Delivery** column showing a per-run rollup (delivered / in-flight / problem counts) computed from a pure `rollupByCorrelation` over the delivery rows keyed by `correlationId = reportRunId`. Nav link "Admin · Notifications" gated on `reports.manage_schedule` (when notifications expand beyond reports, introduce a dedicated `notifications.read` permission). **+4 rollup tests.** CSV-attachment + in-app channel remain from prior slices.

- [x] Rich report parameter forms — **removes the JSON-textarea / hardcoded-from-to friction on the run page**. Reports now carry a declarative `parameterFields` descriptor; the operator console renders typed controls (date pickers, enum selects, multi-select checkbox groups) and the run route coerces + validates generically.

  **What we shipped (single slice)**:
  - **`ReportParameterField`** descriptor (`@pharmax/reporting/parameter-fields.ts`) — a discriminated union (date / enum / multi-enum / text / number) plus a `dateRangeFields()` helper and a `resolveDateFieldDefault` (today / now-7d / now-30d / now-90d → `YYYY-MM-DD`). **Why declarative, not Zod reflection**: Zod internals (`.refine()` / `.strict()` wrappers) are version-unstable and hide the shape; the descriptor carries labels + help + option display names + defaults that don't belong in the validation schema. The Zod schema stays the single validation authority — a descriptor that drifts fails loudly at run time.
  - **`parseReportParameters(fields, source)`** — coerces form strings → typed shape (date → UTC-anchored Date, multi-enum → string[], number → Number, blank-optional → omitted so the schema default applies). Works against both `FormData` and a JSON record via a tiny `ParamSource` adapter. **+7 tests**.
  - **`ReportDefinition.parameterFields`** (optional) added; both shipped reports populated — `order-volume-by-stage` (from/to + statuses multi-enum) and `sla-breach-report` (from/to + kinds multi-enum). Reports without it fall back to `dateRangeFields()`.
  - **`ReportParameterForm`** server component (`apps/web/src/components/`) — renders all five control kinds, no client JS, sticky values from URL searchParams (failed runs redirect back with inputs preserved), date defaults resolved from the descriptor. The run page (`/ops/reports/[reportId]`) replaced its hardcoded from/to markup with it.
  - **Run route** (`/api/ops/reports/[reportId]/run`) now resolves the report's fields, builds a `ParamSource` from the body, and calls `parseReportParameters` — replacing the bespoke from/to date parsing. `RunReport` still re-validates against the report's own schema.
  - **+7 new tests, 0 regressions.**

  **Deferred**: schedule create/edit still uses the JSON template textarea (schedules need placeholder strings like `now-30d` that the typed form doesn't model); a future slice could layer the field descriptor over the template editor.

  **Combined verify across both slices: 243 test files / 2659 tests passing; repo-wide ESLint clean; all touched projects typecheck clean.**

  _Shipping queue (shipped):_ closes the operator-visible workflow loop. The SHIPPING bucket spans three substates (`FINAL_VERIFICATION_APPROVED_READY_FOR_SHIP`, `READY_TO_SHIP`, `SHIPPED`); the page renders inline action chrome per substate plus the joined shipment's carrier + tracking + cached-last-event when one exists. **(1) `listShippingQueue` helper** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/list-shipping-queue.ts`) — pulls SHIPPING-bucket orders with the standard `(priority DESC, slaDeadlineAt ASC, receivedAt ASC)` queue-scanner sort, then fans out a SINGLE shipment query for the order ids and joins per-order in-memory (most-recent-wins, defensive against legacy multi-shipment rows — v1 commands forbid this via `SHIPMENT_ALREADY_EXISTS` but the projection is hardened). Skips the shipment fan-out when the bucket is missing or empty. **(2) `/ops/shipping` page** — visibility gated on `ship.release`; two stacked sections: **Needs action** (everything but SHIPPED) and **Recently shipped** (terminal rows, conditionally rendered). Each row's action set is substate-driven: `FINAL_VERIFICATION_APPROVED_READY_FOR_SHIP` → "Release to ship"; `READY_TO_SHIP` owned by the operator with no shipment → an inline `<form>` with carrier `<select>` (USPS/UPS/FEDEX/DHL/OTHER) + free-text serviceLevel + trackingNumber inputs that POST to `CreateShipment`; `READY_TO_SHIP` owned by the operator WITH a shipment → "Confirm shipment → SHIPPED" button; `SHIPPED` → read-only "Shipped Xm ago". When a shipment row is joined, a sub-card surfaces `ShipmentStatus` (color-coded — DELIVERED green, EXCEPTION/FAILED_DELIVERY/RETURN_TO_SENDER red, OUT_FOR_DELIVERY blue) + carrier + service-level + tracking number + last cached tracking event (powered by the existing EasyPost/FedEx/UPS pollers that stamp `lastTrackingEventAt/Kind` on the Shipment row). **(3)–(5) Three API routes**: `release-to-ship` (gated `ship.release`; transitions and stamps operator as assignee so downstream guards pass), `create-shipment` (gated `ship.create`; validates carrier enum + tracking-number presence at the route; the auto-purchase `PurchaseShipmentLabel` path is intentionally NOT surfaced — needs ship-from address admin), and `confirm-shipment` (gated `ship.confirm`; the success of this command fires `order.shipped.v1` to the outbox which already triggers `MaterializeShippedOrderBilling` per the billing slice). All three dispatched through the shared `dispatchOpsCommand` helper with route-bucketed idempotency keys. **(6) Nav link** — "Shipping queue" added after Final verification, gated `ship.release`. **+3 new tests** (`list-shipping-queue.test.ts`: bucket-missing returns false + zero fan-out queries; empty bucket skips the shipment fan-out; happy-path joins the MOST-RECENT shipment per order and leaves `shipment: null` for orders without one). **151 test files / 1645 tests passing.**

  _Operator console — workflow surface map (complete):_

  ```
  INBOX     → /ops/typing   → Claim (StartTyping) → Complete (CompleteTypingReview → PV1)
  PV1       → /ops/pv1      → Claim (StartPV1)    → Approve (→FILL) / Reject (→TYPING)
  FILL      → /ops/fill     → Claim (StartFill)   → /ops/fill/[id] workbench
                                                  → AssignLot / PrintVialLabel / CompleteFill (scan-validated) → FINAL
  FINAL     → /ops/final    → Claim (StartFinalVerification) → Approve (→SHIPPING) / Reject (→FILL)
  SHIPPING  → /ops/shipping → Release (ReleaseToShip) → CreateShipment (manual tracking) → Confirm (ConfirmShipment) → SHIPPED
  EMERGENCY → /ops/emergency → Resolve disposition (RETURN_TO_SHIPPING / RETURN_TO_FILL / KEEP_IN_EMERGENCY)
  BILLING   → /ops/billing   → list/detail → Finalize / Credit / Refund
  ORDERS    → /ops/orders/[id] → PHI-decrypting detail page (patient + sig + lines + events)
  ```

  _Deferred (queued for follow-up slices):_ (i) `PurchaseShipmentLabel` UI — the backend command is fully shipped (EasyPost/FedEx/UPS adapters + per-tenant carrier credentials), but the operator-facing auto-purchase form is blocked on a ship-from address admin slice. The PharmacySite model today has no address columns; the right shape is an envelope-encrypted `addressEnc` field (PHI-adjacent — pharmacy street address is operationally sensitive but not patient PHI; conservative choice is to encrypt anyway). Once that lands the auto-purchase form slots in as a sibling to the manual `CreateShipment` form already on `/ops/shipping`. (ii) `MarkTypingMissingInfo` command + UI + `ReopenForCorrection` UI surface (workflow engine knows the transitions; command handlers + buttons pending). (iii) `ViewPatient` tamper-evident audit SystemCommand to replace the `phi.viewed` structured-log trace on the order-detail page. (iv) Persistent workstation pairing (today the fill workbench uses URL-pinned per-page selection). (v) Operator self-serve admin: invite users + assign roles + provision Clerk linkage. (vi) Carrier-credential admin UI (backend `RegisterCarrierCredential` shipped; needs a form).

  _Typing queue (shipped):_ closes the upstream end of the workflow — operator console now spans RECEIVED → … → SHIPPED. The typing surface is structurally different from PV1 / FILL / FINAL because the typing flow spans **two buckets**: `RECEIVED` orders sit in `INBOX` (the org-wide intake bucket per `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS`), while `TYPING_IN_PROGRESS`, `TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO`, and (per `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_EXCEPTION_STATE`) `PV1_REJECTED` all live in `TYPING`. **(1) `/ops/typing` page** — visibility gated on `typing.start`; renders three stacked sections so the typist has one screen for the full surface: **Inbox (ready to claim)** lists every `RECEIVED` row from the INBOX bucket with a "Claim (Start typing)" button; **In progress** lists `TYPING_IN_PROGRESS` rows from the TYPING bucket with a "Complete typing review → PV1" button on rows owned by the operator; **Exceptions (bounce-back / missing info)** is a conditionally-rendered third section that lists `PV1_REJECTED` (amber banner: "Bounced back from PV1. Open the order detail to read the rejection reason on the latest verification record…") and `TYPING_PENDING_MISSING_INFO` rows (amber banner: "Resolve the gap (patient, prescriber, or sig) and resume typing"). Same SLA-breach red border + priority/status badges + age countdown + order-detail row link as the other queues. The page issues **two parallel Prisma queries** (INBOX + TYPING) and partitions the TYPING result client-side rather than extending the `listOrdersInBucketByCode` helper to take an array — keeps the helper monomorphic for the consistent (PV1/FILL/FINAL) case and absorbs the typing-stage idiosyncrasy here where the UX requires it. **(2)–(3) Two API routes**: `start-typing` (claim, gated `typing.start`) and `complete-typing-review` (route to PV1, gated `typing.complete`). Both dispatched through the shared `dispatchOpsCommand` with route-bucketed idempotency keys; same-actor SoD on the downstream PV1 approval is enforced at ApprovePV1's `sodRules` (the typist cannot also be the PV1 pharmacist — see `start-pv1.test.ts:726`). **(4) Nav link** — "Typing queue" added as the FIRST workflow-stage entry in `apps/web/app/ops/layout.tsx` (above PV1), gated `typing.start`. **No new tests** — the queue helper is already covered, the two routes are thin dispatches over already-tested commands, and the in-page row-partition logic is pure data with no branching beyond what the rendered HTML reflects. **150 test files / 1642 tests passing** (unchanged — this is a UI-only addition over already-tested infrastructure).

  _Deferred (not on this slice):_ `MarkTypingMissingInfo` command + UI action. The workflow engine + policy already know about the transition (`MARK_TYPING_MISSING_INFO` in `packages/workflow/src/commands.ts` and `policy-v1.ts`), but no `@pharmax/verification` command handler exists yet. Building it is a separate slice: the handler shape is identical to `RejectPV1` (Zod `reasonCode` enum, structured exception transition, audit + outbox), the UI is a button + reason-code `<select>` on each `TYPING_IN_PROGRESS` row. Today the typist hits the missing-info wall by escalating through ops or by holding the order via `PlaceHold` (separate flow). Same applies to a dedicated `ReopenForCorrection` UI surface — the backend command is shipped but operator surfacing lives in a follow-up.

  _Fill queue + tech workbench (shipped):_ biggest UI slice yet — the tech bench is the longest action chain in the workflow (claim → assign-lot → print → scan → complete), and it's where techs spend the majority of their shift. Shipped as a two-page surface (queue + detail workbench) on the now-validated PV1/Final pattern, plus a workstation-context extension to the shared route dispatcher. **(1) `dispatchOpsCommand` enrichment** — added an optional `resolveTenancyExtras` hook that runs after `buildInput` and returns `{ workstationId?, siteId? }` (or `{ error }`). The resolver runs against the parsed body + the resolved operator session, and any returned scope is merged into the tenancy that the command bus sees. This is the bridge that makes `requiresWorkstation: true` commands (PrintVialLabel) dispatchable from the operator console without inventing a per-command auth surface. **Security**: every value the resolver returns is operator-submittable, so the caller MUST authorize the workstation/site itself — see `assertWorkstationBelongsToSite` below. **(2) `getFillWorkbench` projection** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/get-fill-workbench.ts`) — one Prisma round-trip for the order header + lines + per-line lot/vial-label state + per-line prescription drug-identity (non-PHI); then a parallel three-fan-out for (a) candidate lots filtered by `(org, site, ACTIVE, expirationDate ≥ today, product.ndc IN distinctNdcs)` and ordered soonest-expiring-first for FEFO encouragement, capped at 25-per-NDC; (b) site-scoped ACTIVE label printers; (c) site-scoped ACTIVE workstations. Returns `readyForCompletionScans: boolean` so the page knows when to render the scan-to-complete form. Also exports `assertWorkstationBelongsToSite({ orgId, siteId, workstationId })` — the authorization helper the print route uses to validate the operator's workstation pick before threading it into tenancy. **(3) `/ops/fill` queue page** — visibility gated on `fill.start`; two row variants (`PV1_APPROVED_READY_FOR_FILL` ready-to-claim with "Claim (Start fill)" button, `FILL_IN_PROGRESS` in-flight with "Open workbench" / "View workbench" link based on assignment ownership); same SLA-breach red border + priority badges + age countdown as PV1/Final. Rows link the external order number to `/ops/orders/[id]` for the PHI-decrypting detail read. **(4) `/ops/fill/[orderId]` workbench page** — the bench surface. Renders an order header, a URL-pinned workstation picker (`?workstation=<id>` — the page defaults to the first available, the operator can switch via a GET form, and every print form on the page submits that id as a hidden field), and per-line cards. Each card shows lot status + vial-label status side-by-side; for the assignee, missing-lot cards render a candidate-lot `<select>` (sorted FEFO) + Assign button, and lot-assigned-no-label cards render a printer `<select>` + Print button. When every line has both, a "Scan to complete" section opens at the bottom with per-line `lotScan` + `vialLabelScan` `<input>` pairs that POST to CompleteFill (which runs `@pharmax/scan` validation against the assigned lot + printed vial barcodes; mismatches surface as typed `FILL_SCAN_*` errors). Read-only mode for non-assignees and non-IN_PROGRESS rows is explicit. **(5)–(8) Four API routes**: `start-fill` (claim, gated `fill.start`), `assign-lot` (per-line lot pick, gated `fill.assign_lot`), `print-vial-label` (uses `resolveTenancyExtras` to validate + thread the workstation; gated `fill.print_vial_label` + `requiresWorkstation` on the command), `complete-fill` (custom form parser reconstructs `lineScans[i][field]` flat keys into the typed array; gated `fill.complete`). All four dispatched through the shared `dispatchOpsCommand` helper with route-bucketed idempotency keys. **(9) Nav link** — "Fill queue" between PV1 and Final, gated `fill.start`. **(10) Workspace dependency hygiene** — added `@pharmax/command-bus`, `@pharmax/fill`, `@pharmax/labels`, and `@pharmax/verification` as proper workspace dependencies of `apps/web` (they were previously resolved via pnpm hoist; the package.json now matches the imports). **+5 new tests** (`get-fill-workbench.test.ts`: happy-path projection + per-NDC lot bucketing + printer/workstation surfacing; `readyForCompletionScans` only flips when every line has lot+label; order-not-found returns null without secondary fan-out queries; `assertWorkstationBelongsToSite` accepts correct-site-active and rejects wrong-site/inactive). **150 test files / 1642 tests passing.**

  _Deferred (next slice):_ `ReprintVialLabel` UI (exception path with its own reason-code dropdown — straightforward but not on the primary fill loop), and the full workstation-pairing UX (currently the tech picks per-page; future slice bridges workstation into the operator session so the choice persists across pages and survives navigation).

  _Final-verification queue (shipped):_ second pharmacist signature surface — closes the workflow loop from `FILL_COMPLETED_READY_FOR_FINAL` → `FINAL_VERIFICATION_APPROVED_READY_FOR_SHIP`, which is the gate every order must cross before SHIPPED becomes legal. Mirrors the PV1 queue pattern exactly (validated in the previous slice), so this lands as four 30–230-line files + a one-line nav entry. **(1) `/ops/final` page** — visibility gated on `final.start`; lists every order in the `FINAL` bucket (both `FILL_COMPLETED_READY_FOR_FINAL` "ready to claim" rows and `FINAL_VERIFICATION_IN_PROGRESS` "in flight" rows — they share the same bucket per `BUCKET_CODE_FOR_STATUS`); each row links the external order number to `/ops/orders/[id]` for the PHI-decrypting detail read; per-row action set varies by row state: READY → "Claim (Start final verification)" button (gated `final.start`); IN*PROGRESS owned by the operator → "Approve final" + "Reject final" + `<select>` over `FINAL_REJECTION_REASONS` (gated `final.approve` / `final.reject` respectively); IN_PROGRESS owned by another → read-only with assignee id; same SLA-breach red border + age/countdown formatter as PV1. **Critical UX hint**: every operator-owned IN_PROGRESS row carries an inline amber notice — *"Separation of duties: if you also performed PV1 on this order, approval will be rejected at the command bus. Use Reject and route to another pharmacist if needed."\_ — because `ApproveFinalVerification` ships a `sodRules` clause that rejects a same-pharmacist approval at dispatch. The bus is the loud guard; this is the soft hint so the operator isn't surprised when their click bounces. **(2)–(4) Three API routes** (`start-final` / `approve-final` / `reject-final`) — each ≈25 lines, dispatched through `dispatchOpsCommand` with route-bucketed idempotency keys (`route:start-final:<id>` etc.) and per-action `successLogEvent` / `failureLogEvent` for the structured logger. `reject-final` validates `reasonCode` against `FINAL_REJECTION_REASONS` and returns `{ error: ... }` to surface a flash-error redirect when the client posts an unknown code. **(5) Nav link** — "Final verification" added to `apps/web/app/ops/layout.tsx` between PV1 and Emergency, gated `final.start`. **No new tests** — the queue helper (`listOrdersInBucketByCode`) is already covered against bucket / row-state contract from the PV1 slice; the three routes are thin dispatches over already-tested commands and the already-tested `dispatchOpsCommand` helper. **149 test files / 1637 tests passing** (unchanged from the order-detail slice — this is a UI-only addition).

  _Order-detail page (shipped):_ first PHI-decrypting operator surface. PV1 pharmacists cannot sign off on a drug they cannot see; this page is the now-validated read path for that signature. **(1) `getOrderDetail` projection** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/get-order-detail.ts`) — single Prisma round-trip that pulls order + patient (all envelope columns) + lines + lot + prescription + provider + last N order_events, then decrypts all 11 patient PHI envelopes + per-line `sigEnc` in parallel via `@pharmax/crypto::decryptField` with `binding = { tenantId, "patient"|"prescription", column, recordId }`. Each decrypt is wrapped in a per-field `tryDecrypt` shim: a corrupt envelope or KMS misconfig nulls that single field and flips `phiDecryptErrors=true` rather than aborting the page — a partial render with `"—"` placeholders is more useful to a triaging operator than a 500. The flag drives a red banner on the page warning the operator NOT to make a clinical decision until the cause is investigated. Prescriber name (HIPAA Safe Harbor: provider identity is not PHI) is composed from `firstName lastName, credential` and surfaced alongside NPI. Lot number + expiration come from the assigned `Lot` row when present (`"Not yet assigned"` otherwise). Frozen-object returns at every nesting level so callers can't accidentally mutate the projection. **(2) `/ops/orders/[orderId]` page** — visibility gated on `orders.read`; render is structured as four sections (header, patient, prescription lines, recent events); each decrypted value goes through a `<dd>...</dd>` so accidental DOM-scraping can't pull plaintext from a prop / data-attribute. Every successful render emits a structured `logger.info("phi.viewed", { event, orderId, patientId, operatorUserId, phiDecryptErrors })` operational trace — full tamper-evident `ViewPatient` SystemCommand (with audit-chain write) is a follow-up slice. Tenancy-miss → "Order not found" panel; permission-miss → "request orders.read" panel. **(3) Cross-page links** — PV1 queue + Emergency queue rows now link the external order number to `/ops/orders/[id]` so the pharmacist's claim → review → approve loop stays one click apart. **+3 unit tests** (`get-order-detail.test.ts`: happy-path decrypts every field + sets `phiDecryptErrors=false`; one-field failure flips the flag and nulls only that field, others decrypt normally; tenancy-miss returns null and never invokes decryptField). **149 test files / 1637 tests passing.**

  _Clerk + tenancy bridge (shipped):_ first auth-gated surface on the platform. **(1) Schema** — migration `20260606000000_phase5_user_clerk_id` adds `User.clerkUserId` (unique-when-present partial index — one Pharmax user maps to AT MOST one Clerk identity). Nullable because system-only users (`shipping-webhook@*`, `print-agent@*`) never sign in, and operators may be pre-provisioned server-side before their first sign-in. **(2) `@clerk/nextjs`** wired in `apps/web`: `ClerkProvider dynamic` inside `<body>` (Core 3+ contract), `proxy.ts` (Next.js 16 successor to `middleware.ts`) using `clerkMiddleware` with a `createRouteMatcher` allowlist for `/api/health` + `/api/webhooks/(.*)` + `/sign-in(.*)` + `/sign-up(.*)` — webhook routes stay public because signatures are the auth. Everything else gates through `auth.protect()`. Optional env shape: when `NEXT_PUBLIC_CLERK_PUBLISHABLE_KEY` is unset, Clerk's Keyless mode auto-generates dev keys on first SDK init so the app boots cleanly without a Clerk account. **(3) Hosted sign-in / sign-up routes** at `/sign-in/[[...sign-in]]` and `/sign-up/[[...sign-up]]` using Clerk's built-in `<SignIn />` / `<SignUp />` components. **(4) `resolveOperatorTenancyContext()`** in `apps/web/src/server/auth/resolve-tenancy.ts` — the **bridge primitive** for the operator console: `auth()` → Clerk userId → system-context Pharmax user lookup by `clerkUserId` → builds standard `TenancyContext` with fresh `correlationId` per request. Output is the exact shape the existing command bus already understands, so every operator click can dispatch commands through the standard pipeline. Three failure paths surface as typed reasons (`RESOLVE_TENANCY_NO_SESSION` / `RESOLVE_TENANCY_USER_NOT_LINKED` / `RESOLVE_TENANCY_USER_NOT_ACTIVE`) so the UI can render the right "contact your admin" message instead of crashing. **(5) Dashboard landing** at `/` replaces the Phase 0 stub: renders `Welcome, {displayName}` + tenancy snapshot when resolved, or one of three operator-facing messages when not. **(6) eslint Override 3c** allowlists `apps/web/src/server/auth/**` for `withSystemContext` use — same architectural shape as Override 3b (worker drains): a tenant-less external identifier resolves to the Pharmax tenant inside a system-context frame, then every downstream call runs inside the resolved tenancy. **+6 new tests** (resolver: happy path + NO_SESSION + USER_NOT_LINKED + 3 USER_NOT_ACTIVE variants). **145 test files / 1623 tests passing.**

  _Identity model:_ Clerk owns authentication (sign-in, MFA, sessions, password reset, OAuth). Pharmax owns authorization + tenancy (org, role grants, scope, audit). The `clerkUserId` column is the only bridge. Operators are pre-provisioned server-side via `bootstrap-org`; future hardening: webhook handler for `user.created` / `user.updated` Clerk events that auto-links new sign-ins to a pre-staged Pharmax row.

  _EMERGENCY queue page (shipped):_ first real operator surface; validates the entire vertical stack (Clerk auth → tenancy bridge → RBAC → command bus → audit / outbox). **(1) Boot wiring** — `apps/web/src/server/bootstrap.ts` extended to `configureRbac({ loader: new PrismaPermissionLoader(prisma) })` + `configureCommandBus({ prisma, clock, logger })`. Now any operator-driven HTTP route can dispatch a domain command through the same bus + audit chain the worker uses. **(2) `loadOperatorPermissions(tenancy)`** helper in `apps/web/src/server/auth/operator-permissions.ts` — lazy-singleton `PrismaPermissionLoader`, calls `resolveEffectivePermissions` (memoized per `(orgId, userId)`); paired with `hasOperatorPermission(perms, code)` for ergonomic call-site reads. **(3) `app/ops/layout.tsx`** — server-component layout with sidebar nav + topbar.
