Nav items are role-gated against the operator's effective permission set; an operator without `ship.resolve_escalation` doesn't see the "Emergency queue" link. `<UserButton afterSignOutUrl="/sign-in" />` for sign-out. **(4) `listEmergencyOrders` query helper** — read-only projection of orders in the EMERGENCY bucket for a given org, with the most-recent shipment tracking event threaded onto each row (so the operator sees what caused the escalation). Bucket-not-provisioned returns `bucketExists: false` cleanly. **(5) `/ops/emergency` page** — auth-gated by the ops layout, permission-gated against `ship.resolve_escalation`, renders a queue card per row with status / priority / time-since-escalation / latest carrier event. Each row carries an inline form (server-rendered POST, zero client JS) with disposition select + optional operator note. Flash banners on `?resolved=<id>` / `?error=<msg>`. **(6) `POST /api/ops/orders/:orderId/resolve-escalation`** route — resolves tenancy, parses form/JSON body, validates `disposition` against `ESCALATION_DISPOSITIONS`, enters tenancy, dispatches the existing `ResolveOrderEscalation` command with a minute-bucketed idempotency key (`route:resolve-escalation:{orderId}:{disposition}:{minute}` — double-click within 60s is a no-op; cross-minute repeats fall through to the command's own "not-in-EMERGENCY" guard). Success redirects to `/ops/emergency?resolved=<id>`; failure redirects with `?error=<code>: <message>` carrying the typed PharmaxError code. **+9 new tests** (3 `listEmergencyOrders`: bucket-missing / happy-path projection / limit; +6 from prior auth resolver). **146 test files / 1626 tests passing.**

  _Full vertical stack now validated:_ a `BillingManager` operator can sign in via Clerk → see the EMERGENCY queue gated by their permission → click "Resolve" → trigger the same `ResolveOrderEscalation` command path that `scripts/resolve-emergency-bucket.ts` exercises via CLI. Every other operator page from here on follows the same shape: `resolveOperatorTenancyContext()` → optional `loadOperatorPermissions()` → page renders, form posts to a thin `/api/ops/...` route that dispatches an existing command.

  _Billing operator screens (shipped):_ second operator surface; closes the operator-side gap on billing. **(1) Query helpers** in `apps/web/src/server/ops/list-invoices.ts` — `listInvoices` (paginated by `createdAt DESC`, optional `status` + `clinicId` filters, cursor + `nextCursor` pagination) and `getInvoiceDetail` (invoice + lines projection for the detail view). Both stay in `apps/web` until a second consumer needs them; presentation-shape projection is a UI concern, not domain. **(2) `dispatchOpsCommand` helper** — generic shape that centralizes the resolve-session → parse-body → enter-tenancy → dispatch → redirect pattern across all operator route handlers. Three billing routes (`finalize` / `credit` / `refund`) each become 20-line files that just declare the command + body parser + redirect targets. Validation errors return `{ error: string }` from `buildInput`; the helper redirects with `?error=<msg>`. **(3) `/ops/billing` invoice list** — gated by `billing.read`, renders a card-per-invoice list with status badges + filter chips (`ALL` / `DRAFT` / `OPEN` / `PAID` / `VOID` / `UNCOLLECTIBLE`). **(4) `/ops/billing/[invoiceId]` detail page** — invoice header (totals, status, Stripe ids), lines table (negative-amount credits render emerald), and action forms gated by both the operator's permissions AND the invoice's current state: **Finalize** appears only for DRAFT invoices with `billing.finalize_invoice`; **Credit** appears for any non-VOID invoice with `billing.credit_invoice`; **Refund** appears only for PAID invoices with a `stripeChargeId` and `billing.issue_refund`. **(5) Three thin route handlers** under `/api/ops/billing/invoices/[invoiceId]/` — `finalize/route.ts` (parses `daysUntilDue`, dispatches `FinalizeInvoice`), `credit/route.ts` (validates against `CREDIT_INVOICE_KINDS`, builds `CreditInvoiceInput`, redacts `reasonText`), `refund/route.ts` (validates against the 3 Stripe refund reasons, builds `IssueRefundInput`, redacts `operatorNote`). Each carries a minute-bucketed idempotency key. **(6) Nav update** — `Billing` link added to `/ops/layout.tsx`, gated by `billing.read`. **+5 new tests** (`listInvoices` + `getInvoiceDetail`: pagination boundary / filter passthrough / null tenancy miss / projection shape). **147 test files / 1631 tests passing.**

  _Operator can now end-to-end:_ sign in via Clerk → view invoices for their org → open any invoice → finalize DRAFT → apply CREDIT/DISCOUNT/ADJUSTMENT → issue Stripe refund. All four billing commands (`FinalizeInvoice` / `CreditInvoice` / `IssueRefund` / `RecordRefundReceived` via the existing webhook drain) are now reachable from the UI. The CLI tools (`bootstrap-org`, `resolve-emergency-bucket`) coexist with the UI — they call the same bus.

  _PV1 queue page (shipped):_ third operator surface and the first workflow-stage queue. Pharmacist enters the PV1 queue → sees orders waiting (`TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1`) and orders in progress (`PV1_IN_PROGRESS`) → claims a ready order (one click) → approves or rejects with a structured reason code. **(1) Generic `listOrdersInBucketByCode` query helper** (`apps/web/src/server/ops/list-orders-in-bucket.ts`) — projection-shape queue read parameterized by `bucketCode`; reusable for every workflow-stage queue page (typing / PV1 / fill / final / shipping all slot in). Orders are returned in queue-scanner order `(priority DESC, slaDeadlineAt ASC, receivedAt ASC)` — same shape as the existing covering index on `order`. **(2) `/ops/pv1` page** — visibility gated on `pv1.start`; renders each order as a card with priority badge + SLA countdown (red border when breached). Per-row action set varies by row state: TYPED_READY_FOR_PV1 → "Claim (Start PV1)" button; PV1_IN_PROGRESS owned by the operator → Approve + Reject (with a `PV1_REJECTION_REASONS` dropdown); PV1_IN_PROGRESS owned by another operator → read-only with "Claimed by <userId>". **(3) Three thin route handlers** under `/api/ops/orders/[orderId]/{start-pv1,approve-pv1,reject-pv1}` — each ~20 lines, dispatches the matching command through `dispatchOpsCommand` with minute-bucketed idempotency keys. `reject-pv1` validates the structured `reasonCode` against `PV1_REJECTION_REASONS` and returns a typed error on mismatch. **(4) Nav update** — "PV1 queue" link in `/ops/layout.tsx`, gated on `pv1.start`. **+3 new tests** (`listOrdersInBucketByCode`: bucket-missing / projection / queue-scanner order). **148 test files / 1634 tests passing.**

  _Three operator surfaces now live:_ Emergency queue (shipping clerk dispositions) → Billing (BillingManager finalize / credit / refund) → PV1 (pharmacist claim / approve / reject). The pattern is now well-proven: query helper → page → routes via `dispatchOpsCommand`. Every remaining workflow-stage queue (typing, fill, final, shipping) is template-application work using the same primitives — `listOrdersInBucketByCode` already supports them.

  _Remaining for the console:_ remaining workflow-stage queues (typing / fill / final / shipping — same shape as PV1; each is ~half a day of pattern-application work using the existing `listOrdersInBucketByCode` helper and `dispatchOpsCommand`); order-detail page showing patient + prescription + lines (pharmacist needs this BEFORE approving PV1 — today they have to read DB rows manually); reports dashboard (consumes the `@pharmax/reporting` registry; gated by a new `reports.read` permission); Clerk-webhook handler for `user.created` / `user.updated` sync; production-mode tightening (disable `/sign-up` for non-admin emails, force MFA for `BillingManager` + `OrgAdmin`); rich client-component forms (replace server-rendered POSTs for ergonomic validation + optimistic UI as volume warrants).

- [~] Compliance evidence: control matrix, log retention policies, KMS rotation runbook, access-review jobs

  _Control matrix (shipped, deepened):_ the higher-level SOC 2 + HIPAA control matrix (`docs/security/control-matrix.md` + `docs/soc2/controls-inventory.md` + `docs/soc2/trust-service-criteria-mapping.md` + `docs/soc2/evidence-inventory.md`) was in place at the policy + ADR + narrative level. The engineering-grade **code-evidence map** (`docs/soc2/code-evidence-map.md`) shipped this slice — maps every code-grounded control to the exact `.test.ts` files that prove it fires, the Prisma tables that store its runtime evidence, and the CI gate that pins the structural invariant. Eight explicit gaps were enumerated and cross-referenced to follow-up slices; as of 2026-05-28, **six are closed** (`ar1` access-review worker wired + G3a access-review evidence-pack producer, `kms1` KMS inventory + rotation policy consolidated + G4 code+IaC half, `it1` integration test layer expanded to 27 tests across 4 files / G8, `tf1` Terraform CI/CD wiring + deployment runbook shipped / G2 + G4-deployment-half, and `kms3` machine-verified inventory ↔ IaC parity via `scripts/check-kms-inventory.ts`) and **two remain open** (G3b sibling worker-loop wiring for chain-verifier + nightly-digest; `kms2` CMK identity-rotation gap in `AwsKmsAdapter.unwrapDataKey`) — plus three queued follow-ups (`tf1-applyflow` approval-gated production-apply workflow; operator-console UI for historical access-review snapshots; the operator-driven first `terraform apply` against the production AWS account). Each closure is recorded in the code-evidence map's revision history and the gap table.

  _Access-review snapshot persistence (shipped):_ closes the CC6.2 evidence gap end-to-end. Before this slice, `pnpm access-review` produced a JSON file on the operator's laptop — auditable in principle, unverifiable in practice (no chain-of-custody, no integrity proof, no record that the run actually happened). After this slice, every run produces a tamper-evident, operator-attributed, RLS-scoped audit trail per org per quarter.

  **Schema** (migration `20260615000000_phase5_access_review_snapshot`): new `access_review_snapshot` table — per-org row with `digestSha256` (SHA-256 of canonical sorted-key report JSON), `report` JSONB blob, denormalized summary scalars (totalPrincipals / elevatedPrincipalCount / inactivePrincipalCount / staleAssignmentCount / cryptoShredCapableRoleCount), `reportVersion`, `recordedByUserId` (nullable so the future scheduled-worker can record under a system identity), `commandLogId` FK (RESTRICT), and `(organizationId, periodEnd DESC)` index for "most recent snapshot per org" queries. Same RLS regime as every other tenant-scoped table: GRANT to `pharmax_app` + `pharmax_system`, ENABLE + FORCE row level security, single `tenant_isolation` policy on `pharmax.system_context` / `pharmax.organization_id` GUCs. Registered in `TENANT_SCOPED_MODELS` (`{ kind: "organizationId" }`) so future operator-console reads can't leak cross-tenant.

  **Command** (`packages/security/src/access-review/record-access-review-snapshot.ts`): `RecordAccessReviewSnapshot` is a **tenant `Command`** (not `SystemCommand`) — the snapshot row carries `commandLogId NOT NULL` and tenant commands write `command_log` _before_ the handler transaction, which is the only ordering that satisfies the FK without a deferred constraint. Cross-tenant guards: rejects `input.organizationId !== ctx.organizationId` (code `ACCESS_REVIEW_TENANCY_MISMATCH`) and `input.organizationId !== report.organizationId` (code `ACCESS_REVIEW_REPORT_ORG_MISMATCH`). Tamper-evidence: local `canonicalStringify` + `computeAccessReviewDigest` (kept in-package so `@pharmax/security` does not depend on `@pharmax/command-bus`). Emits `compliance.access_review_snapshot.recorded.v1` to the outbox and writes a structured `audit_log` entry. **6 contract tests**: happy path, cross-tenant rejection, report/operator mismatch, RBAC denial, digest determinism, idempotency-key creation.

  **Permission separation**: added `COMPLIANCE_ACCESS_REVIEW_RECORD` (`compliance.access_review.record`) alongside the existing `COMPLIANCE_ACCESS_REVIEW_VIEW`. Default role templates grant `RECORD` only to `OrgAdmin` + `SecurityOfficer` so a viewer cannot retroactively forge a snapshot — the operator who PRODUCES evidence is a deliberate, audited identity. Seeded in `prisma/seed.ts`; permissions registry count bumped 55 → 56.

  **Event** (`packages/events/src/events/compliance/access-review-snapshot-recorded-v1.ts`): `compliance.access_review_snapshot.recorded.v1` with `owner: "security"`, `retention: "7y"`, `phiSafe: true`, `routingKey: "tenant.compliance"`. Payload carries snapshot id + org id + slug + period + summary scalars + `digestSha256` + `recordedByUserId` + `commandLogId` — never the full report (consumers query the DB row by id through tenant RLS). Domain barrel + 4 invariant tests (`compliance/index.test.ts`) pin owner / phiSafe / retention.

  **CLI** (`scripts/security/run-access-review.ts`): now requires `--as-user=<operator-email>` unless `--dry-run`. Generates the report in `withSystemContext`, looks up the operator, then switches to `withTenancyContext` and dispatches `RecordAccessReviewSnapshot` through the command bus. **Dual-write**: DB row (unless `--skip-db`) AND JSON file (unless `--skip-file`), keyed by the same SHA-256 — operator gets a local artifact, auditor gets the database-canonical row, tampering with either is detectable. Idempotency key = `(quarter, orgId, operatorId)`; re-runs on the same day are safe.

  **Docs**: `docs/adr/0027-access-review-snapshot-persistence.md` (full design rationale — schema, tenant-vs-system command choice, permission split, tamper-evidence, outbox event, dual-write, rejected alternatives); `packages/security/src/access-review/README.md` updated with auditor cross-reference instructions (digest is the join key between the JSON file and the DB row) and the new CLI usage.

  **Net effect on the SOC 2 posture**: every run now produces (1) a digest-sealed DB row attributable to a named operator via `commandLogId`, (2) a matching `compliance.access_review_snapshot.recorded.v1` outbox event for downstream archival, (3) a `command_log` + `audit_log` pair the auditor can cross-reference, and (4) the JSON artifact the operator had before — now keyed by the same digest as the DB row. CC6.2 evidence moves from "we run a script quarterly, trust us" to a tamper-evident, operator-attributed, RLS-scoped audit trail per org per quarter. **Verify**: 328 passing across `@pharmax/security` + `@pharmax/rbac` + `@pharmax/tenancy` + `@pharmax/events`; full recursive `tsc --noEmit` clean; every parity guard (`check:schema`, `check:migrations`, `events:validate`, `events:migrate-check`, `check:commands`) green.

  _Quarterly access-review evidence-pack loop wired into worker boot (shipped):_ closes G3a from the code-evidence map. The `createQuarterlyAccessReviewLoop` factory had been built (apps/worker/src/compliance/access-review-job.ts, ~550 lines + 3 contract tests) but was never imported by `apps/worker/src/main.ts` — so although the loop was correct, no production worker actually ran it. This slice connects the wire.

  **What it does on schedule**: fires daily at 03:00 UTC (configurable via `QUARTERLY_ACCESS_REVIEW_HOUR_UTC` / `_MINUTE_UTC`); self-guards on `isFirstDayOfQuarter(now)` so 363 days/year it is a no-op tick. On Apr 1 / Jul 1 / Oct 1 / Jan 1 it walks every organization, generates the access-review report via `generateAccessReview`, aggregates `command_log` + `audit_log` activity by actor (counts only — no payloads), detects anomalies against configurable thresholds, writes a JSONL evidence artifact + a markdown reviewer's summary via the configured `EvidencePublisher`, and emits one notification per organization via the configured `ComplianceNotifier`. Per-org failures are isolated; the loop continues on to the next org and reports `organizationsProcessed` + `organizationsFailed` in the summary.

  **Wiring** (`apps/worker/src/main.ts` lines ~444–500): import added; loop constructed after the merkle-root loop; started after `merkleRootLoop.start()`; added to the shutdown `Promise.all`. Production warning surface: a structured `worker.quarterly_access_review.filesystem_publisher` log line fires at boot when `NODE_ENV=production` and the `FilesystemEvidencePublisher` is in use (an S3 Object-Lock publisher is the right production swap; tracked under `tf1`). Opt-out env knob `QUARTERLY_ACCESS_REVIEW_ENABLED=false` exists for staging environments running on a clone with no orgs.

  **Env knobs** (`apps/worker/src/env.ts`): `QUARTERLY_ACCESS_REVIEW_ENABLED` (boolean, default `true`); `QUARTERLY_ACCESS_REVIEW_HOUR_UTC` (0–23, default 3); `QUARTERLY_ACCESS_REVIEW_MINUTE_UTC` (0–59, default 0); `QUARTERLY_ACCESS_REVIEW_LOOKBACK_DAYS` (1–366, default 92 — covers one full quarter with small spillover for late-running jobs); `QUARTERLY_ACCESS_REVIEW_EVIDENCE_ROOT` (string path, default `./evidence`).

  **Design — why the scheduler does NOT call `RecordAccessReviewSnapshot`**: the user request was "flip RecordAccessReviewSnapshot from manual-invoke to quarterly-cron." The existing architecture intentionally separates two responsibilities: (1) producing the evidence pack on schedule — the worker's job; (2) attesting to the evidence — a human security officer's job, recorded via `RecordAccessReviewSnapshot` under THEIR identity (so `recordedByUserId` on every snapshot row names a real reviewer). If the scheduler dispatched the command itself, the audit trail would record "the scheduler attested" — auditors would lose the human attestor. The right separation is what now ships: scheduler produces evidence + notification, human walks the report + dispatches the CLI to record the attestation row. This is documented in the new CC6.2-2 row in `code-evidence-map.md`.

  **Net effect on SOC 2 posture**: CC6.2-2 moves from "evidence is produced when an operator remembers to run the CLI" to "evidence is produced every quarter without human intervention; the human's role narrows to the attestation step itself." The notification is the cue for the attestation. **Verify**: 162 passing across `apps/worker/`; full `tsc --noEmit` clean for the worker package; prettier + lint clean on `main.ts` + `env.ts`. `code-evidence-map.md` v1.1 updates CC6.2-2 + CC7.2-1 + the gap matrix (G3 → G3a closed + G3b queued for chain-verifier / nightly-digest sibling wiring).

  _KMS key inventory + rotation policy consolidated (shipped, 2026-05-28):_ closes the `kms1` slice of G4 from the code-evidence map. Before this slice the production KMS posture was real (eight customer-managed CMKs provisioned in `infra/terraform/modules/kms/main.tf`; `AwsKmsAdapter` fully wired with `EncryptionContext`-bound tenant isolation per ADR-0023; `KmsAsymmetricSigner` for Merkle root signing per ADR-0024; comprehensive per-key rotation procedures already in `docs/RUNBOOK.md`) but **scattered**. Auditors had no single page to answer "what keys exist, who owns them, what rotates when"; engineers had to read seven runbook sections plus two ADRs plus the Terraform module comments to reconstruct the inventory.

  **What shipped in this slice**: (1) `docs/security/kms-key-inventory.md` (v1.0) — single-source-of-truth table of all eight production keys (RDS storage, S3 documents, S3 audit archive, Secrets Manager, PHI envelope data key, blind-index HMAC search key, asymmetric Merkle signing key, CloudWatch Logs) with per-key purpose, `KeyUsage` + `KeySpec`, rotation cadence, env var, owning app, runbook link, and compromise blast radius. Includes cross-key invariants (no `Principal: *`, application grants live in IAM not key policy, `enable_key_rotation = true` on every symmetric/HMAC key, stable aliases) and an open-follow-ups table (`kms2`, `kms3`). (2) `docs/adr/0028-kms-key-inventory-and-rotation-policy.md` — formal ADR ratifying the inventory + the quarterly rotation drill cadence + the `AwsKmsAdapter` signing-surface clarification, with explicit rejected alternatives (one-ADR-per-key, skip-the-inventory, annual-drill-instead, implement-the-stubs). (3) `docs/RUNBOOK.md` § "Quarterly KMS rotation drill" — new section between "Verifying KMS in production" and "Re-running a missed Merkle manifest" that walks through a non-destructive end-to-end CMK rotation rehearsal in staging on a Q1–Q4 calendar (Q1 + Q4 data key, Q2 search key, Q3 Merkle signing key). Includes pre-flight, 9-step drill flow, per-key drill notes (the search-key drill exercises only synthetic data, the Merkle-signer drill exports the drill PEM without polluting the long-lived trust store), evidence-pack contents, and failure-mode handling. (4) Code cleanup in `packages/crypto/src/aws-kms-adapter.ts`: replaced the misleading "is not yet wired" error messages on `signRoot` / `verifyRoot` with explicit redirection to `KmsAsymmetricSigner` in `@pharmax/security`. The IAM split (PHI-decrypt principal does NOT hold `kms:Sign`) is the load-bearing security property; the stub now documents this rather than implying incomplete work.

  **Gap I uncovered while reading the code** (now tracked as `kms2`): `AwsKmsAdapter.unwrapDataKey` passes `KeyId` to `kms.Decrypt`. AWS KMS validates that the passed `KeyId` matches the key id embedded in the ciphertext, so after a manual CMK identity rotation (alias-swap to a new CMK), envelopes wrapped under the previous CMK become unreadable — `Decrypt` returns `IncorrectKeyException`. Routine annual auto-rotation of key material is unaffected because the CMK identity stays stable. The fix is either to omit `KeyId` from `Decrypt` (loses one defense-in-depth check) or to accept a list of historical data-key ARNs and iterate. Captured in §3.2.5 + §7 of the inventory, the gap matrix of the code-evidence map (new `kms2` row), and the follow-up backlog.

  **Net effect on the SOC 2 posture**: CC6.7 evidence moves from "the procedure exists in the runbook" to "the procedure is rehearsed every 90 days in staging with a dated evidence pack the auditor reads." The asymmetric signing key's non-rotatability is now an explicit Q3 drill scope rather than a footnote. The `AwsKmsAdapter` stub no longer reads as "platform is incomplete." `code-evidence-map.md` v1.2 updates CC6.7-1, CC7.2-3, and closes G4's code+IaC half; only `tf1` (production-environment Terraform apply, env vars, S3 Object-Lock bucket) remains for the deployment half. **Verify**: `pnpm --filter @pharmax/crypto test` clean; `tsc --noEmit` clean for `packages/crypto`; prettier + lint clean on all touched files.

  _DB-truth integration test layer expanded (shipped, 2026-05-28):_ closes the `it1` slice / G8 gap from the code-evidence map. Before this slice the `packages/integration-tests/` package had a single test file (`verification-record.test.ts`, 12 tests) that pinned RLS isolation + REVOKE UPDATE/DELETE + a CHECK constraint for the verification table only. The unit-test layer covered every command handler in isolation behaviorally via fake Prisma, but the load-bearing "RLS actually BLOCKS cross-tenant reads under `pharmax_app`" and "the CAS row-lock pattern actually SERIALIZES under READ COMMITTED" proofs ran against the database only for one table. An auditor (or a regression in a future migration) had no way to know whether the GRANT/RLS/UNIQUE invariants held for the other security-critical tables.

  **What shipped in this slice**: three new test files + a supporting seed helper. (1) `packages/integration-tests/src/audit-log.test.ts` (8 tests across 3 groups): RLS cross-tenant block + same-tenant sentinel + GUC-unset fail-closed; **universal REVOKE UPDATE/DELETE under BOTH `pharmax_app` AND `pharmax_system`** (the immutability invariant is universal — even the BYPASSRLS role cannot tamper with `audit_log`, which is the core SOC 2 CC7.2 guarantee); `UNIQUE(organizationId, seq)` fires as `23505` on a forced duplicate-seq insert (pins the per-tenant chain monotonicity guarantee independent of the advisory-lock primitive); `audit_chain_lock_key(uuid)` is GRANTed + callable from both runtime roles and returns a stable BIGINT (the chain serialization primitive itself); two sequential inserts in the same tenant link `prevHash[N+1] = entryHash[N]` and `audit_chain_state` advances monotonically (the chain-head invariant the production writer maintains atomically). (2) `packages/integration-tests/src/order.test.ts` (4 tests): RLS cross-tenant block + same-tenant sentinel + GUC-unset fail-closed on the central workflow row, plus the load-bearing **two-connection CAS race**: two concurrent `pharmax_app` connections each in their own BEGIN/COMMIT scope both fire `UPDATE "order" SET version=2 WHERE id=$X AND version=1`; T2 blocks on T1's row lock, T1 commits, T2's WHERE re-evaluates against the new tuple (version=2, not 1) under READ COMMITTED and the UPDATE affects 0 rows. Final state is version=2, NOT 3 — the exact guarantee ADR-0007's "every workflow transition must lock the order row" rule depends on. (3) `packages/integration-tests/src/idempotency-key.test.ts` (3 tests): `UNIQUE(organizationId, commandName, key)` fires on a duplicate insert; the constraint is scoped to the tenant (same key under a different org permitted — no global key bleed); the constraint is scoped to the command (same key + tenant + different command permitted). (4) Extended `packages/integration-tests/src/lib/seed.ts` with `insertAuditLogRow`: a chain-head-aware writer that reads `audit_chain_state`, computes the next `seq` and `prevHash`, inserts the row, and upserts the head — mirroring the production writer's atomic chain-head advance without depending on Prisma (the integration suite deliberately uses `pg` directly for explicit role / GUC / advisory-lock control). README updated with the new test-surface table and a "Total: 27 tests across 4 files" summary.

  **Net effect on the SOC 2 posture**: CC6.1-3 (RLS), CC7.2-2 (audit log immutability + chain primitives), and PI1.5-1 (concurrency control) each move from "fake-Prisma unit tests prove the application logic respects the boundary" to "the database itself rejects the boundary violation, and a `.test.ts` against a live Postgres proves it." The REVOKE UPDATE/DELETE on `audit_log` against the BYPASSRLS role is the strongest assertion — it proves no application-layer privilege escalation can ever modify an audit row in place, which is the CC7.2-2 / HIPAA §164.312(c)(1) "integrity" cornerstone. The CAS test pins the rule that lets the platform run workflow transitions without a global lock or a per-order mutex. `code-evidence-map.md` v1.3 updates CC6.1-3 + CC7.2-2 + PI1.5-1 + closes G8. The suite is excluded from the default `pnpm test` (requires local Postgres) and runs via `pnpm test:integration`; runbook in `packages/integration-tests/README.md`. **Verify**: `pnpm --filter @pharmax/integration-tests typecheck` clean; `pnpm eslint --max-warnings=0 packages/integration-tests/src` clean; prettier clean on all touched files. End-to-end test execution requires `pnpm db:up` + `pnpm db:migrate:deploy` first (per the package README); the structural verification above is what the default CI lane catches.

  _Terraform CI/CD wiring shipped (shipped, 2026-05-28):_ closes the IaC + CI half of the `tf1` slice / G2 gap from the code-evidence map. The surprise of this slice was scope: the framing in the original five-task prioritized list was "AWS Terraform + minimal production deployment — the platform is local-only today; one production-promotion slice (VPC, RDS, S3 with Object Lock, Cloudflare/ALB, secrets management) takes it from 'could be deployed' to 'is deployed'." Discovery showed `infra/terraform/` is already 3,745 lines of fully-formed HCL across 12 modules (alb, cloudwatch, ecr, ecs, iam, kms, network, rds, s3-audit-archive, s3-documents, secrets, waf) and 4 env-region working directories (dev/use1, staging/use1, prod/use1, prod/usw2) — VPC + 3 subnet tiers, Postgres 16 Multi-AZ, all eight KMS CMKs (matching the `docs/security/kms-key-inventory.md` document), audit-archive bucket with COMPLIANCE Object Lock + 7-year retention, ECS Fargate cluster + per-service IAM least-privilege, WAFv2 with rate-limit + managed rule groups, CloudWatch alarms + dashboard, Secrets Manager entries. The infra/terraform/README.md is comprehensive and includes a full SOC 2 control-mapping table. **The real gap was CI/CD wiring**: the README references `.github/workflows/deploy-aws-*.yml` workflows that did not exist, so the Terraform code could be `apply`-ed by an operator but no PR-level gate prevented broken HCL from merging and no scheduled job detected drift between the live AWS world and the HCL.

  **What shipped in this slice**: three artifacts that turn "could be deployed" into "is deployed with safety rails." (1) `.github/workflows/terraform-ci.yml` — runs on every PR that touches `infra/terraform/**` (path-filtered to skip app-code PRs); three parallel jobs run `terraform fmt -recursive -check -diff`, `terraform init -backend=false && terraform validate` for the root composition + bootstrap + every env-region working directory, and `tflint --recursive` with the AWS plugin (cached); a `terraform-ci-pass` aggregator job is the single required status check that branch protection points at. No AWS credentials needed — purely static HCL validation. (2) `.github/workflows/terraform-drift.yml` — daily-scheduled (08:00 UTC) plus `workflow_dispatch`; gates every cloud-touching job behind a `preflight` job that no-ops when the `AWS_DRIFT_ROLE_ARN` repository variable is unset (so forks and unconfigured repos do not see false failures); runs `terraform plan -detailed-exitcode -lock=false` against both `prod/us-east-1` and `prod/us-west-2` via GitHub OIDC (no long-lived AWS keys); on exit code 2 (drift) uses `actions/github-script@v7` to either open a new GitHub issue labelled `infra/drift,prod-use1` (or `prod-usw2`) or append a comment to the existing open one — the workflow run page is linked from the issue body and the full plan output is uploaded as an artifact retained for 30 days. Required IAM permissions for the OIDC role are read-only (`*:Describe*` + `*:Get*` + `*:List*` for every resource the stack provisions — no `Create*`/`Update*`/`Delete*`); the future `terraform-apply` workflow will use a separate write-capable role with an approval gate. (3) `docs/operations/production-deployment.md` — the unified deployment runbook (~280 lines), consolidating what was previously scattered across infra README + bootstrap README + RUNBOOK: prerequisites checklist; one-time-per-account bootstrap procedure (state bucket with GOVERNANCE-mode Object Lock + DynamoDB lock + state-encryption CMK); the one-time GitHub Actions OIDC trust-relationship setup with the read-only-policy enumeration + the `AWS_DRIFT_ROLE_ARN` variable wiring; the first-apply procedure with explicit emphasis on plan review as the load-bearing CC8.1 step (review the resource count, spot-check every destroy, confirm no unexpected resources); the routine-apply procedure; the drift-handling procedure (ratify-or-revert, with the CC8.1-compliant ratification path being "update HCL to match the world"); a rollback section that documents the limits of rollback for KMS / audit-archive / RDS (i.e. exactly when crypto-shred and Object Lock are operating as designed); a copy-paste deploy-ticket checklist; an open-follow-ups section that explicitly queues `tf1-applyflow` (approval-gated production-apply workflow) and the cross-region RDS read replica; a compliance crosswalk to CC6.1, CC6.6, CC7.2, CC8.1, and C1.2.

  **Net effect on the SOC 2 posture**: CC6.6-1 evidence moves from "TLS is enforced because we configured the ALB in the console" to "TLS is enforced because `infra/terraform/modules/alb/main.tf` line 124 pins `ssl_policy = ELBSecurityPolicy-TLS13-1-2-2021-06` and the daily `terraform-drift` workflow proves the console hasn't changed it." CC8.1 ("authorized, reviewed, tested change") gains operating evidence at the infrastructure tier: terraform-ci is the required-check that prevents broken HCL from merging, and a clean drift run for >7 consecutive days IS the evidence that infrastructure changes only land via reviewed PRs. CC7.2 ("monitor anomalies") gains a 24h SLA on infrastructure-level drift detection — a previously-uncaught console click on a security group rule or alarm threshold now surfaces as a labelled GitHub issue within a day. `code-evidence-map.md` v1.4 updates CC6.6-1, G2, and the G4 follow-up reference. The IaC + CI + drift detection ship in this slice; the one-time first `terraform apply` against the production AWS account remains operator-driven per the new runbook (the CC8.1 two-person-review posture), and an approval-gated `terraform-apply` workflow is queued as `tf1-applyflow` for when the team grows past two engineers. **Verify**: `node -e 'yaml.load(...)'` parses both workflows; `pnpm prettier --check` clean on all four touched files; structural smoke-check confirms `terraform-ci` has 4 jobs (fmt-check, validate, tflint, terraform-ci-pass aggregator) and `terraform-drift` has 3 (preflight gate, drift-prod-use1, drift-prod-usw2) with correct OIDC `id-token: write` + `issues: write` permissions and correct `needs:` wiring. Actionlint was not available in the sandbox; the workflows use only current major versions of well-known actions (`actions/checkout@v4`, `hashicorp/setup-terraform@v3`, `terraform-linters/setup-tflint@v4`, `aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v4`, `actions/github-script@v7`, `actions/cache@v4`, `actions/upload-artifact@v4`) and were structurally cross-referenced against the existing `.github/workflows/ci.yml` patterns.

  _KMS inventory ↔ Terraform drift check shipped (shipped, 2026-05-28):_ closes the `kms3` slice from the code-evidence map. The `kms1` slice added `docs/security/kms-key-inventory.md` (enumerating eight production CMKs with owner / KeyUsage / KeySpec / rotation cadence / env var / runbook link / blast radius) and §6 of that doc said "CI does not yet enforce this; the review checklist is the gate." Reviewer-as-gate is a SOC 2 CC8.1 anti-pattern — when an engineer ships an IaC change to `infra/terraform/modules/kms/main.tf` without updating the inventory, the auditor-facing surface silently misleads the next auditor reading it and the only way to catch it is a careful human reviewer noticing the missing markdown edit. This slice replaces the checklist with a machine-verified gate.

  **What shipped in this slice**: a focused TypeScript safety linter, mirroring the established `scripts/check-{migrations,schema,commands}.ts` pattern. (1) `scripts/check-kms-inventory.ts` (~510 lines including extensive header documentation): pure-functional parser + comparator + report formatter, all individually exported and testable. The HCL side parses both `aws_kms_key.<name>` resources (extracting `key_usage`, `customer_master_key_spec`, `enable_key_rotation` with AWS-default fallbacks) and `aws_kms_alias.<name>` resources (extracting the suffix after `<prefix>-` so it lines up with the inventory's `alias/<prefix>-<suffix>` convention). A bespoke `findMatchingCloseBrace` walker handles nested HCL blocks (`tags { ... }`, `lifecycle { ... }`, `validation { ... }`) without false-pairing — necessary because the module's resource bodies routinely contain nested blocks that a flat regex cannot pair correctly. A `var.*` reference in `customer_master_key_spec` (e.g. `var.asymm_sign_key_spec`) is resolved by reading the matching `variable "<name>" { default = "..." }` from `variables.tf`; a variable with no default throws (the inventory cannot pin a value the IaC leaves unbound). The markdown side parses the §3.1 summary table by header text (not column index, so column reordering does not silently break the check), and extracts both primary and legacy alias suffixes per row using the same `(+ -<suffix> legacy alias)` convention the inventory already uses. The comparator emits a discriminated `DriftIssue` union covering five drift kinds (key-missing-from-inventory, key-missing-from-terraform, key-usage-mismatch, key-spec-mismatch, rotation-mismatch, alias-missing-from-inventory, alias-missing-from-terraform); the report formatter renders each as a copy-pasteable remediation line naming the file the engineer should edit to fix it. (2) `scripts/check-kms-inventory.test.ts` (44 tests across 11 describe blocks): table-driven coverage of `findMatchingCloseBrace` (nested + commented + unbalanced inputs), `extractResourceBlocks` (nested-brace + ignore-unrelated-resource cases), `parseKmsKeyBody` (defaults + literal + variable-ref cases), `parseKmsAliasResources` (suffix extraction + missing-target rejection), `extractVariableDefault`, `resolveKeySpec` (literal pass-through + variable resolution + no-default rejection), `splitMarkdownRow` (escaped-pipe handling), `extractAliasSuffixes` (primary + legacy + empty), `isRotationYes` (Yes/No/bold variants + unrecognised rejection), `parseInventorySummaryTable` (end-to-end + missing-table rejection), `compareKmsState` (every drift kind individually + the all-clean case), `formatDriftReport` (every issue kind contains the expected remediation hint). (3) `pnpm check:kms-inventory` script added to `package.json`, wired into `pnpm verify` (the local pre-PR gate) and the `safety-linters` job in `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (the universally-running PR gate; alongside the existing `check:migrations`, `check:schema`, `check:commands`). (4) `kms-key-inventory.md` v1.1: §6 rewritten to describe the now-automated enforcement (was: "CI does not yet enforce this; the review checklist is the gate"; now: "CI enforces this via `scripts/check-kms-inventory.ts`..."); §7 marks `kms3` CLOSED with the implementation reference; the documents-key row in §3.1 + the §3.2.2 per-key detail were updated to record `alias/<prefix>-s3` as the legacy alias (the drift the check surfaced on its first end-to-end run — the `aws_kms_alias.documents_legacy_s3` resource was in TF but undocumented in the inventory).

  **Net effect on the SOC 2 posture**: CC6.7-1 evidence moves from "the inventory document exists and humans agree to keep it in sync with the IaC" to "the inventory document is machine-verified against the IaC on every PR, with the check itself unit-tested across 44 cases covering every drift kind." CC8.1 ("authorized, reviewed, tested change") gains a structural enforcement at the KMS inventory boundary: an engineer cannot land an IaC change that adds, removes, or repurposes a KMS key without also updating the auditor-facing surface — the PR is rejected at the `safety-linters` job otherwise. The first end-to-end run against the real files found one piece of latent drift (the undocumented legacy alias), proving the check has positive predictive value beyond "tests that pass on a clean tree." `code-evidence-map.md` v1.5 updates the CC6.7-1 row's inventory-rotation paragraph, the automated-tests cell, and the CI-gates cell to cite the new safety linter. **Verify**: `pnpm vitest run scripts/check-kms-inventory.test.ts` clean (44/44 pass); `pnpm check:kms-inventory` exits 0 against the (now-fixed) real files; `pnpm prettier --check` clean on all touched files; the script itself surfaces and explains every drift kind via the report formatter (verified by the formatDriftReport test). Tracked under the `safety-linters` CI job from this point forward.

  _Remaining for compliance evidence:_ control matrix doc (cross-references each SOC 2 CC to the platform feature + audit table + test that proves it — shipped as `docs/soc2/code-evidence-map.md`); operator-driven first `terraform apply` against the production AWS account (runbook + OIDC role setup in place; one-time human action remaining); approval-gated `terraform-apply` workflow (`tf1-applyflow`); sibling worker-loop wiring for the daily audit-chain verifier and nightly security digest (G3b — both have built but unwired loops in `apps/worker/src/security/`); CMK identity-rotation gap in `AwsKmsAdapter.unwrapDataKey` (`kms2`); operator-console UI to browse historical access-review snapshots (`compliance.access_review.view` permission already exists; ledger + RLS already in place — UI-only follow-up). As of 2026-05-28, **six of the original eight follow-up gaps** from the code-evidence map are closed (G3a access-review producer wired, `kms1` KMS inventory + rotation policy consolidated, `it1` integration test layer expanded to 27 tests across 4 files, G2 Terraform CI/CD + runbook shipped, G4 code+IaC half closed, `kms3` inventory ↔ IaC parity machine-verified); two remain (G3b sibling worker loops; `kms2` CMK identity-rotation) plus the queued `tf1-applyflow` + UI for historical snapshots + one-time first prod-apply.

## Phase 6 — Hardening

- [ ] Read replicas + reporting replica routing
- [ ] OpenTelemetry tracing across web, worker, print-agent
- [ ] Chaos drills: printer outage, queue backpressure, Stripe outage
- [ ] Penetration test remediation
- [~] Terraform-defined AWS environment (RDS, ElastiCache, ECS Fargate, ALB, WAF, S3, KMS, CloudWatch, Secrets Manager) — **HCL + CI + drift detection shipped** (`infra/terraform/` is the 3,745-line reproducible tree; 12 modules + 4 env-regions; `.github/workflows/terraform-ci.yml` enforces fmt + validate + tflint on every infra PR; `.github/workflows/terraform-drift.yml` runs daily OIDC `plan -detailed-exitcode` and opens labelled GitHub issues on drift; full deployment runbook in `docs/operations/production-deployment.md`); **first `terraform apply` against the production AWS account remains operator-driven** per the CC8.1 two-person-review posture (one-time human action, runbook in place); approval-gated routine-apply workflow queued as `tf1-applyflow`.
